inasmuch as they are accepted by heretics,  
and thus are of the same kind as the Buddhist statements on stupa worship. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'vivādādhyāsitaṁ', prāmāṇya-viṣayē vipratipatti-samākrāntam।

'puṇya-pāpayōr' iti viṣaya-saptamī।

caityavandana ... Bhaṭṭa Medhātithi, commenting on Manusmṛti, XII. 95, quotes from some unknown source, the following:

> nodanāḥ caityavandanataḥ svargo bhavati.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi -  

vivādādhyāsitaṁ tantraṁ na mānaṁ puṇyapāpayōḥ ।  
trayībāhyairgr̥hītatvāc caityavandanavākyavat ॥
</details>

## 06 vēda-tiraskāraḥ

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca tēṣāṁ  
trayī-mārga-tyāga--puras-saraḥ sarva-dharmōpadēśa  
iti sva-vākyāny ēva upakhyāpayanti 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Besides, their own texts relate that  
the instruction in all their dharmas  
presupposes the abandoning of the Way of the Veda; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca tēṣāṁ trayīmārgatyāgapurassaraḥ sarvadharmōpadēśa iti svavākyānyēva upakhyāpayanti 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> caturṣu vēdēṣu paraṁ śrēyō'labdhvā  
śāṇḍilya idaṁ śāstramadhītavān  

ityādīni 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> "having failed to find the supreme good in the four Vedas,  
> Sandilya learnt this doctrine...." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This objection is raised by Śaṅkara in his commentary on the Brahma-sūtra: II. ii.45: “vipratiṣedhācca”. Cf. his commentary: “vedavipratiṣedhaśca bhavati; 'caturṣu vedeṣu paraṃ śreyo' labdhvā śāṇḍilya idaṃ śāstramadhigatavān’ ityādivedanindādarśanāt”, etc.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> caturṣu vēdēṣu paraṁ śrēyō'labdhvā  
śāṇḍilya idaṁ śāstramadhītavān  

ityādīni 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad iha  
kathaṁ caturṇām api vēdānāṁ niśrēyasa-sādhanāvabōdhakatva-vyudāsēna ārabhamāṇaḥ  
tat-prasādāvagatam +++(mōkṣākhyam)+++ arthaṁ  
pum-arthatayā kathayatīty utprēkṣyēta ?+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

But how can we presume that a certain text can teach that a certain object,  
which is known from the four Vedas,  
is man's supreme goal in life  
if he rejects at the outset the very authority of the Vedas as sources of knowledge  
about the means which lead to bliss? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadiha kathaṁ caturṇāmapi vēdānāṁ niśrēyasasādhanāvabōdhakatvavyudāsēna ārabhamāṇaḥ tatprasādāvagatamarthaṁ pumarthatayā kathayatītyutprēkṣyēta ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

manv-ādayō hi  
vivakṣita-sakala-samīhita-sādhanāvabōdhakam  
āgamaika-mūlam abhidadhānā dr̥śyantē ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

On the contrary,  
we find that Manu and other authors of Traditions  
declare that their works which expound as their teaching the means of attaining all kinds of desirable ends  
derive solely from Scripture: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

manvādayō hi vivakṣitasakalasamīhitasādhanāvabōdhakamāgamaikamūlamabhidadhānā dr̥śyantē ।
</details>

'vēdō dharma-mūlaṁ', 'tad-vidāṁ ca smr̥ti-śīlē'

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Gautamadharmasūtra: I. 1-2.
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> vēdō'khilō dharmamūlaṁ  
> smr̥tiśīlē ca tadvidām ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> "The Veda in its entirety is the basis of the Law,  
> as well as of the traditions and customs of those who are expert in Law"; 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Manusmṛti: II. 6a.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vēdō'khilō dharmamūlaṁ smr̥tiśīlē ca tadvidām ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> śrutismr̥tivihitō dharmaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> "the Law is enjoined by Scripture and Tradition"; 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vasiṣṭhasmṛti: I. 2.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

śrutismr̥tivihitō dharmaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> sa sarvō 'bhihitō vēdē  
sarva-jñānamayō hi saḥ ।  

iti ca ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"it is entirely expressed in the Veda;  
for the Veda contains all knowledge." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Manusmṛti: II. 7b.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sa sarvō'bhihitōvēdē sarvajñānamayō hi saḥ ।  

iti ca ।  
</details>

## 07 pr̥thak-saṁskara-liṅgam

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad aparam  
upanayanādi-saṁskr̥tānām adhikr̥tānāṁ ca  
agni-hōtrādi-samasta-vaidika-karmasu  
punar api bhagavad-ārādhanādhikāra-siddhayē  
dīkṣā-lakṣaṇa-saṁskāra-varṇanaṁ,  
tad avaidikatām ēvānukārayati, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[15]]  
Further, the assertion that those who have already been consecrated by the sacraments of Investiture etc.  
and are thereby qualified for all the Vedic rituals, agnihotra etc.,  
must yet undergo another sacrament, called Consecration ( namely, dīkṣā),  
in order to be qualified for the worship of the Bhagavan,  
demonstrates that the system is non-Vedic;  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Pādmasaṃhitā Caryāpāda: I. 8b-10a:

> naivādhikāriṇaste ca dīkṣāsaṃskāravarjitāḥ ॥  
yathaiva dīkṣaṇīyeṣṭyā jāyante brāhmaṇādayaḥ ।  
tathaiva dīkṣāvidhinā jāyamānā yathoditāḥ ॥  
pūjāvidhau bhagavataḥ prakalpante 'dhikāriṇaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadaparam upanayanādisaṁskr̥tānāmadhikr̥tānāṁ ca agnihōtrādisamastavaidikakarmasu punarapi bhagavadārādhanādhikārasiddhayē dīkṣālakṣaṇasaṁskāravarṇanaṁ tadavaidikatāmēvānukārayati, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vaidikatvē hi tair ēva saṁskārair bhagavad-ārādhanādāv apy adhikriyēran ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for if it were Vedic,  
they would be qualified for Tantric ritual by the regular sacraments. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vaidikatvē hi tairēvasaṁskārairbhagavadārādhanādāvapyadhikriyēran ।  
</details>

## 08 14-vidyāsthānēṣv anantarbhāvaḥ

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad api dharma-pramāṇatayā  
samastāstika-jana-parigr̥hītēṣu catur-daśa-vidyāsthānēṣv aparigaṇanaṁ  
tad apy avaidkattvē liṅgam - 
anyathā hīdam api tad-anyatamatvēna smaryēta ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Again, another indication of its non-Vedic character is the fact  
that the system is not included among the fourteen sources of knowledge,  
which all orthodox people recognize as giving authoritative information on the Law.  
If it were authoritative,  
then it would have been recognized as such by tradition;  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

fourteen sources of knowledge - namely, the four Vedas, six Vedāngas, the Purāṇas, Mimansā, Nyāya and Dharmaśāstra.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide Yājñavalkyasmṛti: I. 3:

> purāṇanyāyamīmāṃsādharmaśāstrāṅgamiśritāḥ ।  
vedāssthānāni vidyānāṃ dharmasya ca caturdaśa ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadapi dharmapramāṇatayā samastāstikajanaparigr̥hītēṣu caturdaśavidyāsthānēṣvaparigaṇanaṁ tadapyavaidkattvē liṅgam anyathā hīdamapi tadanyatamatvēna smaryēta ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca smaryatē,  
tad avasīyatē - "a-vaidikam ēvēdaṁ pañca-rātra-smaraṇam" iti । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

but as it is not so recognized, this proves that the Pañcarātra tradition is non-Vedic. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca smaryatē, tadavasīyatē avaidikamēvēdaṁ pañcarātrasmaraṇamiti । 
</details>

## 09 bādarāyaṇōktiḥ

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ata ēva ca bhagavatā bādarāyaṇēna  
trayī-mārga-pratyanīka-bhūta--kaṇa-bhug--akṣa-caraṇa--su-gata-matādi--  
bāhya-samaya-nirāsāvasarē  
'sya tantrasya nirāsaḥ ।  
"utpatty-asaṁbhavāt" iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For this reason the venerable Badarāyaṇa,  
when he has occasion to refute the heterodox doctrines of Kanāda, Akṣapada, the Buddha etc. as inimical to the Way of the Veda,  
also refutes the Pancarãtra in his Sutra (BrS. 2.2.42.):  
"Because of the impossibility of origin.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ata ... This is the contention of the Advaitins. The entire Utpattyasambhava or the Pāñcarātra section of the Brahmasūtra [II. ii. 42-45] consisting of the four aphorisms: “utpattyasaṃbhavāt”, “na ca kartuḥ karaṇaṃ”, “vijñānādibhāve vā tadapratiṣedhaḥ” and “vipratiṣedhācca” had been interpreted by Śaṅkarācārya as refuting the validity of the Pāñcarātrāgamas.

utpattyasambhavāt ... Brahmasūtra: II. ii.42. This sūtra is the 42nd one in the second Pāda of the second Adhyāya, according to Śaṅkara. But according to Rāmānuja, this is the 39th aphorism.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ata ēva ca bhagavatā bādarāyaṇēna trayīmārgapratyanīkabhūtakaṇabhugakṣacaraṇasugatamatādibāhyasam ayanirāsāvasarē'sya tantrasya nirāsaḥ ।  
utpattyasambhavāt iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

trayī-vidām ittham a-saṅgrahēṇa  
tathā trayī-bāhya-parigrahēṇa ।  
anantarōktair api hētubhis tan  
na mānavādi-smaraṇais samānam ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore, as the Vedic experts regard the Pañcaratra doctrine as non-Vedic  
since it is not included among the Vedic systems  
and because of other reasons which will be advanced in the sequel,  
it cannot be compared with the Tradition of Manu etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

trayīvidāmitthamasaṅgrahēṇa tathā trayībāhyaparigrahēṇa ।  
anantarōktairapi hētubhistanna mānavādismaraṇaissamānam ॥
</details>

## 10 kṣudra-vidyā-paratā

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ēvaṁ sati  
yāny api lōkaṁ vyāmōhayituṁ  
vidvēṣaṇōccāṭana-vaśīkaraṇādi--kṣudra-vidyā-prāyam ēva bahulam upadiśadbhir  
bhagavad-ārādhanādi--katipaya-vaidika-karmāṇi pāñcarātrikair nirdiśyantē  
tāny anupayōgyāny avisrambhaṇīyāni ca  
śva-dr̥ti+++(=bag)+++-nikṣipta-kṣīravad  
iti manyāmahē । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In view of all this it is our opinion that such infrequent good rites- e.g., the worship of the Bhagavān - which are described by the Pañcaratricas  
(who teach a good many others,  
mostly black arts of exciting hatred, haunting a person out of his occupation, envoutement etc.)  
are merely added to deceive people about their real attentions and do not deserve our faith or consideration: they are like milk that is put in a dog's bladder ! 

[[16]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Tantravārtika under I. iii-4 : pp. 114-115 :

> yad vā yāny ētāni trayī-vidbhiḥ na parigr̥hītāni, kiñcit-tan-miśra-dharma-kañcuka-cchāyāpatitāni lōkōpasaṅgraha-lābha-pūjā-khyāti-prayōjana-parāṇi trayī-viparītāsambaddha-dr̥ṣṭa-śōbhādi-pratyakṣānumānōpamānārthāpatti-prāya-yukti-mūlōpanibaddhāni sāṁkhya-yōga-pāñcarātra-pāśupata-śākya-nirgrantha-parigr̥hīta-dharmādharma-nibandhanāni viṣa-cikitsā-vaśīkaraṇōccāṭanōnmādanādi-samartha-katipaya-mantrauṣadhi-kādācitka-siddhi-nidarśana-balēnāhiṁsā-satya-vacana-dama-dāna-dayādi-śruti-smr̥ti-saṁvādi-stōkārtha-bandha-vāsita-jīvikā-prāyārthāntarōpadēśīni, yāni ca bāhyatarāṇi mlēcchācāra-miśra-bhōjanācaraṇāni nibandhanāni, tēṣām ēvaitac-chruti-virōdha-hētu-darśanābhyām anapēkṣaṇīyatvaṁ pratipādyatē।

It may be noted that the passage quoted above mentions Pāñcarātra along with other non-Vedic schools like Buddhism and Jainism, and it is the nucleus of the anti-Pāñcarātra arguments advanced by the adherents of other schools of thought, from time to time.

In the Tantra-terminology, “vidveṣaṇa” etc. are technically called “ṣaṭkarmas”. Vide Liṅgādhāraṇacandrikā: p. 285, foot-note. These “ṣaṭkarmas” are : “māraṇa” (destruction), “uccāṭana” (driving away), “stambhana” (arrest, that is, staying a storm, striking a man dumb etc.), “vaśīkaraṇa” (bringing under control, which includes hypnotism), “vidveṣaṇa” (causing antagonism between persons) and “svastyayana” (curative and healing power in disease, misfortune and danger).

A number of Pāñcarātra works describe in detail the ways and means of achieving mundane pleasures, effecting enmity, attracting and subduing persons and even the minor gods, curing or healing poisons of insects and reptiles and so on. The Kāśyapasaṃhitā, for instance, is a work entirely devoted to the delineation of the curing of various sorts of poisons.

For “vidveṣaṇa”, see Kāśyapasaṃhitā: III. 32; Śrīviṣṇutilakasaṃhitā: IV. 640-643; and the Hiraṇyagarbhasaṃhitā: XIX.

For “uccāṭana”, see Kāśyapasaṃhitā: III. 26-28; V. 12, 42, 45; Śrīviṣṇutilakasaṃhitā: IV. 634-639; Hiraṇyagarbhasaṃhitā: XIX and Īśvarasaṃhitā: XXV. 115b.

For “vaśīkaraṇa” see Agastyasaṃhitā: XV. 8-11, 49-51 and XXXI; Kāśyapasaṃhitā: III. 8, 21-24; Śrīviṣṇutilakasaṃhitā: IV. 415-422; 430-454; Sāttvatasaṃhitā: XVII. 440 et passim; Hiraṇyagarbhasaṃhitā: XIII. 3 ff; Īśvarasaṃhitā: XXV. 115a.

By the term ‘ādi’ mentioned in the text “vaśīkaraṇādi”, are understood “māraṇa”, “viṣaharaṇa”, “viṣacikitsā”, “unmādana”, “ākarṣaṇa”, “stambhana” and the like.

For “māraṇa”, see Hiraṇyagarbhasaṃhitā: XIX; Agastyasaṃhitā: XXXI; Śrīviṣṇutilakasaṃhitā: IV. 645-666 and the Īśvarasaṃhitā: XXV. 115b.

For “viṣaharaṇa”, see Śrīviṣṇutilakasaṃhitā: IV. 488-490; and Kāśyapasaṃhitā: Chs. VI to XII.

For “unmādana”, see Kāśyapasaṃhitā: III. 33-36; and Īśvarasaṃhitā: XXV. 116a.

For “ākarṣaṇa”, see Kāśyapasaṃhitā: III. 1-3 and Īśvarasaṃhitā: XXV. 115a.

For “stambhana”, see the Īśvarasaṃhitā: XXV. 116a.

Thus, though apparently, the Pāñcarātrasaṃhitās pour down instructions and incantations to be followed and applied, so as to achieve some mundane pleasures, the attitude of a Pāñcarātrin to this question is an altogether different one. According to him, all such Āgamas which are found to give instructions regarding the achievement of some mundane pleasure or other, are intent upon advising men against such pursuits, rather than prescribing such pursuits. Thus, for instance, the Paramasaṃhitā, one of the oldest and the most authoritative Āgamas of the Pāñcarātra literature, also refers to the ways and means of attaining earthly pleasures in chs. VI, XIII, XV and XVI. But it spares no effort to stress upon the futility and undesirability of such pursuits.

Thus it says in VI. 60-61a:

> nānyaḥ siddhyati kāmena tasmāt kāmo nirarthakaḥ  
tasmāt sarvaprayatnena muktvā kāmamanorathaṃ  
bhagavantamupāsīta sarvaṃ tenaiva siddhyati.

Unflinching devotion to God will itself bring to a man all material prosperity, even if he does not himself pray God for it.

Also cf. ibid : XXXI. 69 :

> tasmādanena mārgeṇa pūjayet madhusūdanaṃ  
aiśvaryamapavargaṃ vā nirvyājamadhigacchati.

Also cf. ibid : XXX. 100-101a :

> tasmādubhayamevātra puṃsāṃ bhavati sammataṃ  
aiśvaryamapavargo vā viśeṣeṇa pitāmaha  
madgatā bhaktirevedamubhayaṃ sādhayiṣyati.

This is the norm of all the Pāñcarātra texts. The main concern of their teaching is unflinching devotion to the Lord and the methods of translating that devotion into acts of worship, which are divided into five types: “abhigamana”, “upādāna”, “svādhyāya”, “ijyā” and “yoga”, to be performed in different parts of the day.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvaṁ sati yānyapi lōkaṁ vyāmōhayituṁ vidvēṣaṇōccāṭanavaśīkaraṇādikṣudravidyāprāyamēva bahulamupadiśadbhirbhagavadārādhanādikatipayavaidikakarmāṇi pāñcarātrikairnirdiśyantē tānyanupayōgyānyavisrambhaṇīyāni ca śvadr̥tinikṣiptakṣīravaditi manyāmahē । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atō na vēda-mūlattvaṁ  
pañcarātrasya yujyatē ।  
prāmāṇyaṁ pratipadyēta  
yēna manv-ādi-śāstravat ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

To sum up,  
it is not proper to assume that Pancarātra is based on the Veda  
and therefore equally authoritative as the doctrinal works of Manu' and others. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atō na vēdamūlattvaṁ pañcarātrasya yujyatē ।  
prāmāṇyaṁ pratipadyēta yēna manvādiśāstravat ॥
</details>

## 11 vēda-tulya-pramāṇatvaṁ na

### pūrva-pakṣaḥ (naiyyāyikaḥ)
#### pauruṣēyatvam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atra kaścid āha 

> kāmaṁ kakṣyāntarita-prāmāṇyēṣu manv-ādismaraṇēṣu kāraṇatayā vēdāḥ parikalpyantām,  
pañca-rātra-smaraṇasya tu kiṁ vēdēna?
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The Naiyāyika now argues with the Mīmāṃsaka. His contention is that the Vedas and the Pāñcarātra texts are utterances of one and the same Supreme Being, Who is also the Omniscient Designer-Architect of this wonderful cosmos. He forms the second critic to be refuted by the Siddhāntin, only in so far as the authorship of the Vedas is concerned. For the Siddhāntin, as for the Mīmāṃsaka, the Vedas are revealed, “apauruṣeya”, not composed even by the Supreme.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

kakṣyayā ēkayā antaritaṁ prāmāṇyaṁ manvādi-śāstrāṇām। vēdānāṁ prāmāṇya-sārvabhaumatvāt, tad-anusāraṇāc ca sarva-smr̥tīnām। pañca-rātraṁ tu vēdavad ēva nirapēkṣatayā sarvōtkr̥ṣṭatayā ca pramāṇaṁ, tat-samāna-yōga-kṣēmatvād iti hārdam।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

DISCURSUS: 

18\. At this point someone interjects:  
If you please, by all means assume that the Vedas constitute the cause  
of the delegated and indirect authority of the Tradition of Manu etc.  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

A Naiyayika. Traditionally, Nyaya does not accept the Mimānsā view that the Vedas have not originated from a person.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atra kaścidāha kāmaṁ kakṣyāntaritaprāmāṇyēṣu manvādismaraṇēṣu kāraṇatayā vēdāḥ parikalpyantām, pañcarātrasmaraṇasya tu kiṁ vēdēna?
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tan-mūlatayā 'valambitēna  
vēdānām api yad+++(←īśvara)+++-anubhava-nibandhanaṁ prāmāṇyaṁ  
tad-anubhava ēva hi pañca-rātra-smaraṇasya nidānam,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

But is there any reason why we should have to depend exclusively on the Veda  
as the basis of the Pañcarātra tradition too?  
The same direct knowledge which is the very foundation of the authority of the Vedas themselves  
is also the foundation of the authority of the Pañcarâtra doctrine;  

the authority of the latter is not based upon the relation of supporting authority  
and supported authority which characterizes typical smarta injunctions,
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tanmūlatayā'valambitēna vēdānāmapi yadanubhavanibandhanaṁ prāmāṇyaṁ tadanubhava ēva hi pañcarātrasmaraṇasya nidānam,  na khalu tulyamūlayōraṣṭakācamanasmaraṇayōrmithōmūlamūlibhāvaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na khalu tulya-mūlayōr aṣṭakācamana-smaraṇayōr  
mithō-mūla-mūli-bhāvaḥ ।+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

e.g., astakā and acamana which have their common basis in the Veda. 
In fact, the two traditions of the aştaka rite and the acamana rite are not interdependent, but, they are equally and independently authoritative. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na khalu tulyamūlayōraṣṭakācamanasmaraṇayōrmithōmūlamūlibhāvaḥ ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> paras-param apēkṣētē  
tulya-kakṣyē na hi smr̥tī ।  
pañca-rātra--śrutī tadvan  
nāpēkṣatē parasparam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Similarly, Pañcarātra and Scripture are not interdependent.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

parasparamapēkṣētē tulyakakṣyē na hi smr̥tī ।  
pañcarātraśrutī tadvannāpēkṣatē parasparam ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> vēda-mūlatva-hānēna  
pañcarātrē 'vasīdati ।  
kutas tan-mūlatā-hānād  
āgamō nāvasīdati ॥+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

pañca-rātrasya vēda-mūlatvābhāvād yadi aprāmāṇya-prasaktiḥ, tarhi pāñcarātra-mūlatvābhāvāt vēdasyāpy aprāmāṇya-prasaṅga iti samānadharmē। ubhayōr api vēda-pañca-rātrayōḥ bhagavad-anubhavaika-mūlatayā tulyatvāt, tad-antarē ēkatarāmūlatva-prayuktam aprāmāṇyam anyasya na śakya-śaṅkam iti niṣkarṣaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If Pancaratra collapses as soon as it is denied the support of the Veda,  
why then should the Veda not collapse when the support of Pañcaratra is taken away from it? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vēdamūlatvahānēna pañcarātrē'vasīdati ।  
kutastanmūlatāhānādāgamō nāvasīdati ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> āha - "kim ēvaṁ vēdā api puruṣānubhavādhīnaprāmāṇyāḥ pauruṣēyā ēva?"
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This is the objection raised by the Mīmāṃsaka to the above view.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

19\. The Vedas derive their authority  
from direct knowledge which originates from a person  
and must therefore naturally derive from a person?
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

āha - kimēvaṁ vēdā api puruṣānubhavādhīnaprāmāṇyāḥ pauruṣēyā ēva?
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> kas saṁśayaḥ?  
vākyatvaṁ hi parādhīna-racanatva-svabhāvam upalabhyamānaṁ  
katham aparathā 'vatiṣṭhēta? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The Naiyāyika meets this objection.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Who can doubt it?  
For we perceive that words, from their very nature, depend for their composition  
on some entity that is different from themselves. 

[[17]]  
How else could they exist at all?
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kassaṁśayaḥ, vākyatvaṁ hi parādhīnaracanatvasvabhāvamupalabhyamānaṁ kathamaparathā'vatiṣṭhēta   
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

>> vēdanāmnō granthasyāyaṁ mahimā -  
> yat kēnacid asandr̥bdhō 'pi vākyatvēnāvatiṣṭhata 
> 
> iti cēt,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If it is objected that 

> the significance of the Book called Veda  
just consists in this that  
it does in fact exist as Word 
though nobody has composed it, 

then we reply; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

>> vēdanāmnō granthasyāyaṁ mahimā   
> yatkēnacidasandr̥bdhō'pi vākyatvēnāvatiṣṭhata
> 
> iti cēt,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> hanta tarhi parvata-vartinō dhūmasyāyaṁ mahimā  
yaj jvalanam antarēṇānucchinna-santānō gagana-talam adhirōhatīti  
kim iti na syāt?+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

why, if this were true,  
then the significance of smoke on a mountain consists in this  
that it whirls irrepressibly sky-high without fire!  
It is utterly out of the question. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

The argument is thus:  
The Veda is of personal origin, because it is language;  
language is invariably found to originate from persons.  
The Naiyayika compares the Mimasaka's view in the terms of this argument  
with the standard inference:  
the mountain has fire, because it has smoke.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

hanta tarhi parvatavartinō dhūmasyāyaṁ mahimā yajjvalanamantarēṇānucchinnasantānō gaganatalamadhirōhatīti kimiti na syāt ।  
</details>

#### dharma-sākṣāt-kāraḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

>> nanu katham atikrānta-mānāntarāvatārē dharmē  
> granthaḥ sandr̥bhyatē?  
> 
> maivaṁ - yatas sahaja-saṁvēdana--sākṣāt-kr̥ta-dharmādharma ēva  
> bhagavān jagad-anukampayā vēdam-anāmānaṁ grantham āracayatīti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘saṁvēdanaṁ’ jñānam; tac ca bhagavatas sahajam। indriya-nirapēkṣaṁ tasya pratyakṣam iti bhāvaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

>> 20\. OBJECTION. But since the applicability' of the dharma  
> cannot be shown by any of the means of knowledge,  
> how can a book on it be composed?   
>
> REPLY. Don't argue like that:  
> for the Bhagavan who, of course, has an immediate intuition of dharma and adharma  
> through the knowledge which is natural to Him  
> has had this Book called Veda composed out of compassion for the world. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

avatara "descent, emergence." The meaning is as follows: Dharma is by definition that action which leads to a certain end by suprasensible law. Since the process (the incarnation) is suprasensible, there can be no other authority for it than Scriptural authority. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu kathamatikrāntamānāntarāvatārē dharmē granthaḥ sandr̥bhyatē,  
maivaṁ yatassahajasaṁvēdanasākṣātkr̥tadharmādharma ēva bhagavān jagadanukampayā vēdanāmānaṁ granthamāracayatīti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

>>kim asti dharmādharma-gōcaram api pratyakṣam?  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

21\. OBJECTION. But does this intuition or perception also encompass dharma and adharma? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kimasti dharmādharmagōcaramapi pratyakṣam?  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> bāḍhaṁ katham anyathā tanu-bhuvanādi-kāryam upajanayati?  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> REPLY. Certainly. How else would the Bhagavān be able to give rise to such effects as body, world etc.? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

bāḍhaṁ kathamanyathā tanubhuvanādikāryamupajanayati?  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> sa hi tatra kartā bhavati  
> yō yasyōpādānam upakaraṇañ ca sākṣāt-kartuṁ prabhavati।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For the maker of such effects must be one who is capable of perceiving their material and instrumental causes.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sa hi tatra kartā bhavati yō yasyōpādānamupakaraṇañca sākṣātkartuṁ prabhavati 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> dharmādharmau ca jagad-upakaraṇam  
> iti mīmāṁsakānām api sammatamēva ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Now, dharma and adharma are the instrumental causes of the world;  
this is also the consensus of the Mimāmsakas. 

Consequently we must postulate a certain person who has this perceptual knowledge;  
and that person must also be the one who created the Veda at the beginning. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

This envisages the world as the sum total of the fruits (phala) brought about by observance or non-observance of dharma, which is thus instrumental to world creation.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> dharmādharmau ca jagadupakaraṇamiti mīmāṁsakānāmapi sammatamēva ।
</details>

#### jagat-kāryatā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yastu brūtē  
> "giri-bhuvanā''dayō bhāvā na kāryā" iti,  
pratibrūyādēnam -  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

22\. If one contends that such entities as mountains, earth and the like are not effects,  
the "answer is as follows: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> yastu brūtē giribhuvanā''dayō bhāvā na kāryā iti,  
pratibrūyādēnam -  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> vivāda-gōcarā bhāvāḥ  
**kāryā** +++(bhū=)+++viśvam-bharādayaḥ ।  
vicitra-san-nivēśatvān  
narēndra-bhavanādivat ।  
tathā sāvayavatvēna  
**vināśō** 'py avasīyatē ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘vicitra-sannivēśatvāt’, sāvayavatvād iti yāvat।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[18]]  
The entities in question, earth etc., are effects,  
because they have a complex construction, like a king's palace (cf. Udayana, Kusumanjali 4.1.).  
Similarly, from the fact that they are made up of parts  
we conclude that they are subject to destruction. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vivādagōcarā bhāvāḥ kāryā viśvambharādayaḥ ।  
vicitrasannivēśatvānnarēndrabhavanādibat ।  
tathā sāvayavatvēna vināśō'pyavasīyatē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> vinaśyanti ca yē bhāvās  
tē tat-sādhana-vēdinā ।  
vināśyantē yathā taj-jñair  
asmābhiḥ +++(kamaṇḍalu=)+++karakādayaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Entities that can be destroyed are destroyed by someone who knows the means by which they can be destroyed,  
just as we can destroy clay vessels etc.  
when we know by what means to destroy them. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vinaśyanti ca yē bhāvāstē tatsādhanavēdinā ।  
vināśyantē yathā tajjñairasmābhiḥ karakādayaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yē punar a-paridr̥ṣṭa-buddhimad-adhiṣṭhāna--taru-patanādi-śakalitā bhāvāḥ  
tē'pi vimaty-ākrāntā  
iti nānaikāntikatvam āvahanti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘vimatyākrāntā’ pakṣē krōḍī-kr̥tā ity arthaḥ। pakṣē vyabhicāraśaṅkā tu na dōṣāya, aparathā anumāna-vyavahāra-syaivōcchēda-prasaṅgāt iti āśayaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the case of entities that are shattered, for instance, by a falling tree,  
that is without perceptible intelligent agency,  
the cause of their destruction remains dubious:  
but because of this very dubiety  
there can also be not positive certainty that the cause of their destruction is entirely occasional. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yē punaraparidr̥ṣṭabuddhimadadhiṣṭhānatarupatanādiśakalitā bhāvāḥ tē'pi vimatyākrāntā iti nānaikāntikatvamāvahanti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> kiṁ ca -  
>
> mahattayā sanāthēna  
spandamānatva-hētunā ।  
utpatti-bhaṅgau bhāvānām  
anumātum ihōcitau ॥
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘mahattvē sati kriyāvattvād‘ iti yāvat।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Motion, when there is mass, is sufficient ground to infer in this world  
that an entity which has mass and can move is subject to origination and to destruction. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiṁ ca -  

mahattayā sanāthēna spandamānatvahētunā ।  
utpattibhaṅgau bhāvānāmanumātumihōcitau ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tad ēvam udīrita-nyāya-prasiddhē viśvam-bharādi-kāryatvē  
**sidhyaty ēva** bhagavatas tad-upakaraṇa-dharmādharma-sākṣāt-kāritvam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It being thus established that earth etc. are indeed effects, on the grounds adduced above,  
it follows that the Bhagavan has knowledge of dharma and adharma  
which are the instrumental causes of origination and annihilation. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Since they are products, they have been produced by a person (God) who knew the means by which to produce them (dharma and adharma).
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadēvamudīritanyāyaprasiddhē viśvambharādikāryatvē sidhyatyēva bhagavatastadupakaraṇadharmādharmasākṣātkāritvam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tathā hi -  
>
> vivādādhyāsitā bhāvā  
yē'mī bhū-bhūdharādayaḥ ।  
tē yathōktāvabōdhēna  
kartrā kēnāpi **nirmitāḥ** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Consequently, the entities here in question, earth, mountains and the like,  
have been created by a maker who possesses the described knowledge. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi -  

vivādādhyāsitā bhāvā yē'mī bhūbhūdharādayaḥ ।  
tē yathōktāvabōdhēna kartrā kēnāpi nirmitāḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> utpatti-nāśa-bhāgitvād  
yad utpatti-vināśavad ।  
**dr̥ṣṭan** tat, tādr̥śā kartrā  
**nirmitan** - tad yathā gr̥ham ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Everything that has origin and end is, in our experience, created by such a maker,  
just because it is subject to origination and annihilation, like a house. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

utpattināśabhāgitvādyadutpattivināśavad ।  
dr̥ṣṭantattādr̥śā kartrā nirmitantadyathā gr̥ham ॥
</details>

#### sr̥ṣṭēḥ sakartr̥katvam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na ca vācyaṁ -
>
> > karmaṇām ēva svānuṣṭhātr̥-puruṣa-samīhitāni saṁpādayatām antarā  
nāntarīyakaṁ +++(→nāvinā-bhūtaṁ)+++ tanu-bhuvanādi-kārya-nirmāṇam 
>
> iti …  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ēva-kārēṇa īśvarō niṣidhyatē। 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yad vinā yan na bhavati, tat tasya nāntarīyakam। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[19]]  
23\. Let it not be argued that  

> there is no intermediate production of effects like body, world etc.  
between acts that bring about the desires of the person who undertakes them, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

This is the Mimaṁsā view  
which holds that the dharma and adharma as instruments in creation  
are always the dharma and adharma of a particular intelligent being  
whose body is itself the product of dharma and adharma  
and can therefore never, however intelligent he may be, control them.  
The Mimimsaka admits that the universe, being made up of parts, is subject to origination and destruction,  
but never at one time, since all entities presuppose former acts that have brought them about.

[[127]]  
The law of dharma and adharma necessarily operates eternally.  
No agency is possible which can intervene in this eternal operation from act to act,  
by either beginning or ending the universe.  
On this cf. Prakaraṇapañcikā, p. 137 ff. for the Prabhakara view, and Slokavārttika, Sambandhākṣepaparihāra 47-116 for the Bhitta view.[[127]]  
The law of dharma and adharma necessarily operates eternally.  
No agency is possible which can intervene in this eternal operation from act to act,  
by either beginning or ending the universe.  
On this cf. Prakaraṇapañcikā, p. 137 ff. for the Prabhakara view, and Slokavārttika, Sambandhākṣepaparihāra 47-116 for the Bhāṭṭa view.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca vācyaṁ karmaṇāmēva svānuṣṭhātr̥ puruṣasamīhitāni saṁpādayatāmantarā nāntarīyakaṁ tanubhuvanādikāryanirmāṇamiti …  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yataś cētanānadhiṣṭhitāni tāni  
**na** kāryāṇi **janayitum** utsahantē  
a-cētanatvād vāsīvat, +++(=kṣuravat)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>
Vide Prakaraṇapañcikā; VII. P134:

> na khalv anadhiṣṭhitā vardhakinā vāsī vardhanāya pravartatē। 

Also cf. Nyāyakusumāñjali: V. P51:

> paramāṇv-ādayō hi cētanādhiṣṭhitāḥ pravartantē, acētanatvāt vāsīvat।

Also cf. Śaṅkara's commentary on Brahmasūtra: II. ii-1 : P221 [Nirṇayasāgara Edition]:

> nā'cētanaṁ lōkē cētanānadhiṣṭhitaṁ sva-tantraṁ...dr̥ṣṭam।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for these acts are unable to produce anything 
unless they are used as an instrument by a spiritual being,  
since they are non-spiritual themselves, like an adze:  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yataścētanānadhiṣṭhitāni tāni na kāryāṇi janayitumutsahantē acētanatvād vāsīvat,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na hi cētanēna takṣṇā'nadhiṣṭhitā vāsī  
svayam ēva yūpādīny āpādayitum alam ।+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

without the operation of a spiritual being-- the carpenter-  
an adze is incapable of effecting by itself such objects as a sacrificial pole, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi cētanēna takṣṇā'nadhiṣṭhitā vāsī svayamēva yūpādīnyāpādayitumalam ।
</details>
  
#### apūrva-nirvāhaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> **na** cāpūrvāṇy adhiṣṭhāya  
vayaṁ **nirmātum** īśvarāḥ ।  
**na** hi karmōdayāt pūrvaṁ  
sākṣāt-kartuṁ **kṣamāmahē** ॥+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And we are not able to create through the instrumentality of apurva factors:  
for before the actual fruition of the ritual act we cannot know their instrumentality,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

apūrva lit. "that which is unprecedented, not known before, se. by other means of knowledge" in Mimāmsā it describes especially that suprasensible power inherent in the act which makes it produce its result.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cā pūrvāṇyadhiṣṭhāya vayaṁ nirmātumīśvarāḥ ।  
na hi karmōdayāt pūrvaṁ sākṣātkartuṁ kṣamāmahē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> uktaṁ hi upādānōpakaraṇa-sākṣāt-kāriṇa ēva  
tatra tatra kartr̥tvam iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and it has been said that only a person who has actual knowledge of the material and instrumental causes  
can be a maker with respect to these causes. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

The argument is that one cannot know that the act will indeed produce an effect until this effect has materialized;  
thus the act's power- apūrva- cannot be known beforehand  
as the instrument of effectuation.+++(5)+++  
By the  Naiyayika's definition  
only one who knows what instruments are effective in production  
can actually produce. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

uktaṁ hi upādānōpakaraṇasākṣātkāriṇa ēva tatra tatra kartr̥tvamiti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na ca karma-janyāpūrva-sākṣāt-kāra-kṣamaḥ kṣētra-jñaḥ kaścit prajñāyatē pratijñāyatē vā, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And there is no embodied soul which is known, or claimed, to be capable of having the required actual knowledge of the apurva that is to arise from the act. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca karmajanyāpūrvasākṣātkārakṣamaḥ kṣētrajñaḥ kaścit prajñāyatē pratijñāyatē vā, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> ataḥ kṣētra-jña--tad-upabhōga--tat-sādhana-dharmādharmādi--  
> nikhila-lōkāvalōkana-caturaḥ kō'pi niratiśaya-śakti-vaicitryaḥ puruṣō **'bhyupagantavyaḥ**,  
> tasya cāpratigha-jñānatvādayas sahajāḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide Doctrine of Śakti in Indian Literature, P42:

> God in the conception of the Naiyāyikas is one that is not only the efficient cause and supreme agent of the world, but possesses innumerable qualities such as knowledge, activity, desire, etc.

Cf. Vātsyāyana's commentary on the Nyāyasūtra, IV. i.21, P. 292:

> guṇaviśiṣṭamātmāntaraṃ īśvaraḥ.

Cf. also ibid: P293 :

> na tāvadasya buddhiṁ vinā kaściddharmo liṅgabhūtaśśakya upapādayitum.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore we must admit a Person of absolute omnipotence 
who is able to take in at a glance the entire Universe with dharma and adharma of all embodied souls, their experiencing of karmic results etc.,  
and in whose nature such properties as unrestricted knowledge etc. subsist. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ataḥ kṣētrajñatadupabhōgatatsādhanadharmādharmādinikhilalōkāvalōkanaca turaḥ kō'pi niratiśayaśaktivaicitryaḥ puruṣōbhyupagantavyaḥ tasya cāpratighajñānatvādayassahajāḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yathā'huḥ -  
>
> > jñānam apratighaṁ tasya  
vairāgyañ ca jagatpatēḥ ।  
aiśvaryañ caiva dharmaś ca  
sahasiddhaṁ catuṣṭayam ॥
>
> iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified. This verse is quoted by Sucaritamiśra in his commentary on the Ślokavārtika, P.110 [Trivandrum Skt. Series No. 90].
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As they say (unidentified source): 
"The unobstructed knowledge, perfect impartiality, omnipotence of a universal lord and dharma are all four established together." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā'huḥ -  

jñānamapratighaṁ tasya vairāgyañca jagatpatēḥ ।  
aiśvaryañcaiva dharmaśca sahasiddhaṁ catuṣṭayam ॥

iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> imam ēvārthaṁ mantrārthavādētihāsa-purāṇa-vādā upōdvalayanti -
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Mantras, arthavadas, epic and purana corroborate this point; e.g. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

mantra and arthavada: the terms indicate that the Naiyayika continues to address the Mimimsaka, for these of course are Mimāmsā terms, mantra being the Vedic formula used at the ritual, arthavada the descriptive, noninjunctive passages of Brahmana and later Vedic texts. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

imamēvārthaṁ mantrārthavādētihāsapurāṇavādā upōdvalayanti
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> dyāvā-pr̥thivī janayan dēva ēkaḥ ।  
prajāpatirvēdānasr̥jata ।

ity ēvam ādayaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Mahānārāyaṇīya Upaniṣat: II. 2.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"The one god, Prajapati, creating heaven and earth, created the Vedas," etc. (RV. 10. 90. 14)
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

dyāvāpr̥thivī janayan dēva ēkaḥ ।  
prajāpatirvēdānasr̥jata ।

ityēvamādayaḥ ।
</details>

#### pāñcarātrasya sākṣāt praṇayanam 
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> sa cāyam ādikālē bhagavān  
pralīna-nikhila-karaṇa-kalēvarādi--bhōgōpakaraṇa--  
cētanētarāyamāṇa-jīva-jālāvalōkana-janita-mahānugrahaḥ +++(5)+++… 
</details>

<details><summary>rāmamiśraśāstrī</summary>

ādikalē - pralayakālē।  
yathā hi jaḍās  
tathaiva cētanā api karaṇa-kalēvara-vikalā bhōga-bhājōnābhūvann  
iti tē cētanētarāyamāṇā ity ucyantē ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

At the moment of inception  
the great Grace of this Person who is the Bhagavan  
is evoked by a glance at the aggregate of individual souls  
who are almost in a state of non-spiritual stupor,   
their instruments for the experiencing of karmic results- body, senses and other organs-being completely dissolved.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sa cāyamādikālē (pralayakālē) bhagavān pralīnanikhilakaraṇakalēvarādibhōgōpakaraṇacētanētarāyamāṇajīvajālāvalōkanajanitamahānugrahaḥ 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> sakalam api jagad upajanayya  
tad-abhilaṣita-samasta-sāṁsārika-sampat-prāptyupāya-prakāśana-bahulāṁ trayīm ēkatō nirmāya  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'ēkataḥ' kāranyainēti yāvat। [[??]]
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[20]]  
His Grace evoked, he originates the entire universe  
and simultaneously He creates the triple Veda  
which states pellucidly the means  
by which the souls in transmigration can realize the objects of their desires.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sakalamapi jagadupajanayya tadabhilaṣitasamastasāṁsārikasampatprāptyupāyaprakāśanabahulāṁ trayīmēkatō nirmāya  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> punar api vividha-durita--+++(taraṅga-)+++param-parā''kīrṇa--bhavārṇava-nimagnān udvignān avalōkayan 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Then again, perceiving that they are in a pitiable condition,  
being immersed in the ocean of existence  
which is perturbed by wave upon wave of all manner of iniquities,  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

punarapi vividhaduritaparamparākīrṇabhavārṇavanimagnanudvignānavalōkayan  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> parama-karuṇatayā tapta-mānasaḥ  
parama-niśrēyasa-sādhana-svārādhanāvabōdha-sādhanī-bhūtāḥ pañca-rātra-saṁhitāḥ sanat-kumāra--nāradādibhyō **'bhyavōcad** 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

His heart burns with supreme compassion  
and He promulgates, through Sanatkumara, Narada etc., the Pancarãtra Samhitās  
which constitute the sources of knowledge  
about the manner in which He should be propitiated to attain to perfect bliss. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

paramakaruṇatayā taptamānasaḥ paramaniśrēyasasādhanasvārādhanāvabōdhasādhanībhūtāḥ pañcarātrasaṁhitāḥ sanatkumāra-nāradādibhyō'bhyavōcad 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> iti trayī-samāna--sva-tantrānubhava-mūlāni tantrāṇi  
katham iva yādr̥śa-tādr̥śa-manv-ādi-smaraṇa-gōṣṭhīm adhitiṣṭhanti ?+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Forasmuch as the Tantras are therefore based upon an immediate cognition of the Lord  
and are consequently self-sufficient like the Vedas,  
can they belong in the company of any Tradition, that of Manu or anyone? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

iti trayīsamānasvatantrānubhavamūlāni tantrāṇi kathamiva yādr̥śatādr̥śamanvādismaraṇagōṣṭhīmadhitiṣṭhanti ।  
</details>

### vēdāpauruṣēyatvam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**syād ēvaṁ** yadi vēdānāṁ  
nirmātā'pi pramāṇataḥ ।  
kutaścid upalabhyēta -  
**na** cāsāv **upalabhyatē** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The Mīmāṁsaka raises his objection again.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION.   
24\. If this is true, then on what authority is such a creator of the Vedas known to exist?  
He is not directly perceived. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Yamuna concurs in the Mimāmsaka's refutation of the Naiyayika's views,  
to the extent that  
he too rejects that the existence of God can be proved by reason;  
but he will counter the Mimagisa assertion that God cannot be proved at all,  
that in fact there is neither room nor purpose for a God in the universe.  
For Yamuna, God has all the characteristics He has for the Naiyayika,  
but he proves them from Scripture, not reason.+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

syādēvaṁ yadi vēdānāṁ nirmātā'pi pramāṇataḥ ।  
kutaścidupalabhyēta na cāsāvupalabhyatē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**na** ca vākyatva-liṅgēna  
vēda-kārō **'numīyatē** ।  
abhiprēta-viśēṣāṇāṁ  
viparyāsa-prasaṅgataḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor can we infer from the fact that the Veda is word  
that it therefore must have an author,  
for that would entail the total reversion of your special contentions.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca vākyatvaliṅgēna vēdakārō'numīyatē ।  
abhiprētaviśēṣāṇāṁ viparyāsaprasaṅgataḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vākyaṁ hi yat parādhīna-  
racanaṁ **saṁpradr̥śyatē** ॥  
śarīriṇaiva tat sarvam  
**ucyamānaṁ vilōkyatē** ।+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For an utterance that is perceived to depend for its composition on the agency of some being  
is also perceived to be uttered by no one but an embodied being …
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vākyaṁ hi yat parādhīnaracanaṁ saṁpradr̥śyatē ॥  
śarīriṇaiva tatsarvamucyamānaṁ vilōkyatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

puṇya-pāpa-nimittañ ca  
śarīraṁ sarva-dēhinām ॥  
ēvaṁ puṇyētarādhīna-  
sukha-duḥkhasya dēhinaḥ ।  
anīśvarasya nirmāṇaṁ  
vākyatvam anumāpayēt ॥+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

puṇyavad itarā(pāpā)dhīnēti bhāvaḥ। 

"nirmāṇaṁ" nirmātr̥tvam iti bhāvaḥ। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[21]]  
whose happiness and unhappiness resulted from his good and evil karman,  
and who therefore cannot be God.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

puṇyapāpanimittañca śarīraṁ sarvadēhinām ॥  
ēvaṁ puṇyētarādhīnasukhaduḥkhasya dēhinaḥ ।  
anīśvarasya nirmāṇaṁ vākyatvamanumāpayēt ॥  
</details>

#### dharma-prāmāṇyatā-hāni-prasaṅgaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api caivaṁ pramāṇatvaṁ  
vēdānām api durlabham ।  
**na** hi mānāntarāpūrvē  
dharmē tasyāsti **saṁbhavaḥ** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘tasya’ nirmāṇasyēty arthaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Moreover, in that case it would be impossible  
to establish the authority of the Vedas themselves;  
for if dharma-the Law-is not independent of other means of knowledge,  
there is no exclusive authority of the Vedas. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

That which makes the Veda authoritative, i.e., a means of valid knowledge, is just this that it communicates knowledge of apurva facts, e.g., that a soma sacrifice is a means of attaining heaven, i.e., generally matters pertaining to dharma.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api caivaṁ pramāṇatvaṁ vēdānāmapi durlabham ।  
na hi mānāntarāpūrvē dharmē tasyāsti saṁbhavaḥ ॥
</details>

### akartr̥kaṁ jagat
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu kathaṁ mānāntarāpūrvō dharmaḥ,  
> uktaṁ hi 
> 
> > sākṣāt-karōti dharmādharmau -  
> katham anyathā tad-upakaraṇaṁ jagaj janayati 
> 
> iti।
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This is the contention of the Naiyāyika.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

25\. OBJECTION.  
But why should dharma be independent of other means of knowledge?  
For we have asserted that  

> He has actual knowledge of dharma and adharma:  
how else could He produce the world of which dharma and adharma are the instrumental causes? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> nanu kathaṁ mānāntarāpūrvō dharmaḥ, uktaṁ hi sākṣātkarōti dharmādharmau kathamanyathā tadupakaraṇaṁ jagajjanayati iti,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

satyam **uktaṁ** - "kō'pi nirmātā  
tad+++(=tataḥ)+++ viśvasya jagatō", **na** hi ।  
**vidyatē** kō'pi nirmātā  
yēnaivam api **kalpyatē** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The Mīmāṁsaka refutes the above contention of the Naiyāyika.

Vide Śaivasiddhānta, P.74 ff, for the following:

> It may be noted that even the Lokāyata (Cārvāka) entertains similar view regarding, the world's creatorship, i.e., that there is no creator for it.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REPLY.  
That has indeed been asserted,  
but the assertion is fallacious:  
for no creator of the entire universe can be found  
of whom this can be assumed. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

satyamuktaṁ kō'pi nirmātā tad viśvasya jagatō na hi ।  
vidyatē kō'pi nirmātā yēnaivamapi kalpyatē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

+++(lōkasya→)+++ vicitra-sannivēśatva-  
yuktyā yad api sādhitam +++(sakartr̥katvam)+++ ।  
tatrōcyatē tridhā bhāvā  
laukikaiḥ parilōkitāḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

To your argument that the world must be effected  
because it has a complex construction  
can be objected that empiricists distinguish three kinds of entities: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vicitrasannivēśatvayuktyā yadapi sādhitam ।  
tatrōcyatē tridhā bhāvā laukikaiḥ parilōkitāḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pratyakṣa-dr̥ṣṭa-kartāraḥ  
kēcid ētē ghaṭādayaḥ ।  
a-vidyamāna-nirmāṇās  
tathā'nyē gaganādayaḥ ॥  
sandihyamāna-nirmāṇāḥ  
kēcid viśvam-bharādayaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Pāṇini's sūtra: "nadyṛtaśca" (V. iv-153) would require this to be "pratyakṣadṛṣṭakartṛkāḥ", since the compound intended by the author here is of the Bahuvrīhi-type. But according to the well-known saying "sthitasya gatiḥ kalpanīyā", the term "pratyakṣadṛṣṭakartāraḥ" can be interpreted as a Karmadhāraya compound, thus: "yatra pratyakṣadṛṣṭāḥ kartāraḥ, ete kecit ghaṭādayaḥ", in which case, the expression necessarily has to be split into two parts.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Those whose makers are evident to perception, e.g. pots and the like;  
those which are not found to be made at all (the individual soul) +++(eg. sky)+++;  
and those whose creation remained doubtful, like the earth etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pratyakṣadr̥ṣṭakartāraḥ kēcidētē ghaṭādayaḥ ।  
avidyamānanirmāṇāstathā'nyē gaganādayaḥ ॥  
sandihyamānanirmāṇāḥ kēcid viśvambharādayaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatra prathama-sandarśita-rāśi-dvayē 'navakāśa ēvēśvara-vyāpāraḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the two first-mentioned cases  
there is no room for God's activity. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatra prathamasandarśitarāśidvayē'navakāśa ēvēśvaravyāpāraḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

adyavad ēva viśvam-bharādayaḥ krama-prāptāgantukōpacayāpacayayōr  
na yugapad udaya-vilaya-bhāginaḥ। 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Īśvarasiddhi, P.241, where the same sentence occurs.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As to the third, the earth etc. are not involved in a total origination or disintegrations,  
but merely, as now, subject to varying degrees of increase and decrease which are adventitious. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

adyavadēva viśvambharādayaḥ kramaprāptāgantukōpacayāpacayayōrna yugapadudayavilayabhāginaḥ  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

īdr̥śōtpattibhaṅgau mīmāṁsakānām api sammatāv ēvēti siddha-sādhanatvam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

To say that the Mimāmsakas accept origination and annihilation in this sense is to prove the proved.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

The Mimimsaka admits that the universe, being made up of parts, is subject to origination and destruction,  
but never at one time, since all entities presuppose former acts that have brought them about. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

īdr̥śōtpattibhaṅgau mīmāṁsakānāmapi sammatāvēvēti siddhasādhanatvam ।  
</details>

### apūrva-nirvāhānapēkṣā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

buddhimat kartr̥tā yā'pi  
prayāsēna **samarthitā** ।  
**sādhyatē** sā'pi siddhaiva  
buddhimantō hi cētanāḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

buddhimatkartr̥tā yā'pi prayāsēna samarthitā ।  
sādhyatē sā'pi siddhaiva buddhimantō hi cētanāḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yāgādibhiḥ sva-bhōgāya  
tat tad **utpādayanti** naḥ ॥  
yuktañ cōbhaya-siddhānāṁ  
tatrādhiṣṭhāna-kalpanam ।  
vayañca yāga-dānādi  
sākṣāt kartuṁ **kṣamā** yataḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yāgādibhiḥ ... Vide Karmamīmāṁsā, P.61:

> Though the Mīmāṁsā is so deeply concerned with the sacrifice, it has no belief in the doctrine that the rewards of offering are to be expected either from the deities to whom the offerings are directed to be made, from a God as Creator or apportioner of reward and punishment. The sacrifice generates an unseen potency, whence the goods desired by sacrificers are obtained.

naḥ ... “naḥ” asmad-iṣṭāḥ cētanā ity anvayaḥ। 

yuktaṁ ... Cf. Īśvarasiddhi, P.240:

> “yuktaṁ caitat yadubhayavādisiddhānāmeva cetanānāṁ kartṛtvābhyupagamaḥ, lāghavāt; na copādānādyanabhijñatayā tatpratikṣepaḥ। 

> upādānaṁ pṛthivyādi yāgadānādi sādhanaṁ।  
sākṣātkartuṁ kṣamante yat sarva eva hi cetanāḥ॥

siddhānāṁ ... ubhaya-vādi-sammatānāṁ jīvānām iti bhāvaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[22]]  
In our opinion, too,  
these intelligent agents bring about various results  
by means of sacrifices and other acts,  
in order to enjoy these results themselves;  
and the assumption that they are indeed,  
as is proved for both of us, instrumental therein is quite correct,  
for we can have direct knowledge of these acts, sacrifices, donations and the like.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yāgādibhiḥ svabhōgāya tattadutpādayanti naḥ ॥  
yuktañcōbhayasiddhānāṁ tatrādhiṣṭhānakalpanam ।  
vayañca yāgadānādi sākṣātkartuṁ kṣamā yataḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

karmaṇaḥ śakti-rūpaṁ yad  
a-pūrvādi-padāspadam ।  
**mā** bhūt **pratyakṣatā** tasya  
kin tēnādhyakṣitēna naḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Īśvarasiddhi*, P.241, where this verse is reproduced almost as it is, but for a slight change in the second half of the second line, which reads as “śaktimaddhyakṣagocaraḥ”.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

However, the special power described with terms like apurva 
can never be open to perception.  
How then can we have use for a supervising God?   
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Since the apūrva power is suprasensible,  
it can never be perceived,  
and the assumption of a God who 'supervises' and controls this power  
because he perceives it is absurd. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

karmaṇaḥ śaktirūpaṁ yadapūrvādipadāspadam ।  
mābhūt pratyakṣatā tasya kintēnādhyakṣitēna naḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na khalu kulālādayaḥ  
kumbhādi-kāryam āripsamānāḥ  
tad-upādānōpakaraṇa-bhūta--mr̥d-daṇḍa-cakrādi-kāryōtpādana-śaktiṁ sākṣātkr̥tya  
tat tad ārabhantē ।+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Īśvarasiddhi, P.242, for identical statements.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

26\. Certainly, it is not true that an agent, for instance a potter,  
when he wishes to produce a certain product- pots-  
must first have direct knowledge of the power of their material cause- clay- and instrumental cause- stick- to produce these products  
before he can actually undertake their production.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na khalu kulālādayaḥ kumbhādikāryamāripsamānāḥ tadupādānōpakaraṇabhūtamr̥ddaṇḍacakrādikāryōtpādanaśaktiṁ sākṣātkr̥tya tattadārabhantē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi paraṁ +++(uyyēta)+++- śaktim a-viduṣām +++(kumbhakārādīnāṁ)+++ 
abhilaṣita-sādhanāya tad-upādānādi-vyavahārō 'nupapannaḥ।  
iha tu nityāgama-janmanā pratyayēna 
saṁpraty-ākalita-yāgādi--tat-tad-utpādana-pāṭavāḥ puruṣās +++(←anīśvarā dēvā api)+++  
tair ēva viśvam-bharā+++(=bhū)+++''di-bhāvān āvirbhāvayanti,
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yadi paraṁ ... 'yadi paraṁ' ity asya , 'yadi yat kiñcid vivakṣitaṁ, tarhi ēvaṁ vaktavyam' ity arthaḥ। 

iha tu ... Cf. Ślokavārtika, Saṃbandhākṣepaparihāra: śl. 75:

> kasyacit hetumātṛatvaṁ yadyadhiṣṭhānatocyate  
karmabhiḥ sarvajīvānāṁ tatsiddheḥ siddhasādhanam.

The same idea is expressed in the Īśvarasiddhi, P.242:

> āgamādavagamyante vicitrāḥ karmaśaktayaḥ  
tena karmabhirātmānaḥ sarvaṁ nirmimatāṁ pṛthak.

pratyayēna ...   “Pratyaya” here means “jñāna”.

sampratyākalita ... “Samprati” is used in the sense of “samyak”. Also see the following verse “kṛtārthatvāt krīḍā” etc. where also the word “saṃprati” occurs.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Else people who are unaware of the power of the requisite causes  
would never be able to employ these causes in order to produce the results they want.  
In the case under discussion the persons concerned do indeed know  
which causes are required to bring about the results they want, for they know these causes, such as sacrifices etc.,  
through the knowledge they have obtained from eternal Scripture.  
Thus, aided by these causes, they render manifest such products as earth etc.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi paraṁ śaktimaviduṣāmabhilaṣitasādhanāya tadupādānādivyavahārō'nupapannaḥ tad-upādānādi-vyavahārō 'nupapannaḥ।  
iha tu nityāgamajanmanā pratyayēna saṁpratyākalitayāgāditattadutpādanapāṭavāḥ puruṣāstairēva viśvambharādibhāvānāvirbhāvayanti,
</details>

### dharma-sākṣāt-kārābhāvē'pi sr̥ṣṭiḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ca pratyakṣa-prakr̥ti+++(=upādāna)-+++-karaṇaḥ karma-karaṇa-  
pravīṇō, naivānyaḥ kṣama iti ca nāstyatra niyamaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

By “prakṛti” is meant “upādāna” and by “karaṇa” is meant “nimitta” and the like.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Also, there is no invariable rule  
that only an agent to whom the material and instrumental causes are fully known  
is capable of undertaking an action  
and nobody else.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ca - pratyakṣaprakr̥tikaraṇaḥ karmakaraṇapravīṇō
naivānyaḥ kṣama iti ca nāstyatra niyamaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**a-paśyann** ēvāyaṁ prakr̥ti+++(=upādāna)+++-karaṇē svātma-manasi  
nanu jñānē **kartā bhavati** puruṣas tat katham iva ।  
**vināśīdaṁ** viśvaṁ jagad avayavitvād iti ca yad  
balīyaḥ pratyakṣa-pratihata-mukhatvēna tad asat ॥  
sa ēvāyam mērur divasa-kara-bimbañ ca tadidaṁ  
dharitrī saivēti sphuṭam iha yatō dhīr udayatē ।+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

apaśyannēvāyaṁ ... Cf. Īśvarasiddhi, P.246: “na copādānādisākṣātkāriṇa eva kartṛtvamityapi niyamaḥ; upādānamupakaraṇaṁ ca aviduṣa evātmano jñānādiṣu kartṛtvāt”.

vināśīdaṁ ... Cf. tathā sāvayavatvēna etc., above.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

A man can still be an agent in the action of knowing  
without perceiving in his own mind the material and instrumental causes  
that go into the making of this action of knowing.  
Why, then, contend that the causes must be known first?  
27\. The contention that the entire Universe is subject to annihilation  
because it has parts is incorrect.
Such a conclusion is [[23]] cancelled by stronger perceptual evidence against it.

For the knowledge that does arise in the world of here and now is plainly this:  
'Here is the meru; here is the sun; here is the earth.'
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

apaśyannēvāyaṁ prakr̥tikaraṇē svātmamanasi   
nanu jñānē kartā bhavati puruṣastatkathamiva ॥  
vināśīdaṁ viśvaṁ jagadavayavitvāditi ca yad   
balīyaḥ pratyakṣapratihatamukhatvēna tadasat ॥  
sa ēvāyammērurdivasakarabimbañca tadidaṁ  
dharitrī saivēti sphuṭamiha yatōdhīrudayatē ॥
</details>

### akr̥taṁ jagat
#### anumanam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

śaknōti hi pratyabhijñaiva  
samasta-kāla-sambandham ēṣām avagamayitum,   
santi hi pūrvāpara-kālayōr api tādr̥śāḥ puruṣāḥ,  
prāduḥṣanti yēṣām īdr̥śa-pratyayāḥ,  
prayōgaś ca bhavati ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Recognition conveys to us the knowledge that  
these entities are related to different times;  
and certainly both in former and later ages  
there arise similar persons  
who have the same notion of these entities' present existence.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

śaknōti hi pratyabhijñaiva samastakālasambandhamēṣāmavagamayitum,  santi hi pūrvāparakālayōrapi tādr̥śāḥ puruṣāḥ prāduḥṣanti yēṣāmīdr̥śapratyayāḥ, prayōgaśca bhavati ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

mahī-śaila-pataṅgādi-  
pratyabhijñānavan naraḥ ।  
+++(naraḥ→)+++ atīta-kālaḥ, kālatvād  
idānīntana-kālavat +++(←sanaraḥ)+++ ॥ +++(5)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This long compound qualifies the term “atītakālaḥ”.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

To put it in syllogistic form: 

The past has persons who recognize earth, sun and mountain,  
because the past is time, like the present. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

mahīśailapataṅgādipratyabhijñānavannaraḥ ।  
atītakālaḥ kālatvādidānīntanakālavat ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ēvam anāgatē'pi prayōgō darśayitavyaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The same syllogism can be constructed with regard to the future. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvamanāgatē'pi prayōgō darśayitavyaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**na** cēdr̥śa-prayōgēṇa  
ghaṭādēr api nityatā ।  
**prasajyatē** yatas tatra  
pratyakṣau bhaṅga-sambhavau ॥ +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'sō 'yaṁ ghaṭa' iti pratyabhijñayā ghaṭādēr api nityatvaṁ na śaṅkanīyam iti bhāvaḥ। tatra kāraṇam āha ‘yata‘ iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This reasoning does not entail the fallacious conclusion that pots etc. are eternal,  
for in their case origination and annihilation are directly evident. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cēdr̥śaprayōgēṇa ghaṭādērapi nityatā ।  
prasajyatē yatastatra pratyakṣau bhaṅgasambhavau ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

virōdhē sati yēnātmā +++(→tarka-phalam)+++  
hētunā **naiva labhyatē** ।  
**na labhyatē** 'virōdhē'pi  
tēnātmēty asty **asambhavaḥ** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'virōdhē sati, yēna hētunā ātmā naiva labhyatē [hētutvaṁ hīyata iti yāvat], tēna avirōdhē 'pi sati, ātmā na labhyatay ity ētat na sambhavati ।' iti ślōkasyāsya padānvayaḥ । 

Cf. Tantravārttika under I. iii. 51-54, 55:

> na hi yena pramāṇatvaṁ labdhapūrvaṁ kadācana।  
tena tat sarvadā labhyamityājñāpayatīśvaraḥ॥  
na ca yad balavadruddhamātmānaṁ naiva vindati।  
avirodhe 'pi tenātmā na labdhavyaḥ kathaṁcana॥  
na cāpi bādhakābhāvāt labdha ātmeti sarvadā।  
labdhavyaḥ sa virodhe 'pi pūrvasāmānyadarśanāt॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It does not follow that,  
when a certain fact cannot be proved on the strength of a certain ground,  
since this ground involves a contradiction,  
this same ground cannot prove the same fact  
when it does not involve a contradiction.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

read "na labhyate .avirodhe" pi; the meaning is this: when a certain fact (the eternality of pots) cannot be proved by a ground (recollection)  
because this ground contains a contradiction  
(it is recollected that pots having existed cease to exist),  
this does not prove that the same ground (recollection) cannot prove the eternality of earth, mountains, etc., when there is no contradiction contained in it (nobody has recollection of a vanishing mountain). 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

virōdhē sati yēnātmā hētunā naiva labhyatē ।  
na labhyatē 'virōdhē'pi tēnātmētyastyasambhavaḥ ॥
</details>

#### mahattvādinā na kr̥tatvam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

mahattvē sati spandamānatva-yuktyā  
jagaj-janma-bhaṅgaś ca yaḥ **pratyapādi** ।  
sa ca pratyabhijñā-bala-dhvasta-hētur  
**na** hr̥dyatvam adya **prapadyēta** yuktyā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. mahattayā sanāthēna etc., above.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The other inference that has been given to prove that the world is subject to origination and annihilation,  
namely on the ground of motion when there is mass,  
is likewise incorrect;  
for this ground, too, is cancelled by the greater cogency of recognition.  
Consequently, inference cannot provide positive proof  
that the world is subject to origination and annihilation.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

mahattvē sati spandamānatvayuktyā jagajjanmabhaṅgaśca yaḥ pratyapādi ।  
sa ca pratyabhijñābaladhvastahēturna hr̥dyatvamadya prapadyēta yuktyā ॥
</details>

#### aniṣṭa-guṇāpattiḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca +++(kartranmānē'pi)+++ dharmi-viśēṣa-viruddhaś cāyaṁ +++(īśvarākhyō)+++ hētuḥ kāryatvād iti  
kāryatvaṁ hi  
+++(kartr̥-)+++svabhāva--dr̥ṣṭa-vigrahavattva-+anāpta-kāmatva-+anīśvaratvāsārvajñyādi-  
vyāpti-vitty-upayuktatarānēka-viśēṣānuṣaktaṁ,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[24]]  
28\. Further, you contend that there is a God, on the ground that the world is a product;  
but this ground precludes a specially qualified producer.  
For a product generally implies on the part of its producer  
a number of properties which are natural to him  
and therefore indispensable for the precise knowledge of the concomitance between him and his product -  
Properties like being in possession of a body,  
having something left to desire,  
being deprived of omnipotence and omniscience, etc.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide Karmamīmāṁsā*: pp. 61-62:

> Experience, Prabhākara urges, shows us the bodies of all animals being produced by purely natural means; we can argue hence to the facts of the past and future and need invoke no extraneous aid.....Supervision ( by God ) also is impossible, even had God the necessary knowledge; it must take the form either of contact, which is impossible as merit and demerit being qualities are not subject to contact, or inherence, and plainly a man's qualities cannot inhere in God. If the argument is adduced on the analogy of the carpenter, it may be replied that on this basis, the creator would have to be an embodied spirit, and no embodied spirit can effect such subtle things as the atoms or merit and demerit.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca dharmiviśēṣaviruddhaścāyaṁ hētuḥ kāryatvāditi kāryatvaṁ hi svabhāvadr̥ṣṭavigrahavattvānāptakāmatvānīśvaratvāsārvajñyādivyāptivityupayuktatarānēkaviśēṣānuṣaktaṁ
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**katham** iva tat-pratyanīka-bhūtāśarīra-nitya-tr̥pta-sarvajñatvādy-abhimata-viśēṣān sādhya-dharmiṇy **avagamayati**?+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

How, then, can the fact that the world is a product  
convey to us the knowledge that the producer proposed for it  
possesses the postulated properties, of being bodiless, eternally satisfied, omniscient etc., properties,  
that is, which are the opposite of what would naturally follow? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'sisādhayiṣitē kartari' ity arthaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kathamiva tatpratyanīkabhūtāśarīranityatr̥ptasartrajñatvādyabhimataviśēṣān sādhyadharmiṇyavagamayati,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sva-śarīra-prēraṇam api śarīra-sambandhāsamavāyi-kāraṇaka-prayatnavatō nānyasyēti  
na kathaṁcid aśarīriṇaḥ kartr̥tva-saṁbhavaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The production of a product requires the activation of the body,  
which requires on the producer's part an effort  
whose inherent cause is his relation with a body 
and is impossible of any but just such a producer. 
It follows that under no condition bodiless person can be an agent. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

svaśarīraprēraṇamapi śarīrasambandhāsamavāyikāraṇakaprayatnavatō nānyasyēti na kathaṁcidaśarīriṇaḥ kartr̥tvasaṁbhavaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

athaitad-dōṣa-hānāya  
dēhavān ity upēyatē ।  
sa dēhō janmavān mā vā?  
janmavattvē 'navasthitiḥ ॥  
nityatvē'vayavitvañca  
syād anaikāntikan tava +++("sāvayavam anityam" iti vadataḥ)+++ ।+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or if, in order to remove this fault from the argument,  
it is assumed that the producer indeed possesses a body,  
then the question arises,  
Is that body itself subject to origination or not?  
If it be subject to origination,  
there is infinite regress.  
If it be eternal, then your contention that  
whatever has parts must come to an end is not universally true.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

tāvad-uktasya sāvayavatvahētōr naikāntika-dōṣō bhavēd ity anvayaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

athaitaddōṣahānāya dēhavānityupēyatē ।  
sa dēhō janmavān mā vā janmavattvē'navasthitiḥ ॥  
nityatvē'vayavitvañca syādanaikāntikantava ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad apy ētē'vōcann  
"adhikaraṇa-siddhānta-balatō viśēṣās sidhyantī"ty  
ayam api ca panthā na ghaṭatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The solution of others, namely that God's special properties can be demonstrated by an ad-hoc conclusion, does not hold good either. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

adhikaranasiddhanta is a conclusion which, as soon as one thing is established (e.g., that there is a world creator),  
establishes another topic discussed (e.g., omniscience).  
On this question, ef. Tarkabhāṣā 43. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

“Adhikaraṇasiddhānta” or “Doctrine resting on Implication”, is defined in the Nyāyasūtra under I. i. 30 as “yatsiddhau anvayaprakaraṇasiddhiḥ, so'dhikaraṇasiddhāntaḥ”. Cf. Vātsyāyana's bhāṣya on it: “yasya arthasya siddhau anye arthāḥ anuṣajjyante, na tair vinā so'rthaḥ siddhyati, te arthāḥ tadadhiṣṭhānāḥ, so'dhikaraṇasiddhāntaḥ”. So, Adhikaraṇasiddhānta can be explained as the principle by which, when a certain thing is known or accepted, certain other things automatically follow, by reason of their dependence upon the former. This Adhikaraṇasiddhānta in modern logic is known as “pakṣadharmatā”. Since the fact of earth, etc. having a creator cannot be proved unless that creator is also accepted as a direct perceiver of all entities including the atoms ( the material cause of the cosmos ), the admission of such a power of all-round perception in that creator follows by the principle ‘Adhikaraṇasiddhānta’ ( Implied Doctrine ).
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadapyētē'vōcannadhikaraṇasiddhāntabalatōviśēṣāssidhyantītyayamapi ca panthā na ghaṭatē ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sa hi nyāyō jīvēd api yadi ca mānāntarakr̥tō ।  
virōdhō 'syādr̥ṣṭaḥ, punar +++(atra)+++ api virōdhaḥ sphuṭataraḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For that rule holds only of a case where  
a conflict follows from a means of knowledge  
but does not actually exist.  
In our case, however, the conflict is plain enough. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

“api ca dharmi-viśēṣa-viruddhaś cāyaṁ hētuḥ” iti pūrvam ēva (pu.32) hētu-virōdhaḥ prapañcitaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sa hi nyāyō jīvēdapi yadi ca mānāntarakr̥tō ।  
virōdhō'syādr̥ṣṭaḥ punarapi virōdhaḥ sphuṭataraḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu ca avadhr̥tāvinābhāva-niyamam api yadi  
> na viśvam-bharādi-buddhiman-nimittatām avagamayati  
> pratyastim itas tarhy anumēyavyavahāraḥ।  
> athāvagamayati - avagamayaty ēvāsāv  
> a-khila-trailōkya-nirmāṇa-pravīṇan tamapi kartāram,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[25]]  
29\. OBJECTION. But if even a well-considered invariable concomitance cannot demonstrate that the cause of the earth etc. is an intelligent being,  
then all logical process of deduction is done with.  
But if deduction can indeed convey true knowledge,  
that it must also convey that there is a producer capable of creating the entire universe. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'avadhr̥tāvinābhāva-niyamam' ity ētat ‘kāryatvam’ ity asya padasya adhyāhr̥tasya viśēṣaṇaṁ bhavitum arhati। athavā [[??]]viśvam-bharādi ity asya vā viśēṣaṇatvēna svīkartuṁ śakyatē।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu ca avadhr̥tāvinābhāvaniyamamapi yadi na viśvambharādibuddhimannimittatāmavagamayati pratyastimitastarhyanumēyavyavahāraḥ, athāvagamayati, avagamayatyēvāsāvakhilatrailōkyanirmāṇapravīṇantamapi kartāram,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na brūmō nāvagamayatīti -  
kintu, yāvantō +++(sa-śarīratvādi-)+++viśēṣāḥ vyāpti-grahaṇa-samaya-saṁviditāḥ  
tān apy a-viśēṣēṇōpasthāpayatīti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REPLY. We do not say  
that your deduction fails to demonstrate that there is such a producer,  
but that it also demonstrates without discrimination as many properties in this producer  
as at the moment of grasping the concomitance, are known to obtain in any producer. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na brūmō nāvagamayatīti kintu yāvantō viśēṣāḥ vyāptigrahaṇasamayasaṁviditāḥ tānapyaviśēṣēṇōpasthāpayatīti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca tāvatā'tiprasaṅgaḥ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor do we carry our point too far. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yatra dhūmas tatra vahnir iti vyāptir mahānasādau gr̥hītā। parvatē dhūmaṁ dr̥ṣṭvā vahnim anumātuṁ pravr̥ttasya puruṣasya, tatratyō 'pi vahniḥ mahānasādāv iva phūtkārēṇaiva pravr̥ddha iti, sa ca pākārtham upayujyata ity-ādyāḥ sambhāvanāḥ sambhāvyamānā atra atiprasaṅga-śabdēna sūcitāḥ। ētēṣāṁ viparīta-viśēṣaṇānāṁ pratyakṣa-pramāṇa-bādhyatvam āha pramāṇāntarēty-ādinā। tathā ca parvataṁ gatvā tatratyō vahniḥ kīdr̥śa iti vicārē kriyamāṇē, pūrvaṁ vahni-viṣayē sambhāvitān phūtkāra-pravardhana-pākōpayōgādīn atiprasaṅgān pratyakṣa-pramāṇam ēva nivārayēd iti bhāvaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca tāvatā'tiprasaṅgaḥ 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pramāṇāntara-gōcarē hi liṅgini  
liṅga-balād āpatatō viparīta-viśēṣāṁs  
tat-pramāṇam ēva pratiruṇaddhi
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In a case where the term  
which we seek to establish through deduction  
can also be known through another means of knowledge,  
then this other means of knowledge may exclude from our term certain contrary properties  
which would have applied on the strength of our inferential mark alone. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pramāṇāntaragōcarē hi liṅgini liṅgabalādāpatatōviparītaviśēṣāṁstatpramāṇamēva pratiruṇaddhi
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atra punar atipatita-mānāntara-karma-bhāvē bhagavati siṣādhayiṣitē  
yāvantō 'nvaya-vyatirēkāvadhāritāvinābhāva-bhājō dharmās  
tān apy a-viśēṣēṇōpasthāpayatīti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the present instance, however, we are seeking to demonstrate God whose agency falls completely outside the scope of other means of knowledge;  
in his case therefore all the properties that participate in an invariable concomitance  
elicited through positive and negative consideration  
are indiscriminately established by the deduction, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

atra ... Cf. Īśvarasiddhi, P.244.

karmabhāvē ... ‘sakala-pramāṇāntarānavagatē’ ity arthaḥ।

sthāpayatīti ... kartr̥tvam iva anīśvaratvādikam api dharma-jātaṁ vyāpti-balēna vyavasthāpayatīty arthaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atra punaratipatitamānāntarakarmabhāvē bhagavati siṣādhayiṣitē yāvantō'nvayavyatirēkāvadhāritāvinābhāvabhājō dharmāstānapyaviśēṣēṇōpasthāpayatīti, 
</details>

#### kalpanā-gauravam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ca prāṅgaṇa-nikaṭa-varti-dūrvāṅkurādiṣv anavasita-puruṣa-vyāpāra-janmasv anaikāntaḥ,  
tatrāpy atīndriya-puruṣādhiṣṭhāna-kalpanā kalpanā-mātram ēva ।+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

A similarly occasional relationship between producer and product occurs,  
for instance, with grass that has grown just outside a house-garden.  
We cannot be positive that this grass has sprung from a person's action.  
In this instance, too, the assumption that a person, beyond the ken of our senses, has in fact been instrumental to the creation etc. of the world   
must remain entirely conjectural, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

tathā ca ... atra sandarbhānurōdhēna ‘tathā ca’ ity asya ‘kiñca’ ity arthō varṇanīyaḥ।

anaikāntaḥ ... kāryatva-hētur iti yōjanīyam।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ca prāṅgaṇanikaṭavartidūrvāṅkurādiṣvanavasitapuruṣavyāpārajanmasvanaikāntaḥ, tatrāpyatīndriyapuruṣādhiṣṭhānakalpanā kalpanāmātramēva ।  
</details>

#### sr̥ṣṭi-kāraṇābhāvaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kva vā dēśē **tiṣṭhann**, anavarata-tr̥ptiḥ kim iti vā   
kadā vā niśśēṣañ **janayati** tad ētad **vimr̥śatu** ॥  
kvacit **tiṣṭhann** iṣṭaṁ, kim api phalam uddiśya karaṇaiḥ   
kadācid yat-kiñcij **janayati** kulālādir akhilaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[26]] 
 
30\. Another question to be considered is  
from what point in space,  
at what point in time,  
and to what purpose  
a person who is satisfied in all eternity would produce the universe.  
Every agent, e.g., a potter, produces a product  
by means of certain instruments,  
while occupying a certain space at a certain time  
and aiming at a certain result which he wants.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Nyāyamañjarī Vol. I, P.191:

> kiṁ kimapi prayojanamananusandhāya jagatsarge pravartate prajāpatirevameva vā ? niṣprayojanīyāṁ pravṛttāvaprekṣāpūrvakāritvāt unmattatulyo'sau bhavet.

Vide Śaivasiddhānta P.83 ff.

> To create the world, the Lord should have occupied some place, but where is it exactly, when we definitely know that by then, space itself has not been created ?

Kumārila is the most relentless and vehement critic of the divine origination and dissolution of the universe. Creation of the world is refuted in

Ślokavārtika, under 1-i-5; śl. 47:

> pravṛttiḥ kathaṁ ādyā ca jagataḥ saṁpratīyate।
