leading the faithful into the mysterious abyss of his grand power of illusion, or not?  
This is the question that now arises.  
How are we to resolve it? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Viṣṇupurāṇa: ( Jīvānanda's edn. ) Aṁśa : III. chs. 17-18 give the story of Māyāmohana, preaching non-Vedic doctrines to demons, with a view to delude them. Other instances of Viṣṇu assuming different forms out of his Māyā, are to be found in the Liṅgapurāṇa and the Kāśīkhaṇḍa.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

māyāmōhanavigrahēṇa hariṇā dēvadruhāṁ saṁhatim ।  
hantuṁ mōhayatā'hitānyabhihitānyāhurhi tacchadmanā ॥  
ēvaṁ kinnu nayannayannijamahāmāyāguhāgavharam ।  
vyājahrē kimidaṁ na vēti viśayē jātē kathaṁ nirṇayaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Visnupurāna- ( Jivānanda's edn.) Arśa- III. chs. 17 - 18 give the story of Mayamohana, preaching non-Vedic doctrines to demons, with a view to delude them. Other instances of Viṣņu assuming different forms out of his Māyā, are to be found in the Lingapurana and the Kāsikhanda. 
</details>

#### vaidikair anaṅgīkāraḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

prattyuta **bhramayann** ēva  
**vyājahārēti** gamyatē ।  
vaidikair agr̥hītattvāt  
tathā 'rhatamataṁ yathā ॥+++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or are we rather to understand that  
he composed this Tantra  
while he himself was in error,  
since it is not accepted by the followers of the Veda,  
just as the doctrine of the Jainas is not accepted?
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

prattyuta bhramayannēva vyājahārēti gamyatē ।  
vaidikairagr̥hītattvāt tathā'rhatamataṁ yathā ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vaidikāparigrahaś ca prāg ēva prapañcita iti,  
tasmān na +++(vēdāpēkṣayā→)+++sva-tantrānubhava-mūlatayā pramāṇam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

That the followers of the Veda do not accept it has been set forth at length above.100   
Consequently, then,  Pancaratra Tantra is not authoritative  
because it derives from the cognition of an independent Person. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

supra § 12.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vaidikāparigrahaśca prāgēva prapañcita iti, tasmānna svatantrānubhavamūlatayā pramāṇam ।  
</details>

### na manvādi-smr̥tivat

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi manvādi-smaraṇavad ity - anupapannaṁ pañcarātrasmaraṇam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

47\. Nor is it proper to argue the validity of the Pancaratra Tradition "like the Manu Tradition etc. 101
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

supra §11.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi manvādismaraṇavadityanupapannaṁ pañcarātrasmaraṇam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi manvādivad dēvaḥ  
śuśrūṣā-**paritōṣitāt** ।  
ācāryāl **labdha**-vēdārthas  
tantram ētad **acīklapat** ॥  
svātantrya-**kalpanā** 'muṣya  
vyarthā mithyā tathā sati ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[39]]   
If the God has composed the Tantra after having, like manu etc., learnt the meaning of the Veda from a teacher who was satisfied with his pupil's obedience,  
then the assumption that He was independent is purposeless and false.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi manvādivaddēvaḥ śuśrūṣāparitōṣitāt ।  
ācāryāllabdhavēdārthastantramētadacīklapat ॥  
svātantryakalpanā'muṣya vyarthā mithyā tathā sati ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

anadhītō'pi vēdō'sya  
**pratibhātīty** alaukikam +++(tatō'sambhāvyam)+++॥  
tatra vārtikakārēṇa  
yē dōṣās **samudīritāḥ** ।  
tē ca sarvē **'nusaṁdhēyāḥ**  
puruṣātiśayādayaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It is not borne out by human experience that the Veda was immediately manifest to him, even though he never learnt it. The defects 
which the Author of the Varttika enumerates, those of personal superiority and inferiority etc., (Kumarila, Slokavārttika 2.114)  
are all to be presumed in the case of Pañcarātra, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide Ślokavārtika* I. i. 2, śl. 111b, ff.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anadhītō'pi vēdō'sya pratibhātītyalaukikam ॥  
tatra vārtikakārēṇa yē dōṣāssamudīritāḥ ।  
tē ca sarvē'nusaṁdhēyāḥ puruṣātiśayādayaḥ ॥
</details>

## 14 tāntrikatāyāḥ bāhyam

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kiñca -   

śaivaṁ pāśupatañ caiva  
bauddham apy ārhataṁ tathā ।  
kāpālaṁ pañcarātrañ cēty  
ēvaṁ **pāṣaṇḍatā** smr̥tēḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

48\. Moreover, the Saivite, Pasupata, Buddhist, Jainist, Kāpālika and Pañcarātra teachings are traditionally known as heretical. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiñca -   

śaivaṁ pāśupatañcaiva bauddhamapyārhataṁ tathā ।  
kāpālaṁ pañcarātrañcētyēvaṁ pāṣaṇḍatā smr̥tēḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vaidikaṁ tāntrikaṁ cēti  
**vibhāga-karaṇād** api ।  
**gamyatē** pañcarātrasya  
vēda-bāhyatva-niścayaḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

On the basis of the distinction between Vedic and Tantric  
we arrive at the conclusion that Pañcarātra is outside the Veda. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide Anandasamhitā ch. XIII, folios 43b-44a :  

> athāto devasyārcanaṁ dvividhaṁ śruņu । [sic]  
vaikhānasaṁ pañcarātraṁ vaidikaṁ tantrikaṁ kramāt ॥  
tayor vaikhānasaṁ śreṣṭhamaihikāmuṣmikapradam । 

The (Mahā) Sanatkumārasaṁhitā draws a distinction among the Vaiṣṇava-mantras in terms of Vaidika Tāntrika and Vaidika-tāntrika.

Cf. ṛṣirātra IX. 35:  

> vaidikaṁ tāntrikaṁ caiva tathā vaidikatāntrikam ।  
mantratrayaṁ krameṇoktam........ ॥ 

Cf. Vasiṣṭahasaṁhitā XIII. 16b-17a: 

> Vaidikaṁ tāntrikaṁ caiva tathā vaidikatāntrikam ।  
miśritaṁ vaidikaṁ mantraiḥ tasmāt vaidikatāntrikam ॥ 

Hārita in his Dharmaśāstra, says: srutiśca dvividhā, vaidikī tantrikī ca (Quoted in the Liṅgadhāraṇacandrikā, p. 240).  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vaidikaṁ tāntrikaṁ cēti vibhāgakaraṇādapi ।  
gamyatē pañcarātrasya vēdabāhyatvaniścayaḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> śaivaṁ pāśupataṁ saumyaṁ  
lāguḍañca caturvidham ।  
tantra-bhēdaḥ samuddiṣṭaḥ  
saṅkaraṁ na samācarēt ॥ 

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> "Tantra is of four kinds: Saiva, Pasupata, Saumya and Laguḍa;  
thus are described the divisions of Tantra;  
one should not confuse them." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The Vaikhānōsāgamas call the Vaikhānasa and the Pāñcarātra systems “saumya” and “āgneya” respectively. Cf. Kāśyapajñānakāṇḍa, P.171:

vaikhānasaṁ saumyam; āgneyaṁ pāñcarātram.

See also Vimānārcanākalpa, paṭala 77, P.467:

vaiṣṇavaṁ dvidvidhaṁ, vaikhānasaṁ pāñcarātram iti; vaikhānasaṁ vaidikaṁ, vaidikairarcitam aihikāmuṣmikaphalapradam; pāñcarātramāgneyaṁ avaidikam āmuṣmikaphalapradam; saumyaṁ sarvatra saṁpūjyam.

Cf. also Bhāgavata XI. 27. 7, 49:

> vaidikastāntriko miśra iti me trividho makhaḥ ।  
trayāṇāmipsitenaiva vidhinā māṁ samarcayet ॥  
evaṁ kriyāyogapathaiḥ pumān vaidikatāntrikaiḥ ।  
arcayannubhayataḥ siddhim matto vindatyabhipsitam ॥

It may be noted that such a division is found even among the Śaivāgamas. Thus, the Vāyu Saṁhitā of the Śivapurāṇa (uttarabhāga XXIV. 177-178) says:

> śivāgamo'pi dvidvidhaḥ śrauto'śrautaśca saṁsmṛtaḥ ।  
śrutisāramayaḥ śrautaḥ svatantra itarassmṛtaḥ॥ (Quoted in Liṅgādhāraṇacandrikā, P.290).

Also see Śaivasiddhānta P.43:

> Āgamas are of two kinds: Śrauta and Aśrauta. The Śrautāgamas are dependent upon the Vedas and are full of their essence; not so the Aśrauta. The former Āgamas are accepted but not the latter. The aśrauta-āgamas have been declared by the Lord in order to delude some people. These Āgamas are Vāma, Pāśupata, Lākula, Bhairava, etc.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

śaivaṁ pāśupataṁ saumyaṁ lāguḍañca caturvidham ।  
tantrabhēdaḥ samuddiṣṭaḥ saṅkaraṁ na samācarēt ॥ iti , ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā -  

> bhāktaṁ bhāgavatañcaiva  
sāttvataṁ ca tridhā matam ।  

ity ēvaṁ **tantrabhēdōktiḥ**  
pañcarātrē'pi **dr̥śyatē** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise:  

> "There are three distinct doctrines, the Bhakta, the Bhagavata and the Satvata;"  
this description of the divisions of Tantra is also found in Pancarātra. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā -  

bhāktaṁ bhāgavatañcaiva sāttvataṁ ca tridhā matam ।  
ityēvaṁ tantrabhēdōktiḥ pañcarātrē'pi dr̥śyatē ॥
</details>

## 15 jīva-janmōktiḥ

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kiñca -  

śruti-smr̥ti-pratikṣipta-  
jīva-janmādi-gōcaram ।  
nyāya-hīnaṁ vacas tathyam  
iti **hāsyam** idam mahat ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

49\. Furthermore, that a doctrine destitute of all logic  
and embracing the view that the soul knows birth,  
which is rejected by Revelation and Tradition,  
should be Truth is a highly ludicrous contention.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiñca -  

śrutismr̥tipratikṣiptajīvajanmādigōcaram ।  
nyāyahīnaṁ vacastathyamiti hāsyamidammahat ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ca śrutiḥ - 

> avināśī vā arē'yamātmā anucchittidharmā  
> mātrāsaṁsargas tasya bhavati 

iti tathā 

> jīvāpētaṁ vāva kilēdam mriyatē,  
> na jīvō mriyatē  

iti ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

 Thus we find the śruti,  
 
> "Verily, this soul is unperishing, essentially indestructible;  
> it is not conjoined with sizes" (BA Up. 4.5.14.)

and, 

> "This dies without the soul; the soul does not die."\*104 (Ch Up. 6.11.3.)
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

avināśī ... Bṛhadāraṇyaka IV. v. 14.

Cf. Bhagavadgītā II. 14:

> mātrāsparśāstu kaunteya śītoṣṇasukhaduḥkhadāḥ।  
āgamāpāyino'nityāstān titikṣasva bhārata॥

jīvāpētaṁ ...Chāndogy* VI. 11. 3.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ca śrutiḥ - 

> avināśī vā arē'yamātmā anucchittidharmā mātrāsaṁsargastasya bhavati 

iti tathā 

"jīvāpētaṁ vāva kilēdammriyatē na jīvō mriyatē"  

iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> syād ētat ucchēdābhāva-mātra-pratipādakam ētad vacanaṁ  
> na janmābhāvam avagamayati

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

OBJECTION.  
This is all very well,  
but all that this statement says is that the soul is not destroyed,  
not that it is not born. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

syādētat ucchēdābhāvamātrapratipādakamētadvacanaṁ na janmābhāvamavagamayatīti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na, 

anucchēdābhidhānēna  
janmābhāvō **'vasīyatē** ।  
**na** hy asti **saṁbhavō** bhāvō  
jātō naiva kṣarēd iti ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. No, by stating that it cannot be destroyed,  
it also decides that it cannot be born;  
it is impossible that an entity that has been born  
does not perish. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'jātō bhāvō naiva kṣarēd' ity ētad vacanaṁ na śakya-sambhavam iti bhāvaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na, 

anucchēdābhidhānēna janmābhāvō'vasīyatē ।  
na hyasti saṁbhavō bhāvō jātō naiva kṣarēditi ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu ca,  
>
> sad ēva saumyēdam iti  
sad-ēkatvāvadhāraṇāt ।  
prāk-sr̥ṣṭi-kālāj jīvānām  
a-bhāvō **'dhyavasīyatē** ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

OBJECTION.  
Nonetheless, from the emphasis which in the statement "only sat was here" (ChUp.6.2.1.) is laid on the uniqueness of sat,  
it follows that there were no souls before the time of creation. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Chāndogya: VI. ii. 1: ‘sad ēva sōmyēdam agra āsīt ēkam ēvādvitīyaṁ brahma' ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu ca,  

sadēva saumyēdamiti sadēkatvāvadhāraṇāt ।  
prāksr̥ṣṭikālājjīvānāmabhāvō'dhyavasīyatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yadi jīvāḥ pr̥thagbhūtāḥ  
prāk sr̥ṣṭēḥ syuḥ parātmavat ।  
katham ētat "sad ēvē"ti  
tad-ēkatvāvadhāraṇam ।+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Had the individual soul existed before  
why then this emphasis of "only sat"  
on sat's absolute solitariness?
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Chāndogya VI. ii. 1.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi jīvāḥ pr̥thagbhūtāḥ prāk sr̥ṣṭēḥ syuḥ parātmavat ।  
kathamētatsadēvēti tadēkatvāvadhāraṇam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atrōcyatē "sad ēvē"ti  
yad ēkatvāvadhāraṇam ।  
tat sisr̥kṣita-vāyv-ambu-  
viyat-prabhr̥ti-gōcaram ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[40]]  
REFUTATION.  
The reply to this is that  
here the emphasis on sat's uniqueness  
is with regard to the elements of wind, water and ether  
that were about to be created by sat.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atrōcyatē sadēvēti yadēkatvāvadhāraṇam ।  
tatsisr̥kṣitavāyvambuviyatprabhr̥tigōcaram ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

paryudāsiṣyatā'nēna  
vacasā cētanō yadi ।  
gaganādēr ivāsyāpi  
jananaṁ **niradēkṣyata** ॥+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Were the soul excluded by this statement of sat's solitariness,  
then the soul's origin would have been described in the sequel,  
just as the creation of ether is described.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

paryudāsiṣyatā'nēna vacasā cētanō yadi ।  
gaganādērivāsyāpi jananaṁ niradēkṣyata ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**na** ca **nirdiśyatē** tēna  
**na** jīvō **janim** r̥cchati ।  
tat-tējō'sr̥jatētyādau  
jīvasargō hi na śrutaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This is not done; therefore the soul does not know birth,  
since in the sequel "That sat created fire, etc. (Ch Up. 6.2.3. )  
we do not hear of the creation of the individual soul. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid: VI. ii. 3.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca nirdiśyatē tēna na jīvō janimr̥cchati ।  
tattējō'sr̥jatētyādau jīvasargō hi na śrutaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu ca "yatō vā imāni bhūtāni" ity-atra  
> jīvānām ēva janana-jīvana-prāyaṇābhisaṁvēśanāni pratīyantē?  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

OBJECTION. However, in the text yato va imani bhūtāni etc.  
we hear that the souls too know origin, continuance and reabsorption. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Taittirīya : III. i. 1: "yatō vā imāni bhūtāni jāyantē, yēna jātāni jīvanti" etc.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu ca yatō vā imāni bhūtāni ityatra jīvānāmēva jananajīvanaprāyaṇābhisaṁvēśanāni pratīyantē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tathā hi bhūtaśabdō'yaṁ  
jīvānām **abhidhāyakaḥ** ।  
**bhrāmayan** sarva-bhūtānīty-  
ēvam-ādiṣu darśanāt ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Here the word bhuta denotes the jiva, the individual soul;  
for thus we find the word used in the passage bhrāmayan sarvabhūtāni,  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Bhagavadgītā: XVIII, 61b.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi bhūtaśabdō'yaṁ jīvānāmabhidhāyakaḥ ।  
bhrāmayan sarvabhūtānītyēvamādiṣu darśanāt ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> jīvantīti hi śabdō'yaṁ  
jīvēṣv **ēvāvakalpatē** ।  
tēna **jāyanta** ity-ētaj  
**jñāyatē** jīva-gōcaram ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The verb jianti "they live" in the text can only apply to the souls,  
the expression tena jayante "by whom they are born" evidently refers to these same souls. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Taitt Up. 3.1.1. 
The whole sentence includes tena jivanti, on which the present exegesis of bhuta is based. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

jīvantīti hi śabdō'yaṁ jīvēṣvēvāvakalpatē ।  
tēna jāyanta ityētaj jñāyatē jīvagōcaram ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad idam anupapannaṁ bhūta-śabdō vihāyaḥ-  
pavana--huta-bhug-ambhō-mēdinīṣu prasiddhaḥ ।  
padam idam itarasmiṁl lakṣaṇā-vr̥tti tēṣāṁ  
bahu-vidha-pariṇāmō **gīyatē jīvanañ** ca ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[41]]
REFUTATION. This is not right.  
The word bhuta commonly deonly the elements ether, wind, fire, water and earth.  
If the word is used for something else, it is used metaphorically.
Of these elements, ether etc. which are primarily understood by the word bhuta,  
it is stated that they are variously modified and that they live.  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

namely, that they are born (jātāri) and die (prayanti).
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadidamanupapannaṁ bhūtaśabdō vihāyaḥpavanahutabhugambhōmēdinīṣu prasiddhaḥ ।  
padamidamitarasmiṁllakṣaṇāvr̥tti tēṣāṁ bahuvidhapariṇāmō gīyatē jīvanañca ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

prathamam **adhigatā** yē khādayō bhūta-śabdāt  
tad-anuguṇatayā'rthaṁ **vakti** jīvanti-śabdaḥ ।  
yadi ca **bhavati** jīvē bhūta-śabdas tadānīm  
api **vadati** tadīyañ janma dēhānubandhi ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The verb "they live" describes a condition of being analogous to living.  
And if the word bhuta be used in the sense of individual soul,  
then too the statement declares that the soul is born only in the sense that its entrance into a body is a birth.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

prathamamadhigatā yē khādayō bhūtaśabdāttadanuguṇatayā'rthaṁ vakti jīvanti śabdaḥ ।  
yadi ca bhavati jīvē bhūtaśabdastadānīmapi vadati tadīyañjanma dēhānubandhi ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atō jīva-paratvē'pi  
bhūta-śabdasya **yujyatē** ।  
**jāyanta** iti śabdō'yaṁ  
gaur jātō gacchatīti vat ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore, when the word bhuta refers to the individual soul,  
it can rightly be said that the souls are born,  
just as it is said that the cow,  
once born walks about. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atō jīvaparattvē'pi bhūtaśabdasya yujyatē ।  
jāyanta iti śabdō'yaṁ gaurjjātō gacchatīti vat ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā "'jō hy ēka" ity-ādyāḥ  
śrutayō 'nyāś ca santi naḥ ।  
jīvānutpatti-vādinyas  
tathā bhagavatō vacaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

There are śrutis to this effect, like  
"For the soul, unborn, alone" (Svet Up. 4.5.)  
and we also have other Śrutis which declare that the soul is unborn.  
Similarly, the word of the Lord: 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Śvetāśvatara IV. 5: “ajō hy ēkō juṣamāṇō 'nuśētē ।”
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathājōhyēka ityādyāḥ śrutayō'nyāśca santi naḥ ।  
jīvānutpattivādinyastathā bhagavatōvacaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> prakr̥tiṁ puruṣañcaiva  
> viddhy anādī ubhāv api । (Bh G. 18.61.)
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"Know that both matter and spirit are without beginning;"  (Bh G. 13.19.)
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Bhagavadgītā XIII. 19a.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> prakr̥tiṁ puruṣañcaiva viddhyanādī ubhāvapi ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> ajō nityaś śāśvatō'yaṁ purāṇaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"this ancient spirit is unborn, eternal, everlasting;" (Kath Up. 2.18.)
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid: II. 20c.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ajō nityaśśāśvatō'yaṁ purāṇaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na jāyatē mriyatē vā kadācit ।  

ityādi ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"it is never born nor does it die" etc. (Kath Up. 2.17.)
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid: II. 20a.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na jāyatē mriyatē vā kadācit ।  
ityādi ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nyāyaś ca -  

vivādādhyāsitō jīvō  
**na** jātu **janim** r̥cchati ।  
dravyatvē satya-mūrtatvāc  
cid-rūpatvāt parātmavat ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Finally there is the syllogism:  
the individual soul in question never knows birth; 
for, while being substantial, it is bodiless,  
as it consists of spirit, like the Supreme Soul. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nyāyaś ca -  

vivādādhyāsitō jīvō na jātu janimr̥cchati ।  
dravyatvē satyamūrtatvāccidrūpatvātparātmavat ॥  
</details>

## 16 nāpauruṣēyatā

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> paśyantaḥ pauruṣēyatvē  
dūṣaṇāny uktayā diśā ।  
an-anya-gatayaḥ kēcit  
tantraṁ nityam **atiṣṭhipan** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

50\. There are some who notice the logical defects inherent in the view that Scripture of a personal origin,  
which we have explained above, and having no other course open  
posit that Tantra too must be eternal. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

paśyantaḥ pauruṣēyatvē dūṣaṇānyuktayā diśā ।  
ananyagatayaḥ kēcit tantraṁ nityamatiṣṭhipan ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad ētat sva-hr̥daya-nihita-viśadatara-  
katr̥-smaraṇa-pratihatam **abhidhīyata**  
ity **upēkṣaṇīyam** ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Against this position, we state that  
it is sublated by the fact that its author,  
who is patent enough and tacitly remembered, is not forgotten at all;  
and hence this position does not deserve our 
notice. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadētat svahr̥dayanihitaviśadatarakatr̥smaraṇapratihatamabhidhīyata ityupēkṣaṇīyam ।
</details>

## 17 pāśupatādi-samatā

### pauruṣēyatvam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kiñca -  

itthaṁ pāśupatādīnāṁ +++(tac-chāstra-pauruṣēyatvē)+++  
nyāyaḥ kiṁ-daṇḍa-vāritaḥ ।  
tathā'stv iti yadi brūyād  
vyāghātas syāt parasparam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[42]]  
51\. Besides, why has the argument about the Pasupatas etc. been swept aside with a stick?  
If one replies, let the argument stand,  
we shall have the defect of mutual exclusion. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiñca -  

itthaṁ pāśupatādīnāṁ nyāyaḥ kiṁ daṇḍavāritaḥ ।  
tathā'stviti yadi brūyād vyāghātassyāt parasparam ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sarva-lōka-prasiddhā ca  
vāsudēva-praṇītatā ।  
**na hātuṁ śakyatē**  
yadvad vēdasyāpauruṣēyatā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And Vasudeva's authorship of the Tantra, which is commonly known to everybody,  
can no more be rejected than the preferpersonal origin of the Veda. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sarvalōkaprasiddhā ca vāsudēvapraṇītatā ।  
na hātuṁ śakyatē yadvadvēdasyāpauruṣēyatā ॥
</details>

### anudaya-viparyāsa-viśayāḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

athō kaścid brūyād -  

> anudaya-viparyāsa-viśayais tri-rūpē prāmāṇyē  
katarad iha jōghuṣyata 

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or else, if someone says that 

> (Is) any of the three means of knowledge is, in the case of ~~Pasupata~~ Tantra, cancelled by non-appearance (sc. of knowledge.), reversion and dubiety, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Slokavārtika ( I. 1. 2 ) śl.54a: 

> aprāmāṇyaṁ tridhā bhinnaṁ mithyātvājñāna-saṁśayaiḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

athō kaścid brūyādanudayaviparyāsaviśayaistrirūpē prāmāṇyē kataradiha jōghuṣyata iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sa vaktavyaḥ 

> > +++(yat)+++ kin nu +++(sva-matē)+++ tvad-abhilaṣitaṁ  
lāguḍa-matē tad ēva
> 
> iti jñātvā  
niyamita-madaś śāmyatu bhavān ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

the answer is, your own postulation applies equally well to the Laguḍa doctrine (here used as synonymous with Pasupata),  
and once you know this, it is refuted.  
Your worship better keep quiet. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

lāguḍa-mataṁ pāśupatam iti yāvat । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sa vaktavyaḥ 

> kinnu tvadabhilaṣitaṁ  
> lāguḍamatē tadēvēti jñātvā  
> niyamitamadaśśāmyatu bhavān।
</details>

## 18 upasaṁhāraḥ

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad ēvam udīrita-nyāya-śruti-smr̥tītihāsa-purāṇa-nyāya-viruddhābhidhānēna,  
samasta-śiṣṭa-jana-parigraha-virahēṇa ca,  
svargāpavargāvasānōpadēśa-vyājēna kēnāpi  
jagad **vañcayituṁ viracitāni** pañca-rātra-tantrāṇīti manyāmahē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

52\. To sum up. For the reasons set forth above  
we maintain that the exposure of this Tantra's incompatibility with Revelation, Tradition, Epic and Purana  
as well as with the conclusions of our logical demonstration,  
and the inacceptability of this Tantra to all exemplary persons  
go to show that the Pañcaratra texts must have been composed by someone  
who pretended to teach a path that would lead to heaven and salvation,  
but actually wished to deceive the world.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadēvamudīritanyāyaśrutismr̥tītihāsapurāṇanyāyaviruddhābhidhānēna, samastaśiṣṭajanaparigrahavirahēṇa ca, svargāpavargāvasānōpadēśavyājēna kēnāpi jagadvañcayituṁ viracitāni pañcarātratantrāṇīti manyāmahē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

īdr̥śāpasmr̥ti-viṣayam ēva tadvacaḥ -  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Concerning its apocryphal character, which we have now exposed, we have the declaration: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

īdr̥śāpasmr̥tiviṣayamēva tadvacaḥ -  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yā vēda-bāhyāḥ smr̥tayō  
yāśca kāśca kudr̥ṣṭayaḥ ।  
sarvās tā niṣphalāḥ prētya 
tamō-niṣṭhā hi tāḥ smr̥tāḥ ॥

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> "The traditional teachings that are outside the Veda  
> and all other false doctrines remain fruitless in the afterworld,  
> for they are considered to derive from tamas." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Manusmṛti XII. 95.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yā vēdabāhyāḥ smr̥tayō yāśca kāśca kudr̥ṣṭayaḥ ।  
sarvāstā niṣphalāḥ prētya tamōniṣṭhā hi tāḥ smr̥tāḥ ॥

iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

īdr̥śa-dur-mārgānugāmina ēva tē'pi,  
ēṣāṁ vāṅ-mātrēṇāpi +arcanaṁ niṣidhyatē,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Those who follow the Veda are forbidden to speak with those who follow such evil paths: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

īdr̥śadurmārgānugāmina ēva tē'pi ēṣāṁ vāṅmātrēṇāpi arcanaṁ niṣidhyatē,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

uktañca -  

> ēta ēva ca tē yēṣāṁ  
vāṅmātrēṇāpi **nārcanam** ।  
pāṣaṇḍinō vikarma-sthān  
baiḍāla-vratikāṁñ chaṭhān ॥  
haitukān baka-vr̥ttīṁś ca  
vāṅmātrēṇāpi nārcayēt ।  

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"The following are not to be honoured even with a word: heretics, criminals, impostors, crooks, thieves and hypocrites are not to be honoured even with a word." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. IV. 30.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

uktañca -  

> ēta ēva ca tē yēṣāṁ vāṅmātrēṇāpi nārcanam ।  
pāṣaṇḍinō vikarmasthān baiḍālavratikāṁñchaṭhān ॥  
haitukān bakavr̥ttīṁśca vāṅmātrēṇāpi nārcayēt ।  

iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ity upanyastayā nītyā  
pañca-rātram aśēṣataḥ ।  
apramāṇam iti **prāptam**  
ēvaṁ **praptē 'bhidhīyatē** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[43]]  
53\. In the manner116 presented above the primafacie case can be made  
that the Pañcaritra in its entirety has no validity  
whatever as a means of knowledge.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

I read rityā.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

From here starts the ‘Siddhānta’.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ityupanyastayā nītyā pañcarātramaśēṣataḥ ।  
apramāṇamiti prāptamēvaṁ praptē'bhidhīyatē ॥  
</details>

# +02 uttara-pakṣaḥ

## 01 nirdōṣa-jñāna-janyatayā prāmāṇyānumānam

### pratijñā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> vivādādhyāsitaṁ tantraṁ  
pramāṇam iti **gr̥hyatām**।  
nirdōṣa-jñāna-janmatvāj  
jyōtiṣṭōmādi-vākyavat॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Against this prima-facie case  
we now submit that the Tantra in question must be accepted as valid,  
because it produces faultless knowledge,  
like the scriptural statements on the Vedic sacrifices jyotiştoma etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘jyōtiṣṭōmēna svarga-kāmō yajēta’ iti vākyavat pañca-rātra-tantram api nirdōṣa-jñāna-kāraṇatvād dhētōḥ pramāṇam ēvēti svīkriyatām ity āśayaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vivādādhyāsitaṁ tantraṁ pramāṇamiti gr̥hyatām।  
nirdōṣajñānajanmatvājjyōtiṣṭōmādivākyavat॥
</details>

### anumānay avayavāḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**na** tāvad anumānē'smin  
nyāya-śāstra-parīkṣitāḥ ।  
dōṣā **mr̥gayituṁ** śakyās  
tatra pakṣaḥ **parīkṣyatām** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

54\. Now, such defects as are elicited by the science of logic  
cannot be detected in this inference.  
Let us consider the Object of the Proposition. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na tāvadanumānē'smin nyāyaśāstraparīkṣitāḥ ।  
dōṣā mr̥gayituṁ śakyāstatra pakṣaḥ parīkṣyatām ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pakṣō nāma pratijñā'rthaḥ  
sa ca siddhēna kēnacit ।  
svayaṁ siddhō viśiṣṭas san  
yaḥ sādhayitum īpsitaḥ ॥+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The Object of the Proposition is, by definition,  
the content of a certain thesis is proposed;  
it is a term which itself is established,  
and of which it is now to be proved that it is particularized by another term,  
which is also established." 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

pratijñārthah, the object or content of the pratijñā,  
which is the first step of the five-membered syllogism,  
e.g., "the mountain has fire" (parvatasya agnimattvam).  
It does not therefore coincide with the Subject.  
In the proposition both S and P must be siddha, established as existing somewhere;  
a non-thing like a hare's horn can be neither S nor P. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

pakṣa-śabdaṁ nirvakti । pakṣō nāma (parvatādiḥ) pratijñā-viṣayī-bhūtaḥ kaścana svayaṁ siddhaḥ padārthaḥ । [ pratijñā ‘parvatō vahnimān’ ity ēvaṁ rūpā ।] sa ca siddhēna kēnacid anyēna padārthēṇa hētu-bhūtēna [dhūmādinā] sisādhayiṣitaḥ । sisādhayiṣitō 'pi saḥ kiñcid viśiṣṭākārēṇa [vahnimat-sva-rūpēṇa] sisādhayiṣitaḥ; na tu sāmānyākārēṇa, iti dik ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pakṣō nāma pratijñā'rthaḥ sa ca siddhēna kēnacit ।  
svayaṁ siddhō viśiṣṭassan yaḥ sādhayitumīpsitaḥ ॥
</details>

## 02 pakṣa-sauṣṭhavam

### prasiddhiḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatra na tāvad a-prasiddha-viśēṣaṇaḥ pakṣaḥ -  
prāmāṇya-nāmnaḥ padārthasya ubhaya-vādi-siddhatvāt pratyakṣādau,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the present case the term which particularizes the object is not unknown,  
for this term, ie. "validity," is for both parties established with regard to the valid means of knowledge, Perception, Inference, Verbal Testimony etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatra na tāvadaprasiddhaviśēṣaṇaḥ pakṣaḥ,  
prāmāṇyanāmnaḥ padārthasya ubhayavādisiddhatvāt pratyakṣādau,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpy a-prasiddha-viśēṣyaḥ +++(saviśēṣaṇaḥ pakṣaḥ)+++ pañca-rātra-śāstrasya sarva-lōka-prasiddhatvāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is the subject itself unknown, for the Pañcaratra system is known universally. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpyaprasiddhaviśēṣyaḥ pañcarātraśāstrasya sarvalōkaprasiddhatvāt, 
</details>

### na siddha-sādhanam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi siddha-sādhanaḥ +++(saviśēṣaṇaḥ pakṣaḥ)+++,  
prastuta-śāstra-prāmaṇyasya prativādinō 'siddhatvāt,+++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is the Object to be proved already proved,  
for this Object, "The Pañcaratra is valid," is not proved for the opponent. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi siddhasādhanaḥ, prastutaśāstraprāmaṇyasya prativādinō'siddhatvāt, 
</details>

### na pratyakṣa-virōdhaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca pratyakṣa-viruddhaḥ +++(saviśēṣaṇaḥ pakṣaḥ)+++ a-prāmāṇyasyātīndriyatvāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is this Object incompatible with Perception,  
since its opposite, ie. nonvalidity, is beyond perceptual verifiability. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca pratyakṣaviruddhaḥ aprāmāṇyasyātīndriyatvāt, 
</details>

### nānumānatō virōdhō bāhyatvādibhiḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpy anumānaviruddhaḥ +++(saviśēṣaṇaḥ pakṣaḥ)+++, anupalambhanāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is this Object incompatible with Inference,  
because no inference proving non-validity is found. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpyanumānaviruddhaḥ, anupalambhanāt ।  
</details>

#### na bāhyatvād aprāmāṇyam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> **nanūpalabhyata** ēvānumānam -  
> pañca-rātra-śāstramapramāṇam vēda-bāhyatvāt bauddhāgamavat ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

55\. OBJECTION. But such an inference is actually found: Pañcarātra Sastra is non-authoritative,  
because it is non-Vedic, like Buddhism, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> nanūpalabhyata ēvānumānam -pañcarātraśāstramapramāṇam vēdabāhyatvāt bauddhāgamavat ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atra brūmaḥ katarad ihāprāmāṇyaṁ siṣādhayiṣitam  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. We reply, What is this nonauthoritativeness which this reasoning seeks to prove? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atra brūmaḥ kataradihāprāmāṇyaṁ siṣādhayiṣitaṁ  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi +++(aprāmāṇyam)+++ jñānānutpatti-lakṣaṇaṁ, tataḥ pratyakṣavirōdhaḥ।  
pratyakṣaṁ hi  
vidita-pada--tad-artha--saṅgatēḥ śrōtuḥ  
pañca-rātra-śāstra-vākya-śravaṇa-samanantaram upajāyamānaṁ tad-artha-viṣayaṁ jñānam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[44]] 

If it is defined by the fact that the Tantra does not produce knowledge,  
then this definition militates against Perception;  
for the knowledge which arises in a student, who is able to comprehend the relation between word and meaning, concerning the meaning of the sentences of Pañcaratra Sastra  
he hears is perceptually evident. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi jñānānutpatti-lakṣaṇaṁ tataḥ pratyakṣavirōdhaḥ, pratyakṣaṁ hi viditapadatadarthasaṅgatēḥ śrōtuḥ pañcarātraśāstravākyaśravaṇasamanantaramupajāyamānaṁ tadarthaviṣayaṁ jñānam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi +++(aprāmāṇyam)+++ saṁśaya-lakṣaṇaṁ - tata +++(→pratyakṣataḥ)+++ ēva virōdhāt।  
na khalu  

> padmamadhyē caturbāhuṁ  
> pūjayēt puruṣōttamam 

itīdaṁ vacanaṁ "pūjayēn na vē"ti saṁśayitaṁ pratyayamutpādayati, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is the predicate, sc. "nonauthoritativeness," defined by dubiety,  
since then we have the same conflict with Perception;  
for the statement, "One must worship the four-armed Supreme Person in the centre of the lotus,"  
does not occasion a doubtful cognition:  
"Must one worship Him thus or not?" 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘tata ēva’ pratyakṣād ēvēty arthaḥ ।

padmamadhyē ... To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi saṁśayalakṣaṇaṁ tata ēva virōdhāt na khalu padmamadhyē caturbāhuṁ pūjayētpuruṣōttamam itīdaṁ vacanaṁ pūjayēnna vēti saṁśayitaṁ pratyayamutpādayati, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi viparyaya-lakṣaṇaṁ yōgyānupalambhābhāvāt,  
anāgata-viparyayōtprēkṣāyāḥ pratyakṣa-virōdhāt, aśēṣa-vyavahārōcchēda-hētutvāc ca।  
prapañcayiṣyatē caitad upariṣṭāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor, in the third place, is the predicate, defined by reversion,  
since there is no non-apprehension of what should be there,  
and since, the presumption of future reversion militates against Perception  
and would put an end to all operations.  
This point shall be discussed in detail later on. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

this "non-apprehension of what should be there (yogānupalambha) is the criterion by which we know the absence of a thing. Here it is the absence of truth in Pañcarātra that needs be proved by yoganupalambha, if the objector's contention that Pañcarātra is invalid-through-reversion be correct. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

viparyayō mithyā-jñānam । ‘pañca-rātraṁ mithyā ity ētaj-jñānam idānīṁ nāsti, kālāntarē bhaviṣyati’ iti, tad ādāya aprāmāṇya-vacanaṁ pratyakṣēṇa virudhyatē । tathā sati sakala-lōka-vyavahāra-bādhaś cēti bhāvaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi viparyayalakṣaṇaṁ yōgyānupalambhābhāvāt, anāgataviparyayōtprēkṣāyāḥ pratyakṣavirōdhāt aśēṣavyavahārōcchēdahētutvācca, prapañcayiṣyatē caitadupariṣṭāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

viparyayō mithyājñānam ।  

> 'pañcarātraṁ mithyā ityētaj jñānaṁ idānīṁ nāsti,  
kālāntarē bhaviṣyati' 

iti, tad ādāya aprāmāṇya-vacanaṁ pratyakṣēṇa virudhyatē ।  
tathā sati sakala-lōka-vyavahāra-bādhaś cēti bhāvaḥ । 
</details>

#### vēda-bhinnatvān nāprāmāṇyam

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

+++([vēda-bāhyatvād apramāṇam iti] pañcarātra-)+++āgama-viruddhañ ca -  

pañca-rātrāgamē svārthas  
tathaivēty **avabōdhanāt** ।  

> > atha "+++(pañcarātra→)+++tasyāpramāṇatvē  
+++(pañcarātra→)+++tad-virōdhō na dūṣaṇam" ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

56\. ~~Still, the proposed validity of Pañcarātra militates against Scripture. Since in Pañcarātra Agama we have its meaning conveyed exactly as it is, this conflict between Scripture and Pañcarātra is not vicious only if Pañcaratra is not authoritative.~~
</details>

<details><summary>En - viśvāsaḥ</summary>

The claim that Pañcarātra is invalid is opposed by the Pañcarātra Agama itself. In Pañcarātra, it's validity is understood. Or you say -

> As Pañcarātra itself is invalid, it's opposition (to our inference of invalidity) is not a fault.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'pañca-rātram a-pramāṇaṁ vēda-bāhyatvāt' iti virōdhānumānaṁ pūrva-pakṣiṇā pradarśitam ।  tatrōcyatē siddhāntinā 'āgama-viruddhaṁ ca' iti । āgama-padēna pāñcarātrāgamaḥ abhiprētaḥ । pāñcarātrāgamē pratipādyamānō 'rthaḥ pramāṇam iti tēnaivāgamēna bōdhyatē ity arthaḥ । tatra ākṣipati mīmāṁsaka: 'athē'ti । 'tasya' pāñcarātrāgamasyaiva aprāmāṇyē niścitē sati, mad-uktēnānumāna-vākyēna virōdhaḥ sphuṭa ēva । tatra kō dōṣaḥ ? iti tasya praśnaḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

āgamaviruddhañ ca -  

pañcarātrāgamē svārthastathaivētyavabōdhanāt ।  
atha tasyāpramāṇatvē tadvirōdhō na dūṣaṇam ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

hanta ēvaṁ sati  
tad+++(=pāñcarātra)+++-aprāmāṇyē +++(tvat-prayukta-)+++'numāna-prāmāṇyam +++(iṣyatē)+++,  
+++(asmat-prayukta-)+++anumāna+++(taḥ)+++-prāmāṇyē +++(pradarśitē)+++ tad+++(=pāñcarātra)+++-aprāmaṇyam +++(iṣyatē)+++  
ity anyōnyāśrayaṇam । +++(5)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION.  
Why, if that were so, that would mean that  
~~if its authority is disproved by Scripture  
it is proved by Inference,  
and if it is proved by inference  
it is disproved by Scripture;  
which is a vicious circle.~~
</details>

<details><summary>En - viśvāsaḥ</summary>

Why, if that were so, that would mean that  
for proving it's invalidity,  
you want (your) inference's validity accepted.  
But where we infer it's validity,  
you want it's invalidity (to counter us).
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

I have difficulty in understanding the argument unless I assume an illogicality. By stating as his ground since in agama we have its meaning exactly conveyed as it is the objector not only agrees with the preceding argumentation that on inferential grounds Pañcaratra is not invalid, but even goes so far as accepting that it is valid in other words, confuse non-invalidity with validity. 

Then, because of this validity (svarthasya tathātvāvabodhanāt), there arises a conflict with a deviating statement of the Veda which has its own validity; since only one can be true, it follows that when Pancarãtra is true by inference, it is untrue by Veda. 

But I don't see how the objector can reasonably infer the validity of Pañcarātra, since its meaning or content is admittedly suprasensible. Yamuna himself has not argued that Inference proves the validity, but that Inference cannot disprove the correctness of the thesis.
[[134]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yadā pañca-rātram apramāṇam iti niścitaṁ tadaiva tvad-uktānumānaṁ pramāṇam; tathā tvadīyānumānē pramāṇatayā siddhē pañca-rātrāprāmāṇya-niścayaś cēti anyōnyāśraya-dōṣa-pratipādanaṁ kriyatē 'tra siddhāntinā ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

hanta ēvaṁ sati tadaprāmāṇyē'numānaprāmāṇyam anumānaprāmāṇyē tadaprāmaṇyamityanyōnyāśrayaṇam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca kim idaṁ vēda-bāhyatvam?   
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

57\. Besides, what does this mean, "being nonVedic, or outside the Veda?" 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

parōktānumāna-vākyē hētu-bhūtasya ‘vēda-bāhyatva’ padasya tattvaṁ vicāryatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca kimidaṁ vēdabāhyatvaṁ  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi vēdānyatvaṁ tataḥ +++(vēda-bhinnatvāt)+++ pratyakṣādibhir anaikāntaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[45]]  
If it means that Pañcaratra is different from the Veda,  
we have an occasional application to Perception etc.,  
which are also different from the Veda. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi vēdānyatvaṁ tataḥ pratyakṣādibhiranaikāntaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha +++(pratyakṣa-grahaṇaṁ vārayituṁ)+++ "śabdatvē satī"ti hētur viśēṣyatē tatō nigrahasthānam,  
yathā'huḥ 

> nirviśēṣa-hētu-prayōgē punar viśēṣaṇōpādānaṁ nigrahaḥ, 

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If, in order to avoid this defect, the ground is thus specified, 'because, while being language, it is different from the Veda,' we have a hetvantaram deadlock,  
which, as they say, occurs when into a syllogism with an unqualified ground  
and additional qualification is accepted 120
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

a hetvantaram constitutes on the part of the debator a confession of importance  
since the ground which he gave does not hold  
and he has to produce a different ground.  
By the rules of debate this means a defeat.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Nyāyadarśana V. ii. 6: “aviśēṣōktē hētau pratiṣiddhē viśēṣam icchatō hētv-antaram ।”
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha śabdatvē satīti hēturviśēṣyatē tatō nigrahasthānam,  
yathā'huḥ nirviśēṣahētuprayōgē punarviśēṣaṇōpādānaṁ nigrahaḥ, iti,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

anaikāntikaśca manvādivākyaiḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Also, we then have an occasional application to the statements of Manu, 
which also are language and different from the Veda, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anaikāntikaśca manvādivākyaiḥ ।  
</details>

#### a-vēda-mūlatvān na

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

athaitad-dōṣa-hānāya  
vēda-bāhyatva-śabdataḥ ।  
avēda-mūlatāṁ manda  
**manyasē** kin nu tārkika? ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If then, my slow-witted opponent, in order to remove this defect from your ground  
you claim that being outside the Veda means  
"not deriving from the Veda,"  
then what do you, logician, think of it? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The term ‘Tārkika’ need not necessarily refer to the logician here. Yāmuna makes fun of the dialectical helplessness of the Mīmāṁsaka.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

athaitaddōṣahānāya vēdabāhyatvaśabdataḥ ।  
avēdamūlatāṁ manda manyasē kinnu tārkika? ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tēnāyam arthaḥ  -  
"śabdatvē saty a-vēda-mūlatvād" iti,  
tatō vēdair anaikāntyam,   
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Well, by this definition of the ground we get meaning,  

> "something, namely in case there is question of language-statements, is non-Vedic,  
> because it does not derive from the Veda." 

But then there is an occasional application to the Veda itself,  
which does not derive from the Veda! 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tēnāyamarthaḥ śabdatvē satyavēdamūlatvāditi, tatō vēdairanaikāntyam, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

athavā a-vēdatvē sati śabdatvē sati a-vēda-mūlatvād iti hētuḥ,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

When the ground is redefined as 

> "because it does not derive from the Veda,  
> in case of a language-statement but not a Vedic statement," 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

athavā avēdatvē sati śabdatvē sati avēdamūlatvāditi hētuḥ,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathāpi ।  

> santi nadyās taṭē  
vr̥kṣā ity-ādyāptōpadēśanaiḥ ।  
a-vēda-mūlair durvāram  
anaikāntyaṁ **prasajyatē** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

then again there would inevitably be an occasional application to statements of reliable persons  
which do not derive from the Veda  
and yet are valid, like  
"There are trees on the river-bank." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathāpi ।  
santi nadyāstaṭē vr̥kṣā ityādyāptōpadēśanaiḥ ।  
avēdamūlairdurvāramanaikāntyaṁ prasajyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha 

> avēdatvē sati, śabdatvē sati, kārya-viṣayatvē sati, a-vēda-mūlatvaṁ hētuḥ, 

atrāpi "ajīrṇē mandam aśnīyād" ityādau vyabhicāritā ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If the reason is further corrected into:  
"because it does not derive from the Veda, namely, in case of a language-statement -but not a Vedic statement-  
and this statement concerns an action to be taken,"  
then still we have a vicious applicability to such precepts as  
"One must eat little when one has indigestion."  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This line runs like a verse.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha avēdatvē sati śabdatvē sati kāryaviṣayatvē sati avēdamūlatvaṁ hētuḥ, atrāpi ajīrṇē mandamaśnīyādityādau vyabhicāritā ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha

> ukta-viśēṣaṇa-viśiṣṭatvē dharmādharma-viṣayatvē'pi saty a-vēdamūlatvād iti hētuḥ, 

tatō bhāgāsiddhō hētuḥ, na hi pañcarātraśāstraṁ kr̥tsnaṁ dharmādharma-viṣayam -  
brahmaviṣayāṇāmēva vacasāṁ bāhulyāt ।  
+++(ataḥ pakṣō'siddhō bhavati)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[46]]  
Again, if the ground is then reformulated as 

> "because it does not derive from the Veda, in case of a statement specified by all the above specifications  
> and also concerned with dharma and adharma,"  

then this ground is partly impertinent, because Pancarātra Sastra does not deal with dharma and adharma exclusively,  
since the great majority of its Statements concern Brahman.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

athōktaviśēṣaṇaviśiṣṭatvē dharmādharmaviṣayatvē'pi satyavēdamūlatvāditi hētuḥ, tatō bhāgāsiddhō hētuḥ, na hi pañcarātraśāstraṁ kr̥tsnaṁ dharmādharmaviṣayam brahmaviṣayāṇāmēva vacasāṁ bāhulyāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha "pramāṇāntarāyōgyārthatvē satī"ti viśēṣaḥ  
+++("avēdatvē sati, śabdatvē sati, a-vēda-mūlatvaṁ hētuḥ," ityatra)+++  
tatrāpi saivāsiddhiḥ,  
bhagavat-pratyakṣasya dharmādharmādi-samasta-vastu-gōcarasya śruti-śata-prasiddhatvāt।  
tac-caitad anantaram ēva vakṣyāmaḥ। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If then, the specification is added  
"....when it deals with objects that are outside the scope of other pramāņas,"  
then again the ground does not fully apply,  
for hundreds of śrutis demonstrate  
that the Perception of God encompasses all things related to dharma and adharma. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

asiddhirēvēty arthaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha pramāṇāntarāyōgyārthatvē satīti viśēṣaḥ tatrāpi saivāsiddhiḥ, bhagavatpratyakṣasya dharmādharmādisamastavastugōcarasya śrutiśataprasiddhatvāt taccaitadanantaramēva vakṣyāmaḥ  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad alam anēnāśikṣitākṣapāda-matānām a-pratiṣṭhita-pratibhā-vijr̥mbhitēna ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

We shall discuss this point presently (infra §§ 76 F.);  
this suffices for the time being to expose the baseless fancies  
of those who have not made a study of Akṣapada's system.  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Akshapada - The founder of the school of logic.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadalamanēnāśikṣitākṣapādamatānāmapratiṣṭhitapratibhāvijr̥mbhitēna ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

saṁbhāvyamānāny apy anumānāntarāṇi  
parastād upanyasya nirasyantē  
atō nānumāna-viruddhaḥ pakṣaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Other conceivable inferences will be presented; and refuted, later on.  
We conclude therefore, that the proposition "Pañcarātra is authoritative," is not in conflict with Inference.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

saṁbhāvyamānānyapyanumānāntarāṇi parastādupanyasya nirasyantē atō nānumānaviruddhaḥ pakṣaḥ ।  
</details>

#### nāgama-virōdhaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpy āgama-viruddhaḥ -  
pañca-rātra-śāstra-prāmāṇya-pratipādakasya "idam mahōpaniṣadam" ity-ādy-āgama-śatasya pradarśayiṣyamāṇatvāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

58\. Nor is it in conflict with Scripture,  
for hundreds of scriptural statements, like idam mahopaniṣadam,  
will be adduced which set forth that Pañcarātra is authoritative. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Mahābhārata ( Critical edn., Poona ) XII. 326. 100a:

> idaṁ mahōpaniṣadaṁ catur-vēda-samanvitam।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpyāgamaviruddhaḥ pañcarātraśāstraprāmāṇyapratipādakasya idammahōpaniṣadam ityādyāgamaśatasya pradarśayiṣyamāṇatvāt ।  
</details>

### na sva-vyāghātādi
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sva-vacana+++(→virōdhaḥ)+++--svābhyupagama+++(→virōdhaḥ)+++--sarva-lōka-prasiddhi-virōdhāś  
**śabda-virōdha**-prakārās tv anāśaṅkanīyā ēva, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

There are no grounds to suspect in our proposition  
anyone of the three kinds of contradiction of language-statements;  
namely, contradiction within the terms of the statement;  
contradiction with one's own thesis;  
or contradiction with universally accepted facts. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

svavacana-svābhyupagama-sarvalōkaprasiddhivirōdhāśśabdavirōdhaprakārāstvanāśaṅkanīyā ēva, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā hi na tāvat svavacanavirōdhaḥ,  
sa hi trēdhā - uktimātravirōdhaḥ, dharmōktivirōdhaḥ, dharmyuktivirōdhaś cēti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[47]]  
First, there is no contradiction within the statement.  
This type of contradiction is of three kinds of mere utterance;  
or utterance of property;  
and of utterance of substance. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi na tāvat svavacanavirōdhaḥ, sa hi trēdhā uktimātravirōdhaḥ, dharmōktivirōdhaḥ, dharmyuktivirōdhaścēti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatra na tāvad uktimātra-viruddhō'yaṁ pakṣaḥ,  
na hi "pañca-rātra-śāstraṁ pramāṇam" iti pratijñā-vacanaṁ  
svārthaṁ vyāhanti -  
yathā "yāvaj-jīvam ahaṁ maunī" iti,+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Firstly, the proposition is not contradicted by its mere utterance,  
for the statement of the thesis "Pañcarātra Sastra is authoritative"  
does not cancel its own content, as does, for instance, the statement:  
"During my entire life I have kept silence." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Ślokavārtika (I. i. 5) śls. 61b-62b:

> tridhāśabda-virōdhas syāt prasiddhy-ādi-vibhāgataḥ ।  
pratijñā-pūrva-saṁjalpa-sarva-lōka-prasiddhitaḥ ॥  
yāvaj-jīvam ahaṁ maunīty ukti-mātrēṇa bādhyatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatra na tāvaduktimātraviruddhō'yaṁ pakṣaḥ,  
na hi pañcarātraśāstraṁ pramāṇamiti pratijñāvacanaṁ svārthaṁ vyāhanti yathā yāvajjīvamahaṁ maunī iti,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi dharmōkti-virōdhaḥ,  
**na** hi prāmāṇyaṁ  
pañca-rātrōddēśēna vidhīyamānaṁ pakṣaṁ **pratikṣipati**  
sarva-vākyānām iva mithyātva-vacanam,+++(5)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Secondly, there is no contradiction through utterance of property,  
as for example the statement: "All statements are untrue;"  
for the authoritativeness predicated of Pañcarātra  
does not cancel the proposition. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi dharmōktivirōdhaḥ, na hi prāmāṇyaṁ pañcarātrōddēśēna vidhīyamānaṁ pakṣaṁ pratikṣipati sarvavākyānāmiva mithyātvavacanam, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi dharmy-ukti-virōdhaḥ,  
saty api dharmiṇi,  
dharmānvayasyā'viruddhatvāt।   
na hi jananītvam iva vandhyātvēna  
pañca-rātra-śāstratvaṁ prāmāṇyēna viruddham, (p. 32)+++(5)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Thirdly, there is no contradiction through utterance of substance,  
since in the given substance a connection with the given property is not contradictory:  
Pancarātra is not contradicted by its property authoritativeness,  
as motherhood is contradicted by the property sterility. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. ibid*: śl. 63:

> sarva-vākya-mr̥ṣātvē tu dharmōktyaivātma-bādhanam ।  
dharmy-uktyāhaṁ yatō jātaḥ, sā vandhyā jananī mama ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi dharmyuktivirōdhaḥ, satyapi dharmiṇi dharmānvayasyā'viruddhatvāt, na hi jananītvamiva vandhyātvēna pañcarātraśāstratvaṁ prāmāṇyēna viruddham, (p. 32) 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hi vivādādhyāsitasya prāmāṇya-pratijñānē  
tatra śruty-ukta-dharmi-viśēṣa-virōdhaḥ -  
+++(vēda-)+++vihita-hiṁsānām ivādharmatva-pratijñānē +++(tat-tat-parihārēṇa)+++ vivādādhyāsasyōpalakṣatvāt,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For upon the assertion of the authoritativeness of the substance in question,  
it is not contradicted by any particular substance named in Revelation,  
since the imputation of questionableness is secondary,  
as in the case of the assertion that  
certain acts of violence which are enjoined are against the dharma,12  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

The Vedic injunction na hinṇsyāt sarvabhūtāni "one should not injure any being"  
raises the question of the validity of injunctions which do require injury to beings.  
But this is a secondary question which does not affect the validity of the Veda as a whole.  
Similarly, the thesis "Pañcaratra is valid" is not disproved  
by the possible mention in the valid Veda  
of something that conflicts with something in Pañcaratra.  
So far the argument is not for validity but against invalidity. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi vivādādhyāsitasya prāmāṇyapratijñānē tatra śrutyuktadharmiviśēṣavirōdhaḥ  
vihitahiṁsānāmivādharmatvapratijñānē vivādādhyāsasyōpalakṣatvāt,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atō vā nāgamavirōdhaḥ,  
tad ēvaṁ pratipannaḥ pakṣaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

There is, therefore, no contradiction by language statement;  
so that we conclude that the proposition is presentable. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atō vā nāgamavirōdhaḥ, tadēvaṁ pratipannaḥ pakṣaḥ ।  
</details>

## 03 hētu-sauṣṭhavam

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi hētōr anaikāntikatvādayō dōṣāḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

59\. Nor is the ground affected by logical defects, like occasional application etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide Tarkasaṅgraha (Vavilla edn.) Anumāna-section, P.52:

> savyabhicāra-viruddha-sat-prati-pakṣāsiddha-bādhitāḥ pañca-hētv-ābhāsāḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi hētōranaikāntikatvādayō dōṣāḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā hi na tāvad anaikāntikaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The ground is not occasionally applicable to other terms. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi na tāvadanaikāntikaḥ, 
</details>

### nānaikāntikaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sa hi dvēdhā sādhāraṇāsādhāraṇabhēdāt -  
yathā "pr̥thivī-nityatva-sādhanē pramēyatvaṁ" +++(ity anityēṣv api vartamānō hētuḥ)+++ sādhāraṇaḥ,  
asādhāraṇasya "tatraiva gandhavattvam" +++(ity anyatrādr̥śyamānō hētuḥ)+++,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[48]]  
This fallacy of occasionalness is of two kinds, general occasionalness and special occasionalness.  
An instance of the first kind provides the ground in the argument:  
"The earth is eternal, because it is knowable."  
Of the second kind: "The earth is eternal, because it, possesses smell." 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Since pots are knowable, the ground would also apply to prove the eternality of pots and all things that are knowable. 

Since only earth (as an element) possesses smell, this ground has no general applicability.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

A third variety of ‘anaikāntika’ is ‘anupasaṁhārin’ which the author does not enumerate here. Cf. Tarkasaṅgraha: P.53: ‘savyabhicārō 'naikāntikaḥ । sa tri-vidhaḥ — sādhāraṇāsādhāraṇānusaṁhāri-bhēdāt।’ Quoting the passage ‘na tāvad anaikāntikaḥ’ & c. in his Nyāyapariśuddhi [Deśika Granthamālā], P.130, Deśika says: “bādhitasya tu na pakṣa-dharmatvaṁ, nāpi vyāptir iti dūṣaṇa-dvaya-samuccayaḥ।”
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sa hi dvēdhā sādhāraṇāsādhāraṇabhēdāt  
yathā pr̥thivī nityatvasādhanē pramēyatvaṁ sādhāraṇaḥ,  
asādhāraṇasyatatraiva gandhavattvam,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Our ground, namely,  
'Pañcaratra is authoritative, because it produces faultless knowledge',  
does not apply equally whether it is authoritative or not,  
which would render the ground generally-occasional.126 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Like the ground "because it is knowable" which applies to things regardless of whether they are eternal or not.
</details>

#### na sādhāraṇatvāt
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatra na tāvan nirdōṣa-jñāna-kāraṇatvaṁ pramāṇāpramāṇa-sādhāraṇaṁ,  
yēna sādhāraṇānaikāntikaṁ syāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatra na tāvannirdōṣajñānakāraṇatvaṁ pramāṇāpramāṇasādhāraṇaṁ yēna sādhāraṇānaikāntikaṁ syāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hi nirddōṣa-jñānakāraṇatvam a-pramāṇa-bhūta--vipralambhaka-vacanādiṣu vipakṣēṣu dr̥ṣṭacaram ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For this ground, namely its being a cause of faultless knowledge,  
has not been found before in the alternative propositions  
that Pañcaratra is deceptive and hence nonauthoritative.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi nirddōṣajñānakāraṇatvamapramāṇabhūtavipralambhakavacanādiṣu vipakṣēṣu dr̥ṣṭacaram ।  
</details>

#### nāsādhāraṇatvāt
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpy asādhāraṇaḥ -  
+++(pāñcarātraṁ prāmāṇikaṁ nirdōṣa-jñāna-jananāt - jyōtiṣ-ṭōmādi-vākyavat ityatra)+++  
jyōtiṣ-ṭōmādi-vākya-dr̥ṣṭāntābhidhānēnaiva sa-pakṣānvayasya pradarśitatvāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Neither does the ground have a specially occasional application,  
because the illustration "like statements on Vedic sacrifices such as jyotiṣṭoma etc."  
shows its connection with other instances on the same side of the argument. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpyasādhāraṇaḥ jyōtiṣṭōmādivākyadr̥ṣṭāntābhidhānēnaiva sapakṣānvayasya pradarśitatvāt ।  
</details>
  
### na viruddhaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi viruddhaḥ,  
viparīta-vyāpty-abhāvāt,  
na hi nirdōṣa-jñāna-kāraṇatvam aprāmāṇyēna vyāptam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is the ground precluded,  
since there is no concomitance of its opposite; being a cause of faultless knowledge is not invariably accompanied by nonauthoritativeness.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

viparītēna sādhyābhāvēna vyāptiḥ viparīta-vyāptir iti tr̥tīyā-tatpuruṣaḥ । sā ca vyāptiḥ pañca-rātra-prāmāṇya-pratipādakē vākyē ‘nirdōṣa-jñāna-janmatva’-rūpasya hētōr nāstīty arthaḥ । ‘śabdō nityaḥ kr̥takatvāt’ ity atra kr̥takatva-rūpō hētuḥ sādhyābhāvēna nityatvābhāvēna anityatvēna hi vyāptaḥ, yatra kr̥takatvaṁ tatrānityatvam iti niyamāt । tasmāt sa hētur viruddhaḥ । ēvam atrāpīti bōdhyam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi viruddhaḥ, viparītavyāptyabhāvāt, na hi nirdōṣajñānakāraṇatvamaprāmāṇyēna vyāptam ।  
</details>

### na kālātyayaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca kālātyayāpadiṣṭaḥ -  
pratyakṣa-virōdhābhāvāt  
āgamānuguṇyāc ca ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is the ground cancelled by lapse of time,  
since there is no conflict with Perception  
and in this it is analogous with Scripture. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

kālātyayāpadiṣṭasyaiva ‘bādha’ ity api vyavahāraḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca kālātyayāpadiṣṭaḥ pratyakṣavirōdhābhāvāt āgamānuguṇyācca ।  
</details>

### nāsiddhaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na cāsiddhatvam,  
a-siddhir hi āśrayataḥ svarūpatō vā tāvad āśrayāsiddhiḥ,  
pañca-rātra-śāstrasyāśrayatvāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is the ground itself unproved or unestablished.  
If a ground is unestablished,  
this is because either its locus or its essence is unestablished.  
The first does not apply, for its locus is Pañicarātra Sastra, which is proved to exist. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

hētōr asiddhatā 'pi nāstīty arthaḥ । vyāpyatvāsiddhir ity anyō 'pi asiddhi-prakāraḥ śāstra-granthēṣu parigaṇyatē । sa tu nōdāhr̥tō grantha-kr̥tā ।

atra hētvābhāsēṣu pañcasu ‘anaikāntika-viruddha-kālātyayāpadiṣṭāsiddhā’ iti catvāra ēva prakārāḥ parigaṇitāḥ । anyaḥ prabhēdaḥ sat-prati-pakṣākhyaḥ na pratipāditō 'tra । ‘sādhyābhāvasādhakaṁ hētv-antaraṁ yasya sa sat-prati-pakṣa’ iti hi tal-lakṣaṇam । tādr̥śaṁ ca hētva-antaraṁ naiva sambhāvanā-bhūmir iti mahatā prabandhēna grantha-kārēṇa samanantaram ēva nirūpitam iti, na pr̥thag-uktir iti ca dhyēyam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cāsiddhatvam, asiddhirhi āśrayataḥ svarūpatō vā tāvadāśrayāsiddhiḥ, pañcarātraśāstrasyāśrayatvāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi sva-rūpāsiddhaḥ,  
sō'pi trēdhā - ajñāna-sandēha-viparyayabhēdāt,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor does the second apply:  
for there are three ways in which a ground may be unestablished as to its essence:  
through ignorance, through dubiety, or through reversion. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi svarūpāsiddhaḥ, sō'pi trēdhā ajñāna-sandēha-viparyayabhēdāt,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na tāvad a-jñānāsiddhiḥ,  
tat-pratipādaka-śabdōccāraṇāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Ignorance does not apply,  
as follows from the fact that the words describing the ground are pronounced.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Obviously, if the ground were not known, it could not be stated.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na tāvadajñānāsiddhiḥ, tatpratipādakaśabdōccāraṇāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi saṁdigdhāsiddhaḥ,  
nirdōṣatvasya vādinaḥ svayaṁ siddhatvāt,  
prativādinō 'pi dōṣānupalambhād ēvānāyāsa-siddhatvāt,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor does dubiety apply,  
for that the ground is correct is undoubted and self-evident to the defender of the proposition,  
while for the opponent the same is easily proved by the fact that no defects are apprehended in it. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi saṁdigdhāsiddhaḥ, nirdōṣatvasya vādinaḥ svayaṁ siddhatvāt, prativādinō'pi dōṣānupalambhādēvānāyāsasiddhatvāt,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

viparyayāsiddhistu dūrōtsāritaiva ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[49]]  
That the ground would be unestablished through reversal is utterly out of the question.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

viparyayāsiddhistu dūrōtsāritaiva ।  
</details>

### pauruṣēyasyāpi grāhyatā

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu kathaṁ pauruṣēyatva-sāmānyād āpatantī dōṣa-saṁbhāvanā apanīyatē 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

60\. OBJECTION. But how can we discard the supposition that the Pañcaratra texts are faulty?128  
This supposition arises instantly since the texts are of personal origin. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

This objection seems to speak to the summary denial that the ground is unestablished through reversion.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu kathaṁ pauruṣēyatvasāmānyādāpatantī dōṣasaṁbhāvanā apanīyatē 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pañcarātramantrāṇāṁ kathaṁ vākyatva-sāmānyād āpatantī vēdēṣu sā +++(dōṣasaṁbhāvanā)+++ vāryatē, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. How do you avoid the same supposition in the case of the Vedas?  
There too it arises instantly, since the Vedas are language-statements.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pañcarātramantrāṇāṁ kathaṁ vākyatvasāmānyādāpatantī vēdēṣu sā vāryatē, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

apauruṣēyatvād iti cēt  
tad ihāpi sarva-jñāvāpta-kāma--parama-puruṣa-praṇītatayēty avagamya śāmyatu bhavān ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

When you reply, it is avoided because the Vedas have no personal author,  
then you may realize that in our case, too, it is avoided, since the Tantras have been composed by the Supreme Person,  
who is omniscient and eternally satisfied,  
and you may keep quiet! 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

apauruṣēyatvāditi cēttadihāpi sarvajñāvāptakāmaparamapuruṣapraṇītatayētyavagamya śāmyatu bhavān ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ētaduktaṁ bhavati -  

naiva śabdē svatō dōṣāḥ  
prāmāṇya-paripanthinaḥ ।  
santi kintu svatas tasya  
pramāṇatvam iti sthitiḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

What I mean to say is this.  

Our position is that in language as such there are no defects that invalidate its authority;   
as language, language is authoritative, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Be it repeated that the validity, authoritativeness, etc. of Verbal Statements (ie, shabdapramāna) is founded on the basic assumption that statements truly and accurately communicate their things-meant (artha), that a word accurately conveys its meaning.  
Among these things meant Yamuna includes facts as well as karyas,  
hence the following debate with the Prabhakara,
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ētaduktaṁ bhavati -  

naiva śabdē svatō dōṣāḥ prāmāṇyaparipanthinaḥ ।  
santi kintu svatastasya pramāṇatvamiti sthitiḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vaktur āśaya-dōṣēṇa  
kēṣucit tad **apōdyatē** ।  
aṅguly-agrē **'sti** mātaṅga-  
yūtham ity-ēvam-ādiṣu ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Its authority is in certain cases invalidated by defects in the character of the speaker,  
for instance in a language statement,  
"There is a herd of elephants on my finger-tip." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Prakaraṇapañcikā: II. 4, P.13:

> vināpy arthaṁ hi śabdēna pratītir upajāyatē ।  
aṅguly agrē 'sti kariṇāṁ yūtham ity ēvam ādinā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vakturāśayadōṣēṇa kēṣucittadapōdyatē ।  
aṅgulyagrē'sti mātaṅgayūthamityēvamādiṣu ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

prastuta-grantha-sandarbhē  
vaktur āśaya-gāminīm ।  
dōṣa-śaṅkāṁ trayī-mūrdha-  
dhvanir **ēvāpamārṣṭi** naḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The statements in the upanisad portion of the Veda  
remove whatever suspicion we may have  
about any defects in the character of the speaker in the text collection here under discussion.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

prastutagranthasaṁdarbhē vakturāśayagāminīm ।  
dōṣaśaṅkāṁ trayīmūrddhadhvanirēvāpamārṣṭi naḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vadanti khalu vēdāntāḥ  
sarvajñaṁ jagataḥ patim ।  
mahākāruṇikaṁ tasmin  
+++(vañcana=)+++vipralambhādayaḥ katham ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For the Vedanta texts set forth that the omniscient Lord of the world is supremely compassionate;  
then how can we suppose Him to be deceitful etc.? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Deśika, in his Stotraratnabhāṣya (Deśika Granthamālā), P.37, says that the mercy of the Lord is referred to in the following Upaniṣads:

Śvetāśvatara : III. 17 : ‘sarvasya prabhum īśānaṁ sarvasya śaraṇaṁ suhr̥t’;
Kaṭhavalli : IV. 12a : ‘aṅguṣṭha-mātraḥ puruṣō madhya ātmani tiṣṭhati’ and
Mahopaniṣat : 1 : ‘sa ēkākī na ramēta’

Also cf. Paramasaṁhitā : III. 40b-41a; P.24:

> dhyātavyō bhagavān ēva nānyō viśvasya kāraṇāt ।  
svāmitvēna gurutvēna suhr̥ttvēna ca sarvadā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vadanti khalu vēdāntāḥ sarvajñaṁ jagataḥ patim ।  
mahākāruṇikaṁ tasmin vipralambhādayaḥ katham ॥
</details>

## 04 siddha-vastuni śabda-prāmāṇyam

### pratijñā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu ca   
> 
> siddhē vastuni śabdānāṁ  
prāmāṇyaṁ nētyavādiṣam ।  
tat-parēṣu prayōgēṣu  
vyutpatty-agrahaṇād iti ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

61\. OBJECTION.  
However, I have said that language statements have no authority  
when they concern established facts,  
on the ground that when terms are applied to such facts  
they do not have proper denotative power. 

[[50]] 

</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This is the view of the Prābhākara.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu ca ।  
siddhē vastuni śabdānāṁ prāmāṇyaṁ nētyavādiṣam ।  
tatparēṣu prayōgēṣu vyutpattyagrahaṇāditi ॥  

</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad asat siddham apy artham  
**ācakṣāṇāḥ** prayōgataḥ ।  
laukikāḥ **pratipadyantēḥ**  
śaktiṁ, kārya-parād iva ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION.  
This view is not correct, language, eliciting a fact by direct application,  
even though this fact is established,  
really operates its denoting power  
as fully as it does  
by applications which concern karyas.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This is the reply given by the Siddhāntin.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadasatsiddhamapyarthamācakṣāṇāḥ prayōgataḥ ।  
laukikāḥ pratipadyantēḥ śaktiṁ kāryaparādiva ॥
</details>

### putra-janmōdāharaṇam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad yathā "putras tē jāta"  
iti vacana-śravaṇānantara-janita-viśiṣṭa-vadana-**vikāsāvasāna**-samanantaraṁ  
'hr̥ṣṭō'yam' iti **pratipadya**  
"harṣō'yaṁ priyārthāvagama-nibandhana" iti svātmany **ākalayan**  
madhyama-vr̥ddhasyāpi tan-nibandhanam ēva harṣam **anumimānas**  
tad-bhāva-bhāvitayā śabdasyaiva priyārthā'vabōdhakatām **avyavasyati** ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Consider the illustration that has been given above (supra § 37.),  
When certain manifestations (of joy) in a man's face,  
which follow on his hearing the statement  
"A son has been born to you,"  
make it appear that the man spoken-to is happy,  
one instantly understands  
that his happiness is the result of his receiving from this statement  
a knowledge of an agreeable meaning,  
and one then infers that,  
for a medium-aged person too,  
this happiness derives from the statement.  
Thus one concludes that,  
since this happiness came to exist upon the existence of the statement,  
the statement itself has the power to convey an agreeable meaning.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadyathā putrastē jāta iti vacanaśravaṇānantarajanitaviśiṣṭavadanavikāsāvasānasamanantaraṁ hr̥ṣṭō'yamiti pratipadya harṣō'yaṁ priyārthāvagamanibandhana iti svātmanyākalayan madhyamavr̥ddhasyāpi tannibandhanamēva harṣamanumimānastadbhāvabhāvitayā śabdasyaiva priyārthā'vabōdhakatāmavyavasyati ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatrāpy 

> atītānāgatādi-bhēda-bhinnēṣu harṣa-hētuṣūpaplavamānēṣu  
kasya vaktā'yam 

iti vicikitsōdayē sati -  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If there arises a doubt as to 

> which particular ground of happiness  
amongst the many different grounds that may occur according to past, present and future, then consider this.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatrāpyatītānāgatādibhēdabhinnēṣu harṣahētuṣūpaplavamānēṣu kasya vaktā'yamiti vicikitsōdayē sati   
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

(tad-anantara-saṁjāta--jāta-karmāvabōdhataḥ ।  )
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

(A young boy, who wants to understand the meaning of speech, immediately upon hearing the same statement  
receives knowledge that a birth ceremony is being held. )
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadanantarasaṁjātajātakarmāvabōdhataḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

(tad-antara-sañjātaṁ  
jñāpakam **anviṣyataḥ** ।  
tad-anubhūtaḥ kō 'pīti  
bhinna-vastrābharaṇam purā ॥)  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad-antara-sañjātaṁ jñāpakam anviṣyataḥ¹ ।  
tad-anubhūtaḥ kō 'pīti bhinna-vastrābharaṇam² purā³ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"tad-dhētu-bhūtaḥ kō'pī"ti  
niścinvann ātmanaḥ purā ॥  
"**kartavyaṁ** jāta-karmē"ti  
pratītēḥ kin nu kāraṇam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

He thinks to himself, "There must be a reason for this."  
Then he considers,  
"Is the agreeable meaning which has been understood from the statement the cause of this knowledge that a birth ceremony is to be held ?"  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

taddhētubhūtaḥ kō'pīti niścinvannātmanaḥ purā ॥  
kartavyaṁ jātakarmēti pratītēḥ kinnu kāraṇam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pratītaṁ priyam ity ēvaṁ  
**vimr̥śann avagacchati** ॥  
putra-janmaiva naivānyad  
iti **vyutpitsur** arbhakaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and he realizes that this meaning was precisely this that a son had been born. 13 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Yamuna here takes up the Prabhakara's theory that a child learns the meaning of language  
through the action his elders take on hearing a statement,  
so that the denotativeness of language is defined by its injunctiveness.  
He uses the Prabhakara's example of the factual statement: 
"A child is born to you."  
A child who does not know language has no way of understanding the meaning of this statement  
because the young father's happiness conveys nothing specific.  

But, asks Yamuna, suppose the same child has witnessed his father reception of the cheering news  
and the subsequent preparations for a birth ceremony.  
Since one follows immediately upon the other,  
the child associates one with the other  
and can thus understand the meaning of the statement,  
though the statement itself was no injunction,  
but a communication of an established fact,
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pratītaṁ priyamityēvaṁ vimr̥śannavagacchati ॥  
putrajanmaiva nivānyaditi vyutpitsurarbhakaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatra ca -  

+++(nānā-vākyēṣu)+++ āvāpōddhāra-bhēdēna  
padānāṁ śakti-**niścayaḥ** ।  
**upapadyata** ity ēvaṁ  
siddhāsiddhārtha-vācitā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And on that issue:  
Definite knowledge of the denotion of words in a sentence is had through the words that are included or excluded. This being so, [51] words denote their meanings, whether these are established things or not.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatra ca ।  
āvāpōddhārabhēdēna padānāṁ śaktiniścayaḥ ।  
upapadyata ityēvaṁ siddhāsiddhārthavācitā ॥
</details>

### vidhi-pakṣē'py āvāpōdvāpakramaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu na tad-bhāva-bhāvitā-mātrēṇa kārya-kāraṇa-bhāvaḥ,  
ati prasaṅgāt।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[51]]

> 62\. OBJECTION. However, the relation of cause and effect is not just known from the fact that one comes into existence upon the existence of the other, for that would mean over-extension. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu na tad-bhāva-bhāvitā-mātrēṇa kārya-kāraṇa-bhāvaḥ, ati prasaṅgāt।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na ca jāta-karma-kartavyatā'vagatir niyamēna priyārthāvagama-purassarī, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Nor does the realization that a birth ceremony is to be held follow invariably upon the knowledge of an agreeable meaning; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca jāta-karma-kartavyatā'vagatir niyamēna priyārthāvagama-purassarī, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> dr̥śyatē hi kuṭumba-bharaṇāyāsa-vidūyamāna-manasō 'prīti-pūrvikāpi tat-kartavyatāvagatiḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> for we find also that the same realization follows upon a feeling of distress, namely when the informed father is vexed by the trouble of maintaining his family.132
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[132]: Then, one may suppose, the child would not so readily associate the birth ceremony with the previous commueniation.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

dr̥śyatē hi kuṭumba-bharaṇāyāsa-vidūyamāna-manasō'prīti-pūrvikāpi tat-kartavyatāvagatiḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kāryāvagatiḥ kiṁ śabda-kāraṇikā dr̥ṣṭā  
yēna "gām ānayē"ty ādau  
gav-ānayanādi-kartavyatā'vagatiḥ śabda-kāraṇikā 'bhyupēyatē। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. Don't we find that the realization of a kārya is caused by a verbal statement, so that we can agree that, for example, the realization that a cow is to be fetched following a statement "Fetch the cow" is indeed caused by that statement? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kāryāvagatiḥ kiṁ śabda-kāraṇikā dr̥ṣṭā yēna gām-ānayēty ādau gavānayanādi-kartavyatāvagatiḥ śabda-kāraṇikā'bhyupēyatē। 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha 

> ākasmikatvānupapattēḥ  
sannihita-śabda ēva tad-avagama-hētur 

iti cēt
