samānō'yaṁ vidhir itaratrāpi।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

When you say that, since this realization cannot occur without a cause therefore the proximate statement must in that case be the cause of the realization, then I maintain that the same holds also in the case of "A son is born."
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ākasmika ... kāraṇaṁ vinā kāryaṁ na jāyata iti hētōḥ ।

"vidhiḥ" nyāya ity arthaḥ ।
<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha ākasmikatvānupapattēḥ sannihita-śabda ēva tad-avagama-hētur iti cēt samānō'yaṁ vidhir itaratrāpi।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

yāpi pravr̥tti-hētv-artha-  
pratipādakatā kvacit।  
liṅ-ādi-pratyayāvāpa-  
haitukī sā'vasīyatē +++(pratipakṣiṇā)+++॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It has been decided by our opponent that the verbal denotation of a meaning which causes an action to be taken is a result of the inclusion in the statement of a liṅādi suffix.133 

[133]: supra §36.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

pravr̥tti-hētuḥ kāryam; tad-rūupō 'rthaḥ; tat-pratipādakatā liṅādīnām ity anvayaḥ ।

āvāpaḥ prayōga iti yāvat।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yāpi pravr̥tti-hētv-artha-pratipādakatā kvacit।  
liṅādi-pratyayāvāpa-haitukī sā'vasīyatē॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

yaś ca kārya-paratām ēvākhila-padānām ātiṣṭhatē, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

He who maintains that all words only bear meaningfully on kārya, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yaś ca kārya-paratām ēvākhila-padānām ātiṣṭhatē, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tēnāpy-āvāpōddhāra-vinirdhāritāsaṁsr̥ṣṭa-śarīrāṇām ēva gavāśvādīnāṁ tat-tat-padārthatā samarthanīyā, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

maintains in effect that padārthas134 exist only in kārya statements and that e.g. in the case of cows, horses and the like, which are related to bodies, their being a padārtha is ascertained by the inclusion or exclusion of the words denoting them in a statement concerning kārya. 

[134]: The things-meant or denoted by the word,
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

vinirdhāritā ... āvāpōddhāraiḥ vinirdhāritaṁ kāryam । tad-asaṁsr̥ṣṭa-śarīrāṇām ity anvayaḥ ।

gavāśvādīnāṁ ... śuddha-gavāśvādi-padānām ।

tat-tat-padārthatā, kāryānanvitō 'py arthaḥ ।

</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tēnāpy-āvāpōddhāra-vinirdhāritāsaṁsr̥ṣṭa-śarīrāṇām ēva gavāśvādīnāṁ tat-tat-padārthatā samarthanīyā, 
</details>

### na kāryānvitābhidhāna-mātram
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> samarthyamānā 'pi kāryānvayiny ēva samarthyata 

iti cēt  
alaṁ vyasanēna -  
anyānvitābhidhānēnāpi vyavahārōpapattēḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If he says, indeed, whenever their being a padārtha is significantly construed, it is construed just as connected with kārya, we reply,  
Stop being obstinate; for verbal exchange is also possible through denotation of words that are connected with other things than kāryas.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

bhāṭṭa-matē padēnārthaḥ; tēna jāti-mātrasya bōdha ity abhyupagamaḥ । anvitābhidhānaṁ nōrarīkriyatē ।

</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

samarthyamānāpi kāryānvayiny ēva samarthyata iti cēt alaṁ vyasanēna anyānvitābhidhānēnāpi vyavahārōpapattēḥ।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

avaśyāśrayaṇīyēyam  
anvitārthābhidhāyitā।  
kāryānvitābhidhāyitvam  
anyathā dur-vacaṁ yataḥ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

63\. It is necessary to accept the position that words are denotative of connected meanings, for otherwise it would be impossible to explain that they are denotative of meanings connected with kāryas. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

avaśyāśrayaṇīyēyam ... Yāmuna emphasises here that no speciality should be attached to a statement that speaks of something to be done (kārya). Words, he says, generally depend upon some factors and those factors need not necessarily be ‘kārya’. Pointing out the untenability of the theory of ‘kārya’, he says that it goes astray in the instance of ‘liṅ’ the optative itself. Even the ‘liṅ’—suffix is found to depend upon a host of factors like the qualified aspirant (adhikārin), the means (sādhana) and the thing to be attained (sādhya). *Cf*. the following verse:

> tasmādākāṅkṣitāsannayogyārthāntarasaṅgate ।  
svārthe padānāṁ vyutpattirāstheyā sarvavādibhiḥ॥

Words convey their sense only in connection with such other idea or factor that is required to complete its sense (ākāṅkṣita), that is compatible with it (yogya) and which is supplied by a word uttered along with it (āsanna). Kārya should therefore occupy a subordinate but not the supreme position in the scheme of significance of words.

durvadaṁ ... [[??]]

</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> avaśyāśrayaṇīyēyam anvitārthābhidhāyitā।  
> kāryānvitābhidhāyitvam anyathā dur-vacaṁ(durvadaṁ) yataḥ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

avyāptañ caitat 

> kāryānvitam ēva sarvatra padābhidhēyam  

iti - liṅ-ādiṣu vyabhicārāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The definition 'the thing meant by a word is always connected with a kārya' fails to cover the defined topic completely;  
for it does not apply in the case of injunctive suffixes, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

liṅā sākṣāt kāryam ucyata iti cēt, liṅi kārya-paratvaṁ nāstīti vyabhicāraḥ । liṅ kāryam ēva sākṣāt, na tu kārya-param iti dhyēyam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

avyāptañcaitat kāryānvitamēva sarvatra padābhidhēyamiti liṅādiṣu vyabhicārāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

+++("svargakāmō jyōtiṣṭōmēna yajētē"ti yathā )+++  
liṅ-ādayō hi +++(svargakāmanā yājakē←)+++ pariniṣṭhitādhikārādy-anubandha-saṁbandhinam ēva svārtham abhidadhati ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

since these suffixes denote their own meanings as connected, not with kārya, but with consequences of already established facts, such as proper qualification on the part of the person enjoined etc.135 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[135]: Yamuna's argument is that the injunctive, etc. terminations of the verb denote the injunction as their thing meant (padārtha); but what makes this injunction 'meaningful' is not that it is an injunction, but that it is connected with someone who is qualified to accept the injunction, e.g., in the injunction svargakāmo yajeta. The injunctive yajeta has no meaning or purpose unless there is a "desire for heaven;"  the meaning of the injunction thus is connected with the consequence of this desire is  prepared to do something about it.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

sambandhinamēva ... adhikāraḥ phala-svāmyam — svarga-kāmādi-padōktam ।

svārtham ... svārthaṁ kāryam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

liṅādayō hi pariniṣṭhitādhikārādy-anubandha-saṁbandhinam ēva svārtham abhidadhati ।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

atha 

> tēṣv anvitābhidhānam  
itaratra kāryānvitābhidhānam 

iti cēt  
tad-arddhajaratīyam, tatō varaṁ sarvatrānvitābhidhānam ēvāśrīyatām ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or if it is said that in their case there is denotation of connected meanings and in the other case denotation of meanings connected with kārya, we reply that this is a neither old nor young, argument;136  
it is more appropriate simply to accept the view that there is denotation of connected meanings in general.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[136]: ardhajaratī is a half-old woman; the ardhajaratīyanyāya is used to indicate that the opponent wants to have it both ways and that consequently his argument, like a half-old and half-young woman, is useless either way.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

tēṣu liṅādiṣu ।

jaratīyam ... For an explanation of the ardhajaratī-nyāya see Nyāyasūdhā under I. iii. 3. P.135: 

> kēnacit pāśupatēna sarva-jaratyā yōṣitō 'nupabhōgyatvāt, sarva-taruṇyāś ca vr̥ddhē 'py aruci-prasaṅgāt ardha-jaratyānayanē dūtaḥ prēṣita iti lōka-pravādō 'rdha-jaratī-śabdē ।

Also cf. Bhuvaneśalaukikanyāyasāhasrī, P.104: 

> yatra sarva-tyāgē grahaṇē vā prasaktē, kiñcid niryuktikam ēkāṁśōpādānam aṁśāntara-tyāgaś ca kriyatē tatrāyaṁ nyāyō 'vatarati — yathā jaratī vr̥ddhā strī, tasyāḥ patiḥ tad-ardhaṁ guṇa-mātraṁ gr̥hṇāti hy avayavāntaraṁ tyajatīti yukti-śūnyam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha tēṣv anvitābhidhānam itaratra kāryānvitābhidhānam iti cēt tad-arddhajaratīyam, tatō varaṁ sarvatrānvitābhidhānam ēvāśrīyatām ।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tasmād ākāṅkṣitāsanna-  
yōgyārthāntara-saṅgatēḥ ।  
svārthē padānāṁ vyutpattir  
**āsthēyā** sarva-vādibhiḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

64\. Therefore, the adherents of all schools should accept that words have proper denotation for the meanings they denote because these meanings are connected with other meanings that are required to complete the sense of the statement, are closely collocated and are appropriate. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yōgyārthāntara-saṅgatē svārtha ēva pada-vyutpattiḥ । ētēna padānāṁ yat kiñcid arthānvayaḥ nirastō vēditavyaḥ । arthānāṁ viśiṣṭa-bōdhakatvaṁ svābhāvyam iti bhāṭṭaḥ । śabdasyaiva sambandha-bōdhakatvaṁ, nārthasyēti prābhākarāḥ । tatrāha - 'tasmād' ity-ādinā ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasmād ākāṅkṣitāsannayōgyārthāntarasaṅgatēḥ ।  
svārthē padānāṁ vyutpattir āsthēyā sarvavādibhiḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

+++("tuṣyatu durjana" iti)+++ yady api +++("gām ānayē"ti →)+++ pravr̥tty-anupapatti-samadhigamanīyaiva  
śabda-śaktis, tathā'pi -
</details>

<details><summary>En - viśvāsaḥ</summary>

Even if the denoting power of word is to be known only through the impossibility of operation,  
even so
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Even if the denoting power of language were to be understood only through its proper signification in kārya statements alone,137  
even so 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[137]: Misra's text here has yady api vṛttyanupapattisamadhigamanīyaiva śabdaśaktis "the denoting power of language is to be known only through the impossibility of operation,"  which makes no sense. The reading must be corrupt, in anu papatti we may find a corruption of vyutpati,in pravṛtti perhaps a corruption of kāryārthe or kāryārtha-.  I read conjecturally kāryārtha vyutpattisamadhi gamanīyaiva, which gives the required sense.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘tuṣyatu durjana’-nyāyēnā''ha ‘yady apī'ti । pravr̥ttir gavānayanādiṣu । tasyā anyathā 'nupapattyā prathamaṁ śabda-śaktir abhyupēyā ।

</details>

### vyutpanna-prayōgē kāryānapēkṣā
<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yady api pravr̥tty-anupapatti-samadhigamanīyaiva śabdaśaktis tathā'pi -
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

taṭasthōpāyatā-mātraṁ  
śabda-śakti-viniścayē ।  
**kāryasyāśrayituṁ yuktaṁ**  
prayōktr-ākāśa-dēśavat ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

it is correct when we decide the denotation of language to take the standpoint that kārya is just one of the inessential factors of denotation, like the identity of the speaker, the extent of space in which a statement can be heard etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

prēraka-puruṣasya, ākāśasya, dēśasya vā kvacid api viṣaya-kōṭi-praviṣṭatvaṁ nā'bhyupēyatē, taṭasthatvam ēva ।  
ēvaṁ kāryasyāpīti dhyēyam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

taṭasthōpāyatāmātraṁ śabda-śakti-viniścayē ।  
kāryasyāśrayituṁ yuktaṁ prayōktr-ākāśa-dēśavat ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

ananya-labhyaś śabdārtha  
iti nyāya-vidas sthitāḥ ।  
tasmān nōpāya-bhūtasya  
kāryasyāsti samanvayaḥ ॥  
vyutpanna-vyavahārēṣu +++(→dharaṇē ratnēṣu)+++  
payaḥ-prataraṇādivat ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The logicians hold the view that the meaning of a language statement cannot be known except by language statement.138 Consequently, there exists no inherent relationship with kārya as cause of denotation in uses of words that have their proper signification,  
just as is the case with floating precious stones on water. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes </summary>

[138]: This holds for those statements which are not verifiable by other means of knowledge, for if they are verifiable, they are no incans of knowledge in their own right.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ananyalabhyaḥ ... ‘śabdārthaḥ’ śabda-śakti-gōcara ity arthaḥ । sa ēva śabdasyārthaḥ; yaḥ prakārāntarēṇa na labhyatē । “gaṅgāyāṁ ghōṣa” ity atra gaṅgā-padasya pravāha-rūpārtha-mātrē śakti-svīkārē, tat-sambandhāt tīram api labhyatē । ēvaṁ lakṣaṇayā prakārāntarēṇāpi tīra-lābhān na tatra śakti-svīkāraḥ । ata ēva jāti-mātrē śaktiḥ; vyaktēr ākṣēpād ēva siddhēḥ ।

Cf. Bhuvaneśalaukikanyāyasāhasrī, P.243.

payaḥprataraṇādivat ... Vide Ratnaśāstra of Buddhabhaṭa, śl. 39:

> yat tu sarvair guṇair yuktaṁ vajraṁ tarati vāriṇi ।  
ratnānāṁ samastē 'pi tasya dhāraṇam iṣyatē ॥

The quality of gems is tested by putting them in water. If they float, that is an indication of their superiority. This method of testing or the knowledge regarding the test is no doubt useful in determining the class of gems; but it is of no avail at the time of wearing them. On this analogy, it is argued that the knowledge of 'kārya' though useful to arrive at the significance of words, is not useful at the time of using those words.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ananyalabhyaś śabdārtha iti nyāyavidas sthitāḥ ।  
tasmān nōpāyabhūtasya kāryasyāsti samanvayaḥ ॥  
vyutpanna-vyavahārēṣu payaḥprataraṇādivat ।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

yathaiva hi brahma-jātīyādi-vajra-viśēṣāvadhāraṇōpayōginō'pi payaḥ-prataraṇādēr avadhr̥ta-ratna-sattvasya  
na vyavahāra-daśāyām upayōgaḥ,  
ēvaṁ vyutpatti-grahaṇa-samaya-samupayuktasyāpi kāryasya  
na vyutpanna-daśāyām upayōgaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Just as this floating, however helpful it may be to determine the identity of certain diamonds, e.g. the brahmin diamond, serves no purpose when a stone is being transacted which has already been properly identified, similarly the kārya, however helpful to understand the proper signification of a word, serves no purpose once its proper signification has been identified.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yathaiva ... For a classification of gems as 'male' and 'female', see Ratnadīpikā of Caṇḍeśvara, Śls. 11-13, and for a classification into the four castes 'brāhmana', 'kṣatriya', 'vaiśya' and 'śūdra' see Ratnaśāstra : śls. 21 and 23.

‘vyavahāra-daśā’-padēna, dhāraṇa-samayō vivakṣitaḥ ।

</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathaiva hi brahmajātīyādivajraviśēṣāvadhāraṇōpayōginō'pi payaḥ-prataraṇādēr avadhr̥ta-ratna-sattvasya na vyavahāradaśāyām upayōgaḥ, ēvaṁ vyutpatti-grahaṇa-samaya-samupayuktasyāpi kāryasya na vyutpannadaśāyām upayōgaḥ ॥
</details>

### nadī-tīra-phalam
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

yadi ca kāryānvitam ēvārthaṁ śabdāḥ pratipādayanti kathaṁ tēbhyaḥ pariniṣṭhita-nadī-tīra-phalādisaṁsargāvagamaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[53]]

65\. Moreover, if words denote their meanings only as connected with kārya, then how can we know from them that, for example, there is a relation between a fruit and a river-bank, as in a statement : "There is a fruit on the river-bank?" 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi ca kāryānvitam ēvārthaṁ śabdāḥ pratipādayanti kathaṁ tēbhyaḥ pariniṣṭhita-nadī-tīra-phalādisaṁsargāvagamaḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> nāyaṁ mukhyō lākṣaṇika 

iti cēt kva vā śabdānāṁ mukhya-prayōgaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If you say that a statement of such a substantive relation does not denote the relation it states through its primary sense, but through secondary sense, then, we may ask, where do statements then have their primary sense? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāyaṁ mukhyō lākṣaṇika iti cēt kva vā śabdānāṁ mukhya-prayōgaḥ ।
</details>

### mānāntarānapēkṣā
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> +++(śabdānāṁ mukhya-prayōgaḥ)+++ mānāntarāpūrvē+++(←tēna na sādhyam ity "apūrvam")+++ kārya 

iti cēn na -  
tatrāvyutpannatvēna prayōgānupapattēḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If you answer 

> in a kārya which is not previously known through other means of knowledge, 

we reply: no, for then no use of words would be possible, since their meaning would not yet have been identified. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

138: This holds for those statements which are not verifiable by other means of knowledge, for if they are verifiable, they are no means of knowledge in their own right.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

mānāntarāpūrvē ... Cf. Prakaraṇapañcikā II. P.187:

> kriyādi-bhinnaṁ yat kāryaṁ vēdyaṁ mānāntarair na tat ।  
atō mānāntarāpūrvam apūrvam iti gīyatē ॥

avyutpannatvēna ... śabdasyēti śēṣaḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

mānāntarāpūrvē kārya iti cēn na tatrāvyutpannatvēna prayōgānupapattēḥ ।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

na hi mānāntarāpūrvē+++(←tēna na sādhyam ity apūrvam)+++  
vyutpattir upapadyatē ।  
na cāvyutpanna-śabdēbhyaḥ  
pratyayō'tiprasaṅgataḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Naturally there can be no knowledge of the meaning of a word  
when that word denotes a meaning not previously known through other means of knowledge,  
and no cognition can arise from words with unknown meanings,  
for that would entail over-extension.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi mānāntarāpūrvē vyutpattir upapadyatē ।  
na cāvyutpanna-śabdēbhyaḥ pratyayō'tiprasaṅgataḥ ॥
</details>

### apūrvē śaktiḥ
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

yō'pi manyatē 

> lōkē kriyā+++(-rūpa)+++-kāryē vyutpanna-śabdaḥ +++(←"yajēta")+++  

</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[54]]

> 66\. OBJECTION. My position is this.  
In ordinary language a statement is understood to have its proper signification  
when it bears on a kārya that is to be accomplished with a certain action.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Yāmuna here attacks the theory advanced by the Prābhakaras that the words uttered by human beings gain validity only on inferential evidence because those beings are liable to defects. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yō'pi manyatē 

> lōkē kriyā-kāryē vyutpanna-śabdaḥ  
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> +++(śabdaḥ)+++ phala-pada-samabhivyāhāra--bala-pratilabdha-- tat-sādhana-bhāva-bhaṅgura-yāgādi-dhātv-arthōttīrṇa-  +apūrva+++(-rūpa)+++-kāryābhidhāna-śaktir vēdē mōdatē,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> In Vedic language a statement enjoys a special power of denotation  
which transcends the transitory root-sense of the word "sacrificing ",  
and it has this power of denotation  
because it is the means of realizing a certain fruit  
and acquires this power on account of the collocation of words describing this fruit;  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'phala-padaṁ' phala-vācakaṁ svarga-kāmādi-padam । tat-sādhana-bhāvaḥ svarga-sādhanatvaṁ apūrvasyēty arthaḥ । dhātv-arthōtīrṇaṁ, dhātv-arthātiriktam । 

vēdē ... ‘phala-pada...śaktiḥ’ ity ayaṁ bahu-vrīhiḥ । ‘śabda’ ity asya viśēṣaṇam ।

mōdatē ... vēdē nirvr̥tta iti bhāvaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> phala-pada-samabhivyāhāra--bala-pratilabdha-- tat-sādhana-bhāva-bhaṅgura-yāgādi- dhātv-arthōttīrṇāpūrva-kāryābhidhāna-śaktir vēdē mōdatē,  
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> lōkē tu saṁ-mugdhēnāpi[1] vyavahārōpapattēr  
na śabdārtha-tattvāvadhāraṇam ādriyatē 

iti -
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> whereas in ordinary language,  
since there verbal exchange is possible also to the unsophisticated,  
this determination of the nature of word and meaning is not attended to.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘kriyā-kāryē śaktir lōkē 'py astī’ti bhrāntaḥ puruṣa iti bhāvaḥ ।

Cf. Prakaraṇapañcikā V. P.95:

> kathaṁ tarhi laukika-vākyēbhyō vyavahāra-pravr̥ttiḥ ? ucyatē — artha-saṁśayēnāpi lōkō vyavaharati । sandigdhāyām api vr̥ṣṭau vr̥ṣṭy-āyatta-phalē karmaṇi pravartēntē ।

</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

lōkē tu saṁ-mugdhēnāpi[1] vyavahārōpapattēr na śabdārtha-tattvāvadhāraṇam ādriyatē iti ।
(samamugdhēnēti pā.)
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tasyāpīdaṁ manōratha-mātram, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. This position is just wishful thinking; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasyāpīdaṁ manōratha-mātram, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

na hi kriyā+++(-rūpa)+++-kāryē vyutpannaḥ +++("yajēta"-śabdaḥ)+++  
sthāyi+++(-apūrva-rūpa)+++-kāryaṁ pratipādayati - ati-prasaṅgāt । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for a language statement,  
even if understood in your way as bearing meaningfully only on a kārya to be accomplished with an action,139  
does not by that token set forth a permanent kārya,140  
since that would mean over-extension. 

</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[139]: read na hi kriyakārye vyut pannaḥ sthāyi kāryaṃ.

[140]: sthāyi; the Prābhākara view is that the kārya has a lasting efficacy beyond the inevitably transient action it involves; for the kārya must remain in order to effect the fruit of the action at any time after the completion of the action. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

vyutpannaḥ ... śabda iti śēṣaḥ । 

atiprasaṅgāt ... ghaṭa-jñānāt paṭa-jñānam api bhavēd ity āpattiḥ । 

</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi kriyā-kāryē vyutpanna(ḥ) sthāyi-kāryaṁ pratipādayati ati-prasaṅgāt । 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

yadi vr̥ddha-vyavahārē samadhigata-pada-sāmarthyē 'nurudhyamānē  
'nvayāvagatir +++('svargakāma'padasya)+++ nōpapadyatē, mōpapādi। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If we cannot know the true connection of words  
even when the usage of our elders,  
through which the denotations of these words is understood,  
takes place in accordance with these words,  
then we can never know their connection!  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

anvayāvagatiḥ ‘svarga-kāma’ padasyēti śēṣaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi vr̥ddha-vyavahārē samadhigata-pada-sāmarthyē 'nurudhyamānē 'nvayāvagatir nōpapadyatē, mōpapādi। 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

na tu tad-anupapattyā  
kl̥pta-śakti-parityāgēna śabda-śakty-antaraṁ bhajatē । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If a language statement has lost its postulated true denoting power  
because it is impossible,  
it does not thereby acquire another denoting power. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na tu tad-anupapattyā kl̥pta-śakti-parityāgēna śabda-śaktyantaraṁ bhajatē । 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

kāmaṁ lakṣaṇā'śrīyatām ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In such cases we surely must assume lakṣaṇā.141 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[141]: Yāmuna objects that we cannot have two altogether different denoting powers in langauge, one to convey a transitory thing, another to convey a non-transitory thing. The only possible explanation is that of lakṣaṇa "figurative usage," which remains related to the mukhyā vṛttiḥ "principal usage." But he will deny the entire construction (67).
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kāmaṁ lakṣaṇā'śrīyatām 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

na hi +++('siṁhō māṇavakaḥ', 'agnirmāṇavakaḥ' ityādiprayōgēṣu)+++ viruddhārtha-pada-samabhivyāhārē  
padānām abhidhānam ēvānyathā nīyatē,  
sarva-śabdārthēṣv anāśvāsa-prasaṅgāt ।+++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For when certain words are collocated that have incompatible meanings, these words do not therefore denote something else altogether, for then all word meanings would become unreliable.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'siṁhō māṇavakaḥ', 'agnir māṇavakaḥ' ity-ādi-prayōgēṣu । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi viruddhārtha-pada-samabhivyāhārē padānām abhidhānam ēvānyathā nīyatē, sarva-śabdārthēṣv anāśvāsa-prasaṅgāt ।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

kiṁ ca mānāntarāpūrva+++(←tēna na sādhyam ity apūrvam)+++-  
+++(-rūpa-)+++kārya-bōdhana-śaktatā ।  
na karma-phala-sambandha-  
siddhyai tāvad upēyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

67\. Besides, we do not admit that the fact that a word has the power to communicate a kārya that is not previously known through other means of knowledge proves that there actually exists a relationship between itself and the fruit of the action it enjoins. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

mānāntarāpūrvaṁ = pramāṇāntarēṇājñātaṁ apūrvam; tad-rūpaṁ kāryam ity anvayaḥ । 

na karmaphala ... karmaṇō yāgādēḥ, phalēna svargādinā sambandhaḥ । tat-sidhy-arthaṁ mānāntarājñātasya kāryasya bōdhakatā padānāṁ nābhyupēyā । apūrvasya liṅarthatvaṁ vartata iti prābhākaraḥ; nāstīti bhāṭṭō granthakāraś cēti bōdhyam । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiṁ ca mānāntarāpūrva-kārya-bōdhana-śaktatā ।  
na karma-phala-sambandha-siddhyai tāvad upēyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

naiyōgikas+++(=vidhi-sūcakaḥ)+++ sa +++(karma-phala-)+++sambandhō  
na punar vainiyōgikaḥ +++(=sādhana-sūcakaḥ)+++ ।  
dhātv-arthōttīrṇa+++(-apūrva-)+++-kāryātmā  
na karma-phala-saṅgamāt ॥  
r̥tē sidhyati sambandhas,  
sa +++(karma-phala-saṅgamaḥ)+++ ca tasmād +++(karma-phala-sambandhāt)+++ r̥tē na hi ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The only relation proved of it is that with injunction, not with instrumentality.  
That in a statement there subsists a relation with a kārya  
which transcends the root-sense of the verb  
cannot be proved except by the relation of kārya with the fruit of the act, and the latter relation cannot be proved without the former. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'dhātv-artha'-padēna yāgādir ucyatē । dhātv-arthōttīrṇa-kāryātmā sambandhaḥ । 

tasmādr̥tē ... 'sa ca' karma-phala-saṅgamaḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

naiyōgikas sa sambandhō na punar vainiyōgikaḥ ।  
dhātvarthōttīrṇa-kāryātmā na karma-phala-saṅgamāt ॥  
r̥tē sidhyati sambandhas sa ca tasmād r̥tē na hi ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tataś ca duruttaram itarētarāśrayaṇam ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And therefore there is a vicious interdependence that cannot be refuted. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

svarga-kāma-rūpa-niyōjyasya kriyā-sambandha-jñānam; tēna svarga-yāgayōḥ sambandha-jñānam; tad-anyathānupapattyā 'pūrva-kalpanam; tatas tasya liṅ-vācyatva-kalpanam; vācyē 'pūrvē yāgasya svarga-kāmasya cānvaya-kalpanam; ēvaṁ, svarga-kāmīyaṁ yāga-sambandhy apūrvam' iti jñātē tad-anantaram ēva svarga-yāga-sambandha-kalpanam  
iti anyōnyāśrayaṇa-prakāraḥ samanusandhēyaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tataś ca duruttaram itarētarāśrayaṇam ।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> sādhya-svarga-viśiṣṭasya  
puruṣasya **pravartakaḥ** ।  
**na** syād iti tad-iṣṭārtha-  
**sādhanaṁ na** bhavēd vidhiḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If there is no factor which activates the person who, according to the injunction, is specified by the heaven that is to be achieved,  
the injunction itself cannot be the means of achieving the desired heaven. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sādhya-svarga-viśiṣṭasya puruṣasya pravartakaḥ ।  
na syād iti tad-iṣṭārtha-sādhanaṁ na bhavēd vidhiḥ ॥

</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> bhaṅgurō **na** ca dhātvarthaḥ  
**karaṇatvēna kalpatē** ।  

iti tad-bhinna-+++(-apūrva-)+++kāryārtha-  
bōdhakatvaṁ yad ucyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The root-sense of the words being transitory, the statement itself cannot function as this means.142  
Therefore the assertion that a language statement communicates as its proper meaning a kārya which exceeds this transitory root-sense, cannot be correct. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[142]: This is the prābhākara view, which holds that in the injunction niyoga svargakāmo yajeta the sādhya (object to be realized) is not svarga, but the entire niyoga (cf. Prakaraṇapañcikā, p. 190), so that the statement of the injunction would become the means (sādhana) to realize that sādhya, sc. the injunction. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

bhaṅgurō na ca dhātvarthaḥ karaṇatvēna kalpatē ।  
iti tad-bhinna-kāryārtha-bōdhakatvaṁ yad ucyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tad asan - na hi sādhyēna  
svargēṇāyaṁ +++(puruṣō)+++ viśēṣyatē ।  
svargaṁ kāmayamānō hi  
puruṣō 'tra niyujyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

A person is not specified by heaven as the object to be achieved,143 but it is the person who desires heaven who is enjoined upon to accomplish the act.   

[143]: Cf. Prakaraṇapañcikā p. 182.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'jyōtiṣṭōmēna svarga-kāmō yajētē'ty atra । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad asan na hi sādhyēna svargēṇāyaṁ viśēṣyatē ।  
svargaṁ kāmayamānō hi puruṣō 'tra niyujyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

na hi svargō'dhikāriviśēṣaṇaṁ sādhyatvāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Heaven can not be the specification of the person's qualification, because heaven is yet to be achieved. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi svargō'dhikāriviśēṣaṇaṁ sādhyatvāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

siddham ēva hi sarvasya  
niyōjyasya viśēṣaṇam ।  
+++('yāvaj-jīvam agnihōtraṁ juhōti'→)+++ jīvanādi tathaivēha  
kāmanaiva viśēṣaṇam ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Only something that has already been achieved, that actually exists, can specify the person upon whom an act is enjoined, for instance, the real fact of his being alive etc. Consequently only his desire can specify his qualification for the act.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'niyōjyaḥ' puruṣaḥ 'svarga-kāma'-padābhihitaḥ । 

jīvanādi ... 'yāvaj jīvam agni-hōtraṁ juhōti', 'yāvaj jīvaṁ darśa-pūrṇamāsābhyāṁ yajēta' (see Śābarabhāsya under II iv I ) ity-ādiṣu nitya-vidhiṣu jīvanādikaṁ siddham ēva hi puruṣasya viśēṣaṇaṁ dr̥śyatē, na tu sādhyam । ēvaṁ prakr̥tē 'pīti vibhāvyam । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

siddhamēva hi sarvasya niyōjyasya viśēṣaṇam ।  
jīvanādi tathaivēha kāmanaiva viśēṣaṇam ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

api ca niyōjya-viśēṣaṇatām +++(tvan-matē)+++ anubhavataḥ svargādēḥ  
kīdr̥śaṁ sādhyatvam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[55]]

68\. Furthermore, precisely how is heaven, which in your opinion functions as the specification of the person enjoined, an object to be realized, a sādhya?
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca niyōjya-viśēṣaṇatām anubhavataḥ svargādēḥ kīdr̥śaṁ sādhyatvam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

yadi sādhana-saṁbandha-  
yōgyatvaṁ - naiva tāvatā ॥  
svargēṇa siddhyatā bhāvyaṁ  
yāvad yōgam ajanmataḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[56]]

If its being a sādhya means that it is fit for a relation with a sādhana,  
it is impossible for heaven to be siddha, as long as its relatability obtains,  
since it cannot become siddha in the meantime.144 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[144]: Nothing can become a fact (siddha) as long as it is still to be made a fact (sādhya) by a "factualizing" means (sādhana); thus as long as it is related with such a means it cannot be a fact.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi sādhana-saṁbandha-yōgyatvaṁ - naiva tāvatā ॥  
svargēṇa siddhyatā bhāvyaṁ yāvad yōgam ajanmataḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

siddhi-paryantatā tasya +++(svargasya "niyōjya-viśēṣaṇasya")+++  
+++(apūrva=)+++niyōgaika-pramāṇikā ॥
niyōgas tat-pramāṇaś cēty  
anyō'nyāśrayaṇaṁ dhruvam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The only authority that exists for heaven becoming siddha in the end is the injunction itself, while the only authority for the injunction is just this that heaven does become siddha. This is plainly a vicious circle. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'Niyoga' is another name coined by Prabhakara to denote Apūrva. See Karmamīmāṁsā, pp. 74-75: 

Mīmāṁsā does not believe in any God that receives the offerings from the votaries and rewards them accordingly.

> There must, therefore, be a capacity, which does not exist prior to the sacrificial action, either in the principal performance or in the agent, but which is generated in the course of the performance. Before a man performs a sacrifice, which will lead to heaven, there is an incapacity in the offering and in the man himself to secure that result, but when he has performed it, he becomes, as a result of the action, endowed with a potency, styled 'apūrva', which in the course of time, will secure for him the end desired. The existence of this potency is testified to in the scriptures; its necessity is apparent by the means of proof known as Presumption (arthāpatti). We find in the Veda, assertions that sacrifices produce certain results, and, as the operation of the sacrifice, as we see it, is transient, the truth of the scripture would be vitiated if we did not accept the theory of Apūrva. Nor is there anything illogical in this doctrine; every action sets in force activities in substances or agents, and these come to fruition when the necessary auxiliaries are present. The action specified is called into existence by the injunction contained in the form of an optative in a sentence in the Veda.  

> From this doctrine, Prabhākara dissents, elaborating instead, a theory which is obviously a refinement on the simple view which Kumārila accepts from the older writers of the school and which best suits the Mīmāṃsā Sūtras. In his opinion, the injunction rests in the sentence as a whole, not in the optative verb, and he denies that from the action there arises directly the Apūrva. On the contrary the process is that the injunctive sentence lays down A Mandate, Niyoga; this excites the man to exertion, and this exertion pertains to some form of action, indicated by the verb of the injunctive sentence. The exertion produces in the agent a result (kārya) to which also the name of Niyoga is given by Prabhākara, on the ground that it is this which acts as an Incentive to the agent to put forth exertion towards the performance of the action denoted by the verb of the injunctive clause. The Niyoga, however, is unable to produce its result, unless aided by something which Śālikanātha styles 'fate', nor is it apparent that either in his terminology, or in his view of the process, Prabhākara's doctrine is any superior to that of Kumārila. It seems as if primarily it arose from nothing more important than the observation that The result produced in the agent was in one sense his motive to action as much as the sentence directing the action to be done, leading to a transfer of the term Niyoga, naturally applicable to the sentence, to the condition in the agent to which the more orthodox name of Apūrva was usually applied.

> In simple sacrifices, there is only one Apūrva produced, but in more complicated sacrifices, there may be several, as a rule, four.... But it is not every action which brings out an Apūrva; these actions, which are devoted simply to some material result, though a part of the sacrifice, such as the appointment of priests or the threshing of corn are not credited with any such effect, as they serve an immediate purpose and need no further explanation.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

siddhi-paryantatā tasya niyōgaika-pramāṇikā ॥
niyōgas tat-pramāṇaś cēty anyōnyāśrayaṇaṁ dhruvam ।  
</details>

#### sādhya-dvayāpattiḥ
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

yadi svargasya sādhyatvaṁ,  
na niyōgasya+++(=apūrvasya)+++ sādhyatā +++(iti vācyam)+++॥  
sādhya-dvayaṁ ca naikasmin  
vākyē sambandham arhati ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If heaven is the sādhya, the injunction is not the sādhya. It is not possible to combine two sādhyas in one sentence.144

144: This is the principle of ekavākyatā: a statement can contain only one injunction, otherwise there is vākyabheda: what should be one sentence is split up into two.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi svargasya sādhyatvaṁ na niyōgasya sādhyatā ॥  
sādhya-dvayaṁ ca naikasmin vākyē sambandham arhati ॥
</details>

##### niyōga-svāntantryam
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> svatantraṁ hi sādhya-dvayam ēkavākyatāṁ niruṇaddhi -  
nānuguṇam, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> 69\. OBJECTION. Indeed, the unity of a sentence is broken up145 when it contains two sādhyas that are independent, but not when the two are interdependent. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[145]: This is the principle of ekavākyata: a statement can contain only one injunction, otherwise there is vākyabheda: what should be one sentence is split up into two.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> svatantraṁ hi sādhya-dvayam ēkavākyatāṁ niruṇaddhi nānuguṇam, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

anuguṇaṁ caitat-sādhya-dvayaṁ -  
niyōga-siddhināntarīyakatvāt svarga-siddhēḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And here the two sādhyas are interdependent since the realization of heaven is contained in the realization of the injunction. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anuguṇaṁ caitat-sādhyadvayaṁ niyōga-siddhi-nāntarīyakatvāt svarga-siddhēḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> yad āha  
> 
> "niyōga-siddhau sarvaṁ tad-anuguṇam" iti  
"kēna nēṣyatē niyōga-siddhy-arthā phala-siddhiḥ" iti ca,  
tasmād avirōdha 

iti cēt — 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> That is what the Author says: "When the niyoga is realized, everything else in accordance with it is also realized;" and: "Why should the realization of the fruit not be held to be subservient to the realization of the injunction?"146 Therefore there is no conflict here.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[146]: Quotations not identified; but for the argument, see Prakaraṇapañcikā, p 183 ff
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yad āha "niyōga-siddhau sarvaṁ tadanuguṇam" iti "kēna nēṣyatē "niyōga-siddhyarthā phala-siddhiḥ" iti ca,  
tasmād avirōdha 

iti cēt — 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tan na -

svarga-siddhiṁ vinā kiṁ nu  
niyōgasya na sidhyati ।  
nādhikārō na viṣayō  
na cānyad-vidhy-apēkṣitam ॥
</details>

<details><summary>En - viśvāsaḥ</summary>

REFUTATION. No; 

When heaven is not realized, what of the injunction/ apUrva can not be realized? Neither the qualification, nor the object, nor anything else required by the injunction is not realized.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. No; 

~~unless heaven is realized, how can the injunction not be realized? Without the realization of heaven neither the qualification, nor the object, nor anything else required by the injunction is realized.~~
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tan na ।

svarga-siddhiṁ vinā kiṁ nu niyōgasya na sidhyati ।  
nādhikārō na viṣayō na cānyad-vidhy-apēkṣitam ॥

</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> na hi nityādhikārēṣu  
+++(apūrvaḥ=)+++niyōgas tām +++(svargasiddhiṁ)+++ apēkṣatē ।  
na cānyad icchatō 'nyatra  
niyuktir nōpapadyatē ॥  
niyōgasyaiva māhātmyaṁ  
nityēṣv iva niyujyatē । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

70\. ~~OBJECTION.~~ In the case of the qualifications for periodical rites the injunction (apUrva) does not require the 'realization of any fruit.'147   

[147]: No specific fruits are attached to nitya rites. 

Nor does an injunction to one act  
fail to apply to a person who really desires another fruit.

The pre-eminence148 is really the injunction's;  
a person is enjoined upon by the injunction to any act in the same way  
as he is enjoined upon to perform the periodical acts.

[148]: māhātmya, which corresponds to prādhānya, pradhānatā 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi nityādhikārēṣu niyōgas tām apēkṣatē ।  
na cānyad icchatō 'nyatra niyuktir nōpapadyatē ॥  
niyōgasyaiva māhātmyaṁ nityēṣv iva niyujyatē । 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

niyōgō hi pradhānatayā 'dhigamyamāna-svargam abhilaṣantam apy  
ātmany ākarṣati  
yathā anicchantam api nityē karmaṇi niṣphalē pravartayati ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For the injunction draws unto itself the desirous person who himself thinks that the heaven which he desires is the principal object, in the same way as the injunction to perform the periodical acts activates a person, even though he does not desire anything, to these acts which bear no fruit at all. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

niyōgō hi pradhānatayā'dhigamyamāna-svargam abhilaṣantam apy ātmany ākarṣati yathā anicchantam api nityē karmaṇi niṣphalē pravartayati ॥
</details>

##### nimēṣādi-sādhanatā
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

kiṁ ca ।  

svargaṁ kāmayamānō hi nimiṣaty unmiṣaty api ।  
na ca tē svarga-siddhyarthā yāgaḥ kiṁ naivam +++(nimēṣōnmēṣavat)+++ iṣyatē ॥ +++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Besides, a person who is desirous of heaven also opens and shuts his eyes; for you these actions do not subserve his realization of heaven. Why not consider the sacrificing an action of the same kind? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiṁ ca ।  
svargaṁ kāmayamānō hi nimiṣaty unmiṣaty api ।  
na ca tē svarga-siddhyarthā yāgaḥ kiṁ naivam iṣyatē ॥

</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

"tat-sādhanatayā naitē  
gr̥hyanta" iti cēn matam ।  
yāgādayaḥ kiṁ tad+++(=sādhanatā)+++-buddhi-  
grāhyā vidhi-bahiṣkr̥tāḥ? ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> There are some who do not accept that it is a means of realizing heaven. [[57]]

71\. REFUTATION. If that is the view, we ask: Are the sacrifice etc., which are to be grasped by the cognition that they are such means, eliminated from the injunction? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

"tat-sādhanatayā naitē gr̥hyanta" iti cēn matam ।  
yāgādayaḥ kiṁ tad-buddhi-grāhyā vidhi-bahiṣkr̥tāḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tatra ca -  

sādhya-sādhana-saṁbandha-  
pratipādana-tat-parāḥ ।  
yāvan na vidhayas tāvan  
naiṣphalyaṁ sarva-karmaṇām ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

On this point: When the injunction does not mean to convey a relation between the object to be realized and the means of realizing it, then all acts are fruitless. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatra ca -  

sādhya-sādhana-saṁbandha-pratipādana-tatparāḥ ।  
yāvan na vidhayas tāvan naiṣphalyaṁ sarva-karmaṇām ॥
</details>

#### nigamanam
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tasmāl liṅādibhyaḥ prathamam iṣṭa-sādhanatā-avagamaḥ,  
tatō rāgataḥ pravr̥ttir ity ēva yuktam, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore, it is sound to maintain that  
from the injunctive suffixes  
there results first the cognition that  
they are indeed the means to realize the desired object,  
and that subsequently the desire for this object prompts a person to undertake the act of realization.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasmāl liṅādibhyaḥ prathamam iṣṭa-sādhanatā-avagamaḥ, tatō rāgataḥ pravr̥ttir ity ēva yuktam, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

"tad apūrva-kāryābhidhāna ēva mukhyā śaktiḥ, itaratra lākṣaṇikī"ty anupapannam, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

But it is improper to maintain that  

> the primary denotation occurs in the expressing of a meaning that was previously unknown,  

and that 

> the denotation in the expressing of any other meaning is secondary. 

</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad apūrva-kāryābhidhāna ēva mukhyā śaktiḥ, itaratra lākṣaṇikīty anupapannam, 
</details>

### anumāna-mūlatā na laukika-śabdēṣu
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

ata ēva yathā-yathaṁ laukika-śabdēbhyas tat-siddhārtha-gōcarā buddhayō jāyantē ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

We conclude that ordinary, non-Vedic statements give rise to cognitions concerning meanings that are just so established by these statements.

[[58]]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ata ēva yathā-yathaṁ laukika-śabdēbhyas tat-siddhārtha-gōcarā buddhayō jāyantē ।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> nanu na tāḥ śabda-mahima-bhuvaḥ, ānumānikyō hi tāḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> 72\. OBJECTION. But these cognitions do not arise from the denoting power of language, but result from Inference. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This view of Prabhākara regarding the validity pertaining to the statements made by human beings, has already been stated and refuted briefly by Yāmuna. He now exposes in detail, the untenability and absurdity of this view and proves that even sentences uttered by people in the world possess verbal authority, but not inferential authority. See the verse "tasmādasti madillie"[[??]], etc., following. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> nanu na tāḥ śabda-mahima-bhuvaḥ, ānumānikyō hi tāḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> tathā hi vyutpatti-samaya-saṁviditārtha-pratipādana-sāmarthyāny api padāni  
kvacid +++(śabdēṣu)+++ vyabhicāra-darśana-janita-saṁśaya-pratibaddhāni  
na śruta-mātrāṇy arthaṁ niścāyayanti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> For these statements, though their denotations in conveying certain meanings are consciously known once their proper meanings have been learnt,  
do not furnish complete certainty about their meanings merely upon being heard by a listener,  
when they are accompanied by doubt which is created by the listener's observation that in one case or other statements have deviated from their proper meanings.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Prakaraṇapañcikā II. 24, P.14:

> śaṅkyamānānyathārthatvaracanaṁ tena puṁvacaḥ ।  
śrutamātrakamevārthe na tāvanniścayāvaham ॥

Also vide ibid: śl. 36, P.15:

> arthenaiva viśeṣo hi nirākāratayā dhiyām ।  
na cāpratītenārthena viśeṣaścāvakalpate ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi vyutpatti-samaya-saṁviditārtha-pratipādana-sāmarthyāny api padāni kva-cid vyabhicāra-darśana-janita-saṁśaya-pratibaddhāni na śruta-mātrāṇy arthaṁ niścāyayanti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> na cāniścitō'rthō jñātō bhavati  
aniścayātmanō jñānasyābhāvāt ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> And, unless there be complete certainty, the meaning will remain unknown; for no knowledge can arise in one's mind from uncertainty. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cāniścitō'rthō jñātō bhavati aniścayātmanō jñānasyābhāvāt ।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> tatrājñātē'pi vākyārthē  
śrōtaivaṁ vicikitsatē ।  
> 
> > bravīty anyō'nya-saṁbandha-  
yōgyārthāni padāny ayam ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If the meaning of a statement is not known, the listener wants to discover it: "The speaker uses words whose meanings apparently admit of being connected; 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. ibid. II. 38-40, P.16:

> kiṁ tv ajñātē 'pi śabdārthē pada-jātē śrutē sati ।  
vimarśō jāyatē śrōtur īdr̥śō mati-śālinaḥ ॥  
anyōnyānvaya-yōgyārthaṁ pada-jātaṁ bravīty ayam ।  
āptas tēnāmunā nūnaṁ jñātas tēṣāṁ samanvayaḥ ॥  
na kadācid asambaddhān arthān ēṣa vivakṣati ।  
na vā 'pratīta-sambandhān iti dōṣō na kaścana ॥

Also cf. ibid: V, P.95:

> yō hi puruṣaḥ ēvam avadhāritō nāyam aśaktō, na pramādī, sambhavad ētad artha-viṣaya-pramāṇaḥ sakalāśaya-dōṣa-rahitaś ca; nāyam avijñāyārtham anvitārthāni prayuṅkta iti tad-vākya-prayōgasyānvaya-jñāna-pūrvakatvād anvaya-jñānaṁ tāvad anumīyatē । anvaya-jñānāc cānvayō 'py anumīyatē । jñānaṁ hi jñēyāvinābhāvi, jñēyānumānē bhavaty ēva liṅgam । tad ēvaṁ laukikād vacasō liṅga-bhūtād vaktr̥-jñānam anumīyatē । tatō 'rthaṁ niścitya vyavahāraḥ pravartatē । ēvaṁ ca niścitē 'nvayē nivr̥ttānvayāśaṅkād vākyād apy artha-niścayō jāyatē । kintu tasyāṁ daśāyām anuvādakataiva । ata ēva laukika-vacanē na śabdaṁ pramāṇam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatrājñātē'pi vākyārthē śrōtaivaṁ vicikitsatē ।  
bravīty anyōnya-saṁbandha-yōgyārthāni padāny ayam ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

>> na cāvijñāta-saṁbandhān  
śabdān āptāḥ prayuñjatē ।  
>
> tēnēdr̥śānvaya-jñānam  
asyāstīty avagacchati ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> and reliable persons do not use words whose connections are unknown;" 

and the listener realizes that therefore the speaker has knowledge of such a connection. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cāvijñāta-saṁbandhān śabdān āptāḥ prayuñjatē ।  
tēnēdr̥śānvaya-jñānam asyāstīty avagacchati ॥
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

4 Cf. ibid. II. 38-40, p. 16- 

> ' kintvajñātē'pi śabdārthē  
padajātē śrutē sati ।  
vimarśō jāyatē śrōtur  
īdr̥śō matiśālinaḥ ॥  
anyōnyānvayayōgyārtha-  
padajātaṁ bravītyayam ।  
āptas tēnāmunā nūnaṁ  
jñātastēṣāṁ samanvayaḥ ॥  
na kadācid asambaddhān  
arthānēṣa vivakṣati ।  
na vā'pratīta-sambandhān  
iti dōṣō na kaścana ॥ " 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> ēvam anvaya-jñānē 'numitē  
tad-upadarśitō 'rthō na śabdam ākāṅkṣati, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If the knowledge of connection is thus inferred, the meaning discovered by the listener does not require the authority of verbal testimony. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. ibid. II. śls. 26-28; P.15:

> tasya jñānaṁ ca vākyēna liṅga-bhūtēna gamyatē ।  
jñātvaivārthaṁ bravītīti ya ēvam avadhāritaḥ ॥  
tasya jñānēna niyataṁ vākyaṁ jñānānumāpakam ।  
jñānaṁ cārthāvinābhāvi tēnārthē 'pi viniścayaḥ ॥  
tatō 'rthē niścitē paścāt sō 'rthō vākyēna gamyatē ।  
tasyāṁ daśāyāṁ vākyasya tasya syād anuvādatā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvam anvaya-jñānē 'numitē tad-upadarśitō 'rthō na śabdam ākāṅkṣati, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> atō laukikasya vacasō vaktr-anubhava--para-tantratayā  
tatraiva paryavasānam 

iti ।+++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Consequently, since ordinary language statements are dependent on the speaker's cognition; they terminate in that cognition through Inference alone.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atō laukikasya vacasō vaktr-anubhava-paratantratayā tatraiva paryavasānam iti ।
</details>

#### śabda-śaktir apratihataikatra dōṣē'pi
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tad asat,  
na hi  
svabhāvatō 'rtham avagamayan śabdaḥ  

> "kvacid vaktr-āśaya-dōṣa-vaśīkārād vitatha"  

ity anyatrāpi tat-saṁbhāvanayā svārasikīm arthāvabōdhakatām ujjhitum arhati, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

73\. REFUTATION. This view is not correct;  
for a word conveys its right meaning as its natural function, and the observation that in one case the statement happened to be untrue under the influence of defects in the speaker's character should not give rise to a general suspicion which would cause all statement to give up its natural capacity of conveying its meaning.149 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad asat, na hi svabhāvatō 'rtham avagamayan śabdaḥ  
kvacid vaktrāśaya-dōṣa-vaśīkārād vitatha ity anyatrāpi tat-saṁbhāvanayā svārasikīm arthāvabōdhakatām ujjhitum arhati, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

na hi "mantra-pratihata-daśāyāṁ hutavahō na dahatī"ty  
anyatrāpi tādr̥śa-daśā-śaṅkyā na dahati, +++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The suspicion that a fire may not burn in other cases  
because in one case, when obstructed by mantras, it fails to burn, does not make fire fail to burn! 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi mantra-pratihata-daśāyāṁ hutavahō na dahatīty anyatrāpi tādr̥śa-daśā-śaṅkyā na dahati, 
</details>

<details><summary>rāma-miśraḥ</summary>

atra mantra-pratihati-daśāyām iti yuktaḥ pāṭhō  
'thavā hata-śabdē bhāvē kta-pratyaya ity anusaṁdhēyam ।
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

nāpi 

> śukti-rajata-dhiyam artha-vyabhicāriṇīm indriyaṁ dōṣa-vaśād upalabdham 

iti ghaṭādikam api nāvagamayati, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And the fact that the sense of vision may give rise to a cognition which does not correspond to reality-e.g. that nacre is silver-as the result of some optical error does not signify that the visual sense cannot produce true cognition of the visible presence of a pitcher etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi śukti-rajata-dhiyam artha-vyabhicāriṇīm indriyaṁ dōṣa-vaśād upalabdham iti ghaṭādikam api nāvagamayati, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

atō vidita-pada-padārtha-saṅgatēḥ  
śrōtus sahasaiva śabdō 'rtham avabōdhayati  
mūla-jñānaṁ na pratīkṣatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore, a statement does indeed instantly convey a certain meaning to the listener if he knows the relation between the words and their meanings. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atō vidita-pada-padārtha-saṅgatēḥ śrōtus sahasaiva śabdō 'rtham avabōdhayati mūla-jñānaṁ na pratīkṣatē ।
</details>

#### mūla-jñānāparyāptatā
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

mūla-jñāna-parijñānād  
arvāg arthē 'pi cōditē ।  
"katham ēvam ayaṁ vēda"  
ity anumānaṁ pravartatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It does not require knowledge of the basis. Before there is complete knowledge on the part of the listener about the basic knowledge of the speaker, and, further, when the meaning has been expressed, the question rises: "How does he know this?" and Inference proceeds to resolve that question. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

mūla-jñāna-parijñānād arvāg arthē 'pi cōditē ।  
katham ēvam ayaṁ vēda ity anumānaṁ pravartatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> "kim **ajñāsīd** ayam vaktā  
kiñcid" ity **anumitsasē** ।  
viśiṣṭārthānvaya-jñānam  
**anumātum athēcchasi** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

You want to infer: "Did the speaker know something?" or wish to infer his knowledge of the connection of the different meanings. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kim ajñāsīd ayam vaktā kiñcid ity anumitsasē ।  
viśiṣṭārthānvaya-jñānam anumātum athēcchasi ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

**na** tāvad ayam **ajñāsīd**  
vaktā kiñcid itīyatā ।  
vyāhāra-vyavahārau vā  
syātāṁ vākyārtha-gōcarau +++(vakṣyamāṇa-rītyā)+++॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

But the mere knowledge that the speaker knew something is not enough for utterance and action concerning a statement-meaning to proceed. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

vyavahāraḥ kāyikaḥ vyāhāraḥ vācikaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na tāvad ayam ajñāsīd vaktā kiñcid itīyatā ।  
vyāhāra-vyavahārau vā syātāṁ vākyārtha-gōcarau ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

viśiṣṭārthānvaya-gōcara-cētō 'numānan tu  
prathamatara-pravr̥tta--tad-viṣaya-śēmuṣīm antarēṇānupapannam  

iti prāgēva śabdārthō'vagantavyaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Inference of a cognition concerning the connection of different meanings is impossible without a prior cognition of such a connection.  

This being so, the meaning of the statement must be known first. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

viśiṣṭārthānvayagōcaracētō'numānantu prathamatarapravr̥ttatadviṣayaśēmuṣīmantarēṇānupapannamiti prāgēva śabdārthō'vagantavyaḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

na hy anāsādita-viṣaya-viśēṣa-saṁsargāḥ saṁvidaḥ  
paras-paratō vyatibhidyantē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For cognitions whose particular objects are not connected, are not ~~connected~~ separated themselves. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hyanāsāditaviṣayaviśēṣasaṁsargāḥ saṁvidaḥ parasparatō vyatibhidyantē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

na ca tathā 'numitābhir artha-viśēṣaḥ sidhyati, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is a particular meaning established by cognitions that are inferred to be such. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca tathā 'numitābhir artha-viśēṣaḥ sidhyati, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> yādr̥śānvaya-pratipādana-yōgyā pada-racanā  
sā tad-anvaya-jñānam āpādayati

iti cēt,  
avagatas tarhi prāg ēvārthānām anvayaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If you say that 

> any word combination which is able to convey a certain connection produces knowledge of just this connection, 

I maintain that the connection of the particular meanings must be known previously; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yādr̥śānvaya-pratipādana-yōgyā pada-racanā sā tad-anvaya-jñānam āpādayatīti cēt, avagatas tarhi prāg ēvārthānām anvayaḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

na hi buddhāv anārōpita ēvānvayaḥ prayōgaṁ vyavacchinatti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

unless a connection has already reached the level of cognition it cannot give rise to being expressed in a statement.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi buddhāv anārōpita ēvānvayaḥ prayōgaṁ vyavacchinatti,
</details>

#### upasaṁhāraḥ

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tasmād asti nadī-tīrē  
phalam ity-ēvam-ādiṣu ।  
yā siddha-viṣayā buddhiḥ  
sā śābdī nānumānikī ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

74\. To conclude, the cognition of an established fact in statements like "there is a fruit on the riverbank" is strictly of verbal origin and does not arise from Inference.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasmād asti nadī-tīrē phalam ity-ēvam-ādiṣu ।  
yā siddha-viṣayā buddhiḥ sā śābdī nānumānikī ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tataś ca "apūrva-kārya-gōcara ēva śabdaḥ pramāṇam" iti -  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore the position that statements produce valid knowledge only if they deal with a previously unknown kārya 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tataś ca apūrva-kārya-gōcara ēva śabdaḥ pramāṇam iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

sva-sindhānta-cirābhyāsa-  
vyāmugdha-bala-biddhibhiḥ ॥
uktam, uktēna mārgēṇa  
yuktā 'nyatrāpi śaktatā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

is taken only by people whose judgments are stultified by their continuous preoccupation with their own theories.  
In the manner set forth above  
it is true that statements may bear meaningfully and informatively on other meanings as well. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sva-sindhānta-cirābhyāsa-vyāmugdha-bala-biddhibhiḥ ॥
uktam uktēna mārgēṇa yuktā 'nyatrāpi śaktatā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

vyāmugdhābalabuddhibhiriti pāṭhastu na yukta iti manyāmahē ।
</details>

### vēdāntōkta-puruṣaḥ
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tataś ca yāny ētāni vilakṣaṇa-puruṣa-pratipādakāni vēdānta-vacāṁsi 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Consequently, all the statements of the Upaniṣads which set forth the existence of a categorically different Person 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tataś ca yāny ētāni vilakṣaṇa-puruṣa-pratipādakāni vēdānta-vacāṁsi 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> "sa ēṣa sarvādhipatiḥ", 

> "sarvasyēśānaḥ", 

> "sarvam idaṁ praśāsti",  

> "tasyādhyakṣam idaṁ sarvam" 

ityādīni,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

e.g. 

> "He is the overlord of the Universe, 

> sovereign of all. 

> He commands all the world,"149 

"All this is manifest to Him150 etc."

[149]: BA Up. 5.6.1.
[150]: Not to be found in the major Upanisads.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

148: BĀ Up. 5\.6\.1\.  

149: Not to be found in the major Upaniṣads.  
[[59]]

150: supra §35\.  

</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

sa ēṣa ... Bṛhadāraṇyaka V. vi. 1.

tasyādhyakṣam ... To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

"sa ēṣa sarvādhipatiḥ", "sarvasyēśānaḥ", "sarvam idaṁ praśāsti", "tasyādhyakṣam idaṁ sarvam" ityādīni,
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tāny api tatra pramāṇaṁ  
tad-viṣayāsaṁdigdhāviparyaya-jñāna-hētutvāt । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

are authoritative as to what they state, since they produce indubitable and unreversed knowledge of their contents.

[[60]]

</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tāny api tatra pramāṇaṁ tad-viṣayāsaṁdigdhāviparyaya-jñāna-hētutvāt । 
</details>

### sambhāvitānuvāda-viparyayau

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> **na** ca +++(īśvara-nibhē)+++ siddhē vastuni  
> +++(tad-vastu-)+++sādhaka-bādhakayōr anyatarōpanipāta-sambhava-prasaktēr  
> +++(tad-vastu-)+++bhāvitānuvāda-viparyaya-paryālōcanayā  
> tad+++(vastu)+++-gōcara-vacasaḥ **prāmāṇya-pracyutiḥ**  
> +++(samid-āharaṇādi-)+++kārya-niṣṭhasyāpi tat+++(←pracyuti)+++-prasaṅgāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor do statements concerning a fact lack authority  
because of the consideration that since either a proving or disproving factor may unexpectedly turn up  
there remains the possibility that this fact is thus repeated or reversed;  
for the same may equally well happen to a statement concerning, not a fact, but a karya.  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

The validity of shabda lies in its communicating contents that cannot be known through other means of knowledge.  
What I translate as 'facts' are more literally "established [[129]] entities," established, that is, by other means of knowledge than shabda.  
A scriptural statement of the kind "grass is green" is not strictly valid  
in the sense that, in order to know that grass is green, we need a scriptural statement to that effect.

Another proving factor, c.g., the means of knowledge Perception, may turn up conceivably  
and thus make the scriptural statement superfluous;  
or we may find that grass is not invariably green, but changes its colour,  
which would reverse the scriptural statement.

Scriptural validity, i.e., Scripture's being a means of knowledge, is to the Prabhakara Mimimsaka, its being the sole means of knowing a particular thing.  
To the Prabhakara this validity is ideal in the case of injunctions concerning actions which, suprasensibly, lead to a certain desired end.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca siddhē vastuni sādhakabādhakayōranyatarōpanipātasambhavaprasaktērbhāvitānuvādaviparyayaparyālōcanayā tadgōcaravacasaḥ prāmāṇyapracyutiḥ kāryaniṣṭhasyāpi tatprasaṅgāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> +++(laukikaṁ←)+++kāryam api hi mānāntara-vēdyam ēva +++("ōdanēna hōtavyam" ityatra)+++ laukikaṁ samid-āharaṇādi,  
tac ca mānāntarēṇāpi **vēdyam** ōdana-pākavad ity abhyupagamāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

A kārya, too, may be known from other means of knowledge,  
for it must be admitted that ordinary karyas, like 'fetch firewood'  
are also known through other means of knowledge,  
as in the case of the cooking of the odana.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

(The injunction concerning the odana oblation includes an injunction concerning the preparation of the odana and the fetching of firewood for the cooking. Since experience shows that for a cooking fire one needs firewood, this karya is not strictly known on scriptural authority.)
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kāryamapi hi mānāntaravēdyamēva laukikaṁ samidāharaṇādi, tacca mānāntarēṇāpi vēdyamōdanapākavadityabhyupagamāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

$ Vide Prakaraṇapañcikā II, p. 180- 
> " kr̥tisādhyaṁ pradhānaṁ yat,  
tat kāryam avasīyatē । 
taca mānāntarēṇāpi  
vēdyam ōdana-pākavat ॥ " 
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

>> atha vilakṣaṇāgni-hōtrādi-viṣaya-kāryasyāsambhāvita-mānāntaratayā  
> tat-pratipādayad vacaḥ pramāṇam,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or if it be claimed that,  
inasmuch as a karya concerning a categorically different thing like the agnihotra etc. cannot conceivably find any other authority,  
therefore the verbal testimony which sets forth such a thing must needs be its authority,
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> atha vilakṣaṇāgnihōtrādiviṣayakāryasyāsambhāvitamānāntaratayā tatpratipādayadvacaḥ pramāṇam,  
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

> hanta tarhi niratiśayāvabōdhaiśvarya-mahā''nanda-sandōha-vapuṣi bhagavati  
> na mānāntara-gandha-sambandha  
> iti sarvaṁ samānam anyatrābhinivēśāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

well, then we may say that there is not a ghost of another authority for the Bhagavan  
whose form consists in unsurpassed knowledge, supremacy and beatitude;  
so that it should follow that everything is entirely the same in both cases,  
depending on one's particular partisan views.  
(it is all the same, depending on what partisan view one takes! )
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> hanta tarhi niratiśayāvabōdhaiśvaryamahānandasandōhavapuṣi bhagavati na mānāntaragandhasambandha iti sarvaṁ samānamanyatrābhinivēśāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

api ca -  

pramāṇāntara-dr̥ṣṭārtha-  
viṣayiṇy api śēmuṣī ।  
pramāṇam ēva, tat-pūrvaṁ  
na cēt svārthaṁ vigāhatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Moreover, 

if a cognition concerning a content  
that is also known through another means of knowledge  
does not recognize its own content as authoritative,  
since it has already been taken care of by another authority,  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca -  

pramāṇāntara-dr̥ṣṭārtha-viṣayiṇy api śēmuṣī ।  
pramāṇam ēva tat-pūrvaṁ na cēt svārthaṁ vigāhatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tasya saṁbhāvanā-mātrād  
aprāmāṇyam alaukikam । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

this non-authoritativeness of its content is beyond experience  
for it is a mere matter of assumption.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasya saṁbhāvanā-mātrād aprāmāṇyam alaukikam । 
</details>

### upasaṁhāraḥ
<details open><summary>viśvāsa-prastutiḥ</summary>

tasmāt pariniṣṭhitānuṣṭhēyādi-bhēda-śūnyam  
asandigdhāviparyastavijñānaṁ pramāṇam ēṣṭavyam,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore it must be maintained that all indubitable and unreversed knowledge is authoritative, regardless of whether its content is established, or yet to be performed, or anything else. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

pariniṣṭhir ayaṁ [[??]] siddhārtha-bōdhakatvam; anuṣṭhēyatvaṁ parābhīṣṭaṁ kārya-bōdhakatvam । ubhayōr ētayōr na kutrāpy āgrahaḥ kārya iti [[??]] jñāna-prāmāṇyasya tādr̥śa-bhēdāprayōjakatvāt, viparyayādi-śūnyatvasyaiva tatvāc ca ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasmāt pariniṣṭhitānuṣṭhēyādi-bhēda-śūnyam asandigdhāviparyastavijñānaṁ pramāṇam ēṣṭavyam,  
</details>
</details>

## 05 sārvajñyam

### śabda-pramāṇam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ata idam apāstam -

> prasiddhaiḥ karaṇairēva  
sārvajñyaṁ nānyathēti yat । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Hence we reject our opponent's position. [[61]]  
76\. The objections152 that omniscience is acquired by means of the regular senses is incorrect,153 

[152]: supra §42.
[153]: read ity asat for iti yat.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This line runs like a verse.

Cf. Ślokavārtika under I. 1.2; śl. 111b:

> yadi ṣaḍbhiḥ pramāṇais syāt sarva-jñaḥ, kēna vāryatē ?
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ata idam apāstam -  
prasiddhaiḥ karaṇairēva sārvajñyaṁ nānyathēti yat । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yataḥ śrutirēva tatra paripanthinī - 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

because śruti contradicts it: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yataḥ śrutirēva tatra paripanthinī - 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> paśyaty a-cakṣus  
sa śr̥ṇōty a-karṇaḥ  
yaś cakṣuṣā na paśyati  
yaś cakṣūṁṣi paśyati ।  
na tasya kāryaṁ karaṇaṁ ca vidyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"He sees without eyes,  
hears without ears;  
he who does not see with the eye,  
who sees the eyes,  
has neither effect nor instrument;"154 

[154]: Svet Up. 3.19.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

paśyaty ... Śvetāśvatara : III. 19.

yaḥ ... Kenopaniṣat : I. 6a; but the reading found is:

> yac cakṣuṣā na paśyati, yēna cakṣūm̐ṣi paśyati ।

na tasya ... Śvetāśvatara*: VI. 8.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

paśyatyacakṣus śr̥ṇōtyakarṇaḥ yaścakṣuṣā na paśyati yaścakṣūṁṣi paśyati । na tasya kāryaṁ karaṇaṁ ca vidyatē ।   
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> svābhāvikī jñāna-bala-kriyā ca 

ity-ādikā ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> "knowledge, strength and action are natural to Him,"155 

etc. 

[155]: Svet Up. 6.8. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

svābhāvikī jñānabalakriyā ca ityādikā ।  
</details>

### nārthavādaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na cāsāṁ guṇa-vādatvaṁ pramāṇābhāvāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

These śrutis do not speak metaphorically,  
for there is no authority for this assumption.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cāsāṁ guṇavādatvaṁ pramāṇābhāvāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

alabdha-mukhya-vr̥ttīnāṁ  
guṇa-vāda-samāśrayaḥ ॥  
labhyatē cēha mukhyō'rtha  
iti tat-kalpanā mr̥ṣā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Metaphorical usage is assumed when the primary meanings of the śrutis make no sense.  
Since the primary meaning here makes sense, the assumption of metaphorical use is baseless.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

alabdhamukhyavr̥ttīnāṁ guṇavādasamāśrayaḥ ॥  
labhyatē cēha mukhyō'rtha iti tatkalpanā mr̥ṣā ॥ 
</details>

#### na pratyakṣataḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanv ihāpi mukhya-artha-bhaṅga-kāraṇam asti - pramāṇāntara-virōdhaḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[62]]

77\. OBJECTION. But in this case we have in fact reason to cancel the primary meaning, because the primary sense militates against other means of knowledge. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanv ihāpi mukhya-artha-bhaṅga-kāraṇam asti pramāṇāntara-virōdhaḥ । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kutaḥ pramāṇāntarāt, na tāvat pratyakṣāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. What other means of knowledge? Not, to start, Perception, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kutaḥ pramāṇāntarāt, na tāvat pratyakṣāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hi pratyakṣam udīrita-puruṣābhāvāvabhāsakam udīyamānaṁ dr̥ṣṭam, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for we see no Perception occur which shows that the said Person is non-existent. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi pratyakṣam udīrita-puruṣābhāvāvabhāsakam udīyamānaṁ dr̥ṣṭam, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yōgya-anupalambhād abhāva-niścaya 

iti cēn na -  
pramāṇa-gōṣṭhī-jyēṣṭhēna śāstrēṇaivōpalambhanāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If you retort that non-existence is decided by the nonapprehension of what should be there,  
we reply that this does not hold in our case since the object,  
that is the said Person, is actually apprehended through Scripture itself, which is the highest-ranking among the assembly of the means of knowledge. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This line too is metrical.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yōgya-anupalambhād abhāva-niścaya iti cēn na pramāṇa-gōṣṭhī-jyēṣṭhēna śāstrēṇaivōpalambhanāt, 
</details>

#### nānumānataḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpy anumānāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor does it militate against Inference; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpy anumānāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad dhi śīghra-janmāgamika-pratyaya-prakṣipta-pratibandhaṁ  
katham iva manthara-pravr̥tti prādurbhavati ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for how could an Inference which disproves that Person arise at all, slow-moving as it is, when its object is instantly refuted by the rapidly arising scriptural cognition? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

śabda-pramāṇāpēkṣayā anumānasya daurbalyam ēva । śābdaṁ jñānaṁ śīghrataram । vyāpti-jñānānantara-labdha-pratiṣṭhasyānumānasya manthara-pravr̥ttir ēvēti bhāvaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad dhi śīghra-janmāgamika-pratyaya-prakṣipta-pratibandhaṁ katham iva manthara-pravr̥tti prādurbhavati ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kiṁ caivaṁ sati yāgādēḥ  
svargāpūrvādi-saṅgatiḥ ।  
kriyātvēna virudhyēta  
śāstraṁ cēt tan na bādhatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Moreover, if this were so, the relation of sacrificing etc. to heaven, apūrva156 etc. would logically be contradicted by the fact that sacrificing etc. are actions, when Scripture did not cancel such reasoning. 

[156]: cf supra note.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiṁ caivaṁ sati yāgādēḥ svargāpūrvādi-saṅgatiḥ ।  
kriyātvēna virudhyēta śāstraṁ cēt tan na bādhatē ॥
</details>

#### na yūpādityavat
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yūpādityādi-tādātmyaṁ  
pratyakṣēṇaiva bādhitam ।  
vispaṣṭa-dr̥ṣṭa-bhēdatvāt  
kāṣṭha-sāvitra-bimbayōḥ ॥ +++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

True, the identity of sacrificial pole and sun, which is asserted by Scripture, is cancelled by another means of knowledge, namely Perception alone, because the difference between a piece of wood and the disc of the sun is indeed obvious. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See P.47 above for the Mīmāṁsaka's argument. The illustration of the arthavāda : “ādityo yūpaḥ” [Taittirīya Brāhmaṇa : II-i-5-2] was put forth there. This view is now being refuted.

The figurative statement “ādityo yūpaḥ” is made on the ground of similarity of brightness (tejasvitva) between the Sun and the sacrificial post. The relevant sūtra is “sārūpyāt” [Pūrvamīmāṁsā : I. iv. 25].
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yūpādityādi-tādātmyaṁ pratyakṣēṇaiva bādhitam ।  
vispaṣṭa-dr̥ṣṭa-bhēdatvāt kāṣṭha-sāvitra-bimbayōḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca  
tatra sannihita-yūpāñjana-vidhy-ēkavākyatayā  
artha-vādatvād yuktaṁ guṇa-vādatvāśrayaṇam,  +++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Besides, in this case it is legitimate to assume metaphorical usage, for the statement of this identity is an arthavāda,156 since it forms one single statement with the proximate injunction about the unction of the sacrificial pole.157 

[157]: supra note 86.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The ṛk to be repeated while anointing the yūpa with ghee is: "añjanti tvāmadhvare devayantaḥ" ( Taittirīya Brāhmaṇa - VI-ii. p. 142 ). For the derivation of the term yūpa, see ibid- VI-i, the opening part. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca tatra sannihita-yūpāñjana-vidhy-ēkavākyatayā artha-vādatvād yuktaṁ guṇa-vādatvāśrayaṇam, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na cēha tathā vidhy-antaram asti yac-chēṣatayā artha-vādaḥ syāt ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

There is no other injunction to which it could be accessory as an arthavāda.157 

157: supra § 36\.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cēha tathā vidhy-antaram asti yac-chēṣatayā artha-vādaḥ syāt ।
</details>

#### na kalpita-vidhēḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> atha vidhy-anvayābhāvē  
puruṣārthatvāhānataḥ ।  
adhyāhr̥tya vidhiṁ tatra  
śēṣatvaṁ parikalpyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Alternatively, inasmuch as the human importance of a statement would be lost if there were no injunction to connect it with, an injunction may be supplemented and then the arthavāda is regarded as accessory to that supplemented injunction.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha vidhy-anvayābhāvē puruṣārthatvāhānataḥ ।  
adhy-āhr̥tya vidhiṁ tatra śēṣatvaṁ parikalpyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yad āhuḥ -  
> 
> > yāvat khalu pramātr̥̄ṇāṁ  
> pravartana-nivartanē ।  
> śabdā na kurvatē tāvan  
> na nirākāṅkṣa-bōdhanam ॥
> 
> iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[63]]

> 78\. The objection158 that as long as statements fail to prompt the operator of the means of knowledge to being active or to prevent him from being active, they do not communicate self-sufficient information, 

[158]: supra § 36.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yad āhuḥ -  

> yāvat khalu pramātr̥̄ṇāṁ pravartana-nivartanē ।  
> śabdā na kurvatē tāvan na nirākāṅkṣa-bōdhanam ॥

iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tan na । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

does not hold good. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tan na । 
</details>

##### vidhy-anapēkṣā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

r̥tē 'pi vidhi-saṁbandhād  
dr̥ṣṭaiva hi pum-arthatā ।  
"putras tē jāta" ity-ādau  
tathēhāpi bhaviṣyati ॥ +++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>
