For, we find that statements have human importance also outside any connection with an injunction; in such a case it will be as in the statement “A son has been born to you," and the like. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

r̥tē 'pi vidhi-saṁbandhād dr̥ṣṭaiva hi pum-arthatā ।  
"putras tē jātaḥ" ity-ādau tathēhāpi bhaviṣyati ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca tatra vidhy-adhyāhāraḥ,  
antarēṇāpi vidhiṁ putra-janana-avagamād ēva harṣōtpattēḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor need an injunction be supplemented in these cases. For without an injunction, too, joy arises from the information that a son has been born. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca tatra vidhy-adhyāhāraḥ,  
antarēṇāpi vidhiṁ putra-janana-avagamād ēva harṣōtpattēḥ । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā "kā kriyā", "pākaḥ" ityādi-praśnōttara-vyavahārēṣu  
praṣṭr̥-jana-jijñāsita--kriyā-viśēṣa-- pratipādana-mātra--nirākāṅkṣaḥ śabdō  
na vidhy-adhyāhāram apēkṣatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise, a statement which is self-sufficient in merely expressing particular actions which questioners want to know in exchanges of question and answer-e.g. "Which action?" "Cooking!"-do not require the supplementation of an injunction. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā "kā kriyā", "pākaḥ" ityādi-praśnōttara-vyavahārēṣu praṣṭr̥-jana-jijñāsita-kriyā-viśēṣa-pratipādana-mātra-nirākāṅkṣaḥ śabdō na vidhy-adhyāhāram apēkṣatē ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

iha tu brahma-vijñānaṁ  
mahānanda-phalaṁ śrutam ॥  
"brahmavid brahma bhavati",  
"prāpnōti brahma-vit param" ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the upaniṣadic texts the knowledge of brahman is declared to be rewarded by great bliss: "the brahman-knower becomes brahman";159 "the brahman-knower attains the supreme";160 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[159]: This must refer to the śruti sa yo ha vai tat paraṃ veda brahma veda brahma bhavati (quoted Rāmanuja, Vedārthasṃgraha, 91), which I have been unable to locate.

[160]: Taitt Up. 2.1.1. brahmavid āpnoti param.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

iha tu ... Note the way in which Yāmuna connects the previous discussion with the main theme, viz, the validity of the Pāñcarātra-texts, based upon the authorship of Nārāyaṇa, the Supreme and Omniscient Being.

brahmavit ... Cf. Muṇḍaka: III-ii-9: “brahmaiva vēda brahmaiva bhavati” ।

prāpnōti ... Cf. Taittirīya: II-i-1: “brahmavid āpnōti param” ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

iha tu brahma-vijñānaṁ mahānanda-phalaṁ śrutam ॥  
"brahmavid brahma bhavati", "prāpnōti brahma-vit param" ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"aśnutē brahmaṇā sārdhaṁ  
sarvān kāmān sa sāmagaḥ" ॥  
idam-ādi-trayī-vākyair  
vyaktā tasya pum-arthatā । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"the sāman cantor attains with brahman  
all that he desires:"161  
the human importance of statements without injunctions is quite clear from these and other scriptural words. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[161]: This must refer to Taitt Up. 2.1.1 so'śnute sarvān kāmān saha brahmaṇā vipaścitā, but sa sāmagaḥ is obscure, unless one may regard it as a corruption of vipaścitā.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. ibid: “sō 'śnutē sarvān kāmān saha brahmaṇā vipaścitā” ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

"aśnutē brahmaṇā sārdhaṁ sarvān kāmān sa sāmagaḥ" ॥  
idam-ādi-trayī-vākyair vyaktā tasya pum-arthatā । 
</details>

### nigamanam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad ēvam udīrita-śruti-śata-samadhigatāvitatha- sahaja-sarva-sākṣāt-kārākāruṇyādi-kalyāṇa-guṇaika-rāśau bhagavati sidhyati,  
sidhyaty ēva tad-anubhava-mūlatayā tantra-prāmāṇyam ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

To sum up, when it is established that the Bhagavān is the treasury solely of beautiful qualities of direct universal cognition, compassionateness etc., qualities which are true and natural to Him, and which we know from hundreds of quoted śrutis, then it is also established that the Tantra which is based on His universal cognition is authoritative indeed.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Aniruddhasaṁhitā* : II. 7-8:

> tathā sarvēṣu śāstrēṣu pañca-rātraṁ variṣṭhakam ।  
śruti-mūlam idaṁ tantraṁ pramāṇaṁ kalpa-sūtravat ॥  
pañca-rātrē viśēṣēṇa viṣṇunā bhāṣitaṁ yathā ।  
ataḥ pramāṇaṁ lōkē 'smin dharma-śāstrēṣu sarvaśaḥ ॥

Also cf. Viṣṇusaṁhitā : ch. II:

> vēda-mūlatayā tantram āpta-mūlatayā 'thavā ॥ [11b]  
purāṇavat pramāṇaṁ syāt tathā manv-ādi-vākyavat। [12a]

> āpta-prōktatayā tantraṁ pramāṇam iti yē viduḥ ।  
vēda-prāmāṇyam apy āhur āpta-mūlatayaiva tē ॥ [19]

> viṣṇōr dharma-pravaktr̥tvāt tat-prōktaṁ manu-vākyavat ।  
brahma-viṣṇū hi dharmāṇāṁ pravaktārau budhais smr̥tau ॥ [21]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad ēvam udīrita-śruti-śata-samadhigatāvitatha-sahaja-sarva-sākṣātkārākāruṇyādi-kalyāṇa-guṇaika-rāśau bhagavati sidhyati,  
sidhyaty ēva tad-anubhava-mūlatayā tantra-prāmāṇyam । +++(4)+++
</details>

## 06 viṣṇuḥ paramaḥ

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu viracita-nītyā kaścid āmnāya-mūrddha--  
pramita-sahaja-sarva-jñānavān astu nāma ।  
sa ca harir iti yāvan nāvagamyēta samyak  
na khalu bhavati tāvatpañcarātraṁ pramāṇam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[64]]

> 79\. OBJECTION. Granted that, as you have described it, there exists some Person who is endowed with natural omniscience, as it is known from the upaniṣads, yet, unless it is absolutely certain that this Person is indeed Hari, Pañcaratra will not be authoritative. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The doubt expressed here by the opponent is as to who, among the trinity—Brahmā, Viṣṇu and Śiva, is the Supreme Deity. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu viracitanītyā kaścidāmnāyamūrddhapramitasahajasarvajñānavānastu nāma ।  
sa ca haririti yāvannāvagamyēta samyak na khalu bhavati tāvatpañcarātraṁ pramāṇam ॥  
</details>

### śrutiḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atyalpam ētat -  
na hy atra trayī-vidō vivadantē yad 

> vāsudēvaḥ paramātmā akhila-jagat-kāraṇam  

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. This is a worthless remark; no experts in the Veda dispute that the Supreme Soul, cause of the entire universe, is Vāsudeva. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The following is a brief exposition of the Supremacy of Nārāyaṇa. The Puruṣanirṇaya of Yāmuna, solely devoted to this question is yet to be traced out and as such, the importance of this part of the text need not be overemphasised. It indicates the way at least, in which the author had dealt with this question in the work.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atyalpamētat na hyatra trayīvidō vivadantē yadvāsudēvaḥ paramātmā akhilajagatkāraṇamiti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

śrūyatē hi sa vēdāntēṣv  

> ātmā nārāyaṇaḥ paraḥ ।  
satyaṁ jñānam anantañ ca  
tad viṣṇōḥ paramaṁ padam ॥  
parā prakr̥tir, adhyakṣō  
vāsudēvas tathā 'paraḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For He is revealed in the upaniṣads as the Supreme Soul: "Truth, knowledge, infinite; that is the supreme step of Viṣṇu. Vāsudeva is the ultimate matter, the ultimate spirit".162  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[162]: Partial quotations from Taitt Up. 2.1.1, Muṇḍ Up. and an unidentified source.

[162a]: Nrsiṃhapūrvatāpani Up. 2.4 (which reads purastād for parastād) and śvet Up. 3.9.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

vēdāntēṣvātmā ... Mahānārāyaṇa : XI. 4

satyaṁ ... Taittirīya : II-i-1.

tadviṣṇōḥ ... Yajurveda : VI-5; also Kaṭhopaniṣat : III-9.

parā ... To be traced out.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

śrūyatē hi sa vēdāntēṣvātmā nārāyaṇaḥ paraḥ ।  
satyaṁ jñānamanantañca tadviṣṇōḥ paramaṁ padam ॥  
parā prakr̥tiradhyakṣō vāsudēvastathā paraḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> ēkaḥ parastād ya idaṁ babhūva  
yasmāt paraṁ nāparam asti kiñcit ।  

ity ukta-vācyānuguṇaṁ "yatō vā  
imāni bhūtāni", "sadēva saumya" ॥  
ity-ādi-vākyañ ca tatas sa viṣṇus  
trayī-śiraḥ siddha-viśuddha-bōdhaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> He was alone beyond who became this world;162 "higher than whom there is nothing at all".  

In accordance with the subject expressed in these statements there are passages like: 

"From whom these beings..." "Sat alone, my son..."  

Therefore Viṣṇu's perfect knowledge is established by the upaniṣads. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

162: Nṛsiṃhapūrvatāpanī Up. 2\.4 (which reads purastāt for parastāt) and Śvet Up. 3\.9\.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ēkaḥ ... This appears in the Āyuṣyasūkta, beginning with “yō brahmā brahmaṇa ujjahāra”. The reading found is “ēkaḥ purastād ya idaṁ babhūva”. It appears on folio 15 b of palm-leaf ms. in Grantha, under R. No. 657, deposited in the Govt. Or. Mss. Library, Madras, and also on folio 42 a of another p.l. ms. in Grantha, R. No. 67 from the same library.

yasmātparaṁ ... Śvetāśvatara : III-9;

yatō ... Taittirīya : III-i-1;

sadēva ... Chāndogya : VI-ii-1.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēkaḥ parastādya idaṁ babhūva yasmāt paraṁ nāparamasti kiñcit ।  
ityuktavācyānuguṇaṁyatō vā imāni bhūtāni sadēva saumya ॥  
ityādivākyañca tatassa viṣṇustrayīśiraḥ siddhaviśuddhabōdhaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na cānyasmāj jagaj-janma-  
sthiti-dhvaṁsāś śrutau śrutāḥ ।  
yataś caitē sa sarvajñaḥ  
paramātmēti sammatam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And it is not declared in śruti that the origination, subsistence and destruction of the world are caused by anyone but Him. Hence there is a consensus that He is the supreme omniscient soul. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Brahmasūtra I-i-2 : “janmādyasya yataḥ” ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cānyasmājjagajjanmasthitidhvaṁsāśśrutau śrutāḥ ।  
yataścaitē sa sarvajñaḥ paramātmēti sammatam ॥  
</details>

### itihāsa-purāṇādi
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

amum ēva paramātmānaṁ  
dvaipāyana-parāśara--nārada-prabhr̥ti--maharṣi-vacanēbhyaḥ pratipadyāmahē।  
tathā hi -
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

That He is the Supreme Soul we learn also from the statements of Dvaipāyana, Parāśara, Nārada and other great seers. 

Thus -
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

amumēva paramātmānaṁ dvaipāyana-parāśaranāradaprabhr̥timaharṣivacanēbhyaḥ pratipadyāmahē। tathā hi -
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> viṣṇau jagat-sthitaṁ sarvam  
iti viddhi parantapa ।  
sr̥jaty ēṣa mahā-viṣṇur  
bhūta-grāmaṁ carācaram ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> "Know thou, O tormentor of thy foes, that the entire world rests on Viṣṇu. The Great Viṣṇu creates the totality of creatures, moving and unmoving. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Mahābhārata (Cr. edn.) XII. 271. 7-8. Variant : mahā-bāhō for mahā-viṣṇuḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

viṣṇau jagatsthitaṁ sarvamiti viddhi parantapa ।  
sr̥jatyēṣa mahāviṣṇurbhūtagrāmaṁ carācaram ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> ēṣa cākṣipatē kālē  
kālē visr̥jatē punaḥ ।  
asmin gacchanti vilayam  
asmācca prabhavantyuta ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> In him they go to their reabsorption, from Him they originate," 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> ēṣa cākṣipatē kālē kālē visr̥jatē punaḥ ।  
asmin gacchanti vilayamasmācca prabhavantyuta ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> anādinidhanaḥ śrīmān  
munir nārāyaṇaḥ prabhuḥ ।  
sa vai sr̥jati bhūtāni  
sthāvarāṇi carāṇi ca ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"The glorious Sage Nārāyaṇa, without beginning or end, is the sovereign Lord. He creates the creatures, those that stand still and those that move."163 

163: not identified.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. XII. 271. 19. Variant : hariḥ for muniḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> anādinidhanaḥ śrīmān munirnārāyaṇaḥ prabhuḥ ।  
sa vai sr̥jati bhūtāni sthāvarāṇi carāṇi ca ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sa brahma paramaṁ cēti  
tathā'nyatrāpi paṭhyatē ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

That He is the Supreme Brahman is also learnt elsewhere. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. XII. 280. 26 b. Variant paramō for paraṁ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sa brahma paramaṁ cēti  
tathā'nyatrāpi paṭhyatē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> kēśavō bharataśrēṣṭha!  
bhagavān īśvaraḥ paraḥ ।  
puruṣaḥ sarvam ity ētac  
chrūyatē bahudhā śrutau ॥

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> "Kesava, O best of the Bhāratas, the Blessed One, is the sovereign, the supreme soul, the entire universe: thus it stands revealed in many places of the Scripture."163 

[163]: not identified.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. XII. 200.5. Variants : prabhuḥ for paraḥ; ity ēva for ity ētat; vibhuḥ for śrutau ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kēśavō bharataśrēṣṭha! bhagavānīśvaraḥ paraḥ ।  
puruṣaḥ sarvamityētacchrūyatē bahudhā śrutau ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tattvaṁ jijñāsamānānāṁ  
hētubhiḥ sarvatō mukhaiḥ ।  
tattvam ēkō mahā-yōgī  
harir nārāyaṇaḥ prabhuḥ ॥ 

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> For those who seek to know the supreme principle by means of many-sided reasonings Hari alone is the Principle, the great Yogin, Nārāyaṇa the Lord.164 

[164]: not identified.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

165: Could this refer to Varāha Purāṇa Cf. infra. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. XII. 335. 83b-84a.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tattvaṁ jijñāsamānānāṁ hētubhiḥ sarvatō mukhaiḥ ।  
tattvamēkō mahāyōgī harirnārāyaṇaḥ prabhuḥ ॥ 

iti,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā dānadharmē -  

> paramātmā paraḥ śāntaḥ  
padma-nābhaḥ parāyaṇaḥ ।  
iti vēda-rahasyantu  
kin na vētsi purandara ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise in the Dānadharma, 

> "Padmanābha is the Supreme Soul, the highest One, the pure One, the Refuge. This is the secret doctrine of the Veda; dost thou not know, sacker of cities? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā dānadharmē -  

> paramātmā paraḥ śāntaḥ padmanābhaḥ parāyaṇaḥ ।  
iti vēdarahasyantu kinna vētsi purandara ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tat-prasādād vayaṁ sarvē  
lōkānāṁ sthiti-hētavaḥ ।  
āptāś cāmara-mukhyāś ca  
dēvāś ca sthāninō matāḥ ॥  
yadi viṣṇurudāsīnō  
nāsmākaṁ vidyatē śubham ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> By His grace do we all cause the worlds to exist. And the trusted ones, and the first among the immortals, and the gods are held to be His representatives, If Viṣṇu is indifferent, no good will come to us." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> tatprasādādvayaṁ sarvē lōkānāṁ sthitihētavaḥ ।  
āptāścāmaramukhyāśca dēvāśca sthāninō matāḥ ॥  
yadi viṣṇurudāsīnō nāsmākaṁ vidyatē śubham ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

iti rudrasya vacanaṁ,  
tathā bhāratamātsyayōḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Thus Rudra's word.165 Similarly, in the Mahābhārata and Matsya Purāṇa, 

[165]: Could this refer to Varaha Purana? Cf. infra.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

iti rudrasya vacanaṁ tathā bhāratamātsyayōḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tatra yaḥ paramātmā hi  
sa nityō nirguṇaś śubhaḥ ।  
sa vai nārāyaṇō jñēyaḥ  
sarvātmā puruṣō hi saḥ ॥ 

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> "He who amongst them is the Supreme Soul, He indeed is the eternal, unqualified, perfect One; He is to be known as Nārāyaṇa, for He is the world-soul, the Spirit." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Mahābhārata XII. 339. 14. Variants: nityaṁ for nityō; hi for vai ।

Cf. also ibid. XIII. App. 13, lines 20-21:

> ālōḍya sarva-śāstrāṇi vicārya ca punaḥ punaḥ ।  
idam ēkaṁ suniṣpannaṁ dhyēyō nārāyaṇaḥ sadā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatra yaḥ paramātmā hi sa nityō nirguṇaśśubhaḥ ।  
sa vai nārāyaṇō jñēyaḥ sarvātmā puruṣō hi saḥ ॥ 

iti,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā varāhē -  

> yasya dēvasya caritaṁ  
vrataṁ samabhavad bhuvi ।  
kō'nyas tasmād abhyadhikō  
muktvā nārāyaṇaṁ prabhum ॥

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise in the Varāha Purāṇa, 

"Who, excepting the Lord Nārāyaṇa, is superior to the God whose conduct has become the life-order on the earth?" 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be traced out.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā varāhē -  

yasya dēvasya caritaṁ vrataṁ samabhavadbhuvi ।  
kō'nyastasmādabhyadhikō muktvā nārāyaṇaṁ prabhum ॥

iti,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nārāyaṇātparō dēvō  
na bhūtō na bhaviṣyati ।  
ētad rahasyaṁ vēdānāṁ  
purāṇānāṁ ca sattamāḥ ॥ 

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"There has been no God greater than Nārāyaṇa, nor shall there be; this is the secret doctrine of the Vedas and the Purāṇas, O excellent ones."
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ch. 73. śl. 52.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nārāyaṇātparō dēvō na bhūtō na bhaviṣyati ।  
ētadrahasyaṁ vēdānāṁ purāṇānāṁ ca sattamāḥ ॥ iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā laiṅgēḥ -  

> sa ēkaḥ puruṣaḥ śrēṣṭhaḥ  
paramātmā janārdanaḥ ।  
yasmād brahmā tatō rudraḥ  
tataś caivākhilaṁ jagat ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise in the Liṅga Purāṇa, 

> "Janārdana is the sole Spirit, the highest One, the Supreme Soul, from whom Brahmā was born;  
from Him Rudra and from Him all the world." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Liṅgapurāṇa: uttarabhāga: Ch. I. śl. 7b-8a. There the reading is:

> ya ēkaḥ puruṣa-śrēṣṭhaḥ paramātmā janārdanaḥ ।  
yasmād brahmā tatas sarvaṁ samāśrityaiva mucyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā laiṅgēḥ -  
sa ēkaḥ puruṣaḥ śrēṣṭhaḥ paramātmā janārdanaḥ ।  
yasmād brahmā tatō rudraḥ tataścaivākhilaṁ jagat ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ।  

> viṣṇōs sakāśād udbhūtaṁ  
jagat tatraiva ca sthitam ।  
sthiti-saṁyama-kartā 'sāv  

iti pārāśaraṁ vacaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise Parāśara's word, 

> The world has originated from Viṣṇu and on Him it rests.  
He is the maker of its subsistence and its destruction."166

[166]: viṣṇu Pur., 1.1.31.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Viṣṇupurāṇa: I. 1. 35. The remainder of the śloka is: ‘jagatō 'sya jagac ca saḥ’
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ।  
viṣṇōssakāśādudbhūtaṁ jagattatraiva ca sthitam ।  
sthitisaṁyamakartā'sāviti pārāśaraṁ vacaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā mānavē -  

> nārāyaṇaḥ parō'vyaktād  
aṇḍam avyakta-saṁbhavam ।  
aṇḍasyāntas tv imē lōkāḥ  
sapta-dvīpā ca mēdinī ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise in the Mānavadharmaśāstra,167 

"Nārāyaṇa is higher than the unmanifest; the World-Egg originates from the unmanifest. Within the Egg are all these worlds as well as the earth with her seven continents." 

[167]: Not in manusmṛti.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This verse is not found in the Manusmṛti commented by Bhaṭṭa Medhātithi. It is however, found inserted between the 10th and 11th verses of the first chapter in the Manvarthamuktāvalī with Kullūka's commentary [ Kāśī Skt. Series, 1935 ]. Kullūka too did not comment upon it.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā mānavē -  

nārāyaṇaḥ parō'vyaktādaṇḍamavyaktasaṁbhavam ।  
aṇḍasyāntastvimē lōkāḥ saptadvīpā ca mēdinī ॥  
</details>

### nigamanam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tasmād īdr̥śa-śruti-smr̥tītihāsa-purāṇa-paryālōcanayā  

> akhila-jagat-kāraṇaṁ paramātmā vāsudēva  

iti niścīyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore, the study of these and similar śrutis, smṛtis, epical texts and Purāṇas proves that Vāsudeva is the universal cause, the Supreme Soul.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasmādīdr̥śaśrutismr̥tītihāsapurāṇaparyālōcanayā akhilajagatkāraṇaṁ paramātmā vāsudēva iti niścīyatē ।  
</details>

### na śivādiḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na caivaṁ paramātmatvaṁ  
rudrādēḥ śrutiṣūditam ।  
pratyutōtpattim ēvāhus  
tasyaikāyana-śākhinaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

80\. Nor do the śrutis declare that Rudra is the Supreme Soul, or that any other deity is. On the contrary, the followers of the Ekāyana śākhā 168 say that he has an origin,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[168]: A little known Vedic branch (if it was a Vedic tradition), from which certain vaiṣṇava sects derive their authority; cf. infra §138.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The Pāñcarātrins are the followers of the Ekāyanaśākhā, one of the redactions of the Śukla Yajurveda.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na caivaṁ paramātmatvaṁ rudrādēḥ śrutiṣūditam ।  
pratyutōtpattim ēvāhus tasyaikāyana-śākhinaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"tamō vā idam" ity-ādau  
tathā vēdē 'pi dr̥śyatē ।  
"yatō hi rudras sañjajñē  
tat śrēṣṭhaṁ bhuvanēṣv" iti ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and the same is found in the Veda itself:  

> "Darkness was here....  
from which Rudra is born;  
that is the greatest in all the worlds," 

169: These quotations could not be identified.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Maitrīyopaniṣat V. 2.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

"tamō vā idam" ity-ādau tathā vēdē 'pi dr̥śyatē ।  
yatō hi rudras sañjajñē tat śrēṣṭhaṁ bhuvanēṣv iti ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"tat id āsa bhuvanēṣu jyēṣṭham" iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"that indeed is the oldest in the worlds." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ṛgveda X. 120. i.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

"tat id āsa bhuvanēṣu jyēṣṭham" iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā raudraṁ padaṁ spaṣṭaṁ  
karma-janyaṁ pratīyatē ॥  
"mahimānaṁ nijaṁ lēbhē  
viṣṇōr abhyarthanād" iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Similarly, Rudra's position is clearly known to be a result of his karman: "He obtained his greatness by propitiating Viṣṇu." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā raudraṁ padaṁ spaṣṭaṁ karma-janyaṁ pratīyatē ॥  
"mahimānaṁ nijaṁ lēbhē viṣṇōr abhyarthanād" iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"asya dēvasyē"ti,  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. VII. 40. 5.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

"asya dēvasyē"ti,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"lalāṭād abhavad-bindus  
tasmād rudrō vyajāyata ।"  
ity-ādikāś ca śrutayō  
rudrōtpattiṁ vadanti vai ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"From the forehead sprang a drop; from that Rudra was born,"169  
These and other śrutis declare that Rudra was born. 

[169]: These quotations could not be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Subālopaniṣat II. 1: “lalāṭāt krōdha-jō rudrō jāyatē ।”
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

"lalāṭād abhavad-bindus tasmād rudrō vyajāyata ।"  
ityādikāś ca śrutayō rudrōtpattiṁ vadanti vai ।
</details>

#### purāṇa-vāda-nirvāhaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ēvañca sati rudrādi-  
mahimāvēdikā iva ।  
yā vācas tās stuti-parāḥ  
"śrōtraṁ brahma" iti gīr iva ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This being so, the statements that in appearance convey the greatness of Rudra and others really serve as laudatory statements, like the śruti: "the ear is brahman."170

[[67]]

[170]: BA Up 4.1.5.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Bṛhadāraṇyaka IV. i. 5: “śrōtraṁ vai brahma” ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvañca sati rudrādi-mahimā-vēdikā iva ।  
yā vācas tās stuti-parāḥ "śrōtraṁ brahma" iti gīr iva ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ētēna rudrādīnāṁ paramātmatva-pratipādaka-purāṇa-vādāḥ  
pratyakṣa-śruti-virōdhān na mukhya-arthāḥ । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Consequently, the passages in the Purāṇas which declare Rudra etc. to be the Supreme Soul have not their primary meaning, because they are in conflict with ~~Perception and~~ clear Scripture.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ētēna rudrādīnāṁ paramātmatva-pratipādaka-purāṇa-vādāḥ  
pratyakṣa-śruti-virōdhān na mukhya-arthāḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad vā tyājyatayā tantra-  
siddhānta-pratipādakāḥ +++(purāṇa-vādāḥ)+++।  
a-vaidikēṣu tantrēṣu  
tan+++(←rudrādi)+++-māhātmyaṁ hi kathyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

81\. Concerning the objection that the assertions of the doctrines of the Tantras are to be rejected  
since their greatness is set forth only in non-Vedic Tantric texts,  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yad vā tyājyatayā tantra-siddhānta-pratipādakāḥ ।  
avaidikēṣu tantrēṣu tan-māhātmyaṁ hi kathyatē ॥
</details>

### vēdānukūla-purāṇāni
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vēda-siddhānta-mārgēṣu viṣṇur ēva paraḥ smr̥taḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

we say that Viṣṇu is stated to be the Supreme One in the texts of the Way of the Vedic doctrine. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This line occurs below. It is from the Bhaviṣya Purāṇa, to be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vēda-siddhānta-mārgēṣu viṣṇur ēva paraḥ smr̥taḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad yathā vaiṣṇavē -

> paramātmā ca sarvēṣām  
ādhāraḥ paramēśvaraḥ ।  
viṣṇu-nāmā sa vēdēṣu  
vēdāntēṣu ca gīyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For example in the Viṣṇu Purāṇa, "The Supreme Soul, the Basis of all creatures, the Supreme Lord is called by the name of Viṣṇu in Vedas and Upaniṣads."171 

[171]: viṣṇu Pur. 6.4.40.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Viṣṇupurāṇa VI. iv. 39.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad yathā vaiṣṇavē -

> paramātmā ca sarvēṣām ādhāraḥ paramēśvaraḥ ।  
> viṣṇu-nāmā sa vēdēṣu vēdāntēṣu ca gīyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vārāhē ।

> viṣṇur ēva paraṁ brahma  
tri-bhēdam iha paṭhyatē ।  
vēda-siddhānta-mārgēṣu  
tan na jānanti mōhitāḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the Varāha Purāṇa, "The Supreme Brahman is Viṣṇu; the triple division in the pathways of the Vedic doctrine is here set forth; the ignorant do not know this."172 

[172]: cf. Varāha Pur., 72.4, which reads padyate in b. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Varāhapurāṇa [Sri Venkatesvara Press, Bombay], Ch. 72. śl. 4.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vārāhē ।

> viṣṇur ēva paraṁ brahma tri-bhēdam iha paṭhyatē ।  
> vēda-siddhānta-mārgēṣu tan na jānanti mōhitāḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nārāyaṇāt parō dēvō  
na bhūtō na bhaviṣyati ।  
> ētad rahasyaṁ vēdānāṁ  
purāṇānāṁ ca sattamāḥ ॥ 

iti ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"There has been no god greater than Nārāyaṇa, nor shall there be;173 this is the secret doctrine of Vedas and Purāṇas, O excellent ones." 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[173]: cf. Varāha Pur. 70.26 na tasmāt parato devo bhavitā na bhaviṣyati. It is clear from several quotations from this Purāṇa that Yāmuna's text had different readings, not all of them better.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ch. 73, śl. 52.

Also cf. ibid. Ch. 70, śl. 26a:

> na tasmāt paratō dēvō bhavitā na bhaviṣyati।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> nārāyaṇāt parō dēvō na bhūtō na bhaviṣyati ।  
> ētad-rahasyaṁ vēdānāṁ purāṇānāṁ ca sattamāḥ ॥ iti ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā mātsyē ।

> sāttvikēṣu tu kalpēṣu  
viṣṇōr māhātmyam ucyatē ।  
agnēś śivasya māhātmyaṁ  
tāmasēṣu prakīrtyatē ॥ 

iti ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise in the Matsya Purāṇa, "In those aeons where sattva prevails, the greatness of Viṣṇu is declared. In aeons predominated by tamas the greatness of Fire and Śiva is expounded."174 

[174]: Matsya Pur. 290.15.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Matsya Purāṇa Ch. 53, śl. 67b-68a.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā mātsyē ।

> sāttvikēṣu tu kalpēṣu viṣṇōr māhātmyam ucyatē ।  
> agnēś śivasya māhātmyaṁ tāmasēṣu prakīrtyatē ॥ 

iti ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā laiṅgē ।

> na hi viṣṇum r̥tē kācid  
gatir anyā vidhīyatē ।  
ity ēvaṁ satataṁ vēdā  
gāyantē nātra saṁśayaḥ ॥ 

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise in the Liṅga Purāṇa, 

> "For there is no other recourse ordained but Viṣṇu; this the Vedas constantly declare, no doubt about it."175 

175: The Liṅga, Vāyu and Bhaviṣyat quotations could not be verified.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Liṅga Purāṇa [ Pūrva ] Ch. 24, śl. 143.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā laiṅgē ।

> na hi viṣṇum r̥tē kā-cid gatir anyā vidhīyatē ।  
> ity ēvaṁ satataṁ vēdā gāyantē nātra saṁśayaḥ ॥ iti,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā vāyavīyē ।

> sahasra-bāhuḥ paramaḥ prajāpatiḥ ।  
> trayī-pathēyaḥ puruṣō nirucyatē ॥ 

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[68]]

Likewise in the Vāyu Purāṇa,

"The Spirit that belongs to the Way of the Veda is explained to be the thousand-armed supreme lord of creatures." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Passages to be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā vāyavīyē ।

> sahasra-bāhuḥ paramaḥ prajāpatiḥ ।  
> trayī-pathēyaḥ puruṣō nirucyatē ॥ 

iti,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā bhaviṣyati ।

> vēda-siddhānta-mārgēṣu  
viṣṇur ēva paraḥ smr̥taḥ ।  
viṣṇur ēva nara-śrēṣṭhō  
mahiṣṭhaḥ puruṣōttamaḥ ॥ 

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise in the Bhaviṣyat Purāṇa, "Visnu is traditionally known to be the Supreme in the pathways of the Vedic doctrine. Viṣṇu is the greatest among persons, the most exalted Supreme Person."175 

[175]: The Linga, Vayu and Bhavisyat quotations could not be verified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā bhaviṣyati ।

> vēda-siddhānta-mārgēṣu viṣṇur ēva paraḥ smr̥taḥ ।  
> viṣṇur ēva nara-śrēṣṭhō mahiṣṭhaḥ puruṣōttamaḥ ॥ 

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

All this has already been explained in great detail in the Puruṣanirṇaya176 and is therefore not further enlarged upon here. 

[176]: Title of one of Yāmuna's treatises.
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sarvaṁ caitat puruṣa-nirṇayē nipuṇataram upapāditam iti nēha prapañcyatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Puruṣanirṇaya is another work of Yāmuna, which is yet to be recovered.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sarvaṁ caitat puruṣa-nirṇayē nipuṇataram upapāditam iti nēha prapañcyatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>rāma-miśraḥ</summary>

puruṣa-nirṇaya-nāmā bhagavan-mahima-pratipādana-puraḥsarō-dēvatāntara-vyāvartana-mukhēna viṣṇu-para-tattva-pratipādana-parō granthaḥ paramācārya-praṇītaḥ ।
</details>

## 07 pāñcarātra-dānam

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tataś ca ।  

śruti-mūrdhni prasiddhēna  
vāsudēvēna bhāṣitam ।  
tantraṁ mithyēti vaktuṁ naḥ  
kathaṁ jihvā pravartatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore, how can our tongue endeavour to say that the Tantra which is revealed by Viṣṇu who is known from the Upaniṣads is false? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tataś ca ।  
śruti-mūrdhni prasiddhēna vāsudēvēna bhāṣitam ।  
tantraṁ mithyēti vaktuṁ naḥ kathaṁ jihvā pravartatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> sa hi sahaja-saṁvēdana-sākṣāt-kr̥ta--dīkṣā''rādhanādi-dharmaḥ  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> For He is such that He has an immediate insight into the dharma of Consecration, Propitiation etc., by virtue of the omniscience that is natural to Him.177

[177]: read sa hi sahajasaṃvedanasākṣātkṛta dīkṣārādhanādidharmaḥ
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> sa hi sahaja-saṁvēdana-sākṣāt-kr̥ta--dīkṣā''rādhanādi-dharmaḥ  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

svarga-putrādi-vaiṣayika-sukham anēka-duḥkha-saṁbhinnam,  
na cāticiram anuvartata 

iti
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

82\. Considering that 

> the sensual pleasure to be had  
from attainment of heaven, the birth of a son etc.  
is inseparable from various forms of misery and does not, continue for long,  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi sahajasaṁvēdanasākṣātkr̥tadīkṣā''rādhanādidharmaḥ svargaputrādivaiṣayikasukhamanēkaduḥkhasaṁbhinnam,
na cāticiramanuvartata iti
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad api duḥkha-pakṣa ēva nikṣipya  
mōkṣāya gr̥hēbhyaḥ pravrajadbhyaḥ śāṇḍilya-nāradādi-parama-r̥ṣibhyas  
tad-abhilaṣita-niratiśaya-niśrēyasaika-sādhana--  
svāvagamārādhanāvabōdhinīṁ pañcarātra-saṁhitāṁ niramimītēti niścīyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

the supreme sages Sandilya,. Narada and others have rejected this pleasure,  
which in their view was really misery,  
and in order to attain the release left their dwellings to become mendicants;  
and they have decided definitively that  
He has created the Pañcarātra Sastra  
which sets forth the knowledge and manner of propitiation of Himself  
which constitute the sole means of attaining the unparalleled beatitude they sought. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadapi duḥkhapakṣa ēva nikṣipya  
mōkṣāya gr̥hēbhyaḥ pravrajadbhyaḥ śāṇḍilyanāradādiparamar̥ṣibhyastadabhilaṣitaniratiśayaniśrēyasaikasādhanasvāvagamārādhana avabōdhinīṁ pañcarātrasaṁhitāṁ niramimītēti niścīyatē ।  
</details>

## 08 tantrāntarād bhēdaḥ

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**na** ca tantrāntarēṣv ēṣa  
nyāyaḥ **prasaram** arhati ।  
yatas tat-tan-nibanddhr̥̄ṇāṁ  
vibhramādy api **saṁbhavi** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

83\. This argument cannot be extended to other Tantras,  
for in the various authors of those Tantras error etc. is possible.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca tantrāntarēṣvēṣa nyāyaḥ prasaramarhati ।  
yatastattannibanddhr̥̄ṇāṁ vibhramādyapi saṁbhavi ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pratyakṣādi-pramāṇānāṁ  
na hi +++(tantrāntara-)+++mūlatva-sambhavaḥ ।  
tantrāntarēṣu +++(prāmāṇika-)+++śāstran tu  
mūlaṁ tair ēva nēṣyatē ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It is impossible that Perception [[69]] 
or another means of knowledge forms the basis for the other Tantras,  
and they themselves do also not claim that Scripture is the basis.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pratyakṣādipramāṇānāṁ na hi mūlatvasambhavaḥ ।  
tantrāntarēṣu śāstrantu mūlaṁ tairēva nēṣyatē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

anyac ca vēda-siddhānta-  
viruddhārthābhidhānataḥ ।  
pratyakṣa-śruti-mūlatva-  
kalpanā tēṣu **bādhyatē** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Besides, because they communicate a meaning  
that is incompatible with the conclusions of the upanisads  
the view that these Tantras are based on Perception or Scripture is sublated. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anyacca vēdasiddhāntaviruddhārthābhidhānataḥ ।  
pratyakṣaśrutimūlatvakalpanā tēṣu bādhyatē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā māhēśvarē tantrē  
**viruddhaṁ** bahu **jalpitam** ।  
catur-vidhā hi tat-siddha-  
caryā-mārgānusāriṇaḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For there are four kinds of followers of the way of life set forth in those Tantras, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The followers of the Māheśvara Doctrine are fourfold : Śaivas, Pāśupatas, Kāpālikas and Kāruṇikasiddhāntins, according to Vācaspati and Ānandagiri. Yāmuna calls the fourth group, Kālāmukhas. Rāmānuja follows Yāmuna in calling them so. The term Māheśvara is a name common for the followers of all these sects.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā māhēśvarē tantrē viruddhaṁ bahu jalpitam ।  
caturvidhā hi tatsiddhacaryāmārgānusāriṇaḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā kāpālikāḥ kālā-  
mukhāḥ pāśupatās tathā ।  
śaivās, tatra ca kāpālaṁ  
matam ēvaṁ pracakṣatē ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

the Kāpālikas, Kālamukhas, Pasupatas and Saivas.  
The Kapalika doctrine is described as follows: 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See M. R. Sakhare, Liṅgādhāraṇacandrikā, pp.331-332:

> In the Vāyupurāṇa (ch. 23) and the Liṅgapurāṇa (ch. 24) it is said that Maheśvara told Brahmā that when Vāsudeva is born, he would incarnate himself as a Brahmacārin by the name of Lakulin and that Lakulin would have four pupils of names Kushika, Garga, Mitra and Kaurushya, these would be Pāśupatas. The refutation of the Pāśupata system is found in the Brahmasūtra: “patyurasāmañjasyāt” (II. ii. 37).

> From all this it appears that the Pāśupata school was founded by Lakulīśa (the holder of lakula or lakuṭa — a club or staff). This Lakulīśa (also called Nakulīśa) is the last of the 28 incarnations of Śiva as mentioned by the Purāṇas. This has been confirmed by inscriptions too.

The Kālāmukhas and Kāpālikas were two different sects of the Māheśvaras. Dr. Bhandarkar (in his Śaivism and Vaiṣṇavism, etc., P.183), identifies the Kālāmukhas with Mahāvratadharas on the authority of Śivapurāṇa but M. R. Sakhare, on the evidence of a Jain author, states that the Kāpālikas but not the Kālāmukhas were the same as Mahāvratadharas (pp.344 f.).

The Kālāmukhas, according to T. A. Gopinatha Rao (Elements of Hindu Iconography, Vol. II, P.26), were so called as they marked their forehead with black streak and were said to be the offspring of “nara” and “rākṣasa” parents.

> The Kāpālika system is very ancient since it is mentioned in the Maitrī Upaniṣad (‘atha ye cānye ha vṛthā kaṣāyakuṇḍalinaḥ kāpālinaḥ’)

[Liṅgādhāraṇacandrikā, P.344].

> The allegorical drama, Prabodhacandrodaya of Kṛṣṇamiśra (III. 12, 13) introduces a Kāpālika, who describes himself and his practices as follows:
>
> narāsthi-mālā-kr̥ta-cāru-bhūṣaṇaḥ  
śmaśāna-vāsī nr̥-kapāla-bhōjanaḥ ।  
paśyāmi yōgāñjana-śuddha-jakṣuṣā  
jagan mithō bhinnam abhinnam īśvarāt ॥  
mastiṣkāntra-vasabhi-pūrita-mahā-māṁsāhutīḥ juhvatāṁ  
vahnau brahma-kapāla-kalpita-surā-pānēna naḥ pāraṇā ।  
sadyaḥ-kr̥tta-kaṭhōra-kaṇṭha-vigalat-kīlāla-dhārōjjvalaiḥ  
arcyō naḥ puruṣōpahāra-balibhir dēvō mahā-bhairavaḥ ॥

[Ibid. P.345]

Also vide Indian Philosophy by Dr. S. Radhakrishnan, Vol. I, P.488:

> The Rudra of the Ṛgveda (I. 114.8), the personification of the destructive powers of nature, becomes in the Śatarudrīya, the Lord of Cattle, ‘paśūnāṁ patiḥ’. In the Brāhmaṇas, Śiva becomes the distinctive term for Rudra. The Pāśupata system continues the tradition of Rudra-Śiva. In the Mahābhārata, we find a theology named Pāśupata centring round Śiva [Śāntiparvan, ch. 149, v. 64]. We have an account of this system in Sarvadarśanasaṅgraha and Advaitānanda's Brahmavidyābharaṇa. Śaṅkara criticises this theology in his commentary (II. ii. 37-39).

For a history and philosophy of these different schools of Śaivism from inscriptional data, see V. S. Pathak, History of Śaiva Cults in Northern India from Inscriptions, pp.4-28.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā kāpālikāḥ kālāmukhāḥ pāśupatāstathā ।  
śaivāstatra ca kāpālaṁ matamēvaṁ pracakṣatē ॥  
</details>

### kāpālikāḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

mudrikā-ṣaṭka-vijñānāt  
punas tasyaiva **dhāraṇāt** ।  
apavarga-phala-**prāptir**  
**na brahmāvagamād** iti ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

the reward of release is attained by knowing  
what the six mudrikas are and by wearing them,  
not by knowing Brahman. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

External signs worn by Saiva sectarians.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Passages to be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

mudrikāṣaṭkavijñānāt punastasyaiva dhāraṇāt ।  
apavargaphalaprāptirna brahmāvagamāditi ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā'huḥ ।  

> mudrikā-ṣaṭka-tattva-jñaḥ  
para-mudrā-viśāradaḥ ।  
bhagāsana-stham ātmānaṁ  
dhyātvā nirvāṇam r̥cchati ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As they say, 

> "He who knows the identities of the six mudrikas  
> and is expert in the supreme Mudra,  
> and meditates upon the self in the vulva posture, attains nirvana." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā'huḥ ।  
mudrikāṣaṭkatattvajñaḥ paramudrāviśāradaḥ ।  
bhagāsanasthamātmānaṁ dhyātvā nirvāṇamr̥cchati ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā -  

> karṇikāṁ rucakañ+++(=hāraṁ)+++ caiva  
kuṇḍalañ ca śikhā-maṇim ।  
bhasma yajñō-pavītañ  
ca mudrā-ṣaṭkaṁ **pracakṣatē** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The six mudrikas of the Kāpālikas are stated to be the earring, necklace, pendent, head ornament, ashes and the sacrificial thread: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā -  
karṇikāṁ rucakañcaiva kuṇḍalañca śikhāmaṇim ।  
bhasma yajñōpavītañca mudrāṣaṭkaṁ pracakṣatē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> kapālam atha khaṭvāṅgam  
upamudrē **prakīrtitē** ।  
ābhir **mudrita**-dēhas tu  
**na** bhūya iha **jāyatē** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

there are two more subsidiary mudras described, namely skull and skull-staff.  
One whose body is marked by these mudras will not be reborn in the world." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kapālamatha khaṭvāṅgamupamudrē prakīrtitē ।  
ābhirmudritadēhastu na bhūya iha jāyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**na** cēdr̥śa-mudrikā-ṣaṭka-parijñāna--tad-dhāraṇa--  
nindita-bhagāsana-stha-dēha-dhyānasyāpavarga-sādhanatvaṁ śrutayō **mr̥ṣyanti**,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Now, the śrutis do not bear out their view that the knowledge of such paraphernalia, the wearing of them  
and the concentration on the body in the immoral vulva posture  
are means to attain release,  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cēdr̥śamudrikāṣaṭkaparijñāna -taddhāraṇa -ninditabhagāsanasthadēhadhyānasyāpavargasādhanatvaṁ śrutayō mr̥ṣyanti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tā hy aihikāmuṣmika-sakala-viṣayābhilāṣa-vimukhasya  
a-khila--jagat-kāraṇa-vāsudēvātma-bhāvaika-labhyaṁ mōkṣam  
**ācakṣatē** -
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for the śrutis expound that  
release is attainable only by one who has renounced all sensual desires of this world and the other world  
and who concentrates on the soul Vasudeva as the cause of the entire Universe: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tā hyaihikāmuṣmikasakalaviṣayābhilāṣavimukhasya akhilajagatkāraṇavāsudēvātmabhāvaikalabhyaṁ mōkṣamācakṣatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tam ēva viditvā atimr̥tyumēti 

> nānyaḥ panthā ayanāya vidyatē 

ity-ādyāḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"knowing Him one goes beyond death;  
there is no other path to tread etc." (Svet Up. 3.8.) 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Taittirīya Āraṇyaka III. xiii. 1; also Śvetāśvatara VI. 15.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tamēva viditvā atimr̥tyumēti nānyaḥ panthā ayanāya vidyatē ityādyāḥ, 
</details>

### kālāmukhāḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ēvaṁ kālāmukhā api  
samasta-śāstra-pratiṣiddha--kapāla-bhōjana--śava-bhasma-snāna--  
tat-prāśana--laguḍa-dhāraṇa--surā-kumbha-sthāpana--tat-stha-dēvatārcanādēr ēva  
dr̥ṣṭādr̥ṣṭābhīṣṭa-**siddhim abhidadhānāḥ** śruti-bahiṣkr̥tā ēva ।  
</details>

<details><summary>viśvāsa-ṭippanī</summary>

iha kāpālika-kālāmukhayōr bhramō bhāti।  
tad ēva śrībhāṣyē 'nuvartitaṁ rāmānujēnēti ca śrībhāṣyē (ii.2.35-37)।  

sambaddham - [TW](https://manasataramgini.wordpress.com/2005/03/26/dvijas-and-non-dvijas-in-the-shaiva-cults/)।

> Many antinomian Kapalika rituals were first developed by Lakula-s/Kalamukha-s, the former just took it further. In his thesis Schwartz compares Ramanuja's description of the Kalamukha to the Pingalamata I believe; it matches up very well, but the latter is not Atimargic per se. - Andra 

</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The same is. true of the Kalamukhas who teach 
that certain practices,  
which are condemned by all the [[70]] sāstras,  
like eating from a skull,  
bathing in and tasting of ashes of cremated corpses,  
carrying a laguḍa staff,  
putting up wine-cups and worshipping the deity in them,  
will secure all material and immaterial desires:  
these teachings are outside the Veda. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvaṁ kālāmukhā api samastaśāstrapratiṣiddhakapālabhōjana-śavabhasmasnāna tatprāśana -laguḍadhāraṇa surākumbhasthāpana tatsthadēvatārcanādērēva dr̥ṣṭādr̥ṣṭābhīṣṭasiddhimabhidadhānāḥ śrutibahiṣkr̥tā ēva ।  
</details>

### pāśupatāḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad api pāśupata-śaivābhyāṁ viruddhāviruddha-sama-+++(miśraṇa-)+++mugdhaṁ kiñcid abhihitaṁ  
tad api śruti-bahiṣ-kr̥tam ēva ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

84\. Also some of the teachings of the Pasupatas and the Saivas  
in which compatible and incompatible elements are indiscriminately mixed  
are likewise outside the Veda, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadapi pāśupataśaivābhyāṁ viruddhāviruddhasamamugdhaṁ kiñcidabhihitaṁ tadapi śrutibahiṣkr̥tamēva ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatraiṣā pāśupataprakriyā ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The Pasupata system is as follows: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatraiṣā pāśupataprakriyā ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

jīvāḥ paśava **ucyantē**  
tēṣām adhipatiś śivaḥ ।  
sa tēṣām **upakārāya**  
pañcādhyāyīm **acīkl̥pat** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

there are individual souls which are called paśus, cattle,  
and their overlord is Siva, the Lord of Cattle.  
To assist the souls Siva has composed the Paficādhyāyi. ("The Doctrine of the Five Chapters.")
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

jīvāḥ ... Vide Pāśupatasūtra with Kauṇḍinya's commentary, I. 1, P.5:

> paśyanāt pāśanāc ca paśavaḥ । tatra pāśā nāma kārya-kāraṇākhyāḥ kalāḥ ।

Also see ibid:

> sāṅkhya-yōgēna yē muktāḥ, sāṅkhya-yōgēśvarāś ca yē ।  
brahmādayas tiryag-antāḥ sarvē tē paśavaḥ smr̥tāḥ ॥

pañcādhyāyīm ... This Pañcādhyāyī* is, in all probability, same as the Pāśupatasūtra, referred to above. This work is in five chapters, dealing with the five characteristics of this cult, viz., Kāraṇa, Kārya, Vidhi, Yoga and Duḥkhānta, which also go by the name Pañcapadārthas or Pañcārthas.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

jīvāḥ paśava ucyantē tēṣāmadhipatiśśivaḥ ।  
sa tēṣāmupakārāya pañcādhyāyīmacīkl̥pat ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatra pañca padārthās tu  
vyākhyātāḥ kāraṇādayaḥ ।  
kāraṇaṁ kāryaṁ vidhir yōgō  
duḥkhāntaḥ …॥  

iti,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

There the five Categories are explained, namely,  
Cause, Effect, Injunction, Yoga and the Cessation of Misery. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Kauṇḍinya's commentary on the Pāśupatasūtra : I-i, P.6:

> ēvaṁ saduḥkhāntaṁ kāryaṁ kāraṇaṁ yōgō vidhir iti pañcaiva padārthāḥ samāsata uddiṣṭāḥ ।

Vide Indian Philosophy, Vol. I, P.489:

> The five categories are:

> 1.  Kāraṇa or Cause: The Cause is the Lord, the Pati, the Eternal ruler, who creates, maintains and destroys the whole existence.

> 2.  Kārya or Effect: It is what is dependent on the cause. It includes knowledge or vidyā, organs or kalā and individual souls or paśu. All knowledge and existence, the five elements and the five qualities, the five senses and the five organs of actions and the three internal organs of intelligence, egoism and mind are dependent on the Lord.

> 3.  Yoga or Discipline: It is the mental process by which the individual soul gains God.

> 4.  Vidhi or Rules: It relates to the practices that make for righteousness.

> 5.  Duḥkhānta or the end of misery: It is final deliverance or destruction of misery and obtaining an elevation of spirit, with full powers of Knowledge and Action.

For a more detailed explanation of these categories, see Liṅgādhāraṇacandrikā, pp.351-57.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatra pañca padārthāstu vyākhyātāḥ kāraṇādayaḥ ।  
kāraṇaṁ kāryaṁ vidhiryōgō duḥkhāntaḥ ॥  

iti,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

upādānaṁ nimittañ ca  
vyākhyātaṁ **kāraṇaṁ** dvidhā ।  
nimitta-kāraṇaṁ rudras  
tat-kalā kāraṇāntaram ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The Cause is of two kinds, material and instrumental.  
Rudra is the instrumental cause  
and a sixteenth part of him is the material cause.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

upādānaṁ nimittañca vyākhyātaṁ kāraṇaṁ dvidhā ।  
nimittakāraṇaṁ rudrastatkalā kāraṇāntaram ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

mahy-antaṁ mahad-ādi **kāryam** uditaṁ, tadvad **vidhir** gīyatē  
gūḍhācāra-mukha-smaśāna-bhasita-snānāvasānaḥ, paraḥ ।  
**yōgō** dhāraṇam ucyatē hr̥di dhiyām ōṅkāra-pūrvan tathā   
**duḥkhāntō** hi matō 'pavarga - iti tē pañcāpi **saṁkīrtitāḥ** +++(pūrvaślōkastha-kāraṇēna saha)+++ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The Effect comprises the elements from Mahat to earth.  
The Injunction is stated to comprehend principally a number of rites, secret practices, bathing and lying in ashes etc. 182  

The Yoga is said to be concentration and the muttering of formula, OM etc.   
The Cessation of Misery is held to be release;   
The term "cessation' of misery" means total and final cessation of misery.  
thus the five Categories are enumerated.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Mahat - The highest material evolute.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

gūḍhācāra ... Cf. Pāśupatasūtra : IV. 2 : ‘gūḍhavataḥ’; IV. 3 : ‘gūḍha-pavitra-pāṇiḥ’; IV. 4: ‘sarvāṇi dvārāṇi pidhāya’; IV. 5 : ‘buddhyā’।

smaśāna ... Ibid. V. 30 : ‘smaśāna-vāsī’

bhasita ... Ibid. I : 2, 3, 4 : ‘bhasmanā tri-ṣavaṇaṁ snāyīta’, ‘bhasmani śayīta’, ‘anusnānam’।

hr̥di ... Ibid. V. 23, 24 & 25 : ‘atō yōgaḥ pravartēta’, ‘ōṅkāram abhidhyāyīta’, ‘hr̥di kurvīta dhāraṇam’।

duḥkhāntō ... Ibid. V. 40 :    

> apramādī gacchēt duḥkhānām antam īśa-prasādāt ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

mahyantaṁ mahadādikāryamuditaṁ tadvadvidhirgīyatē ।  
gūḍhācāramukhasmaśānabhasitasnānāvasānaḥ paraḥ ॥  
yōgō dhāraṇamucyatē hr̥di dhiyāmōṅkārapūrvantathā ।  
duḥkhāntō hi matō'pavarga iti tē pañcāpi saṁkīrtitāḥ ॥
</details>

### mukti-kalpanā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ātyāntikī duḥkha-nivr̥ttir dukhānta-śabdēnōktā  
tām ēva niśśēṣa-vaiśēṣikātma-guṇōcchēda-lakṣaṇāṁ muktiṁ **manyatē**। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The system holds that this cessation or release is defined by the annihilation of all the qualities of the differential soul. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ātyāntikī duḥkhanivr̥ttirdukhāntaśabdēnōktā tāmēva niśśēṣavaiśēṣikātmaguṇōcchēdalakṣaṇāṁ muktiṁ manyatē
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

iyamēva cēśvarakalpanā śaivānāmanyēṣāṁ ca ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This conception of God is held by the Saivas as well as the others. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

iyamēva cēśvarakalpanā śaivānāmanyēṣāṁ ca ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sēyaṁ sarvā śruti-viruddhā kalpanā yataḥ -  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[71]]  
And this view of God is entirely, incompatible with Scripture, for   
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This line is wanting in two syllables. Or, this may be taken as a prose passage.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sēyaṁ sarvā śrutiviruddhā kalpanā yataḥ -  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

jagan-nimittōpādānaṁ  
paraṁ brahma śrutau śrutam ।  
mahānandātmakō mōkṣas  
tatra tatrāsakr̥c chr̥taḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

it is revealed in śruti that the Supreme Brahman is both the material and the instrumental cause of the Universe.  
Also, it is repeatedly revealed in the scriptures that release consists in perfect bliss. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

jagannimittōpādānaṁ paraṁ brahma śrutau śrutam ।  
mahānandātmakō mōkṣastatratatrāsakr̥cchr̥taḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

parasparavirōdhēna  
**vyāhataiṣāṁ** pramāṇatā ।  
trayī-daṇḍa-pratikṣēpaṁ  
kiñcin naiva **pratīkṣatē** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As the authoritativeness of these Tantras is already vitiated by their mutual contradictions,  
it is not really necessary for them to be rejected with the stick of the Veda. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

parasparavirōdhēna vyāhataiṣāṁ pramāṇatā ।  
trayīdaṇḍapratikṣēpaṁ kiñcinnaiva pratīkṣatē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kiñca śaivādayō vēda-  
siddhavarṇāśramād bahiḥ ।  
**kalpayanty** āśramādīni  
tatō'pi śruti-bāhyatā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

85\. Moreover, the Saivas etc. accept stages of life etc.  
that are outside the varnasrama system  
that is proved by the Veda  
and are consequently outside the Veda. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiñca śaivādayōvēdasiddhavarṇāśramādbahiḥ ।  
kalpayantyāśramādīni tatō'pi śrutibāhyatā ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadāhuḥ -  

> dīkṣā-pravēśa-mātrēṇa  
brāhmaṇō **bhavati** kṣaṇāt ।  
kāpālaṁ vratam āsthāya  
yatir **bhavati** mānavaḥ ॥

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As they say," merely by entering Consecration one becomes instantly a Brahmin.  
A man becomes an ascetic by accepting the Kāpālika vow." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.

Every school of thought stresses the importance of its own dīkṣā-ceremony. See Śaivasiddhānta, P.47.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadāhuḥ -  

dīkṣāpravēśamātrēṇa brāhmaṇō bhavati kṣaṇāt ।  
kāpālaṁ vratamāsthāya yatirbhavati mānavaḥ ॥

iti ।  
</details>

### tantrāntara-mūlam
#### śivāpraṇītatā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca vācyam "a-pramāṇa-bhūtam iyantaṁ grantharāśiṁ kathaṁ pratyayitatarō rudraḥ praṇayatī"ti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

86\. Let it not be said, How could Rudra, who is very trustworthy, promulgate such a vast collection of texts which are not authoritative?
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca vācyam apramāṇabhūtamiyantaṁ grantharāśiṁ kathaṁ pratyayitatarō rudraḥ praṇayatīti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca samāna-nāma-nirmātr̥-smaraṇa-nibandhanam iti yuktam  
ati-prasaṅgāditi, yataḥ-
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

 Nor is it right to hold  
 that these texts are based upon the recollection of an author of the same name as Siva,  
 because the ground is overextensive. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca samānanāmanirmātr̥smaraṇanibandhanamiti yuktam ati-prasaṅgāditi, yataḥ-
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

+++(śivākhyō'paraḥ kartēti)+++ nāmaikatva-kr̥ta-bhrānti-  
kalpanā 'py **upapadyatē** ।  
vēda-bādhān, **na** cānyatra +++(pāñcarātrādau)+++  
tāvatā **'tiprasajyatē** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For the theory that the author was in error  
and could be in error,  
because he was not Siva  
but some other person with the same name,  
can only follow if the Veda sublates the system;  
this latter ground is sufficient to prove the lack of authority of these texts  
and entails no overextension to other texts. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See the verse “vāsudevābhidhānena” etc. on P.52 above for the pūrvapakṣa-view.

Cf. Tantraśuddha, P.17:

> yataḥ kēnacid arvāktanēna kṣētra-jñēna mahēśvara-samāna-nāmnā trayī-mārga-bahiṣkr̥tēyaṁ prakriyā viracitā । tan nāma nārāyaṇaṁ kēcid vyākhyāya tan nāma …[[??]] mahēśvara-nāmakōpadiṣṭa-mārgam avalambitavantaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāmaikatvakr̥tabhrāntikalpanā'pyupapadyatē ।  
vēdabādhānna cānyatra tāvatā'tiprasajyatē ॥  
</details>

#### pramādaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pramādō'pi ca nātyantaṁ rudrādiṣu na sambhavī ।+++(4)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And error is not entirely impossible in the case of such persons as Rudra etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pramādō'pi ca nātyantaṁ rudrādiṣu na sambhavī ।  
</details>

#### mōha-śāstram
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad vā rudrasya mōha-śāstra-praṇētr̥tayā 'vagatatvād  
vyāmōhayitum ēva hīdr̥śa-śāstra-praṇayanam upapadyata 
iti nāvaśyaṁ pramāda ēvāśrayitavyaḥ,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or else one may reason that since Rudra may have composed such a system  
for the purpose of deceiving the world  
because he is known as a promulgator of deceitful doctrines,  
it is not even necessary to assume error on his part. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadvā rudrasya mōhaśāstrapraṇētr̥tayā'vagatatvād vyāmōhayitumēva hīdr̥śaśāstrapraṇayanamupapadyata iti nāvaśyaṁ pramāda ēvāśrayitavyaḥ,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ca vārāhē ।  

> tvaṁ hi rudra! mahābāhō!  
mōhaśāstrāṇi kāraya ।  
kuhakādīndra-jālāni  
viruddhācaraṇāni ca ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[72]]  
For thus it reads in the Varaha Purana, 

> "For Thou, strong-armed Rudra, must cause deluding doctrines to be expounded, 
> the deceptions of jugglers (sic) and the like as well as conflicting practices.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

tvaṁ ... Ch. 70, śl. 36b.

kuhakādīndra ... To be traced out.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ca vārāhē ।  
tvaṁ hi rudra! mahābāhō! mōhaśāstrāṇi kāraya ।  
kuhakādīndrajālāni viruddhācaraṇāni ca ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> darśayitvā'lpamāyāsaṁ  
phalaṁ śīghraṁ pradarśaya ।  
darśayitvā janaṁ sarvaṁ  
mōhayāśu mahēśvara! ॥

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Having shown that the fruit can be won with little effort,  
> you must delude all these people quickly."84
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[[139]]  
corresponds to Varaha Purana. 70.36 tvam ca rudra mahābaho mohaśāstrāṇi kāraya  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The ptd. text of the purāṇa has the following line in the place of this verse:

> alpāyātaṁ darśayitvā mōhayāśu mahēśvara। 

( ch. 70, śl. 37a )
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

darśayitvā'lpamāyāsaṁ phalaṁ śīghraṁ pradarśaya ।  
darśayitvā janaṁ sarvaṁ mōhayāśu mahēśvara! ॥

iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā tatraiva bhagavān rudraḥ  
prastuta-śaivādy-āgamānāṁ svayam ēva  
vēda-bāhyatvaṁ vēda-mārgāpa-bhraṣṭa-janādhikāritvaṁ tad-vyāmōhaika-prayōjanatāṁ ca **darśayati** ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Similarly, the venerable Rudra himself shows in the same Purana  
that the Saiva and the like scriptures which are there being discussed  
are apostate from the Veda,  
that only apostates from the Veda are qualified for these doctrines 
and that their only purpose is just to deceive them. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā tatraiva bhagavān rudraḥ prastutaśaivādyāgamānāṁ svayamēva vēdabāhyatvaṁ vēdamārgāpabhraṣṭajanādhikāritvaṁ tadvyāmōhaikaprayōjanatāṁ ca darśayati ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yē vēda-mārga-nirmuktās  
tēṣām **mōhārtham** ēva ca ।  
naya-siddhānta-mārgēṇa  
mayā śāstraṁ **pradarśitam** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"I have propounded this sastra  
as though it were correct doctrine  
in order to deceive those who have deserted the Way of the Veda.185 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

cf. Varāha Pur., 70.41, which in cd reads nayasiddhanta sam jñabhir maya shāstran tu darshitam.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The ptd. edn. has the following reading:

> naya-siddhānta-saṁjñābhiḥ mayā śāstraṁ tu darśitam। 

( ch. 70, śl. 41b-42a )
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yē vēdamārganirmuktāstēṣāmmōhārthamēva ca ।  
nayasiddhāntamārgēṇa mayā śāstraṁ pradarśitam ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tasmād ārabhya kālāt tu  
mat-praṇītēṣu sattamāḥ ।  
śāstrēṣv abhiratō lōkō  
**na** vēdān bahu **manyatē** ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

From that time onward, O excellent Ones,  
the people who believe in the scriptures promulgated by myself  
do not respect the Vedas.16 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

cf. Variha Pur., 70.38, which reads in cd shastreśv abhirato loko bahulyena bhaved atah. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ch. 70. śl. 38b-39a. Variant for the second line:

> śāstrēṣv abhiratō lōkē bāhulyēna bhavēd ataḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasmādārabhya kālāttu matpraṇītēṣu sattamāḥ ।  
śāstrēṣvabhiratō lōkō na vēdān bahu manyatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tathā pāśupatādīni  
> pravartantē kalau yugē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Thus the Pasupata and like doctrines are active in the Kali Age.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

nearest is Varaha Pur., 70.42, tada pasupatam sastram jāyate vedasanjaitam.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid*. śl. 43a. Variant:

> tadā pāśupataṁ śāstraṁ jāyatē vēda-saṁjñitama ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā pāśupatādīni pravartantē kalau yugē ॥
</details>

### viruddhācaraṇam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ca bhagavat-parivāratva-vyatirēkēṇa  
sva-pradhāna-pūjāṁ pāśupatādi-tantra-siddhāṁ vēda-bāhyāṁ darśayati । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise he shows that the worship concerning himself  
as it is propounded in the Pasupata Tantras and other such Tantras  
is different  
and does not form part of the worship of the Bhagavan: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ca bhagavatparivāratvavyatirēkēṇa svapradhānapūjāṁ pāśupatāditantrasiddhāṁ vēdabāhyāṁ darśayati ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tad vēdabāhyaṁ karmōktaṁ  
mām uddiśyōpasēvyatē ।  
tad vai pāśupataṁ nāma  
kaniṣṭham mōhanaṁ nr̥ṇām ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"The said act of worship concerning me which is being observed is really outside the Veda.  
This ritual called Pasupata is the lowliest and deceives men.188" 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

cf. Varaha Pur., 70.21, yad vedabāḥyam karma …
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadvēdabāhyaṁ karmōktaṁ māmuddiśyōpasēvyatē ।  
tadvai pāśupataṁ nāma kaniṣṭhammōhanaṁ nr̥ṇām ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"māṁ viṣṇu--vyatirēkēṇa  
pūjayanti narādhamāḥ ।"  
ity-ādi-vākya-jātāni  
na likhyantē'tigauravāt ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"Only the lowest people worship me with exclusion of Visņu."  
The large numbers of statements like the preceding ones will not be written out here,  
because they are too numerous. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[189]: cf. Varaha Pur., 70.40, mam vimor oyatiriktam ye brahmasiat ca doijottama bhajante pāpakarmāņas te panti narakam narāḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ch. 70. śl. 40b. Variant: 

> māṁ viṣṇōḥ vyatiriktaṁ yē brahmaṇaś ca dvi-jōttama ।

The next line ( 41a ) of the purāṇa may also be noted: 

> bhajantē pāpa-karmāṇas tē yānti narakaṁ narāḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

māṁ viṣṇuvyatirēkēṇa pūjayanti narādhamāḥ ।  
ityādivākyajātāni na likhyantē'tigauravāt ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vyaktañca vēdabāhyatvam ētac-chāstrānugāminām ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It is clear enough that those who follow these scriptures  
are outside the Veda, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vyaktañca vēdabāhyatvamētacchāstrānugāminām ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā tatraiva -  

> śaśāpa tāñ jaṭā-bhasma-  
kapāla-vrata-dhāriṇaḥ ।  
**bhaviṣyatha** trayī-bāhyā  
vēda-karma-bahiṣ-kr̥tāḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

as is stated in the same Purana: 

> "He cursed those who kept the observances of hairtuft, ashes and skull,  
> Be you outside the Veda and disqualified for Vedic rites. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ch. 71. śl. 40b-41a. Variant for the first line: 

> ..jaṭā-bhasma-mithyā-vrata-dharās tadā ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā tatraiva -  
śaśāpa tāñjaṭābhasmakapālavratadhāriṇaḥ ।  
bhaviṣyatha trayībāhyā vēdakarmabahiṣkr̥tāḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> kalau tad-rūpiṇas sarvē  
jaṭā-laguḍa-**dhāriṇaḥ** ।  
sva-cchanda-vrata-**vēṣāś** ca  
mithyā-liṅga-**dharās** tathā ।  
brahma-śāpāgni-**nirdagdhā**  
rudra-bhaktā jaṭā-dharāḥ ॥ 

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[73]]
In the Kali Age all those who assume that appearance,  
wearing hairtuft and carrying a laguḍa stick, exhibitng arbitrary observances and carrying false lingas about,  
all these hair-tuft wearing devotees of Rudra are consumed by the fire of Brahma's curse."  
(not identified.)
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

kalau ... Ch. 71. śl. 51*. Variant:

> kalau tvad-rūpiṇas sarvē jaṭā-mukuṭa-dhāriṇaḥ ।  
svēcchayā prēta-vēṣāś ca mithyā-liṅga-dharāḥ prabhō ॥

brahma ... Passages to be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kalau tadrūpiṇassarvē jaṭālaguḍadhāriṇaḥ ।  
svacchandavratavēṣāśca mithyāliṅgadharāstathā ।  
brahmaśāpāgninirdagdhā rudrabhaktā jaṭādharāḥ ॥ iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

prasiddhañ caitac chaivāgamēṣu ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

These practices are well-known in the Saiva scriptures: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

prasiddhañcaitacchaivāgamēṣu ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> rudrākṣaṁ kaṅkaṇaṁ hastē  
jaṭā caikā ca mastakē ।  
kapālaṁ bhasmanā snānam 

ityādi ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"Rosary, and bracelet in the hand, a hair-tuft on the head, a skull, bathing in ashes etc," 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

rudrākṣaṁ kaṅkaṇaṁ hastē jaṭā caikā ca mastakē ।  
kapālaṁ bhasmanā snānam ityādi ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā caitēṣāmāditya-purāṇē'pi  
bhagavat-tyāgēna samaṁ vēda-tyāgaṁ kathayati ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Similarly, he declares in the Aditya Purana that  
along with relinquishing the Bhagavan they relinquish the Veda: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā caitēṣāmādityapurāṇē'pi bhagavattyāgēna samaṁ vēdatyāgaṁ kathayati ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> anyē bhasmajaṭōpētā  
yathōktā gautamāt purā ।  
śāpāt santyājitā vēdaṁ  
dēvaṁ nārāyaṇaṁ tathā ॥

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"Others, those that wear ashes and hair-tufts as described  
have formerly been made to relinquish the Veda  
as well as God Nārāyaṇa on account of Gautama's curse."
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Passages to be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anyē bhasmajaṭōpētā yathōktā gautamāt purā ।  
śāpātsantyājitā vēdaṁ dēvaṁ nārāyaṇaṁ tathā ॥

iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> kiñcaitē vāsudēvasya  
mandā **nindāṁ vitanvatē** ।  
tē ca pāṣaṇḍinō **jñēyā**  
yathā laiṅgai **samīritam** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Moreover, those fools who pass censure on Vasudeva  
are to be regarded as heretics,  
for thus it is declared in the Linga Puriņa, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiñcaitē vāsudēvasya mandā nindāṁ vitanvatē ।  
tē ca pāṣaṇḍinō jñēyā yathā laiṅgai samīritam ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yē tu sāmānyabhāvēna  
**manyantē** puruṣōttamam ।  
tē vai pāṣaṇḍinō **jñēyā**  
vēda-mārga-bahiṣkr̥tāḥ ॥+++(5)+++

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"Those who consider the Supreme Person to be equal (to Siva)  
are to be regarded as heretics who are expelled from the Way of the Veda," (not identified.)
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yē tu sāmānyabhāvēna manyantē puruṣōttamam ।  
tē vai pāṣaṇḍinō jñēyā vēdamārgabahiṣkr̥tāḥ ॥

iti,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tataśca -  

> ēta ēva ca tē ēṣāṁ  
"vāṅmātrēṇāpi nārcanam ।  
pāṣaṇḍinō vikarmasthān"  
ity-ādi-smr̥tiṣūditam ॥  
"yā vēda-bāhyā" ity-ētad  
api cēdr̥śagōcaram ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

To conclude, it is these followers of other Tantras of whom it is said, in the smrtis:  
"Heretics, criminals etc.", that they should not be honoured even with a word;  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

read yesAm for eṣām.

supra §52.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

pāṣaṇḍinō ... Cf. Manusmṛti IV-30:

> pāṣaṇḍinō vikarmasthān baiḍāla-vratikān śaṭhān ।  
haitukān baka-vr̥ttīṁś ca vāṅ-mātrēṇāpi nārcayēt ॥

yā vēdabāhyā ... Ibid*. XII-95:

> yā vēda-bāhyās smr̥tayō yāś ca kāś ca ku-dr̥ṣṭayaḥ ।  
sarvās tā niṣphalāḥ prētya tamō-niṣṭhā hi tās smr̥tāḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tataśca -  

ēta ēva ca tē ēṣāṁ vāṅmātrēṇāpi nārcanam ।  
pāṣaṇḍinōvikarmasthānityādismr̥tiṣūditam ॥  
"yā vēda-bāhyā" ityētad api cēdr̥śagōcaram ।
</details>

#### na vēdāḥ, na pratyakṣam

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tasmān na vēda-mūlatvaṁ  
nāpi pratyakṣa-mūlatā ॥  
tantrāntarāṇāṁ yuktēti  
**kalpyatē** kāraṇāntaram ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and the declaration "Which are outside the Veda..."  refers to them.  
Consequently, since it cannot properly be said of the other Tantras  
that they are based either on Veda or on Perception,  
another cause must be assumed for them. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasmānna vēdamūlatvaṁ nāpi pratyakṣamūlatā ॥  
tantrāntarāṇāṁ yuktēti kalpyatē kāraṇāntaram ।  
</details>

### paratō 'prāmāṇyam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu mūlāntarāpēkṣā  
yadi syād astu +++(avēda-mūlatva-)+++dūṣaṇam ॥  
svataḥpramāṇaṁ vijñānaṁ  
bhavatāṁ nanu darśanē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

87\. OBJECTION. If it is true that for these Tantras another basis must be assumed,  
let the defect be granted. 
But is in your own view knowledge not self-proved? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu mūlāntarāpēkṣā yadi syādastu dūṣaṇam ॥  
svataḥpramāṇaṁ vijñānaṁ bhavatāṁ nanu darśanē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

satyaṁ tad ēva vijñāna-  
prāmāṇyam **apanīyatē** ॥  
bādha-kāraṇa-dōṣābhyāṁ  
tāv api dvāv iha sphuṭau ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[74]]   
REFUTATION.  
Certainly; but this self-validity of knowledge is here negated by these two defects of sublation,  
namely, sublation through ~~Perception~~ origin and through Scripture,  
for both these defects are plain in their case. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

satyaṁ tadēva vijñānaprāmāṇyamapanīyatē ॥  
bādhakāraṇadōṣābhyāṁ tāvapi dvāviha sphuṭau ।  
</details>

### nāmādi-sāmyam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ēvaṁ śrutiviruddhasya  
sphuṭa-mūlāntarasya yat ॥  
pañca-rātrēṇa sādharmyaṁ  
+++(hētunā ←)+++ tantratvēnābhidhitsitam …।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The equality of Pañcaratra Tantra and those other Tantras  
which has been postulated on the ground that both happen to be Tantra,  
while in fact one of the two is incompatible with Scripture and plainly shows a different provenance,  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvaṁ śrutiviruddhasya sphuṭamūlāntarasya yat ॥  
pañcarātrēṇa sādharmmyaṁ tantratvēnābhidhitsitam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kriyātvēna tu sādharmyaṁ  
brahma-hatyā'śvamēdhayōḥ ॥+++(5)+++  
śruti-pratyakṣayōs tatra  
yatō mūlatva-niścayaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

would mean that Brahmin Murder and Horse Sacrifice are on the same level because both are actions, (which are seen in the scripture, For in that case, we've determined their source).  
~~For in the case of Pañcaratra Sastra we have positive certainty that it is based on Scripture and Perception.~~  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kriyātvēna tu sādharmmyaṁ brahmahatyā'śvamēdhayōḥ ॥  
śrutipratyakṣayōstatra yatōmūlatvaniścayaḥ ।  
</details>

## 09 śruty-anuvādaucityam

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu ca śruti-mūlatvē  
vēdād ēvārtha-siddhitaḥ ॥  
tat-praṇētr̥--sva-tantratva-  
kalpanā nēty **acūcudam** ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

88\. OBJECTION. I made the objections (supra 12) that  
if its being based on Scripture follows from its being established by the Veda,  
then it cannot be assumed that the author was independent.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu ca śrutimūlatvē vēdādēvārthasiddhitaḥ ॥  
tatpraṇētr̥svatantratvakalpanā nētyacūcudam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

naivaṁ **na kalpyatē** puṁsi  
svātantryaṁ, **śrūyatē** hi tat ॥  
"tasyādhyakṣam idaṁ sarvaṁ"  
"bhīṣā'smād idam" ādiṣu ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. No. Surely, we can assume no independence in man,  
but for God it is revealed in Scripture, e.g.,  
"To Him all the world is manifest..." (Taitt Up. 2.8.1.)  
"From fear for Him..." (Aitareya Br.) 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

tasyādhyakṣa ... To be traced out.

bhīṣāsmādi ... Taittirīya Āraṇyaka : VIII. 8. 1a; also Taittirīyopaniṣat: II. 8. 1a.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

naivaṁ na kalpyatē puṁsi svātantryaṁ śrūyatē hi tat ॥  
tasyādhyakṣamidaṁ sarvaṁ bhīṣā'smādidamādiṣu ।  
</details>

## 10 na vēda-bāhyam

### vēda-mūlatā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu vēdamūlā ēva cēdētāḥ pañcarātra-smr̥tayaḥ -  
> kiṁ tarhi tad-artha-smaraṇavat tan-mūla-bhūta-vēda-vākya-smaraṇaṁ nānuvartatē pāñca-rātrikāṇām ?  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

89\. OBJECTION.  
But if the Pañcaratra traditions are really derived from the Veda,  
then how is it that no recollection of the Vedic words which furnishes this basis  
has persisted among the Pañcaratrikas,  
whereas the meaning of these words apparently does persist?  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu vēdamūlā ēva cēdētāḥ pañcarātrasmr̥tayaḥ kiṁ tarhi tadarthasmaraṇavattanmūlabhūtavēdavākyasmaraṇaṁ nānuvartatē pāñcarātrikāṇām ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na "cārthasmaraṇasya prayōjanavattvāt  
> tasya viphalatvāt, tad-anādaraṇīyam"  
> iti yuktam,   
na hi yataḥ prāmāṇyaṁ tadēva vismartuṁ yuktam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It is not right to contend that  
only the recollection of the meaning is important  
because that has purpose  
while the recollection of the actual Vedic statements is to be disregarded  
because it is purposeless;  
for it is not proper to forget that from which the meaning's authority derives. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘tasya’ mūla-bhūta-vēda-vākya-smaraṇasyēty arthaḥ ।

na hi ... Cf. Tantravārtika under I. iii. 1, P.73:

> na hi yat kr̥taṁ prāmāṇyaṁ, tad ēva vismartuṁ yujyatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cārthasmaraṇasya prayōjanavattvāt tasya viphalatvāt tadanādaraṇīyamiti yuktam,   
na hi yataḥ prāmāṇyaṁ tadēva vismartuṁ yuktam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> atha vismaraṇōpapattayē pralīna-nityānumēya-śākhā-mūlatā āśrīyatē।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[75]]  
Or if, in order to justify this oblivion,  
the standpoint is taken that the doctrine is based on a Vedic sakha which has been lost or which is always deducible,  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. ibid : I-iii-1, P.73:

> yadi tu pralīna-śākhā-mūlatā kalpyēta, tatas sarvāsāṁ buddhādi-smr̥tīnām api, tad-dvāraṁ prāmāṇyaṁ prasajyēta । yasyaiva ca yad abhiprētaṁ sa ēva tat pralīna-śākhā-mastakē nikṣipya pramāṇī-kuryāt । atha vidyamāna-śākhā-gatā ēvaitē 'rthāḥ; tathāpi manvādaya iti sarvē puruṣās ēvōpalapsyantē । yuktatarā ca svādhyāyādhyayana-vidhēḥ sākṣād vēdād ēva pratītir iti smr̥ti-praṇayana-vaiyarthyaṁ syāt ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha vismaraṇōpapattayē pralīnanityānumēyaśākhāmūlatā āśrīyatē।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tadā yad ēva yēna pramāṇatayā parigr̥hītaṁ  
> sa tat-pralīna-śākhā-mastakē nikṣipya pramāṇī-kuryāt।  
> nityānumēya-pralīna-śākhayōstu sva-rūpa-siddhir ēva durlabhā ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

then whatever doctrine a person adopts  
he can always make authoritative simply by attributing it to a lost śākhā;  
however, it is hard to prove what a lost or deducible śākhā actually contain. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> tadā yadēva yēna pramāṇatayā parigr̥hītaṁ  sa tatpralīnaśākhāmastakē nikṣipya pramāṇīkuryātnityānumēyapralīnaśākhayōstu svarūpasiddhirēva durlabhā ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> atha vidyamāna-śākhā-mūlā ēva tāḥ smr̥tayaḥ।  
tadā tat-praṇētr̥vad  
anyē'pi tata ēvōpalabhēran  
iti grantha-praṇayana-prayāsa-vaiyarthyam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or if these traditions are based on an extant Sakha,  
then others would know it as well as the author,  
and hence his taking the trouble of promulgating these texts would be purposeless. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha vidyamānaśākhāmūlā ēva tāḥ smr̥tayaḥ tadā tatpraṇētr̥vadanyē'pi tata ēvōpalabhēran iti granthapraṇayanaprayāsavaiyarthyam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atrōcyatē -
