sa khalu bhagavān amōgha-sahaja-saṁvēdana-sākṣād-bhavad--akhila-vēda-rāśir  
viprakīrṇa-vividha-vidhy--artha-vāda--mantrātmakān  
ēka-śākhādhyayana-dhāraṇādiṣv a-dhīra-dhiyō bhaktān **avalōkya**  
tad-anukampayā laghunōpāyēna  
tad-arthaṁ **saṁkṣipyōpadidēśēti**  
na kiñcid anupapannam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION.  
The reply to this is as follows:  
The Bhagavan, who has an immediate presentation of the entire collection of the Veda  
by virtue of the perfect knowledge that is natural to Him,  
observed that his devotees were not firm enough in their minds  
to retain and transmit the lessons of all the various sakhas  
which consist of widely scattered injunctions, arthavadas and mantras of many different kinds,  
and having observed this he was moved by his compassion  
to condense the meaning of the Veda in an easily comprehensible way and to teach it so.  
On this showing, nothing is unestablished.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atrōcyatē sa khalu bhagavān amōghasahajasaṁvēdanasākṣādbhavadakhilavēdarāśirviprakīrṇavividhavidhyarthavādamantrātmakānēkaśākhādhyayanadhāraṇādiṣvadhīradhiyō bhaktānavalōkya tadanukampayā laghunōpāyēna tadarthaṁ saṁkṣipyōpadidēśēti na kiñcidanupapannam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā'huḥ -  

> vēdāntēṣu yathāsāraṁ  
**saṅgr̥hya** bhagavān hariḥ ।  
bhaktānukampayā vidvān  
**sañcikṣēpa** yathā-sukham ॥

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As they say 

> "The blessed Hari took the essence of the Upanisads and condensed it,  
the Sage, out of compassion with his devotees for their convenience."
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Mahābhārata, śāntiparvan, ch. 348. śl. 64.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā'huḥ -  

vēdāntēṣu yathāsāraṁ saṅgr̥hya bhagavān hariḥ ।  
bhaktānukampayā vidvān sañcikṣēpa yathāsukham ॥

iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ētē ca manv-ādi-samasta-smaraṇa-sādhāraṇāḥ paryanuyōgās  
tantra-ṭīkā-kr̥ta-pariśramāṇām anāyāsa-parihāryā  
iti nēha prapañcyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The other objections made,  
which are equally applicable to all Traditions of Manu and the others,  
are easily answered by all those who have made a diligent study of the commentaries on the Tantras and are not further enlarged upon here.  

[[76]] 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This is another name for Tantravārtika of Kumārila Bhaṭṭa.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ētē ca manvādisamastasmaraṇasādhāraṇāḥ paryanuyōgāstantraṭīkākr̥tapariśramāṇāmanāyāsaparihāryā iti nēha prapañcyatē ।  
</details>

### na vēda-nindā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu cēdaṁ vēda-mūlatvaṁ pañca-rātra-tantrāṇām anupapannaṁ vēda-nindā-darśanāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

90\. OBJECTION.  
The thesis that the Pañcarātra Tantras are based on the Veda  
is disproved by the fact that  
we find in these very Tantras a condemnation of the Veda. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See p. 17 above, for the pūrvapakṣa-view.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu cēdaṁ vēdamūlatvaṁ pañcarātratantrāṇāmanupapannaṁ vēdanindādarśanāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> uktaṁ hi 
> 
> > caturṣu vēdēṣu puruṣārtham alabhamānaḥ  
> śāṇḍilya (p. 52) idaṁ śāstramadhītavān 
> 
> iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For it is said that 

> Sandilya, failing to find a meaning of human importance in the four Vedas, learnt this shastra. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Aniruddha Saṁhitā Ch. I:

> śr̥ṇu vēdavidāṁ śrēṣṭham ātma-dhyāna-parāyaṇam ॥ (9 b)  
pārśva-rathā munayas sarvē praṇipatya jagad-gurum ।  
ūcus taṁ munayaḥ sarvē ētad vākyam atandritāḥ ॥ (12)  
vēdās sarvē samāsēna sāṅgōpāṅgās savistarāḥ ।  
svataḥ kamala-patrākṣa śrutāḥ pūrvaṁ dayāpara ॥ (13)  
śrēyō-mārgaṁ na paśyāmaḥ, tad vadasva mahā-munē । (14 a)
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

uktaṁ hi caturṣu vēdēṣu puruṣārthamalabhamānaḥ śāṇḍilya (p. 52) idaṁ śāstramadhītavān iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

anavagata-vacana-vyaktēr ayaṁ paryanuyōgaḥ,  
na hi nindā nindyaṁ nindituṁ pravartatē  
api tu - ninditād itarat praśaṁsituṁ -
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION.  
This is the objection of someone  
who does not know the distinct meaning of the statement.  
For this censure does not mean to censure something deserving of censure,  
but rather to praise something else than that which is censured.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

anavagata ... Cf. Śrībhāṣya under II-ii-42, P.831:

> yaś caiṣa kēṣāñcid udghōṣaḥ
>
>> sāṅgēṣu vēdēṣu niṣṭhām alabhamānaḥ śāṇḍilyaḥ pañca-rātra-śāstram adhītavān, sāṅgēṣu vēdēṣu puruṣārtha-niṣṭhā na labdhēti vacanāt vēda-viruddhaṁ tantram iti’, 
>
> sō 'py anāghrāta-vēda-vacasām anākalita-tad-upabr̥ṁhaṇa-nyāya-kalāpānāṁ śraddhā-mātra-vijr̥mbhitaḥ । yathā 
>
>> prātaḥ prātar anr̥taṁ tē vadanti purōdayāt juhvati yē 'gni-hōtram
>
> iti, anudita-hōma-nindā udita-hōma-praśaṁsārthēty uktam, yathā ca bhūma-vidyā-prakramē nāradēna 
>
>> r̥g-vēdaṁ bhagavō 'dhyēmi yajur-vēdaṁ sāma-vēdam ātharvaṇaṁ caturtham itihāsa-purāṇaṁ pañcamam 
>
>> ity ārabhya, sarvaṁ vidyā-sthānam abhidhāya, 
>
>> sō 'haṁ bhagavō mantravid ēvāsmi nātmavit
>
> iti bhūmi-vidyā-vyatiriktāsu sarvāsu vidyā-svātma-vēdanā-lābha-vacanaṁ vakṣyamāṇa-bhūma-vidyā-praśaṁsārthaṁ kr̥tam, athavā 'sya nāradasya sāṅgēṣu vēdēṣu yat paratattvaṁ pratipādyatē, tad-alābha-nimittō 'yaṁ vādaḥ; ēvam ēva śāṇḍilyasyēti paścād vēdānta-vēdya-vāsudēvākhya-para-brahma-tattvābhidhānād avagamyatē । tathā vēdārthasya durjñānatayā sukhāvabōdhārtha-śāstrārambhaḥ parama-saṁhitāyām ucyatē ।
>
>> adhītā bhagavan ! vēdāḥ sāṅgōpāṅgāḥ savistarāḥ ।  
śrutāni ca mayāṅgāni vākōvākya-yutāni ca ॥  
na caitēṣu samastēṣu saṁśayēna vinā kvacit ।  
śrēyō-mārgaṁ prapaśyāmi yēna siddhir bhaviṣyati ॥ 
>
> iti । [ I, 3, 4 ]

na hi ... Vide Śābarabhāṣya under II-iv-20, P.139, lines 27 & 28.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anavagatavacanavyaktērayaṁ paryanuyōgaḥ, na hi nindā nindyaṁ nindituṁ pravartatē  
api tu  ninditāditaratpraśaṁsituṁ
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathaitarēyaka-brāhmaṇē - 

> prātaḥ prātar anr̥taṁ tē vadanti 

ity-anudita-hōma-nindā udita-hōma-praśaṁsārthēti gamyatē ।+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For instance, in the Aitareya Brahmana  
the censure passed on the pre-dawn oblation  
"Morning upon morning they speak untruth,"  
is understood to praise the post-dawn oblation.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Aitareya Brāhmaṇa: V-31-6.

Cf. also Taittirīya Brāhmaṇa II. 1. 2. 7: 

> yad anuditē sūryē prātar juhuyāt ubhayam ēvāgnēyasyād uditē sūryē prātar juhōti ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathaitarēyakabrāhmaṇē prātaḥ prātaranr̥taṁ tē vadanti ityanuditahōmanindā uditahōmapraśaṁsārthēti gamyatē।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

mānavē

> r̥gvēdō dēva-daivatyō  
yajur-vēdastu mānuṣaḥ ।  
sāma-vēdas tu pitryaḥ syāt  
tasmāt tasyāśucir dhvaniḥ ॥  

iti sāma-vēda-nindā itara-vēda-praśaṁsārthā, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It is as in the Manavadharma Shastra (Manusmrti, 4.124.):  

> "The Rgveda is of gods and deities,  
> the Yajurveda of man,  
> and the Samaveda of the deceased;  
> therefore its sound is impure;" 

here the censure of the Samaveda serves to praise the other Vedas. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Manusmṛti IV. 124.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

mānavē

r̥gvēdō dēvadaivatyō yajurvēdastu mānuṣaḥ ।  
sāmavēdastu pitryaḥ syāt tasmāttasyāśucirdhvaniḥ ॥  
iti sāmavēdanindā itaravēdapraśaṁsārthā, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā vā bhāratē -  

> catvāra ēkatō vēdā  
bhārataṁ caikam ēkataḥ ।  
samāgatais tu r̥ṣibhis  
tulayā **'rōpitaṁ** purā ॥  
mahattvē ca guruttvāc ca ca  
**dhriyamāṇaṁ** yatō 'dhikam ।  
mahattvāc ca guruttvāc ca  
mahā-bhāratam ucyatē ॥

iti mahā-bhārata-praśaṁsārthēti gr̥hyatē  
na vēda-nindēti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or as in the Mahabharata (Mahabharata 1.265 f):  
"Formerly the assembled seers placed the four Vedas and the Mahabharata in the balance,  
one at one side, the other at the other side.  
And since in bulk and in weight the latter preponderated,  
it is called the Great Bharata for its bulk and weight."  
This is said, not to belittle the Vedas,  
but to bestow praise on the Mahabharata. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ādiparvan I. 208-209.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā vā bhāratē -  

catvāra ēkatō vēdā bhārataṁ caikamēkataḥ ।  
samāgataistu r̥ṣibhistulayā'rōpitaṁ purā ॥  
mahattvē ca guruttvācca ca dhriyamāṇaṁ yatō'dhikam ।  
mahattvācca guruttvācca mahābhāratamucyatē ॥

iti mahābhāratapraśaṁsārthēti gr̥hyatē na vēdanindēti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ēvaṁ pañcarātrapraśaṁsēti gamyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In this same way the above statement must be taken as praise of the Pancarãtra. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvaṁ pañcarātrapraśaṁsēti gamyatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

athānudita-hōmādēr  
anyatra stuti-**darśanāt** ।  
a-tat-paratvaṁ nindāyās  
tathā 'trāpi **bhaviṣyati** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Just as the censure of the pre-dawn oblation etc.  
does not really intend censure,  
since elsewhere in the same texts they are praised,  
so will it be in our case too. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

athānuditahōmādēranyatra stutidarśanāt ।  
atatparatvaṁ nindāyāstathātrāpi bhaviṣyati ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vēdapraśaṁsā bahuśaḥ pañcarātrē'pi dr̥śyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[77]]  
In Pañcaratra, too, we frequently find praise of the Veda; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vēdapraśaṁsā bahuśaḥ pañcarātrē'pi dr̥śyatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na hi tēbhyaḥ paraṁ kiñcid  
vāṅmayaṁ kamalāsana ।  
vēdāntair idam ēvōktaṁ  
tattva-jñānōpapādakaiḥ ॥  

ityādau ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for example: "Nothing that is made up of words is superior to the Veda,  
thou who art seated on the Lotus.  
That is said by the Upanisads which set forth the knowledge of truth"  
etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi tēbhyaḥ paraṁ kiñcid vāṅmayaṁ kamalāsana ।  
vēdāntairidamēvōktaṁ tattvajñānōpapādakaiḥ ॥  
ityādau ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca "caturṣu vēdēṣu" iti nāyam arthaḥ -  
vēdēṣu puruṣārthō nāstīti  
kintu 

> yas tēṣu puruṣārthas  
tam alabhamāna 

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

91\. Besides in the quotation caturşu vedeşu  (supra §17)  
the meaning is not that there is no purpose of human importance in the Vedas  
but simply "failing to find the purpose of human importance which is in the Vedas..." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca "caturṣu vēdēṣu" iti nāyamarthaḥ vēdēṣu puruṣārthō nāstīti kintu yastēṣu puruṣārthastamalabhamāna iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nanu "puruṣārtham" "alabhamāna" ityanvayō na "vēdēṣu puruṣārtham" iti,  
+++(yēna "vēdēṣu puruṣārthō vartatay" ity arthaṁ gr̥hṇīyāt)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

OBJECTION. However, the principal connection in this sentence is between  
"failing to find" and "a purpose of human importance;"  
not between "purpose of human importance" and "in the Vedas." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu "puruṣārtham" "alabhamāna" ityanvayō na "vēdēṣu puruṣārtham" iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

maivaṁ - vyāvartyābhāvāt,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. Don't argue like that,  
for there is no negation in the sentence. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

maivaṁ - vyāvartyābhāvāt,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na hi vēdēṣv ēvāyaṁ puruṣārthō na labhyatē।  
atō vēdēṣu yaḥ puruṣārthas  
tam **alabhamānaḥ**  
tad-abhilāṣī pañca-rātra-śāstram **adhītavān**  

iti pañca-rātra-śrutyōr aikārthyam ēva pratīyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For it is not so that this purpose of human importance is absent from the Vedas;  
hence the sentence "failing to find that purpose of human importance which is in the Vedas,  
and desirous of finding it,  
he learnt the Pañcarātra Sastra,"  
conveys that both Revelation and Pañcaratra have the same meaning.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi vēdēṣvēvāyaṁ puruṣārthō na labhyatē atō vēdēṣu yaḥ puruṣārthastamalabhamānaḥ tadabhilāṣī pañcarātraśāstramadhītavāniti pañcarātraśrutyōraikārthyamēva pratīyatē ।  
</details>

### dīkṣādau
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yat punar uktam 

> upanayanādi-saṁskr̥tānāṁ bhagavad-ārādhanārthatayā dīkṣā-lakṣaṇa-saṁskāra-vidhānād avaidikatvam  

iti, tad ayuktaṁ,  
na hy upanayanādi-saṁskr̥tānāṁ jyōtiṣ-ṭōmādi-karmāṅgatayā  
dīkṣādi-saṁskāra-vidhāyakam "āgnā-vaiṣṇavam" ity-ādi-vākyam avaidikaṁ bhavati ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

92\. The further objection (Supra § 17) that Pañcaratra is non-Vedic because of the injunction that  
those who are qualified for Vedic sacraments etc.  
must undergo such sacraments described as Consecration  
because they are propitiations of the Lord,  
does not hold good.  
For such statements as agnavaiṣṇavam.. 201  
which enjoin the sacrament of consecration upon those qualified for Initiation etc. as accessory to the ritual of the jyotiştoma etc.  
do not therefore become non-Vedic. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

āgnavaisNava, name of a sacrificial cake offered at the dikşaniyeşti.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yatpunaruktam ... See 18 above, for the opponent's argument.

āgnāvaiṣṇavam... Cf. 

> āgnāvaiṣṇavam ēkādaśa-kapālaṁ purōḍāśaṁ nirvapēd dīkṣiṣyamāṇaḥ, 

quoted by Śabara under XII. 1-25, P.319.

Also cf. Aitareya Brāhmaṇa. I. 1:

> āgnāvaiṣṇavaṁ purōḍāśaṁ nirvapanti dīkṣaṇīyam ēkādaśa-kapālam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yatpunaruktamupanayanādisaṁskr̥tānāṁ bhagavadārādhanārthatayā dīkṣālakṣaṇasaṁskāravidhānādavaidikatvamiti tadayuktaṁ na hyupanayanādisaṁskr̥tānāṁ jyōtiṣṭōmādikarmāṅgatayā dīkṣādisaṁskāravidhāyakam āgnāvaiṣṇavam ityādivākyamavaidikaṁ bhavati ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha vaidika-saṁskārāt saṁskārāntara-vidhānaṁ hētuḥ,  
tad anupapannaṁ -  
siddhē hi pañca-rātra-śāstrasya a-vaidikatvē  
tasya saṁskārāntaratva-siddhiḥ,  
tat-siddhau ca tasyāvaidikatva-siddhir ity anyōnyāśrayaṇāt ।+++(4)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[78]]  
Or if the ground for its non-Vedic character is the injunction of sacraments other than the Vedic ones,  
the ground is inappropriate,  
because of the circular argument it involves:  
only if the non-Vedic character of Pancarātra Sastra is proved,  
it is proved that these sacraments are really different;  
and if the latter is proved, it is proved that Pañcaratra Sastra is non Vedic.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha vaidikasaṁskārāt saṁskārāntaravidhānaṁ hētuḥ, tadanupapannaṁ siddhē hi pañcarātraśāstrasya avaidikatvē tasya saṁskārāntarattvasiddhiḥ tatsiddhau ca tasyāvaidikatvasiddhirityanyōnyāśrayaṇāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kiñca samasta-vaidika-saṁskārēbhyaḥ saṁskārāntaratvaṁ vā hētuḥ,  
uta katipayēbhyaḥ saṁskārēbhyaḥ?  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Moreover, the ground is either that the Pancarātra sacraments are different from all Vedic sacraments,  
or that they are different from some Vedic sacraments. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiñca samastavaidikasaṁskārēbhyaḥ saṁskārāntaratvaṁ vā hētuḥ,  
uta katipayēbhyaḥ saṁskārēbhyaḥ?  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na tāvad anantaraḥ kalpaḥ  
upanayanādi-saṁskārasyāpi caulādi-saṁskārāt saṁskārāntaratvēnāvaidikatva-prasaṅgāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Not the latter alternative,  
for this would mean that the sacrament of Initiation ctc. is non-Vedic  
because it is different from the sacrament of Tonsure; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na tāvadanantaraḥ kalpaḥ upanayanādisaṁskārasyāpi caulādisaṁskārāt saṁskārāntaratvēnāvaidikatvaprasaṅgāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na cāntyaḥ kalpaḥ - ukta-dōṣānativr̥ttēḥ,  
na hy upanayanaṁ samasta-vaidika-saṁskārēbhyaḥ saṁskārāntaram।  
asiddhaśca samasta-vaidika-saṁskāra-vyatirēkaḥ -  
pañca-rātra-śāstrasyāpi vaidikatvād ity uktam ēva ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

nor the first alternative,  
because it does not escape the said defect?  
for the sacrament of Initiation is not different from all Vedic sacraments;  
and we have said that the difference (of Pañcarātra sacraments) from Vedic sacraments  
is disproved on the ground that Pañcarātra Sastra is Vedic. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cāntyaḥ kalpaḥ, uktadōṣānativr̥ttēḥ, na hyupanayanaṁ samastavaidikasaṁskārēbhyaḥ saṁskārāntaramasiddhaśca samastavaidikasaṁskāravyatirēkaḥ pañcarātraśāstrasyāpi vaidikatvādityuktamēva ।  
</details>

### vidyā-sthāna-parigaṇanā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad api 

> dharma-pramāṇatvābhimata-catur-daśa-vidyā-sthānēṣv a-parigaṇitatvāt  
> pāśupatāditantravat trayī-bāhyattvam 

iti tad api dvaipāyana-vālmīki-praṇīta-bhārata-rāmāyaṇādi-granthair anaikāntikam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

93\. The objection (supra § 17) that Pancarātra is outside the Veda,  
because like the Pasupata Tantra it is not included among the fourteen sciences  
which are held to be authoritative of dharma,  
would also have an occasional application to the texts of the Bharata and Rāmāyaṇa composed by Dvaipayana and Valmiki. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See P.19 above, for pūrvapakṣa.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadapi dharmapramāṇatvābhimatacaturdaśavidyāsthānēṣvaparigaṇitatvāt pāśupatāditantravat trayībāhyattvamiti tadapi dvaipāyana -vālmīkipraṇītabhāratarāmāyaṇādigranthairanaikāntikam ।  
</details>

### vyāsēnāṅgīkāraḥ

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yattu "bhagavatā bādarāyaṇēna nirastatvād" iti tad asat,  
kathaṁ hi bhagavān dvaipāyanaḥ sakala-lōkādarśa-bhūta-parama-bhāgavatō  
bhāgavataṁ śāstraṁ nirasyatīty utprēkṣyēta ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The objection that Pancharatra is non-Vedic  
because it is rejected by the blessed Badarayana is incorrect.  
For how could the blessed dvaipAyana be thought to reject the Bhagavata doctrine,  
while he himself is a supreme Bhagavata,  
model for the all the world?
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[[140]] The author of the Brahmasutras is identified with Vyasa Dvaipayana, composer of the Mahabharata
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See ibid.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yattu bhagavatā bādarāyaṇēna nirastatvāditi tadasat,  
kathaṁ hi bhagavān dvaipāyanaḥ sakalalōkādarśabhūtaparamabhāgavatō bhāgavataṁ śāstraṁ nirasyatītyutprēkṣyēta ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ya ēvamāha -  

> idaṁ śatasahasrāddhi  
bhāratākhyānavistarāt ।  
**āvidhya** matimanthānaṁ  
daghnō ghr̥tam **ivōddhr̥tam** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[79]] 
This has been extracted from the Bharata in its full length of thousand Slokas after it had been churned with the stick of thought,  
as butter is extracted from curds, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Māhābhārata, śānti, 331. 2-3.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ya ēvamāha -  
idaṁ śatasahasrāddhi bhāratākhyānavistarāt ।  
āvidhya matimanthānaṁ daghnō ghr̥tamivōddhr̥tam ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> navanītaṁ yathā daghnō  
dvipadāṁ brāhmaṇō yathā ।  
āraṇyakaṁ ca vēdēbhya  
ōṣadhībhyō yathā'mr̥tam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and curds from milk,  
the Brahmin from the bipeds,  
the Aranyaka from the Vedas,  
and the amṛta from the herbs 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

navanītaṁ yathā daghnō dvipadāṁ brāhmaṇō yathā ।  
āraṇyakaṁ ca vēdēbhya ōṣadhībhyō yathā'mr̥tam ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> idaṁ mahōpaniṣadaṁ  
catur-vēda-samanvitam ।  
sāṅkhya-yōga-kr̥tāntēna  
pañca-rātrānu-**śabditam** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

this Mahopanisada which is consistent with the four Vedas and the demonstrations of Sankhya and Yoga is called the Pañcaratra. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. 326. 100.

> idaṁ pañca-rātraṁ mahōpaniṣadaṁ — mahatīnām upaniṣadām artha-pratipādakam, vēdārtha-pratipādakam, sāṅkhya-yōga-siddhānta[[??]] cēty arthaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

idaṁ mahōpaniṣadaṁ caturvēdasamanvitam ।  
sāṅkhyayōgakr̥tāntēna pañcarātrānuśabditam ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> idaṁ śrēya idaṁ brahma  
idaṁ hitam anuttamam ।  
r̥g-yajus-sāmabhir juṣṭam  
atharvāṅgirasais tathā ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This is bliss, this is brahman,  
this is the summum bonum.  
Being consistent with Rk, Yajuh and Saman and the Atharvāngirasas,  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. (Gorakhpur edn.) 322. 33a, 41b.

r̥gbhiḥ, sāmabhiḥ, atharvēṇa, aṅgirasā ca dr̥ṣṭā yē mantrāḥ tair api juṣṭaṁ sahitam iti bhāvaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

idaṁ śrēya idaṁ brahma idaṁ hitamanuttamam ।  
r̥gyajussāmabhirjuṣṭamatharvāṅgirasaistathā ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> bhaviṣyati pramāṇaṁ vai ētadēvānuśāsanam ।  

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

this discipline will of a certainty be authoritative.204

[204]: Mahābhārata, 12 340 (129.76) ff.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. (Critical edn.) 322.41a.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

bhaviṣyati pramāṇaṁ vai ētadēvānuśāsanam ।  
iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

bhīṣma-parvaṇy api -  

> brāhmaṇaiḥ kṣatriyair vaiśyaiḥ  
śūdraiś ca kr̥ta-lakṣaṇaiḥ ।  
**arcanīyaś** ca **sēvyaśca**  
**pūjanīyaś** ca mādhavaḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And in the Bhismaparvan too: 

"Brahmins, Ksatriyas, Vaisyas and Sūdras as described are all to worship, serve and honour Madhava  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

brāhmaṇaiḥ ... Ibid. 62. 38-39.

One of the chief characteristics of the Pañcarātra-religion is its liberal catholicity. It offers hope of salvation to all, without the distinctions of caste and sex.

kr̥talakṣaṇaiḥ ... 'kr̥ta-lakṣaṇaiḥ', kr̥ta-dīkṣair ity arthaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

bhīṣmaparvaṇyapi -  

brāhmaṇaiḥ kṣatriyairvaiśyaiḥ śūdraiśca kr̥talakṣaṇaiḥ ।  
arcanīyaśca sēvyaśca pūjanīyaśca mādhavaḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> sāttvataṁ vidhim āsthāya  
**gītas** saṁkarṣaṇēna yaḥ ।  
dvāparasya yugasyāntē  
ādau kaliyugasya ca ॥

iti । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

according to the Satvata ritual that has been promulgated by Samkarṣaṇa,  
at the end of the Dvapara age and the beginning of the Kali age."205 

[205]: Mahābhārata, 6.66 (3012). 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Īśvarasaṁhitā I. 10 for a similar statement.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sāttvataṁ vidhimāsthāya gītassaṁkarṣaṇēna yaḥ ।  
dvāparasya yugasyāntē ādau kaliyugasya ca ॥

iti । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā śāntiparvaṇyapi  -  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā śāntiparvaṇyapi  -  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

avaśyaṁ vaiṣṇavō dīkṣāṁ  
praviśēt sarvayatnataḥ ।  
dīkṣitāya viśēṣēṇa  
prasīdēn nānyathā hariḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Also in the Śāntiparvan: 

> "Certainly, the Vaiṣṇava must undergo Consecration with all effort: for Hari will be particularly graceful to one who has been consecrated and to no one else.204 

204: Mahabharata not identified.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.

As all schools of Śaivism, Vaiṣṇavism too insists upon the performance of Dīkṣā-ceremony.

See Sāttvata Saṁhitā II. 11b-12a:

> karmavāṅmanasaissamyag bhaktānāṁ parameśvara ॥
caturṇāmadhikāro vai prāpte dīkṣākrame sati ।

This Dīkṣā is three-fold, yielding different results to the followers.

Cf. ibid. XIX. 4:

> kaivalyaphaladāpyekā bhogaikaphaladā parā ।  
bhogadaiva tṛtīyā ca prabuddhānāṁ sadaiva hi ॥

Ch. XIX of this āgama deals with Dīkṣā in detail.

Also see Parama Saṁhitā XXXI. 53:

> tisro dīkṣāḥ kṛtā yena vaiṣṇavena tapasvinā ।  
sa eva vaiṣṇavaṁ jñānamakhilaṁ śrotumarhati ॥

Ibid. XXVII. 41b:

> evaṁ dīkṣāṁ tridhā bhinnāṁ uttarottarabhūyasīm ॥

Also cf. ibid. VIII. 3:

> sā tu bhaktivaśāt nṝṇāṁ triṣu karmasu niṣṭhitā ।  
prathamāṁ samaye paścāt tantrajñāne tato 'rcane ॥

The Dīkṣā-ceremony is dealt with in ch. VIII of this Saṁhitā, in detail.The purpose of Initiation is given in VIII. 1-2:

> ata ūrdhvaṁ pravakṣyāmi dīkṣāyā lakṣaṇaṁ param ।  
yāmavāpya viśuddhātmā vaiṣṇavaḥ siddhimṛcchati ॥  
apratiṣṭhasya manasaḥ śreyomārgamavindataḥ ।  
upāyaṁ bandhanasyāhur dīkṣāṁ dīkṣāviśāradāḥ ॥

Also cf. ibid. śl. 6b-7a:

> yastu tīvrḥ prayuñjīta dīkṣāṁ bhaktisamanvitaḥ ॥  
tasya devaprasādena sakalaṁ siddhyatīpsitam ।

The three types of Dīkṣā called Samaya, Tantra and Arcana, are defined and explained in ch. VIII. śls. 7b-11a.

Also, cf. ibid. III. 29b-30a:

> brāhmaṇāḥ kṣatriyā vaiśyāśśūdrā yoṣita eva ca ॥  
bhaktiyuktāḥ svabhāvena kuryād devasya pūjanam ।

It is said that one who undertakes Dīkṣā is better qualified than one without it. Cf. ibid. III. 39:

> dvidvidhaḥ puruṣo brahman dīkṣito 'dīkṣitastathā ।  
dīkṣitassakalaṁ kuryāt ekadeśamadīkṣitaḥ ॥

Cf. also Aniruddha Saṁhitā ch. IV and Viṣṇu Saṁhitā ch. X for different treatments of Dīkṣā.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

avaśyaṁ vaiṣṇavō dīkṣāṁ praviśēt sarvayatnataḥ ।  
dīkṣitāya viśēṣēṇa prasīdēnnānyathā hariḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vasantē dīkṣayēdvipraṁ  
grīṣmē rājanyamēva ca ।  
śaradaḥ samayē vaiśyaṁ  
hēmantē śūdramēva ca ॥  
striyaṁ ca varṣākālē  
tu pañcarātravidhānataḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

One should consecrate a Brahmin in spring, a Kṣatriya in summer, a Vaiśya in the autumn, a Śūdra in winter, a woman in the rainy season according to the Pañcarātra doctrine."206 

[206]: Mahābhārata not identified.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be traced out.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vasantē dīkṣayēdvipraṁ grīṣmē rājanyamēva ca ।  
śaradaḥ samayē vaiśyaṁ hēmantē śūdramēva ca ॥  
striyaṁ ca varṣākālē tu pañcarātravidhānataḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā -  

> vēdaiś caturbhis samitaṁ mērau mahāgirau ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And likewise: "It has been made commensurate with the four Vedas on the great Mountain Meru."207 

[207]: Mahābhārata not identified.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Mahābhārata, śānti*, 322. 28b:
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā -  
vēdaiścaturbhissamitaṁ mērau mahāgirau ।  
</details>

<details><summary>rāma-miśraḥ</summary>

(sama -śabdāttāddhitēna itacpratyayēna vyutpannaḥ samitaśabdō bhavati tulyārthaḥ ।)
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ēvam-ādi-vacō-bhaṅgī-  
śatais sādaram īritaiḥ ॥  
vēdāntasāra-sarvasvam  
ātmīyaṁ paramaṁ matam ।  
pañca-rātraṁ nirākuryāt  
kathaṁ dvaipāyanaḥ svayam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Now, how could Dvaipāyana reject the Pañcaratra, which is his own supreme doctrine, comprising the sense of the Upaniṣads, as follows from these and a hundred direct and circumlocutory declarations made with full respect?

[[80]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Yāmuna holds Vyāsa, the author of the Mahābhārata to be one with Bādarāyaṇa, the author of the Brahmasūtra.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvamādivacōbhaṅgīśataissādaramīritaiḥ ॥  
vēdāntasārasarvasvamātmīyaṁ paramaṁ matam ।  
pañcarātraṁ nirākuryāt kathaṁ dvaipāyanaḥ svayam ।  
</details>

## 11 brahma-sūtrē 'nirākāraḥ

### jīvādy-utpattāv āpattiḥ pūrva-pakṣa-mātram
#### utpattyasaṁbhavāt
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> kathaṁ tarhīdaṁ sūtram "utpattyasaṁbhavāt" iti?  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> 95\. OBJECTION. But then how to explain the sūtra utpattyasaṃbhavāt!? 208

[208]: BrS, 2.2.42. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Brahmasūtra II. ii. -39.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> kathaṁ tarhīdaṁ sūtram "utpattyasaṁbhavāt" iti?  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kiṁ vā'sya sūtrasya hr̥dayam ? 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REPLY. What is the intention of the sūtra?
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiṁ vā'sya sūtrasya hr̥dayam ? 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> idam asya sūtrasya [bhāvaḥ]  
> 
> > bhāgavata-śāstrē jīvōtpattēḥ pratipādyamānatvāt  
tasyāś ca śruti-nyāya-virōdhēnāsambhavād  
asamīcīnaṁ śāstram  
> 
> iti । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

OBJECTION. The following: Since it is expounded in the Bhāgavata Śāstra that the individual soul has an origin, and since this is impossible as it militates against Scripture and Logic, therefore this śāstra is erroneous. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

idamasya ... The ‘pūrvapakṣa’ arguments advanced here are those made by Śaṅkara. See his commentary on the four sūtras comprising the ‘Utpattyasambhava’ or the ‘Pāñcarātra’ section : Brahmasūtra II. ii. 42-45.

sūtrasya ... ‘hr̥dayam’ iti śēṣaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

idamasya sūtrasya [bhāvaḥ] bhāgavataśāstrē jīvōtpattēḥ pratipādyamānatvāt tasyāś ca śruti-nyāya-virōdhēnāsambhavād asamīcīnaṁ śāstram iti । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yady ēṣa sūtrārthas  
tarhi pañcarātra-śāstra-nirākaraṇa-paraṁ sūtram । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REPLY. If that is the meaning of the sūtra,  
the sūtra is intended to reject the Pāñcarātra Śāstra.

~~then how can the sūtra be intended to reject the Pāñcarātra Śāstra?~~
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yady ēṣa sūtrārthas tarhi pañcarātra-śāstra-nirākaraṇa-paraṁ sūtram । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hi pañcarātra-śāstrēṣu jīvōtpattir aṅgīkr̥tā yēnaivam ucyatē ।  
+++(atō na siddhānta-sūtram idam। )+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For the Pāñcarātra Śāstras do not accept that the individual soul has an origin, which assumption would have justified the sūtra's rejection. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi pañcarātra-śāstrēṣu jīvōtpattir aṅgīkr̥tā yēnaivam ucyatē ।
</details>

##### vyūha-prayōjanam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanv astīdaṁ vacanaṁ -  
> 
> > vāsudēvaḥ parā prakr̥tiḥ paramātmā,  
tatas saṅkarṣaṇō nāma jīvō jāyatē ।  
saṅkarṣaṇāt pradyumna-saṁjñaṁ manō jāyatē ।  
tatō'niruddha-nāmā ahaṅkārō jāyatē iti ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> OBJECTION. But is it not their assertion that Vāsudeva is at once the supreme material cause and the supreme spirit; that from him the individual soul Saṅkarṣaṇa is born, from Saṅkarṣaṇa the mind called Pradyumna, and from the latter the ego called Aniruddha?
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Ahirbudhnya Saṁhitā V. 28a:

> bhagavān vāsudēvas sa paramā prakr̥tiś ca sā ।

Cf. Śaṅkara under Brahmasūtra II. ii. 42:

> yat punar idam ucyatē — vāsudēvāt saṅkarṣaṇa utpadyatē, saṅkarṣaṇāc ca pradyumnaḥ, pradyumnāc cāniruddha iti । 

etc.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanv astīdaṁ vacanaṁ vāsudēvaḥ parā prakr̥tiḥ paramātmā tatas saṅkarṣaṇō nāma jīvō jāyatē । saṅkarṣaṇāt pradyumna-saṁjñaṁ manō jāyatē । tatō'niruddha-nāmā ahaṅkārō jāyatē iti ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api tu vyūha-rūpēṇa  
vyaktir dēvasya kīrtyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REPLY. NO. The personal manifestation of God is described as being constituted by vyūhas,209 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[209]: 'Divisions' of the Supreme God as Vāsudeva, Saṃkarṣaṇa, Pradyumna and Aniruddha.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Ahirbudhnya Samhitā, ch. V- 

> **vyūhā** ētē viśālākṣāś  
cātvāraḥ puruṣōttamāḥ।  
nirdōṣā niraniṣṭhāś ca  
niravadyāḥ sanātanāḥ ॥ 5.41 ॥  
anantamakṣaraṁ [#32]caitac  
**cāturātmyaṁ** mahāmunē।  
…  
tatra sthūla-daśāyāṁ tē  
**vyakti-bhāvam** upāgatāḥ ॥ 5.43 ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api tu vyūha-rūpēṇa vyaktir dēvasya kīrtyatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatra saṁvyavahārārthaṁ  
jīva-śabdaḥ prayujyatē ॥  
varṇānām ānulōmyēna  
pūjya-bhēda-prasiddhayē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and the word "individual soul" is assigned to one of these vyūhas for practical purposes, in order to prove clearly the differences that exist within the Adorable One, which differences are in accordance with those of the varṇas. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Ahirbudhnya Samhitā- V. 44- 

> jagatām **upakārāya**  
sac-cid-ānanda-lakṣaṇāḥ।  
mana-ālambanāyaiṣā[#34]  
cāturātmya-vyavasthitiḥ ॥ 5.44 ॥

This Saṃhitā thus clarifies that the four-fold manifestation of the Supreme Lord Vāsudeva, as Saṅkarṣaṇa, Pradyumna and Aniruddha is for the welfare of the creation, by facilitating mental concentration in different degrees for aspirants of different capacities. 

This four-fold manifestation has got a purpose, says the Sāttvata Saṃhitā, namely, facilitating the worship by the four castes, Brāhmana, Kṣatriya, Vaiśya and Sūdra, respectively. 

It is only the Brāhmaṇa that is entitled to worship all these four manifestations of God, viz., Vāsudeva, Saṅkarṣaṇa, Pradyumna and Aniruddha. For the remaining castes, however, only particular forms of God are ordained for worship. For further details, see the Sāttvata Saṃhitā ch. VII. 

Cf. the following passages from the Sāttvata Samhitā

> abjāntam arcanaṁ viṣṇōr  
niṣkāmēṇāgra-janmanā ॥ 29 ॥  
ēvaṁ saṅkarṣaṇādyaṁ tu vāsudēvāntam arcanam ।  
vihitaṁ kṣatra-jātēr vai kartavyatvēna sarvadā ॥ 30 ॥  
pradyumnādyaṁ tu vaiśyasya  
musalāntam udāhr̥tam ।  
sac chūdrasyāniruddhādyaṁ  
pradyumnāntaṁ sadaiva hi ॥ 31 ॥  
sarvatrādhikr̥tō viprō  
vāsudēvādi-pūjanē ।  
yathā tathā na kṣatrādyās  
tasmāc chāstrōktam ācarēt ॥ 55 ॥  
caturṇāṁ brāhmaṇādīnāṁ  
svayam ēvānukampayā ।  
cāturātmyēna rūpēṇa  
caturdhā vyaktimēti ca ॥ 12.17 ॥  
ēvam astv anugrahārthaṁ tu  
śaktyātmā bhāvitātmanām ।  
bibharti bahu-bhēdōtthaṁ 
rūpaṁ sad-vāhana-sthitam ॥ [ 176 ]

the following from the Parama Saṃhitā 11. 99b-101- 

> sa tu dēvaś caturvyuhō  
bhuvanēṣv adhitiṣṭhatē ॥  
dhurmādiṣu parāṁ siddhim  
avāpya hita-kāmyayā ।  
vasudēvas smr̥tō dharmō  
jñānam sankarṣaṇas smr̥taḥ ॥  
tathā vimuktaḥ pradyumnaḥ  
aniruddhas sakalēśvaraḥ 
tatra vyaktās samastāś ca  
catvāras tu guṇā imē ॥

The above passages from the Parama saṃhitā point out that the four forms of the Lord, viz., Vāsudeva, Saṅkarṣaṇa, Pradyumna and Aniruddha are intended by the Lord to initiate the qualities of Dharma, Jñāna, Vimukti and Aiśvarya respectively, in the beings created. 

The fact that the four manifestations of the Lord are designed by the Ford Himself to facilitate the worship by the four different castes is briefly set both by the Pauṣkara Saṃhitā ( ch. 38. śl. 4a, 5a), which Rāmānuja quotes in his śrībhāṣyā under II. ii. 41, p. 829- 

> kartavyatvēna vai yatra  
cātarātmyam upāsatē  
kramāgataiḥ sva-saṁjñābhiḥ  
brāhmaṇair āgamam tu tat । 

C. also Viṣvaksena Saṃhitā XI. 146-147- 

> vasudēvaḥ parā mūrtis  
sthāpanīyā dvijōttamaiḥ ।  
dvitiyā sthāpyatē mūrtiḥ  
kṣatriyair mōkṣa-kāṅkṣibhiḥ ॥  
pradyumnākhyā tu viprēndra  
vaiśyais sthāpyā mumukṣubhiḥ  
śūdrais saṁsthāpyatē mūrtir  
aniruddhō jagad-guruḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatra saṁvyavahārārthaṁ jīva-śabdaḥ prayujyatē ॥  
varṇānām ānulōmyēna pūjya-bhēda-prasiddhayē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā 'huḥ —  

> "varṇaiś caturbhiś catvāraḥ  
pūjanīyā yathā-kramam ।"  

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It is as they say: "The four vyūhas are to be worshipped successively by the four varṇas successively." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā 'huḥ —  

> "varṇaiś caturbhiś catvāraḥ  
pūjanīyā yathā-kramam ।"  

iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca 

> jīva-manō'haṅkāra-śabdā  
na tan-mātra-vacanāḥ  
api tu tat-tad-adhiṣṭhānādhikr̥ta-vilakṣaṇa-vigrahavat-puruṣābhidhānā 

iti ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Besides, the words 'individual soul,' 'mind' and 'ego' do not denote these tanmātras210 themselves, but refer to a person who is the superintending deity of these orders and whose personality is entirely different from the order he superintends. 

[210]: tanmātras here in the sense of the "higher evolutes." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca jīva-manō'haṅkāra-śabdā na tan-mātra-vacanāḥ api tu tattad-adhiṣṭhānādhikr̥ta-vilakṣaṇa-vigrahavat-puruṣābhidhānā iti ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vicitra-dēha-saṁpattir  
janmēti vyapadiśyatē ।  
"tōyēna jīvān" ity ētad  
yajur-mūrdhni yathā vacaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Birth is described as the acquisition of various bodies, as is said in the statement toyena jīvān in the Yajurmūrdhan.211 

[211]: toyena jīvān visasarja bhūmyām, MahānārUp., 1.4.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Taittirīya Āraṇyaka X-i-1b; also Mahānārāyaṇa I-4b.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vicitra-dēha-saṁpattir  
janmēti vyapadiśyatē ।  
tōyēna jīvān ity ētad  
yajur-mūrdhni yathā vacaḥ ॥
</details>

##### nirvāha-sūtrāntaram
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca  
jīvōtpatti-pralayādi-gōcarāḥ śruti-smr̥ti-lōka-vādāḥ 

> "carācara-vyapāśrayas tu syāt -  
tad+++(=brahma)+++-vyapadēśō bhāktas - tad-bhāva-bhāvitvāt" 

ity-atraiva sūtra-kārēṇa kr̥ta-nirvāhāḥ ॥  
+++(atō na siddhānta-sūtram idam। )+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Besides, the Author of the Sūtras has already discarded the śruti, smṛti and profane views concerning the origination and reabsorption of the individual soul in the sūtra carācaravyapāśrayas tu syāt tadvyapadeśo bhāktas tadbhāvabhāvitvāt.212  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[212]: BrS. 2.3.16 (17). Translation: "A word descriptive of moving or unmoving beings, has not a secondary meaning [in referring to Brahman], because such a being's existence depends on Brahman's existence."
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

api ca ... Here Yāmuna points out the discrepancy in Śaṅkara's division of the Brahmasūtra into Adhikaraṇas. According to Śaṅkara, the aphorism “carācaravyapāśrayastu” etc., forms another topic (adhikaraṇa). He argues that the origination of the jīva is not of primary significance. But according to Yāmuna, this point has already been clarified by the sūtra : *nātmā śruteḥ”, etc., so much so that the sūtra “carācara” etc., becomes redundant and thus becomes “anadhikaraṇīya”, that is to say that it does not deserve treatment as a separate topic.

carācara ... Brahmasūtra II. iii. 17.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca jīvōtpatti-pralayādi-gōcarāḥ śruti-smr̥ti-lōka-vādāḥ "carācara-vyapāśrayas tu syāt tad-vyapadēśō bhāktas tadbhāva-bhāvitvāt" ity-atraiva sūtrakārēṇa kr̥ta-nirvāhāḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kiṁ ca 

> "nāmātmā śrutēr,  
+++(tasya)+++ nityattvāc ca tābhyaḥ" 

ity-atraiva brahmaṇō jīvōtpattiḥ śruti-smr̥ti-nyāya-virōdhēna nirastā satī  
na punar upanyāsaṁ prayōjayatīti  
anadhikaraṇīyam adhikaraṇam āpadyēta । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And since, moreover, the origination of the individual soul out of Brahman has been rejected in the sūtras 

> "nātmā śruter nityatvāc ca tābhyaḥ",213 

it does not occasion a renewed exposition:  
an issue which does not need being made a topic would then be made a topic.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[213]: BrS., 2.3.17 (18). Translation: "The ātman is not born because there is no śruti to that effect, and because of its eternality, which is proved by the śrutis."
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. II. iii. 18.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiṁ ca "nāmātmā śrutēr nityattvāc ca tābhyaḥ" ity-atraiva brahmaṇō jīvōtpattiḥ śruti-smr̥ti-nyāya-virōdhēna nirastā satī  
na punar upanyāsaṁ prayōjayatīti anadhikaraṇīyam adhikaraṇam āpadyēta । 
</details>

#### na ca kartuḥ karaṇam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ētēna "na ca kartuḥ karaṇam" iti sūtraṁ vyākhyātam । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[81]]

96\. This also explains the sūtra na ca kartuḥ karaṇam;214  

[214]: BrS, 2.2.43.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. II. ii 40.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ētēna "na ca kartuḥ karaṇam" iti sūtraṁ vyākhyātam । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hy atra karttuḥ saṅkarṣaṇāt karaṇasya manasa utpattir ucyatē । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for it is not said here  
that the instrument, Sc. the mind, originates from the agent, sc. Saṅkarṣaṇa.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hy atra karttuḥ saṅkarṣaṇāt karaṇasya manasa utpattir ucyatē । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

uktaṁ hi vilakṣaṇa-puruṣa-vacanāḥ ētē śabdā iti ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For we have already stated that these names solely refer to the persons who uperintend these orders but are themselves different from them
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

uktaṁ hi vilakṣaṇa-puruṣa-vacanāḥ ētē śabdā iti ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kim iti vā "kartuḥ karaṇaṁ nōtpadyatē" +++(iti sūtram)+++?
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

OBJECTION. Then why this sūtra at all? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

† Cf. Śaṅkara on II-ii-43- 

> na ca kartuḥ karaṇam । itaś cāsaṅgataiṣā kalpanā —  yasmān na hi lōkē kartur dēvadattādēḥ karaṇaṁ paraśv-ādy utpadyamānaṁ dr̥śyatē । varṇayanti ca bhāgavatāḥ 
>
>> kartur jīvāt saṅkarṣaṇa-saṁjñakāt karaṇaṁ manaḥ pradyumna-saṁjñakam utpadyatē, kartr̥jāc ca tasmād aniruddha-saṁjñakō 'haṁkāra utpadyata 
>
> iti । na caitad-dr̥ṣṭāntam antarēṇādhyavasātuṁ śaknumaḥ । na caivaṁbhūtāṁ śrutim upalabhāmahē ॥ 43 ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kim iti vā kartuḥ karaṇaṁ nōtpadyatē ?
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> dēvadattādēḥ kartuḥ paraśu-prabhr̥ti-karaṇōtpatty-adarśanād 

iti cēt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> For we do not find that instruments, like a hatchet, originate from an agent, like Devadatta, so that an instrument out of an agent makes no sense. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

dēvadattādēḥ kartuḥ paraśu-prabhr̥ti-karaṇōtpattyadarśanād iti cēt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

hanta hatas tarhi  apagata-sakala-karaṇa-kalāpa--sva-mahima-pratiṣṭha-brahmaṇaḥ  
prāṇa-manaḥ-prabhr̥ti-nikhila-karaṇōtpattyabhyupagamaḥ

> "ētasmāj jāyatē prāṇō manaḥ sarvēndriyāṇi" 

iti +++(śrutyā)+++।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. Well, then you reject the general view that all instruments, vital airs, mind etc. have their origin in Brahman which itself is without the entire collection of all instruments and rests solely on its own power; this view is stated in the text: "From it springs the vital air, the mind and all the senses."215 

[215]: Muṇḍ Up., 2.1.3.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Muṇḍakopaniṣat II-i-3.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

hanta hatas tarhi apagata-sakala-karaṇa-kalāpa-sva-mahima-pratiṣṭha-brahmaṇaḥ prāṇa-manaḥ-prabhr̥ti-nikhila-karaṇōtpattyabhyupagamaḥ -  
"ētasmāj jāyatē prāṇō manaḥ sarvēndriyāṇi" iti [śrutyā] ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha "śruti-prasiddhatvāt  
tat tathaivābhyupēyatē" ।  
pañcarātra-prasiddhatvād  
idaṁ kiṁ nābhyupaiṣi bhōḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or if you do agree on this because it is clearly proved in Revelation, I ask you why you don't agree on it because it is clearly proved in Pañcaratra. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Yāmuna here pleads for the validity of the Pāñcarātrāgamas on the ground that they, like the Vedas, are based upon knowledge that is free from all defects. Cf. the inferential statement made by Yāmuna above:

> vivādādhyāsitaṁ tantraṁ pramāṇam iti gṛhyatām ।  
nirdoṣajñānajanmatvāt jyotiṣṭomādivākyavat ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha śruti-prasiddhatvāt tat tathaivābhyupēyatē ।  
pañcarātra-prasiddhatvād idaṁ kiṁ nābhyupaiṣi bhōḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hi smr̥ti-prasiddhārtha-  
parityāgō 'tiśōbhanaḥ ।  
nirdōṣa-jñāna-janmatvāt  
prāmāṇyaṁ hi samaṁ dvayōḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It is not a very proper procedure to deny things that are proved by smṛti; since both śruti and smṛti spring from perfect knowledge, they are equally valid.

[[82]]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi smr̥ti-prasiddhārtha-parityāgō 'tiśōbhanaḥ ।  
nirdōṣa-jñāna-janmatvāt prāmāṇyaṁ hi samaṁ dvayōḥ ॥  
</details>

### vyūha-rūpa-bhagavattvay utpatti-karaṇa-sambhavau
#### vijñānādi-bhāvē vā tad-apratiṣēdhaḥ
##### caturdhā-bhāva upapannaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> > yat tu "catvāra ētē kiṁ  
samānaiśvarya-bhāginaḥ ।  
svatantrāḥ kim utaikasya  
svēcchā-mūrti-catuṣṭayī ॥"
> 
> iti vikalpya  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> The Author raises the question which one of two alternatives may be true:  
Are these four equally and independently sovereign,  
or has one a quaternity of personalities which he has assumed at his own desire?  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Śaṅkara on II. ii. 44. 

> atrōcyatē — ēvam api,  
**tad-apratiṣēdhaḥ** utpatty-asambhavasyāpratiṣēdhaḥ, yadi tāvad ayam abhiprāyaḥ — paraspara-bhinnā ēvaitē vāsudēvādayaś catvāra īśvarās tulya-dharmāṇaḥ, naiṣām ēkātmakatvam astīti; tatō 'nēkēśvara-kalpanā'narthakyam , ēkēnaivēśvarēṇēśvara-kārya-siddhēḥ।
>
> siddhānta-hāniś ca, bhagavān ēvaikō vāsudēvaḥ paramārtha-tattvam ity abhyupagamāt ।
>
> athā 'yam abhiprāyaḥ —  
> 
>> ēkasyaiva bhagavata ētē catvārō vyūhās tulya-dharmāṇa 
> 
> iti, tathāpi tad-avastha ēvōtpatty-asambhavaḥ। na hi vāsudēvāt saṅkarṣaṇasyōtpattiḥ sambhavati, saṅkarṣaṇāc ca pradyumnasya, pradyumnāc cāniruddhasya, atiśayābhāvāt। bhavitavyaṁ hi kāryakāraṇayōr atiśayēna, yathā mr̥d-ghaṭayōḥ। na hy asaty atiśayē, kāryaṁ kāraṇam ity avakalpatē। na ca pañca-rātra-siddhāntibhiḥ vāsudēvādiṣv ēkasmin sarvēṣu vā jñānaiśvaryādi-tāratamya-kr̥taḥ kaścid bhēdō 'bhyupagamyatē। vāsudēvā ēva hi sarvē vyūhā nirviśēṣā iṣyantē। na caitē bhagavad-vyūhāś catuḥ-saṅkhyāyām ēvāvatiṣṭhēran , brahmādi-stamba-paryantasya samastasyaiva jagatō bhagavad-vyūhatvāvagamāt ॥ 44 ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yat tu "catvāra ētē kiṁ  
samānaiśvarya-bhāginaḥ ।  
svatantrāḥ kim utaikasya  
svēcchā-mūrti-catuṣṭayī ॥"

iti vikalpya   
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> > "samānaiśvarya-bhāgitvē  
tulyatvān naiva kāryatā ।  
ēkasya mūrti-bhēdaś cēt  
kiṁ bhēdēna prayōjanam ॥"
> 
> iti dūṣayati

iti vyākhyātaṁ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> and then he points out the defect: if they are equally sovereign, none of them can be effects because they are equal; when they are different forms of one, what is the purpose of this division? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

"samānaiśvarya-bhāgitvē tulyatvān naiva kāryatā ।  
ēkasya mūrti-bhēdaś cēt kiṁ bhēdēna prayōjanam ॥"

iti dūṣayatīti vyākhyātaṁ 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"vijñānādi-bhāvē vā tad-apratiṣēdhaḥ" iti , 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

97\. OBJECTION. The sūtra  vā tadapratiṣedhaḥ 216 is explained as ~~follows:~~ above.

[216]: BrS., 2.2.44.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Brahmasūtra-II-ii-41.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

"vijñānādi-bhāvē vā tad-apratiṣēdhaḥ" iti । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad ayuktam - a-sambhāvanīyatvād vikalpasya । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. That is not correct, because an alternative is impossible. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad ayuktam asambhāvanīyatvād vikalpasya । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hi kēnacid īśvara-vādinā  
anēkēśvaraṁ jagad abhyupagataṁ  
viśēṣataś ca pāñcarātrikaiḥ -  
vāsudēva ēvaikaḥ parā prakr̥tir iti vadadbhiḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For no one who holds that there is a God theorizes that the world has several Gods, least of all the Pāñcarātrikas who hold that "Vāsudeva is the ultimate material cause". 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Ahirbudhnya Saṁhitā V-28a:

> bhagavān vāsudēvaḥ sa paramā prakr̥tiś ca sā ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi kēnacid īśvaravādinā anēkēśvaraṁ jagad abhyupagataṁ viśēṣataś ca pāñcarātrikaiḥ -  
vāsudēva ēvaikaḥ parā prakr̥tir iti vadadbhiḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kintu sa ēva bhagavān līlā-viracita-caturbhēdaḥ sakalam api jagat saṁrakṣatīti ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

But this one Bhagavān, who has divided Himself into four for reasons of sport, protects the entire world. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. ibid. śls. 21b-24- 

> tatra jñānamayatvēna  
dēvas saṁkarṣaṇō balī ॥  
vyanakty aikāntikaṁ mārgaṁ  
bhagavat-prāpti-sādhanam ।  
vīryaiśvaryamayō dēvaḥ  
pradyumnaḥ puruṣōttamaḥ ॥  
sthitaḥ śāstrārtha-bhāvēna  
bhagavat-prāpti-vartmanā ।  
śāstrārthasya phalaṁ yat tad  
bhagavat-prāpti-lakṣaṇam ॥  
prāpayaty aniruddhas san  
sādhakān puruṣōttamaḥ ।  
śāstra-śāstrārtha-tat-sādhya-  
phala-nirvāhakā imē ॥ 

Cf. Philosophy of Viśiṣṭādvaita, p. 156- 

> Vasudeva, the perfect self, manifests Himself in the interests of the meditational needs of the devotee, as Saṅkarṣaṇa with the two qualities of jñāna and bala, as Pradyumna with the qualities of aiśvarya and vīrya, and as Aniruddha with Śakti and Tejas without any diminution of Divinity. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kintu sa ēva bhagavān līlā-viracita-caturbhēdaḥ sakalam api jagat saṁrakṣatīti ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na cēdam anupapannaṁ -  
bala-bharatāvarajāgrajādi-prādurbhāvavad upapattēḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And this position is not unjustified, because it is justified in the same manner as the appearance of second-born and first-born brothers like Bala and Bharata. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cēdam anupapannaṁ -  
balabharatāvarajāgrajādiprādurbhāvavadupapattēḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathaiva hi bhagavataḥ sva-līlā-viracita-gagana-pavana-hara-viriñcy- ādi-prapañcasya  
acintya-mahima-līlaika-prayōjanasya  
rāma-lakṣmaṇa-bharata-śatrughnādi--sva-cchandā vigrahā  
na virōtsyantē  
ēvaṁ saṅkarṣaṇa-pradyumnādi-bhēdā iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For just as the Bhagavān, who has created the variety of phenomena of ether, Wind, Śiva, Brahmā etc. for His sport, whose sole motivation is the sport of his unfathomable power, has voluntarily assumed the personalities of Rāma, Lakṣmaṇa, Bharata, Śatrughna etc., without there being the possibility of logical conflict in the same manner the divisions of Saṅkarṣaṇa, Pradyumna and Aniruddha, too, are unconflicting.

[[83]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

CJ. Sāttvata Saṁhitā IV. 33-34- 

> yathāmbara-sthas savitā  
tvēka ēva mahā-matē ।  
jalāśrayāṇi cāśritya  
bahutvaṁ sampradarśayēt ।  
ēvam ēkō 'pi bhagavān  
nānā-mantrāśrayēṣu ca ।  
turyādi-pada-saṁsthēṣu  
bahutvam upayāti ca ॥ +++(5)+++  

The cause behind the manifestation of the Lord into different forms is His mere sport ( krīḍā or līlā) and the purpose of this manifestation is protection for the good. 

Cf. Ahirbudhnya Saṁhitā ch. 36 Śls. 64, 65. 

> pratitrētāyugaṁ dēvaḥ  
sādhu-trāṇa-kr̥tē iriḥ ।  
rāma-lakṣmaṇa-śatrughna-  
bharatādy ātmanā svayam ॥  
caturdhā 'vasthitas tadvat  
cakrātmā harir ēva hi ।  
guṇa-pradhāna-bhāvas tu  
rāmādēr iva yujyatē ॥ 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cēdamanupapannaṁ bala-bhāratāvarajāgrajādiprādurbhāvavadupapattēḥ, yathaiva hi bhagavataḥ svalīlāviracitagagana-pavana-hara-viriñcyādiprapañcasya acintyamahimalīlaikaprayōjanasya rāma-lakṣmaṇa-bharata-śatrughnādisvacchandā vigrahā na virōtsyantē ēvaṁ saṅkarṣaṇapradyumnādibhēdā iti ।  
</details>

### śabda-vipratiṣēdhō na
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yat paraṁ "vipratiṣēdhād" iti  
"caturṣu vēdēṣv" iti +++(adhyāhr̥tya)+++ śruti-vipratiṣēdhāt,  
tantrāṇāṁ paras-para-vipratiṣēdhād vā ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

98\. Furthermore, vipratiṣedhāt 217 may mean "because of conflict with Revelation",  
on the basis of the citation "failing to find in the four Vedas..."  
or "because of mutual conflict between the Tantras themselves". 

[217]: BrS., 2.2.45.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Brahmasūtra- II-ii-42. The reading found in the Śrībhāṣya and Śāṅkarabhāṣya is- 'vipratiṣēdhāc ca'. But Yāmuna, throughout has it as 'vipratiṣēdhāt'. 

Cf. Śaṅkara on II-ii-45 - 'vipratiṣēdhāc ca'

> vipratiṣēdhaś ca +asmin śāstrē bahu-vidha upalabhyatē —  
guṇa-guṇitva-kalpanādi-lakṣaṇaḥ।  
>
>> jñānaiśvarya-bala-vīrya-tējāṁsi guṇāḥ, ātmāna ēvaitē, bhagavantō vāsudēvā 
>
> ity-ādi-darśanāt।  
> 
> vēda-vipratiṣēdhaś ca bhavati —  
> 
>> caturṣu vēdēṣu paraṁ śrēyō 'labdhvā śāṇḍilya idaṁ śāstram adhigatavān 
> 
> ity-ādi-vēda-nindā-darśanāt।  

tasmāt asaṅgataiṣā kalpanēti siddham ॥ 45 ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yatparaṁ vipratiṣēdhāt iti caturṣu vēdēṣu iti śrutivipratiṣēdhāt tantrāṇāṁ parasparavipratiṣēdhādvā ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

apramāṇam iti tatra śruti-vipratiṣēdhastu prāgēva pratyuktaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The former alternative, incompatibility with Revelation has already been refuted as being without valid basis. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

apramāṇamiti tatra śrutivipratiṣēdhastu prāgēva pratyuktaḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

paras-para-vipratiṣēdhas tu  
pradhāna-guṇa--sāmānya-viśēṣādi-nyāya- saṁpādita-vacana-vyaktīnāṁ tantrāṇāṁ nāsty ēva 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Mutual conflict between the Pañcarātra Tantras themselves, whose terminological precision has been perfected by the rules of logic governing principal matter, generality, peculiarity, quality and the like, does not exist. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘pradhāna-guṇa-nyāyaḥ’ = aṅgāṅgi-bhāvaḥ; ‘sāmānya-viśēṣa-nyāyaḥ’ = chāga-paśu-nyāyaḥ।

vacana-vyaktīnāṁ = vacanānvaya-kramāṇām।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

parasparavipratiṣēdhas tu pradhānaguṇasāmānyaviśēṣādinyāyasaṁpāditavacanavyaktīnāṁ tantrāṇāṁ nāstyēva 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nyāyānugraha-rahitānāṁ tu vacasāṁ  
na kvacid api pariniścāyakatvam,  
yathā 'ha 

> (padajātaṁ śrutaṁ sarvaṁ  
smāritānanvitārdhakam । )  
nyāya-saṁpādita-vyakti  
paścād-vākyārtha-bōdhakam॥ 

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

On the other hand, statements that lack the corroboration of logic can have no cogency; 

as the maxim says: 

> "A statement must have precision perfected by logic before it can communicate its meaning." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The source is yet to be identified. This verse, however, is quoted in full by Sudarśani, in his commentary on the Śrībhāṣya, I-i-1; pp. 168-169- 

> pada-jātaṁ śrutaṁ sarvaṁ smāritānanvitārthakam । 
nyāya-sampādita-vyakti paścād vākyārtha-bōdhakam ॥ 

Vedāntadeśika too quotes this in his Nyāyapariśuddhi, p.151. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nyāyānugraharahitānāntu vacasāṁ na kvacidapi pariniścāyakatvam,yathā 'ha —

> nyāya-sampādita-vyakti  
paścād-vākyārtha-bōdhakam॥ 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tasmāt sūtrakārēṇa  
"idaṁ mahōpaniṣadam" ity-ādi-vacanair  
vēdēbhyō 'viśēṣēṇābhimatatara-prāmāṇyēṣu pañca-rātra-tantrēṣv  
a-vidyamāna-jīvōtpatti-pratipādanādhyārōpēṇa  
tan-nirākaraṇa-paratayā sūtraṁ vyākhyāyamānaṁ  
vyākhyātr̥̄ṇām ēvākhyātiṁ khyāpayatītyalaṁ prabandhēna । +++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Consequently, the Author of the Sūtras gives the lie to those exegetes who,  
by superimposing on the Pañcarātra Tantras  
(whose validity he strongly affirms as no less than that of the Vedas, in such assertions as "idaṃ mahopaniṣadam," etc.)  
the non-existent doctrine of the soul's origination,  
explain that the sūtra means to reject the Pañcaratra Tantras. 

Enough.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

idaṁ ... Mahābhārata, Sānti, ch. 326.100. 

'aviśēṣēṇa' samānatayā ity arthaḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasmāt sūtrakārēṇa idaṁ mahōpaniṣadam ityādivacanairvēdēbhyōviśēṣēṇābhimatataraprāmāṇyēṣu pañcarātratantrēṣvavidyamānajīvōtpattipratipādanādhyārōpēṇa tannirākaraṇaparatayā sūtraṁ vyākhyāyamānaṁ vyākhyātr̥̄ṇāmēvākhyātiṁ khyāpayatītyalaṁ prabandhēna ।
</details>

## 12 brahma-sūtrē 'ṅgīkāraḥ

### sandarbhaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatraiṣa sūtrārthaḥ -  
pūrvaṁ svābhiprēta-samaya-paripanthi--kapila- kāśyapa-sugata-jina-paśupati-matānāṁ  
śruti-nyāya virōdhād asāmañjasyaṁ pratipādya 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

99\. The meaning of the Sūtras is this. First the Author has set forth that the doctrines of Kapila, Kaśyapa, Buddha, Jina and Paśupati,218  
who oppose the Author's own accepted doctrine, are unnatural219 because they conflict with Revelation and logic. 

[218]: In BrS., 2,2.
[219]: asāmañjasya, taken from BrS., 2.2.37.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatraiṣa sūtrārthaḥ pūrvaṁ svābhiprētasamayaparipanthikapila-kāśyapasugata-jina-paśupatimatānāṁ śrutinyāya virōdhādasāmañjasyaṁ pratipādya 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

adhunā svābhiprēta--pañca-rātra-tantrāṇām api itara-samaya-samāna-parigaṇanād  
buddhau sannihitānām itara-samayavad a-sāmañjasyam āśaṅkya  
prāmāṇyaṁ vyutpādyatē +++(sthūṇā-nikhanana-nyāyēna)+++।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Now, in order to remove the suspicion that the Pancarãtra Tantras (which are his own accepted doctrine) are equally unnatural with the other doctrines because their usual enumeration on an equal plane with the others has made them closely associated with them in people's thinking, he elicits their validity. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

sannihitānām ... tantratva-sāmānyēna sannihitānām iti bhāvaḥ।

vyutpādyatē = sthāpyatē।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

adhunā svābhiprētapañcarātratantrāṇāmapi itarasamayasamānaparigaṇanād buddhau sannihitānām itarasamayavadasāmañjasyam āśaṅkya prāmāṇyaṁ vyutpādyatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>rāma-miśraḥ</summary>

sthūṇā-nikhanana-nyāyēna +ityarthaḥ -  
yathā hi sthūṇāṁ draḍhayitum icchavas  
tām svayam ēva hastēna paricālya parīkṣantē ।
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

+ vyutpādyatē = sthāpyatē । 
</details>

### jīva-karaṇōtpatty-arthēna
#### pūrvapakṣaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatrādyēna sūtradvayēna pūrvapakṣa upakṣipyatē,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the first two Sūtras the prima-facie case is laid down:  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

According to Śaṅkara, all the four aphorisms of the utpattyasambhava section [ 11-ii-42-45 ] put forth the refutation of the Pañcarātra. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatrādyēna sūtradvayēna pūrvapakṣa upakṣipyatē,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā hi -  

> pañcarātraśāstram apramāṇam **utpattyasaṁbhavāt** -  
pratipādyamānāyāḥ saṁkarṣaṇādyutpattēḥ asaṁbhavāt। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

the Pancarãtra likewise has no validity, utpattyasaṃbhavāt, i.e., on account of the impossibility of Saṅkarṣaṇa's origination which is taught there. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi pañcarātraśāstram apramāṇam utpattyasaṁbhavāt pratipādyamānāyāḥ saṁkarṣaṇādyutpattēḥ asaṁbhavāt
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> katham asaṁbhavaḥ? ubhayathā 'pyanupapattēḥ। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Why should it be impossible? Because it cannot be established in either of two possible cases; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

katham asaṁbhavaḥ, ubhayathā 'pyanupapattēḥ। 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tathā hi ।
>
> kintu catvāra ēvaitē  
samānaiśvaryabhāginaḥ ।
ēkō vā syāt catur-bhēdē  
dvēdhā vyutpattyasaṁbhavaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> either the four vyūhas are equally sovereign, or else one God exists in four persons; and in either case there is impossibility of origination. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi ।

kintu catvāra ēvaitē samānaiśvaryabhāginaḥ ।
ēkō vā syāt caturbhēdē dvēdhā vyutpattyasaṁbhavaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> samānaiśvaryabhāgitvē tulyatvān naiva sr̥jyatē ।
ēkātmatvē 'bhyupētē 'pi tathōtpattēḥ asaṁbhavāt ।
sraṣṭr̥sr̥jyavibhāgō hi naikasmin avakalpatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> If they are equally sovereign, they cannot be created because they are equal; if only one being is admitted no origination is possible either, since a distribution within one being of creating and created parts is inconceivable.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> samānaiśvaryabhāgitvē tulyatvān naiva sr̥jyatē ।
ēkātmatvē 'bhyupētē 'pi tathōtpattēḥ asaṁbhavāt ।
sraṣṭr̥sr̥jyavibhāgō hi naikasmin avakalpatē ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā 

> na ca kartuḥ karaṇam  
itaś ca +apramāṇaṁ kartuḥ saṅkarṣaṇa-saṁjñāj jīvāt karaṇasya pradyumnasaṁjñasya manasa utpatty-a-saṁbhavāt,  
na hi dēvadattāt paraśurutpadyata 

iti ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[84]]

> 100\. Similarly na ca kartuḥ karaṇam: Pañcarātra has no validity for the further reason that it is impossible that the instrument, sc. the mind called Pradyumna, originates from the agent, sc. the individual soul called Saṅkarṣaṇa, for the hatchet does not originate from Devadatta. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Brahmasūtra II. ii. 40.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā na ca kartuḥ karaṇam itaśca apramāṇaṁ kartuḥ saṅkarṣaṇa-saṁjñāj jīvāt karaṇasya pradyumnasaṁjñasya manasa utpattyasaṁbhavāt, na hi dēvadattāt paraśurutpadyata iti ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ēvaṁ vā -  

> "na ca kartuḥ karaṇam"।  
itaśca kartuḥ saṁkarṣaṇāt na karaṇam utpadyatē -  
brahmaṇa ēva samasta-karaṇōtpatti-śrutēḥ,  
> 
> > ētasmāj jāyatē prāṇō,  
manaḥ sarvēndriyāṇi ca 
> 
> iti।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Or there is this alternative explanation of na ca kartuḥ karaṇam:  
and for the further reason that the instrument does not originate from the agent Saṅkarṣaṇa,  
since according to the text: 
> 
> > "From it spring the vital air, the mind and all the senses,"  
> 
> it is revealed that all instruments really originate from Brahman.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

na ca ... Cf. Śrībhāṣya under II. ii. 40, where almost the same words are used. 

ētasmājjāyatē ... Mundakopanisad II. 1. 3. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvaṁ vā na ca kartuḥ karaṇam itaśca kartuḥ saṁkarṣaṇāt na karaṇam utpadyatē brahmaṇa ēva samastakaraṇōtpattiśrutēḥ, ētasmājjāyatē prāṇō manaḥ sarvēndriyāṇi ca iti।  
</details>

#### uttara-pakṣaḥ - vyūha-brahmatva-mātrēṇa 
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> vijñānādi-bhāvē vā tad-a-pratiṣēdha 

iti,  
vā-śabdāt pakṣō viparivarttatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

101\. Then follows: vijñānādibhāve vā tadapratiṣedhaḥ.  
By the particle va this prima-facie case is now reversed.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Śrībhāṣya under II.ii. 41- "vijñānādibhāve vā tadapratiṣedhaḥ," where again the same words are used. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vijñānādibhāvē vā tadapratiṣēdha iti, vā-śabdāt pakṣō viparivarttatē ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad uktam 

> ubhayathā'pi saṁkarṣaṇādy-utpattēr asaṁbhavād aprāmāṇyam 

iti naitad asti।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

What has been said, viz., that there is no validity since in neither case origination of Saṅkarṣaṇa etc. is possible, is untrue: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yaduktamubhayathā'pi saṁkarṣaṇādyutpattērasaṁbhavādaprāmāṇyamiti naitadasti।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tasyās saṅkarṣaṇādy-utpattēr apratiṣēdhaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

it is not contradictory that Saṅkarṣaṇa etc. have originated. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasyāssaṅkarṣaṇādyutpattērapratiṣēdhaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi hi vijñānādaya ētē +++(saṅkarṣaṇādayaḥ)+++ na bhavēyuḥ - syād utpatti-pratiṣēdhaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Indeed, it would be contradictory if they were not vijñānādi. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'ētē' saṅkarṣaṇādayaḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi hi vijñānādaya ētē na bhavēyuḥ syādutpattipratiṣēdhaḥ ।  
</details>

##### vijñānādiḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vijñānañ cādi+++(ś)+++ cēti vijñānādi brahma,  
tad-bhāvē brahma-bhāvē utpattēr apratiṣēdhaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Vijñānādi is a dvandva compound: "knowledge and beginning," that means: Brahman;   
thus vijñānādibhāve means brahmabhāve.  
Inasmuch as they are Brahman (brahmabhāve), the origination is not contradictory. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vijñānañcādi cēti vijñānādi brahma tadbhāvē brahmabhāvē utpattērapratiṣēdhaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>rāma-miśraḥ</summary>

ādīyatē -upādīyatē upayujyatē sarvakāryārtham ity ādi sarvajagannidānaṁ brahma।+++(5)+++  

atra yadyapi  
"upasargē ghōḥ kir" iti pāṇinīyēna  
kipratyayāntādi-śabdasya nityapuṁstvaṁ prāpnōti  
tathāpīha auṇādika-pratyayēna sādhi-bhāvō 'vagantavyaḥ  
"śiṣṭaprayōgē saṁjñāsu dhāturūpāṇī"tyadinā tathaivānuśiṣṭatvēna  
śiṣṭa-śiṣṭēr ēva ca prayōgamūlatayā anauṇādikasyaiva puṁstva-kalpanāt ॥  

athavā vijñānaṁ cādiścētyēva pāṭhaḥ ।  
tataśca vijñānaṁ cādiśca vijñānādi iti samāhāradvandvaḥ, vijñānādīti-kr̥ta-samāhāra-dvandvakē vijñānādi-padē  
nirvisargaka-pāṭhāvalōkana-bhrāntita ēva  
prācīnakōśēṣvapi vijñānaṁ cādiścēti vivakṣaṇīyē  
vijñānaṁ cādi cēti lilikhuriti kēcin manyantē । +++(4)+++ 

ita ēvāsvarasēna kalpāntaram avalalambirē granthācāryāḥ।  
ēvam ēva ca vijñānādi-sūtrē śrībhāṣyē'pi -  
śaṅkāsamādhy-abhyūhanam iti kr̥taṁ  
"kusr̥ṣṭyā vācām" iti cāparē ।  

vastutastu śrībhāṣyakōśēṣu āgama-prāmāṇya-kōśēṣu ca  
prāyaśō dēśa-viśēṣa-nairapēkṣyēṇa vijñānādi-sūtrē  
(vijñānaṁ cādi ca vijñānādi -brahma tadbhāvē)  
ityēva prāmāṇikaḥ pāṭha  
ity avaśyaṁ tātparya-viśēṣēṇa sa prayōgō vaktavyō,  
na tu yathā-śrutārthakādi-padēnācaramārthēna a-brahma-sādhāraṇēna ।  

atraivam ācācakṣmahē ā-samantād attuṁ śīlam asyēty ādin paramaṁ brahma supyajātau ṇinistācchīlyē ।  
iti pāṇinīyēna tācchīlyē'rthēṇiniḥ,  
āṅgā cāsādhāraṇyaṁ vivakṣyatē tacca attā carācaragrahaṇād ity-adhikaraṇōktarītyā  
brahmāsādhāraṇaṁ karmēti  
tādr̥śārthakādipadēna  
nikhila-jagad-adana-kartr̥-paraṁ brahmābhihitaṁ bhavati  
tacca sāṅkhyādyuktadiśā pradhānadharmō mābhūditi vijñānapadēna viśēṣyatē ।  

ēvaṁ ca janmādyasya yata iti sūtrē  
ādipadēna jagatsthitipraṇāśahētutāyā lakṣaṇatvēnābhimatatayā  
lakṣaṇēnētarabhēdasādhanē janmādi-tritayasya saṁhaty-ahētutāyāṁ vyāpyatvāsiddhyā  
pratyēkam ēva hētutāyā vācyatvēna svāsādhāraṇarūpēṇādin padēna brahmōpasthāpitaṁ bhavatīti ।  

sati caivaṁ (vijñānaṁ cādi ca vijñānādi brahma) iti śrībhāṣyācāryāṇāṁ  
paramācāryāṇāṁ śrī-yāmunamunīnāṁ cābhidhānam  
añjasā samañjasam  
iti yathāśrutārthagrāhiṇāṁ kēṣāṁcid amīṣām ācārya-tātparyanabōdha-nibandhanam ēvānupapatty-abhidhānam ।  

parē tu saṁpad-āditvāt kvipaṁ kr̥tvā  
tasmāt svārthē vidhāya  
āda iti prasādhya  
tatō matvarthīyēninā ādinapadaṁ siṣādhayiṣanti ।  
tadidam api prakriyā-gaurava-parāhatam  
iti nātitr̥ptayē viduṣām ।  

kiṁ ca ac-chabdasya saṁpadādi-kvib-antasya nitya-strītvē  
tatō'ṇi jātē aṇantatvēna ṅīpi'vaśyaṁ bhāvēna  
ādī iti syāditi tatō'pi nēṣṭasiddhisaṁbhāvanā ।  

yadapi adanam āda iti "bhāvē" iti sūtrēṇa  
bhāvē ghañaṁ kr̥tvā bhāvaghañantāc ca matv-arthīyēninā  
ādinpada-prasādhanaṁ -  
tad idaṁ ghañapōś cēti pāṇinīyānuśāsana-vismaraṇa-nibandhanaṁ  
ghañi ghaslādēśa-vidhānāt ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ētad uktaṁ bhavati -  

> ēkasyaiva paramātmanō vāsudēvasyāparicchinna-śaktēḥ  
svamāyāvēśa-vaśāt kārya-kāraṇa-bhāvōpapattir 

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

That is to say by virtue of the fact that the unique Supreme Soul Vāsudeva, whose omnipotence is unbounded, enters into them through His māyā, a cause-effect relation is justified. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ētaduktaṁ ... catvāra īśvarā iti pakṣaḥ parityaktaḥ । tad-ēkatva-pakṣaḥ samādr̥taḥ। ēka ēva bhagavān sarvēśvaraḥ svalīlayā jagad-avanāya caturdhā 'vataratīti siddhāntaḥ । 

ēkasyaiva ... Vide Ahirbudhnya Saṁhitā Ch. V- 

> puruṣāḥ puṇḍarīkākṣā  
vyūhāḥ śaktimayā harēḥ ।  [25a ]

> sarva-śaktimayō dēvō  
vāsudēvaḥ sisr̥kṣayā ॥  
vibhajaty ātmanā ''tmānaṁ  
yas sa saṅkarṣaṇas smr̥taḥ । [ 29b-30a ] 

> ananta ēva bhagavān  
vāsudēvas sanātanaḥ ।  
tatra jñāna-balōnmēṣāt  
sva-saṅkalpa-pracōditāt ॥  
ananta ēva bhagavān  
dēvas saṅkarṣaṇō 'cyutaḥ ।  [ 34-35a ]

> ananta ēva bhagavān  
pradyumnaḥ puruṣōttamaḥ । [36a ]  

ananta ēva bhagavān  
aniruddhō bhavaty uta ॥ [38b ] 

The words "ananta eva bhagavān" occuring in 34a, 35a, 36a & 38b quoted above, stress the point that he Lord is One and only One and that He assumes different forms, without any diminution of His powers and perfections in this process. Therefore, the question raised by Śaṅkara regarding the plurality of God is unwarranted. 

svamāyāvēśa ... This Māyā is the Śakti or the Power of the Lord, termed also Jñāna, Vidyā, Saṅkalpa and so on. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ētaduktaṁ bhavati ēkasyaiva paramātmanō vāsudēvasyāparicchinnaśaktēḥ svamāyāvēśavaśāt kāryakāraṇabhāvōpapattiriti ।  
</details>

##### karaṇōtpattiḥ - vipratiṣēdhāt
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yat tu  

> na saṅkarṣaṇān mana utpadyatē  
brahmaṇa ēva utpatti-śrutēr 

iti -  
tad api tasya vijñānāditvēna parihr̥tam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The objection that the mind cannot originate from Saṅkarṣaṇa, on the authority of the śruti that the mind originates from Brahman, is invalidated by the fact that he, sc. Saṅkarṣaṇa is vijñānādi, i.e., Brahman.

[[85]]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yattu na saṅkarṣaṇānmana utpadyatē brahmaṇa ēva utpattiśrutēriti tadapi tasya vijñānāditvēna parihr̥tam ।  
</details>

#### uttara-pakṣaḥ - yuktyā karaṇōtpatti-siddhyā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca "na ca kartuḥ karaṇam" iti kimuktaṁ bhavati? 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

102\. Furthermore, what is being said in the argument na ca kartuḥ karaṇam?  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

api ca ... These different interpretations are not included by Rāmānuja in his Śrībhāṣya. 

na ca ... Vide Brahmasūtra: II.ii.40.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca na ca kartuḥ karaṇam iti kimuktaṁ bhavati ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kiṁ yasyāḥ kriyāyā yat karaṇaṁ  
tat kriyā-kartur nōtpadyatē,  

uta yad yatra kvāpi +++(kriyāyāṁ)+++ karaṇaṁ  
tat kutaścid api kartur nōtpadyata iti vā ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Is it that the instrument of a certain action does not originate from the agent of that same action;  
or that no instrument of any action whatever originates from any agent whatsoever? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'yatra kvāpi kriyāyām' iti śēṣaḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiṁ yasyāḥ kriyāyā yatkaraṇaṁ tatkriyākarturnōtpadyatē, uta yad yatra kvāpi karaṇaṁ tat kutaścidapi karturnōtpadyata iti vā ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatrādyē kalpē +++(←"kriyāyāḥ karaṇaṁ kartur nōtpadyatē")+++  
siddha-sādhanatayā anumānasya vipratiṣēdhaḥ -   

na hy atra  
saṅkarṣaṇāt kartur utpadyamānaṁ manaḥ  
svōtpādanē karaṇaṁ - karmatvāt,  

nāpi svōtpattau +++(siddhāyām)+++ - +++(tadā tasya)+++ kartr̥tvāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If the first view is taken, we have a conflict with Inference, because the argument contains the fallacy of proving the proved.  

The mind, originating from the agent Saṅkarṣaṇa cannot be the instrument of Saṅkarṣaṇa's action of originating it,  
since it itself is the object of the action;  

nor can it be the instrument of the action of being originated, since it itself is the agent of that action. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatrādyē kalpē siddhasādhanatayā anumānasya vipratiṣēdhaḥ,  
na hyatra saṅkarṣaṇātkarturutpadyamānaṁ manaḥ svōtpādanē karaṇaṁ karmatvāt, nāpi svōtpattau kartr̥tvāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

aparē'pi kalpē pratyakṣa-vipratiṣēdhaḥ -  

udakāharaṇādau karaṇa-bhūtānām api ghaṭādīnāṁ  
kartuḥ kulālādēr utpatti-darśanāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If the alternative view is taken, we have a conflict with Perception, because we see that for instance a pitcher, though it be the instrument of an action of fetching water, yet originates from the agent of such an action, the potter. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

aparē'pi kalpē pratyakṣavipratiṣēdhaḥ udakāharaṇādau karaṇabhūtānāmapi ghaṭādīnāṁ kartuḥ kulālādērutpattidarśanāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad idam āha - vipratiṣēdhād iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This the Author says in the sūtra vipratiṣedhāt: 'because there is conflict.'
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Brahmasūtra: II.ii.42.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadidamāha vipratiṣēdhāditi ।  
</details>

#### uttara-pakṣaḥ - brahma-kartr̥tva-niścayēna
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad vā sūtra-dvayasyāsya  
**vyākhyānāntaram** ucyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>En - viśvāsaḥ</summary>

Or, we state an alternative explation for the two sutras.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[86]]

103\. ~~As to the other explanation that has been given of these two Sūtras,220 

[220]: supra §§96, 97.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

siddhānta-sūtra-dvayasya - 'vijñānādi-bhāvē vā tad-apratiṣēdhaḥ, vipratiṣēdhāt' iti sūtra-dvayasyēti bhāvaḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadvā sūtradvayasyāsya vyākhyānāntaramucyatē ।  
</details>

##### vijñānam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vijñānādēḥ +++(brahmaṇaḥ)+++ pramāṇatva-  
hētōr +++(sad-)+++**bhāvē, na yujyatē** ॥  
pañca-rātra-pramāṇatva-  
**niṣēdhō** 'tiprasaṅgataḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

since it is vijñānādi, i.e. "a ground for validity",221 the denial of the validity of Pāñcarātra is not justified, because it entails overextension. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[221]: ie., as a tatpuruṣa compound "the beginning (source) of (valid) knowledge:" vijñānādibhāve "since He (God) is a source of valid knowledge." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

'vijñānādēḥ' brahmaṇa ity arthaḥ । 

bhāvē - sad-bhāvē । 

atiprasaṅgaḥ ... anyathā manvādi-smr̥tēr api aprāmāṇya-prasaktēr ity āśayaḥ । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vijñānādēḥ pramāṇatvahētōr bhāvē na yujyatē ॥  
pañcarātrapramāṇatvaniṣēdhō'tiprasaṅgataḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatrānuvāda-sandēha-  
jñānānutpatti-lakṣaṇam ॥  
nirastam a-pramāṇatvaṁ  
vijñāna-grahaṇād iha +++(→"vijñānādēr vā")+++ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The invalidity, which is defined by the non-origination of knowledge through repetition or dubiety in the Tantras, is rejected, because vijnAna is taken up here ~~knowledge is actually had from them.~~ 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatrānuvādasaṁdēhajñānānutpattilakṣaṇam ॥  
nirastamapramāṇatvaṁ vijñānagrahaṇādiha ।  
</details>

##### ādi
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vaktr-āśaya-vaśa-prāpta-  
mithyā-śaṁkā'panuttayē ॥  
**ādi**-śabdēna tantrāṇām  
āptōktatvaṁ vivakṣitam । +++(5)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In order to remove the suspicion of untruth occasioned by the speaker's character, the word ādi is used to convey the intended meaning that the Tantras are in fact spoken by a trustworthy person. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The term ādi is from Brahmasūtra II. ii. 41- 'vijñānādi-bhāvē vā tad-apratiṣēdhaḥ ।' ādi-śabdēna dōṣa-rāhityam, vijñāna-śabdēna guṇa-sāhityaṁ cābhiprētam । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vaktrāśayavaśaprāptamithyāśaṁkā'panuttayē ॥  
ādiśabdēna tantrāṇāmāptōktatvaṁ vivakṣitam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā hi -  

yas sākṣāt **kurutē** sadā sahajayā buddhyā samastaṁ jagad  
yaḥ puṁsām abhivāñchitāni **diśati** dhyānaika-saṁtarpitaḥ ॥  
**nityāvāpta**-samasta-kāma iti yaṁ **prāhus** trayī-pāragāḥ ।  
tasmin **vibhrama-vipralambhana**-mukhā dōṣā bhavēyuḥ **katham** ॥ +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Consequently the meaning is this: He always has direct knowledge of the entire world by virtue of the omniscience which is part of His nature; He bestows man's wishes upon him, when He is satisfied—and he is satisfied by meditation alone; Him the experts in the Veda describe as eternally satisfied in all His desires: how then can there be defects in Him like error, deceit etc.?
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>
