Cf. The following verse, which, according to tradition, forms the opening verse of Nāthamuni's Nyāyatattva- 

> yō vētti yugapat sarvaṁ  
pratyakṣēṇa sadā svataḥ ।  
taṁ praṇamya hariṁ śāstraṁ  
nyāya-tattvaṁ pracakṣmahē ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi -  
yassākṣāt kurutē sadā sahajayā buddhyā samastaṁ jagat ।  
yaḥ puṁsāmabhivāñchitāni diśati dhyānaikasaṁtarpitaḥ ॥  
nityāvāptasamastakāma iti yaṁ prāhustrayīpāragāḥ ।  
tasmin vibhramavipralambhanamukhā dōṣā bhavēyuḥ katham ॥  
</details>

##### vipratiṣēdhāt
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

utpatty-asambhavō yaś ca  
pūrva-sūtra-dvayōditaḥ ।  
saṁkarṣaṇādi-mūrtīnāṁ  
tatra pratividhīyatē +++(vakṣyamāṇa śāstrēṇa)+++॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

104\. The 'impossibility of origination,' which has been stated in the first two Sūtras, is thereupon denied for Saṅkarṣaṇa and the other forms of God in the sūtra vipratiṣedhāt. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

pūrvaṁ jīva-mana-ādīnām utpattir na sambhavatīty asya pūrva-pakṣasya samādhānam uktam । idānīṁ 'utpatty-asambhava' ity-ādinā 'mūrti-bhēdō 'pi katham ?' iti śaṅkāyāḥ samādhānam ucyatē । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

utpattyasambhavō yaśca pūrvasūtradvayōditaḥ ।  
saṁkarṣaṇādimūrtīnāṁ tatra pratividhīyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"vipratiṣēdhāt" iti pañca-rātra-smaraṇānumita-bhagavat-pratyakṣa-vipratiṣēdhāt tad-anumita-śruti-vipratiṣēdhād vēti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This means either; "Because there is conflict with the Bhagavān's perception which is inferred through Pañcaratra;" or "Because there is conflict with Śruti which is inferred from the same Tradition."

[[87]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Brahmasūtra II.ii. 42. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vipratiṣēdhāt iti pañcarātrasmaraṇānumitabhagavatpratyakṣavipratiṣēdhāt tadanumitaśrutivipratiṣēdhādvēti ।  
</details>

### viruddha-pramity-utpatty-arthēna 
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad vā sūtrāṇāṁ nyāya-pradarśana-paratvāt  
pañca-rātra-śrutyōr a-santam api virōdhaṁ kr̥tvā  
'tra cityantē । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

105\. Or there is another interpretation: since the Sūtras intend to illustrate the rules of exegesis, the author first assumes that there is a conflict between Śruti and Pañcaratra, though in fact there is no such conflict, and then reasons this out as follows: 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadvā sūtrāṇāṁ nyāyapradarśanaparatvāt pañcarātraśrutyōrasantamapi virōdhaṁ kr̥tvā'tra cityantē ।  
</details>

#### pūrva-pakṣaḥ 
##### utpatty-asambhavāt pāñcarātrāprāmāṇyam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā - 

sati vēdāviruddhatvē  
kin nu manv-ādi-vākyavat ।  
a-pramāṇam idaṁ śāstraṁ  
pramāṇaṁ vēti saṁśayē …॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

suppose that Pañcaratra is in conflict with the veda, is this śāstra then, like the statements of Manu etc., valid or invalid? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā - 

sati vēdāviruddhatvē kinnu manvādivākyavat ।  
apramāṇamidaṁ śāstraṁ pramāṇaṁ vēti saṁśayē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

apramāṇaṁ +++(vēda-)+++viruddhārtha-  
pramity--utpatty-a-sambhavāt ।  
+++(pūrvōkta-)+++a-sambhavaś ca +++(smr̥ty-antaravat)+++ sāpēkṣa-  
+++(vēdavat→)+++nirapēkṣatva-hētukaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This question is thereupon answered: "It is invalid, because of the impossibility of the origination of valid knowledge concerning a conflicting sense;  
and this impossibility itself is proved on the ground that there is independence of something that is dependent." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

apramāṇaṁ viruddhārthapramityutpatty-asambhavāt ।  
asambhavaśca sāpēkṣanirapēkṣatvahētukaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yāvad dhi  
sāpēkṣaṁ pañca-rātra-smaraṇaṁ  
na mūla-pramāṇōpasthāpana-mukhēna svārthaṁ pramātum upakramatē  

tāvan nirapēkṣāpauruṣēyāgama-bhuvā pratyayēna  
tad-arthasyānyathā paricchēdāt  

tad-viruddhāyāḥ pramitēr "utpatty-asambhavāt" ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Thus the sūtra utpattyasaṃbhavāt means: 

"because it is impossible that a valid knowledge originates,  
since, as long as the dependent Pañcaratra Tradition does not start proving the validity of its own sense by establishing the validity of its basis,  

the cognition which originates from the independent preterpersonal scripture  
determines the Tradition's sense as being different,  
and consequently conflicting with itself.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

For a discussion on the validity of smṛtis when they are in opposition to more powerful means of knowledge, see Tantravārtika under I. iii. 3, pp. 82-103.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yāvaddhi sāpēkṣaṁ pañcarātrasmaraṇaṁ  
na mūlapramāṇōpasthāpanamukhēna svārthaṁ pramātumupakramatē tāvannirapēkṣāpauruṣēyāgamabhuvā pratyayēna tadarthasyānyathā paricchēdāttadviruddhāyāḥ pramitērutpatty-asambhavāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tāvaddhi pañcarātrasya  
mūla-śruty-avabōdhanam ।  
pratyakṣa-śāstra-śastrēṇa  
yāvan mūlaṁ na lūyatē ॥ +++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For Pāñcarātra conveys that scripture is its basis only as long as the sword of direct scripture does not cut its root.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. ibid. p. 87- 

> tāvadeva sphurantyarthāḥ purastādānumānikāḥ।  
yāvat pratyakṣaśāstreṇa mūlameṣāṁ na kṛtyate॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tāvaddhi pañcarātrasya mūlaśrutyavabōdhanam ।  
pratyakṣaśāstraśastrēṇa yāvanmūlaṁ na lūyatē ॥
</details>

##### na ca kartuḥ karaṇaṁ vēdaḥ

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu kathaṁ vēdā vā nirapēkṣā?  
yāvatā tēṣām api bhagavad-anubhava-sāpēkṣam ēva pramāṇatvaṁ -  
+++(bhagavataḥ)+++ tat+++(=vēda)+++-kāraṇatvāt। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> 106\. OBJECTION. But why should the Vedas themselves be independent, since their validity, too, depends on the direct cognition of the Bhagavān, because this cognition is their cause?221 

221: cf. supra § 18\.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This is the contention of the Naiyāyika. He does not accept the “apauruṣeyatva” of the Vedas. They, according to him, are dependent upon the Supreme Being, like the Pāñcarātrāgamas, for their validity, so much so they too are “pauruṣeya”, i.e., composed by the Divine Person. This is the point on which Yāmuna differs from the Naiyāyika. The aphorism “na ca kartuḥ karaṇam” (Brahmasūtra II. ii. 40) is ingeniously interpreted by Yāmuna to refute the above concept of the Logician, and to establish the “apauruṣeyatva” or the revealed character of the Vedas.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu kathaṁ vēdā vā nirapēkṣā?  
yāvatā tēṣāmapi bhagavadanubhavasāpēkṣamēva pramāṇatvaṁ tatkāraṇatvāt। 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yathaiva hi pañca-rātra-smr̥tayaḥ tad-anubhava-sāpēkṣāḥ,  
ēvaṁ vēdā api 

iti 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Just as the Pāñcarātra Traditions are dependent on His cognition, so are the Vedas too dependent on His cognition.222

[222]: cf. supra § 18.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathaiva hi pañcarātrasmr̥tayaḥ tadanubhavasāpēkṣāḥ ēvaṁ vēdā apīti 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatrōcyatē -  

> na ca kartuḥ karaṇaṁ - 

na kartur īśvarasya karaṇaṁ vēdāḥ।  
kriyanta iti karaṇam,  
karmaṇi lyuṭ,  
apauruṣēyā vēdā iti yāvat ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. To refute this view, the statement is made: 

> na ca kartuḥ karaṇam:  

> The Vedas are not the product of a maker, i.e. the Bhagavān. 

Karaṇa here in the sense of "things that are made or produced",  
by the rule "suffix lyuṭ" in the sense of the object of the action.223  
This then means that the Vedas are preterhuman.

[223]: karmaṇi lyuṭ Pāṇini.

[[88]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

na ca ... Brahmasūtra, II. ii. 40.

karaṇaṁ ... ‘karaṇaṁ’ = ‘kriyamāṇaṁ’ = ‘kāryam’ ity arthaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatrōcyatē na ca kartuḥ karaṇaṁ na karturīśvarasya karaṇaṁ vēdāḥ kriyanta iti karaṇam,  karmaṇi lyuṭ, apauruṣēyā vēdā iti yāvat ।  
</details>

#### uttarapakṣaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vijñānādibhāvē vā tadapratiṣēdhaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

107\. Vijñānādibhāve vā tadapratiṣedhaḥ. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Brahmasūtra, II. ii. 41.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vijñānādibhāvē vā tadapratiṣēdhaḥ
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na caitad asti pañcarātraśāstram apramāṇamiti। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

~~If, on the other hand,~~ it is not true that the Pāñcarātra Śāstra is invalid, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na caitad asti pañcarātraśāstram apramāṇamiti। 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kim tarhi? tad-apratiṣēdhaḥ। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

then what? tadapratiṣedhaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kim tarhi? tad-apratiṣēdhaḥ। 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pramityutpattēr apratiṣēdhaḥ।  
viruddhārtham api vikalpēna pramāṇam ityarthaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

i e. non-rejection of the origination of valid knowledge (namely, even when partly conflicting, the conflicting statement may be valid optionally), 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pramityutpattēr apratiṣēdhaḥ।  
viruddhārtham api vikalpēna pramāṇam ityarthaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

asambhavad--bhrama-vipralambha-- bhagavad-anubhavamūlatvāt, "vijñānādi-bhāvē"।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

because it is based upon the direct cognition of the Bhagavān in whom error and deceit are impossible as He is a source of vijñāna (vijñānādibhāve): 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

asambhavadbhramavipralambhabhagavadanubhavamūlatvāt, vijñānādibhāvē।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vijñānaṁ viśiṣṭaṁ jñānam - asambhavatskhalanam iti yāvat, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Vijñāna means "knowledge par excellence in which no mistake is possible. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vijñānaṁ viśiṣṭaṁ jñānam asambhavatskhalanam iti yāvat, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

anyēṣāṁ hi sarvadharmaśāstra-nibandhanāṁ  
sāṁsārikattvēnāsārvajñyāt  
anavāptan-akāmatvāc ca  
sambhāvyamāna-vividha-viplavaṁ jñānam, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For since all other authors of Dharmaśāstras are not omniscient, as they are involved in saṃsāra, and since therefore they are also not entirely self-sufficient,  
various lapses are conceivable in their knowledge. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anyēṣāṁ hi sarvadharmaśāstra-nibandhanāṁ sāṁsārikattvēnāsārvajñyāt anavāptakāmatvāc ca sambhāvyamānavividhaviplavaṁ jñānam, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

bhagavatas tu svābhāvika-niraṅkuśaiśvaryasya  
śruti-śata-samadhigatāvitatha- sahaja-samasta-dharmādharmādi-sākṣāt-kāram jñānam  
iti vijñānam ityuktam, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Whereas in the case of the Bhagavān, whose supremacy is natural and unlimited, His knowledge is the immediate insight in all dharma and adharma, which is natural to Him and true, as is known from hundreds of śrutis; it is this knowledge which in the sūtra is described as vijñāna, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Pādma Saṁhitā, Jñānapāda, II. 5b:

> vijñānaṁ bhagavaj-jñānaṁ taj-jñānān muktir ucyatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

bhagavataḥ tu svābhāvikaniraṅkuśaiśvaryasya śrutiśatasamadhigatāvitathasahajasamastadharmādharmādisākṣātkāram jñānam iti vijñānam ityuktam, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tādr̥śasya tasya  
ādibhāvē mūlatvē sati  
tad-apratiṣēdhaḥ pramāṇam ēva iti । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

When such knowledge is the 'beginning,' i.e. the basis, there is non-rejection, sc. the śāstra is valid.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘tad-apratiṣēdhaḥ’ prāmāṇyasyāpratiṣēdhaḥ, prāmāṇyam iti yāvat।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tādr̥śasya tasya ādibhāvē mūlatvē sati tad apratiṣēdhaḥ pramāṇam ēva iti । 
</details>

<details><summary>rāma-miśraḥ</summary>

asmin arthē vijñānasya ādibhāvō vijñānādibhāva iti ṣaṣṭhītatpuruṣaḥ jñēyaḥ
</details>

## 13 vēda-tulya-prāmāṇyam

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu kathaṁ śruti-viruddhasya tantrasya prāmāṇyābhyupagamaḥ?  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

108\. OBJECTION. But how can it be assumed that the Tantra,  
which conflicts with scripture, has validity? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu kathaṁ śrutiviruddhasya tantrasya prāmāṇyābhyupagamaḥ?  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatprāmāṇyē hi śrutyā saha vikalpaḥ prāpnōti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For if it is valid,  
it becomes optional beside 89 scripture;  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatprāmāṇyē hi śrutyā saha vikalpaḥ prāpnōti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> +++(pāñcarātrēṇa)+++ vikalpaś ca aṣṭa-dōṣa-duṣṭaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and optionality is deficient in the case of the Tantras by eight defects. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide Tantravārtika, pp. 89-90.
Cf. Tantraśuddha, pp. 11-12:

> “vrīhibhir yajēta”, “yavair yajēta” ity ubhayam api vākyaṁ pramāṇam । tatra vrīhi-vākyāśrayaṇē yava-vākyam anāśrayaṇīyaṁ bhavati । aśyakyatvāt yugapat ubhayānuṣṭhānasya । tatra prāptaṁ yava-vākya-gataṁ prāmāṇyaṁ vinā kāraṇēnāpahnutavyam; aprāmāṇyasya pramāṇatvaṁ ṣaṣṭha-gōcara-kalpam abhāva-pramāṇāvasēyam aṅgīkartavyam; ēvam api kēnāpi hētunā prayōga-sādhanatvēna yavābhyupagamē pūrvam apāśrayya[[??]] prāmāṇyasya punar āśrayaṇīyatvam; tan-nirāsēnāṅgīkr̥tasya aprāmāṇyasya punaḥ parityāga iti catvārō dōṣā ēkasmin vākyē prasajyantē । dvitīyē 'pi prāpta-parityāgō 'prāptāśrayaṇaṁ parityaktōpādānaṁ yat ānītasya parityāga iti catvārō dōṣāḥ । tathā 'pi tulya-balatvāt gaty-antarābhāvāc ca vrīhi-yavayōr vikalpa āśritaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vikalpaśca aṣṭadōṣaduṣṭaḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> sa ca kvacid anyatara-parityāga-kāraṇābhāvād **agatyā 'bhyanujñāyatē**,  
yathā "vrīhibhir yajēta yavair yajēta" iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Option is assumed  
when there is no invariable rule that something should be such and not otherwise,  
because there is no reason to reject, in one case or another, an alternative statement;  
for instance: "He must sacrifice with rice,"  
beside "he must sacrifice with barley." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘kvacit’ = vēda-vākyē

vrīhibhiryajēta ... Āpastamba Śrautasūtra, VI. 3.1.13.

yavairyajēta ... To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sa ca kvacidanyataraparityāgakāraṇābhāvādagatyā'bhyanujñāyatē, yathā vrīhibhiryajēta yavairyajēta iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na hi tatrānyatarad apahartuṁ śakyam -  
ubhayōr apy an-apēkṣatvāviśiṣṭatvāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the latter case it is impossible to eliminate one or the other  
because both ~~neither~~ of these statements is characterized by independence. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

anapēkṣatvāviśiṣṭatvāt = apauruṣēyatvāt ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi tatrānyataradapahartuṁ śakyam ubhayōrapyanapēkṣatvāviśiṣṭatvāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> **na** caivam api pañca-rātra-śrutyōr **vikalpēna bhavitavyam** atulyatvāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the former case, however, there can be no such option between scripture and Pafcarātra,  
because the two are not equal; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na caivamapi pañcarātraśrutyōrvikalpēna bhavitavyam atulyatvāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nirapēkṣaṁ hi vaidikaṁ vacanaṁ - apauruṣēyatvāt,  
sāpēkṣaṁ ca pañca-rātra-vacanam iti।  
katham anayōr vikalpaḥ?  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for the Vedic statement is independent, because it is preterhuman,  
whereas the Pañcaratra statement is dependent.  
So how can they be alternatives and optional? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nirapēkṣaṁ hi vaidikaṁ vacanaṁ - apauruṣēyatvāt,  
sāpēkṣaṁ ca pañcarātravacanamiti।  
kathamanayōrvikalpaḥ ।  
</details>

### itara-nirapēkṣatā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

śrūyatāṁ - pañca-rātra-śāstrasyāpi nirapēkṣatvād ēva +++(vikalpatvam)+++।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

109\. REFUTATION. Listen: because Pañcarātra too is independent.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘nirapēkṣatvāt’, vacanāntara-mūlāntara-nirapēkṣatvāt ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

śrūyatāṁ pañcarātraśāstrasyāpi nirapēkṣatvādēva ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> kathannu pauruṣēyasya  
> vacasō nirapēkṣatā ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

OBJECTION. How can a statement deriving from a person be independent? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kathannu pauruṣēyasya vacasō nirapēkṣatā ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

iti cēd idam **ācaṣṭāṁ**  
**pr̥ṣṭas** sann ēṣa tārkikaḥ ॥  
kim asya bōdhakatvāya  
parāpēkṣā **'bhyupēyatē** ।  
kiṁ vā niścāyakattvāya  
yathā'rtha-jñāpanāya vā ॥  
pum-arthatvāya vā tatra  
caturṇām apy asambhavaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION.  
Let us ask the logician to explain this-  
must dependence on something else  
be assumed for a statement to be informative,  
to give positive certainty,  
or to state the truth about its content,  
or to serve a purpose of human importance?  
All four are impossible. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

iti cēdidamācaṣṭāṁ pr̥ṣṭassannēṣa tārkikaḥ ॥  
kimasya bōdhakatvāya parāpēkṣā'bhyupēyatē ।  
kiṁ vā niścāyakattvāya yathārthajñāpanāya vā ॥  
pumarthatvāya vā tatra caturṇāmapyasambhavaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na khalu "cakravarty-upacārēṇa bhagavantaṁ samarcayēd"  
itīdaṁ vacanaṁ śrūyamāṇaṁ  
bōdhakatvāya kiñcid apēkṣatē,  
anyatra vyutpatti-grahaṇāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

When the statement is heard,  
"One must worship the Bhagavan with the attendance due an emperor," (not identified)  
nothing else is required for this statement to be informative,  
because the meaning of the words has already become known from other contexts. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

cakravartyupacārēṇa ... To be identified.

vyutpatti-grahaṇaṁ vinā anyat kim api nāpēkṣata iti bhāvaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na khalu cakravartyupacārēṇa bhagavantaṁ samarcayēditīdaṁ vacanaṁ śrūyamāṇaṁ bōdhakatvāya kiñcidapēkṣatē anyatra vyutpattigrahaṇāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca tāvatā sāpēkṣatvēna daurbalyaṁ -  
śrutāv api daurbalya-prasaṅgāt ।+++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor does this small measure of dependence prove the weakness of the statement's [[90]] validity, for the same weakness would follow for śruthi too.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

in order to understand any statement, one must first know the meaning of the words that compose it;  
this may be called dependence,  
so that to this extent any statement is dependent for its informativeness on other and prior knowledge;  
but this must also apply to Vedic statements. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca tāvatā sāpēkṣatvēna daurbalyaṁ śrutāvapi daurbalyaprasaṅgāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi niścaya-jananāya,  
na hi "arcayēd" ity ētat "arcayēn na vē"ti saṁśayitaṁ pratyayam utpādayati -  
vyutpatti-pratipatti-vyākōpa-prasaṅgāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is anything else required for the statement to give positive certainty;  
for the statement "One must worship...." does not occasion doubt  
whether one must or must not worship,  
since that would entail a negation of the direct declaration of the real sense.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi niścayajananāya,  
na hi arcayēdityētat arcayēnna vēti saṁśayitaṁ pratyayamutpādayati vyutpattipratipattivyākōpaprasaṅgāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi yathārthatvāya,  
**na** hy **utpannaṁ** jñānaṁ  
sva-kāraṇa-vyatirēkēṇa yathārthatvāya aparam **apēkṣatē** -  
+++(vēda-vākya-)+++guṇataḥ prāmāṇyasyāyuktatvāt, +++(guṇatva-)+++anabhyupagamāc ca ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is anything required for the statement to be true to the facts,  
for the knowledge produced by the statement does not require anything outside its own cause226 to be true to the facts,  
because secondary validity is inappropriate and not admitted.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

If the cause (here: God) is above suspicion, the statement will be accurate.

gunataḥ prāmāṇyasyājuktateūd anabhjupagamãe; my understanding is that a statement has its validity by itself,  
and no secondary validity in the sense that its content must first be validated by some other means.  
The validity itself must be proved (namely by the character of the personal author or by its preterpersonal origin), but once proved, the statement itself is valid.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi yathārthatvāya, na hyutpannaṁ jñānaṁ svakāraṇavyatirēkēṇa yathārthatvāya aparamapēkṣatē guṇataḥ prāmāṇyasyāyuktatvāt anabhyupagamācca ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca puruṣārthatvāya parāpēkṣā -  
śāstra-śarīra-paryālōcanād ēva tat-siddhēḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is it necessary for the statement to be dependent on something else  
in order to serve a purpose of human importance,  
for the proof of this purpose follows from a consideration of the entire body of doctrine. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca puruṣārthatvāya parāpēkṣā śāstraśarīraparyālōcanādēva tatsiddhēḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

iha hi yathōkta-saṁskāravatāṁ śāstra-śravaṇāt tad-artha-jñānaṁ,  
tatas tad-arthaṁ pāñcakālikānuṣṭhānam,  
tatō niratiśaya-saṁpat-prāptir  
iti śāstrād ēvāvagamyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In this case, those who have undergone the afore-mentioned sacraments have knowledge of the content of the statement  
when they have heard the doctrine,  
and hence they perform the "five-timesa-day" rites ([228]: Vaisnava rite observed five times a day: pañcakálika.), which form this content,  
and hence they attain to supreme perfection;  
this is learnt solely from the Sastra itself.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Ahirbudhnya Saṁhitā ch. XV:

> pāñcakālikam acchidraṁ kurvāṇaḥ śata-vārṣikam॥ [15b]  
kṣētra-jñaṁ sarva-bhūtānāṁ vāsudēvaṁ viśanti tē॥ [17b]  
pañca-kāla-ratō nityaṁ dayā-kṣānti-dhr̥ti-sthitiḥ॥ [49b]  
prāpta-vēdānta-vijñānō vaiṣṇavaṁ śrayatē padam॥ [53b]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

iha hi yathōktasaṁskāravatāṁ śāstraśravaṇāt tadarthajñānaṁ tatastadarthaṁpāñcakālikānuṣṭhānam,  tatō niratiśayasaṁpatprāptiriti śāstrādēvāvagamyatē ।  
</details>

#### āpti-niścayō nāpēkṣitaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

athōcyēta 

> saty api pañca-rātra-tantrāṇāṁ svataḥ-prāmāṇyē  
> yāvat tad-vaktur āpti-niścaya-purassaraṁ dōṣābhāvō nāvadhāryatē  
> na tāvat prāmāṇyaṁ niṣpādyata 

iti 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

110\. Or if the objection is raised that,  
granted the self-validity of Pañcaratra,  
this validity is not complete  
as long as it has not been made certain  
that there are no defects,  
after it has been made certain that the speaker is reliable,-  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

athōcyēta satyapi pañcarātratantrāṇāṁ svataḥprāmāṇyē yāvattadvakturāptiniścayapurassaraṁ dōṣābhāvō nāvadhāryatē na tāvatprāmāṇyaṁ niṣpādyata iti 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad asat,  
**na** hi dōṣābhāva-jñānaṁ prāmāṇyaṁ **niṣpādayati**  
nirdōṣa-jñāna-kāraṇād ēva tad-utpattēḥ । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

I reply that this view is not correct;  
knowledge that there are no defects does not completely establish validity,  
since the validity arises from the cause itself of defectless knowledge  
and not from the defectlessness of this knowledge.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadasat, na hi dōṣābhāvajñānaṁ prāmāṇyaṁ niṣpādayati nirdōṣajñānakāraṇādēva tadutpattēḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca nirdōṣatvāyāptatvādi-guṇa-niścayaḥ -  
sattā-mātrēṇa tat-siddhēḥ,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[91]] 111\. Nor is positive certainty about such of the speaker's qualities as his reliability  
required for his statement to be defectless,  
because the statement's defectlessness is proved solely by its being defectless.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca nirdōṣatvāyāptatvādiguṇaniścayaḥ sattāmātrēṇa tatsiddhēḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathāha vārtikakāraḥ -  

> tadā **na vyāpriyantē** tu  
+++(aduṣṭatāyā)+++ jñāyamānatayā +++(vaktr̥-)+++guṇāḥ ।  

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As the Author of the Varttika declares, 

> "Then the qualities (of the speaker) do not exert any influence (on the validity of his statement)  
because (its defectlessness) is already known."229 

[229]: ślokavārttika, 2.6 7 ab.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ślokavārtika under I.i.2, śl. 67a.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathāha vārtikakāraḥ -  

> tadā na vyāpriyantē tu  
jñāyamānatayā guṇāḥ ।  

iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

dōṣābhāva-jñānē'pi  
guṇānāṁ sattayōpayōgō darśitaḥ,  

> dōṣābhāvē tu vijñēyē  
sattāmātrōpakāriṇaḥ ।  

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The same Author also shows that,  
even when there is certainty about its defectlessness,  
the existence of qualities (like reliability in the speaker) is helpful:  

> "When defectlessness is known,  
they are helpful by merely existing." 

[230]: ib. 2.67 cd.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ibid. 67b.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

dōṣābhāvajñānē'pi guṇānāṁ sattayōpayōgō darśitaḥ, dōṣābhāvē tu vijñēyē sattāmātrōpakāriṇaḥ ।  
iti, 
</details>

##### hānōpādānādi
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na cōtpannam api pramāṇaṁ  
hānōpādānādi-vyavahārāyāparamam apēkṣatē  -  
smaraṇābhilāṣābhyām ēva tatsiddhēḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor does the validity, when it has been established  
require something else in order that  
consequent actions of acceptance, rejection etc. proceed,  
because action proceeds on the basis of recollection and desire. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cōtpannamapi pramāṇaṁ hānōpādānādivyavahārāyāparamamapēkṣatē smaraṇābhilāṣābhyāmēva tatsiddhēḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathāhuḥ 

> smaraṇād abhilāṣāc ca  
vyavahāraḥ pravartatē 

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As they say, 

> "Action proceeds on the basis of recollection and desire." 

[231]: not identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathāhuḥ smaraṇādabhilāṣācca vyavahāraḥ pravartatē iti ।  
</details>

#### (a)kartr̥vattā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca  

> svataḥ-prāpta-prāmāṇyānāṁ vēdānām api  
yāvat kartr̥-bhāva--niścaya--puras-saraṁ dōṣābhāvō nāvadhāryatē  
na tāvat prāmāṇyaṁ pratiṣṭhiti

iti samānaṁ sāpēkṣatvam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Moreover, in the case of the self-valid Vedas, too,  
we find this same dependence in that their validity would not be completely established  
as long as there were no certainty of their defectlessness  
after the certainty about the non-existence of their author.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca svataḥprāptaprāmāṇyānāṁ vēdānāmapi yāvatkartr̥bhāvaniścayapurassaraṁ dōṣābhāvō nāvadhāryatē na tāvatprāmāṇyaṁ pratiṣṭhitīti samānaṁ sāpēkṣatvam ।  
</details>

##### īśvarakr̥tatayā dōṣābhāvaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha

> yōgyānupalambhād ēvānāyāsa-siddhē vaktr-abhāvē  
+++(tad-abhāvāt)+++ nirāśraya+++(←vaktr̥)+++-dōṣāṇām a-sambhavād  
a-prāmāṇya-śaṅkaiva vēdē nāsti 

iti cēt 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> 112\. OBJECTION. But when the non-existence of their author is proved without effort  
by the non-apprehension of what ought to be there,  
the question of the non-validity does not arise for the Veda, for defects are impossible without something or someone in which they could reside.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha yōgyānupalambhādēvānāyāsasiddhē vaktrabhāvē nirāśrayadōṣāṇāmasambhavādaprāmāṇyaśaṅkaiva vēdē nāsti iti cēt 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yathāhuḥ ।  
>
> > +++(vaktr-abhāvē)+++ tatrāpavāda-nirmuktir +++(prāmāṇyē)+++  
vaktr̥-bhāvāl laghīyasī ।  
vēdē tēnāpramāṇatvaṁ  
**na śaṅkām adhigacchati** ॥

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As they say: 

> "In that case (the Veda) the absence of non-validity follows quite naturally from the absence of an author;  
therefore its validity cannot be questioned."\*\*" 

[[92]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ślokavārtika under I.i.2, śl. 68.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> yathāhuḥ ।  
tatrāpavādanirmuktirvaktr̥bhāvāllaghīyasī ।  
vēdē tēnāpramāṇatvaṁ na śaṅkāmadhigacchati ॥

iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

hanta tarhi pañca-rātra-tantrē'pi  
sarva-jña--sarvēśvara-vaktr̥-bhāvād ēva  
a-yatna-siddhē dōṣābhāvē  
aprāmāṇya-śaṅkā nāvataratīti samānaś carcaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. Why, in the case of Pañcarátra too no question can arise about its validity, since the absence of defects is easily proved by the fact that the omniscient and omnipotent God is its speaker; so the argument is the same.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The similarity of status between the Vedas and the Āgamas, according to Yāmuna, lies in the fact that both of them are understood to be free from the defects that generally stand in their way. The way in which this ‘faultlessness’ is understood, however, differs between the Vedas and the Āgamas. As regards the Vedic texts, there being no author (apauruṣeya), there is no question of any defect ever appearing at all. As regards the Pañcarātrāgamas too, there could be no question of any defect ever arising, on the ground that they are the direct utterances of Vāsudeva, the Omniscient Supreme Lord of the Universe. This is what Yāmuna explains in the succeeding para: “etaduktaṁ bhavati” etc.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

hanta tarhi pañcarātratantrē'pi sarvajñasarvēśvaravaktr̥bhāvādēva ayatnasiddhē dōṣābhāvē aprāmāṇyaśaṅkā nāvataratīti samānaścarcaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ētad uktaṁ bhavati -  

> ubhayōr api svataḥprāmāṇyayōr ēkatra dōṣābhāvaniścayaḥ  
tad-āśraya-puruṣābhāva-niścayāt,  
anyatra tad-viruddha-guṇa-vaktr̥katva niścayād 

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In other words, in both cases of self-validity there is positive certainty that there are no defects; in the case of the Veda because there is positive certainty that no person is involved who could possess these defects; in the case of Pañcarātra because there is positive certainty that its speaker possesses virtues which preclude defects. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ētaduktaṁ bhavati ubhayōrapi svataḥprāmāṇyayōrēkatra dōṣābhāvaniścayaḥ tadāśrayapuruṣābhāvaniścayāt, anyatra tadviruddhaguṇavaktr̥katva niścayāditi ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā 

> auṣṇyābhāva-niścayō nabhasi  
tad-ādhārābhāva-niścayāj,  
jalē tu tad-viruddha-śaityōpalambhād 

iti । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It is here as in the following two cases of absence of heat: there is no heat in ether because it is certain that there is no locus for heat in ether; nor is there heat in cold water because there is coldness which precludes heat.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā auṣṇyābhāvaniścayō nabhasi tadādhārābhāvaniścayājjalē tu tadviruddhaśaityōpalambhāditi ।  
</details>

#### sāpēkṣatā na bādhikā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kiñca -  

sāpēkṣa-nirapēkṣatvē  
na hi bādhasya kāraṇam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

113\. Moreover, neither dependence nor independence is by itself a cause of invalidation.29  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[232] this speaks to 108, that the independent cognition cancels the dependent cognition, if there is conflict between them. Yamuna makes the point that this is not invariably true; that neither dependence nor independence is a cause of invalidation, sapeksanirapeksatve is a dual and requires the correction of karanam into kārane, If my understanding of the text is correct.+++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kiñca ।  
sāpēkṣanirapēkṣatvē na hi bādhasya kāraṇam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

śuktau rajata-bōdhasya  
nirapēkṣasya bādhakam …॥  
"nēdaṁ-rajata"-vijñānaṁ  
tat-sāpēkṣam apīṣyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The independent cognition that some substance is silver  
while in reality it is nacre  
is invalidated by the cognition: "This is not silver:"  
this cognition itself is considered as dependent. 

([233]: namely, because it requires another cognition in order to be denied.)
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

śuktau rajatabōdhasya nirapēkṣasya bādhakam ॥  
nēdaṁ rajatavijñānaṁ tatsāpēkṣamapīṣyatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"sēyaṁ +++(samānā)+++ jvālē"ti saṁvittēs  
taila-varti-vināśa-jā ॥  
anumā bādhikā dr̥ṣṭā  
sāpēkṣā'py - akṣa-janmanaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The cognition "This is that flame," is found to be invalidated  
by the inferential cognition that arises from the disappearance of oil";  
the latter cognition itself is dependent because it arises from a sense-perception. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[234]: namely, in the example of the burning lamp: is it the same flame that burns at six o'clock and at seven o'clock? We don't see the flame change or be succeeded by another flame. Only inference shows that since there is a different amount of oil in the lamp at different times, it is different oil that is burning as a flame, so that the flame is really different. The sense perception is of the varying amounts of oil.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sēyaṁ jvālēti saṁvittēstailavartivināśajā ॥  
anumā bādhikā dr̥ṣṭā sāpēkṣā'pyakṣajanmanaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atō niravakāśēna  
sāvakāśaṁ **niṣidhyatē** +++(na tu nirapēkṣēṇa)+++ ॥  
na cēha sāvakāśatvaṁ  
bhagavac-chāstra-vēdayōḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The simple truth therefore is  
that which is susceptible to invalidation  
is invalidated by that which is not so susceptible;  
in our present case there is no such susceptibility either of Scripture or of Pañcaratra.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atō niravakāśēna sāvakāśaṁ niṣidhyatē ॥  
na cēha sāvakāśatvaṁ bhagavacchāstravēdayōḥ ।  
</details>

### kartā

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha śrutiviruddhasya  
tantrabhāgasya duśśakam ॥  
vāsudēva-praṇītatvaṁ  
niścētum iti manyasē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[93]]  
114\. Or if you think that it is impossible to give positive certainty that the Tantra is promulgated by Vasudeva,  
as it is in conflict with Scripture, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha śrutiviruddhasya tantrabhāgasya duśśakam ॥  
vāsudēvapraṇītatvaṁ niścētumiti manyasē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pañcarātra-viruddhasya  
vēdabhāgasya vā katham ॥  
apauruṣēyatā-jñānam  
āvirbhavati bādhitam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

I ask you :  
Why then does the knowledge arise that Scripture is preterpersonal,  
while it is invalidated because it conflicts with Pañcaratra? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pañcarātraviruddhasya vēdabhāgasya vā katham ॥  
apauruṣēyatājñānamāvirbhavati bādhitam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tasyāpi vēda-bhāgatvāt  
tathābhāvō'bhyupēyatē ॥  
asyāpi pañcarātratvāt  
tat-praṇītatvam iṣyatām ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

They accept it that the Veda is preterpersonal just because it is Veda; but then one can equally claim that Pañcaratra is promulgated by Vasudeva just because it is Pañcaratra. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tasyāpi vēdabhāgatvāt tathābhāvō'bhyupēyatē ॥  
asyāpi pañcarātratvāt tatpraṇītatvamiṣyatām ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kartur asmaraṇāt tatra  
yadi cāpauruṣēyatā ॥  
tat-kartr̥katva-smr̥tyā'tra  
kin na syāt tat-praṇītatā ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If the preterpersonal origin of the Veda is proved by the fact that there is no recollection of an author, then why not agree that Pañcaratra is promulgated by Vasudeva just because there is recollection of his authorship? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

karturasmaraṇāttatra yadi cāpauruṣēyatā ॥  
tatkartr̥katvasmr̥tyā'tra kinna syāttatpraṇītatā ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

asti hy ā-strī-kumāraṁ sā  
dr̥ḍhā smr̥ti-paramparā ॥  
pañcarātrasya nirmātā  
kēśavō bhagavān iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For there exists a strong transmission of the recollection, extending to women and children, that Kesava is the author of the Pancarãtra. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

asti hyāstrīkumāraṁ sā dr̥ḍhā smr̥tiparamparā ॥  
pañcarātrasya nirmātā kēśavō bhagavāniti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatpraṇītatvaviśvāsād  
gajānaśvān dhanaṁ bahu ॥  
dakṣiṇāṁ vividhāṁ dattvā  
pratiṣṭhādīni kurvatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

So great a faith do people have in His authorship that they erect monuments according to the precepts of Pañcarātra, donating elephants, horses and great wealth in various fees, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

For pratiṣṭhā-rite, see Sāttvatasaṁhitā Ch. XXV and Jayākhyasaṁhitā, paṭala 16.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatpraṇītatvaviśvāsād gajānaśvān dhanaṁ bahu ॥  
dakṣiṇāṁ vividhāṁ dattvā pratiṣṭhādīni kurvatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sāṅkhyasya kapilō vaktā  
pañcarātrasya kēśavaḥ ॥  
iti skandapurāṇē'pi  
paṭhyatē bhāratē tathā ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the Skanda Purana it is said that "Kapila is the promulgator of Samkhya, Kesava of Pañcaratra." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

sāṅkhyasya ... To be identified. See Tantraśuddha, p.22, for the second half of this verse:

> vaktā pañca-padārthānāṁ sākṣāt dēvō mahēśvaraḥ॥

Cf. Mahābhārata, XII. 337.60a:

> sāṅkhyasya vaktā kapilaḥ paramarṣis sa ucyatē ।

bhāratē ...  

> The Nārāyaṇīya section of the Mahābhārata ( XII. chs. 334-348 ) is valuable as it is the only fairly full account of the Pāñcarātra doctrines that we possess in original Sanskrit....All the bhakti-writers from Rāmānuja down to the present day, assume the reader's familiarity with the principles inculcated therein. 

[ See G. A. Grierson, “The Nārāyaṇīya and the Bhāgavatas”, The Indian Antiquary, vol. 37, pp. 261-62. ]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sāṅkhyasya kapilō vaktā  
pañcarātrasya kēśavaḥ ॥  
iti skandapurāṇē'pi  
paṭhyatē bhāratē tathā ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> pañcarātrasya kr̥tsnasya  
vaktā nārāyaṇaḥ svayam ॥  
idaṁ mahōpaniṣadaṁ  
catur-vēda-samanvitam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise in the Mahabharata: 

> "Narayana Himself is the promulgator of the entire Pañcaratra.  
This great Upanisada, consistent with the four Vedas,  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

pañcarātrasya ... Mahābhārata, XII. 337. 63a. Variant: vaktā tu bhagavān svayam। Also cf. ibid. śl. 63b-64a:

> sarvēṣu ca nr̥pa-śrēṣṭha jñānēṣv ētēṣu dr̥śyatē ।॥  
yathāgamaṁ yathā jñānaṁ niṣṭhā nārāyaṇaḥ prabhuḥ ।

Quoting the line ‘pañca-rātrasya kr̥tsnasya’ etc. in his Śrībhāṣya II. ii. 42 (p. 834), Rāmānuja says:

> pañca-rātrasya kr̥tsnasya vaktā nārāyaṇaḥ svayam ity uktavān । ēvaṁ vadataś cāyam āśayaḥ। pauruṣēyāṇāṁ hi tantrāṇāṁ paraspara-viruddha-vastu-vāditayā, apauruṣēyatvēna nirasta-pramādādi-nikhila-dōṣa-gandha-vēdya-vastu-viruddhābhidhāyitvāc ca, yathāvasthita-vastuni prāmāṇyaṁ durlabham। vēda-vēdyaś ca para-brahma-bhūtō nārāyaṇaḥ। ataḥ tat-tantrābhihita-pradhāna-puruṣa-paśu-pati-prabhr̥ti-tattvasya vēdānta-vēdya-para-brahma-bhūta-nārāyaṇātmakatayaiva vastutvam abhyupagamanīyam iti। ... atō vēdānta-vēdyaḥ para-brahma-bhūtō nārāyaṇaḥ svayam ēva pañca-rātrasya kr̥tsnasya vaktēti, tat--sva-rūpa--tad-upāsanābhidhāyi tat-tantram iti ca tasminn-itara-tantra-sāmānyaṁ na kēnacid udbhāvayituṁ śakyam।

idaṁ ... Mahābhārata, XII. 326, 100-101.

Discussing the position of the Pañcarātra with reference to the Upaniṣads, Dr. D. L. De in his article “Pāñcarātra and the Upaniṣads” [ Indian Historical Quarterly, Vol. IX ], p.648, says:

> The Upaniṣads, with no set theory of philosophy or dogmatic scheme of theology to propound, form the root of all the later religio-philosophic systems of the country.

> It cannot be said definitely whether the Pāñcarātras confined themselves wholly to the contemporary Upaniṣads in the matter of borrowing. They borrowed probably from the contemporary Upaniṣads as well as from the pre-existing Upaniṣads. The Upaniṣads are the sources from which they drew most of their doctrines.

For a detailed account of these borrowings, see ibid., pp.648-660.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pañcarātrasya kr̥tsnasya vaktā nārāyaṇaḥ svayam ॥  
idaṁ mahōpaniṣadaṁ caturvēdasamanvitam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> sāṅkhya-yōga-kr̥tāntēna  
pañca-rātrānuśabditam ॥  
nārāyaṇa-mukhōdgītaṁ  
nāradō'śrāvayan munīn ।  
brahmaṇassadanē tāta!  
yathādr̥ṣṭaṁ yathāśrutam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> as well as with the doctrines of Samkhya and Yoga, called Pañcaratra,  
which was revealed by Nārāyaṇa's tongue,  
has been taught to the sages by Narada  
as he had seen it and heard it in the abode of Brahma."
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

sāṅkhyayōga ... See G.A. Grierson, Indian Antiquary, vol. 37, p. 261:

> Nearly the whole Mokṣadharma-parvan consists lectures on Sāṅkhya-Yoga, together with attempts to reconcile it with Brahmaism. One system which results from the attempted reconciliation of these two opposite philosophies is attributed to Pañcaśikha and is explained at some length ...The Nārāyaṇīya, while claiming to describe Sāṅkhya-Yoga really describes the Bhāgavata monotheism as united with this system, but also with more of a Brahmaist colouring than we find in the Gītā.

pañcarātrānuśabditam ... See ibid., p.258:

> The Nārāyaṇīya sometimes alludes to the religion which it preaches as the doctrine of the Bhāgavatas, and sometimes as that of the Pāñcarātras. The two terms are not exactly synonymous, for the Pāñcarātras formed only one sect of the great Bhāgavata religion. Prof. R.G. Bhandarkar tells us that Dhruvasena I, one of the earliest princes of the Valabhi dynasty (C. 530 A.D.) is called a Bhāgavata, and Bāṇa (C. 600 A.D.) in the 8th chapter of the Harṣacarita mentions both the Bhāgavatas and the Pāñcarātras.

nārāyaṇamukhōdgītaṁ ... According to the Śāntiparvan of the Mahābhārata (Gorakhpur edn.), the Sāttvata-teaching is said to have been announced by the sun:

> sāttvataṁ vidhim āsthāya prāk sūrya-mukha-niḥsr̥tam ।  
pūjayāmāsa dēvēśaṁ tac-chēṣēṇa pitāmahān ॥

See G.A. Grierson, Indian Antiquary, vol. 37, p.253:

> We have no literary evidence as to the train of reasoning by which this doctrine (Bhāgavata) was reached, but to me it appears more than probable that it was a development of the Sun-worship that was the common heritage of both branches of the Aryan people—the Eranian and the Indian. All the legends dealing with the origins of the Bhāgavata religion are connected in some way or other, with the sun.

See also in this connection, L.D. Barnett, “The Hindu Gods and Heroes,” pp. 82-83.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sāṅkhyayōgakr̥tāntēna pañcarātrānuśabditam ॥  
nārāyaṇamukhōdgītaṁ nāradō'śrāvayanmunīn ।  
brahmaṇassadanē tāta! yathādr̥ṣṭaṁ yathāśrutam ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ēvamādipurāṇōktaiḥ  
sahasrair nyāya-br̥ṁhitaiḥ ।  
vāsudēva-praṇītatvaṁ  
pañcarātrasya nirvyatham ॥  
kintu vēdasya nityatvē  
**vivadantē** vipaścitaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

From these and thousands of other statements in the Puranas, which are supported by the rules of interpretation, the conclusion follows naturally that Pañcaratra was indeed composed by Vasudeva Himself. 

On the other hand, some experts dispute that the Veda is eternal! ([[142]] [235]: The Naiyayikas.) [[91]]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvamādipurāṇōktaiḥ sahasrairnyāyabr̥ṁhitaiḥ ।  
vāsudēvapraṇītatvaṁ pañcarātrasya nirvyatham ॥  
kintu vēdasya nityatvē vivadantē vipaścitaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tēna nirdōṣa-vijñāna-  
kāraṇatvād dvayōr api ॥  
nirviśaṅkaṁ pramāṇatvaṁ  
bhagavacchāstravēdayōḥ ।  +++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore, the real ground for the thesis that the validity of the doctrine of the Bhagavan and that of the Veda is above question  
is this that both are causes of defectless knowledge.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tēna nirdōṣavijñānakāraṇatvād dvayōrapi ॥  
nirviśaṅkaṁ pramāṇatvaṁ bhagavacchāstravēdayōḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>viśvāsa-ṭippanī</summary>

antatō 'smad-āptānāṁ cirantanānubhavē nirdōṣatvē sākṣātkr̥tē, nānavasthā, na cānyō'nyāśrayaḥ।  
kaścana nūtanō granthaś cēt samasyā syāt। nānayōḥ।  
āpti-niścayaḥ - rakta-vidyādi-sambandha-paramparayā saphalayā।  
sāphalya-niścayaḥ - 

- dhāraṇād dharmam ityāhuḥ। kēna prajā varaṁ dhr̥tā iti sākṣātkāryam
</details>

### nigamanam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tataś ca tulyaśiṣṭatvād  
vikalpēna pramāṇatā ॥  
iti matvaitad ācaṣṭē  
sūtrakārō mahāmanāḥ ।  
vijñānādibhāvē vā  
tad-a-pratiṣēdha iti ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Consequently, because both are equally exemplary, they are optionally valid. It is with this view in mind that the wise Author of the Sūtras has explained: vijñanādibhave vaa tadapratiṣedhah.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Brahmasūtra II. ii. 41.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tataśca tulyaśiṣṭatvād vikalpēna pramāṇatā ॥  
iti matvaitadācaṣṭē sūtrakārō mahāmanāḥ ।  
vijñānādibhāvē vā tadapratiṣēdha iti ॥
</details>

## 14 amōhakatā

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu ca bhagavatas sarva-jñatvēnāsaṁbhāvyamānāyām api bhrāntau  
sarva-śaktitvēna vipralabdhamapi bhavatīti  
kim idam api śāstraṁ vyāmōhayitum abhihitam?  
uta vastutō'vahitabuddhyā nibaddham iti? 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> 115\. OBJECTION. However, granted that error is made inconceivable by the Bhagavan's omniscience,  
yet, since He is also omnipotent,  
He can also have composed the Pancarātra in order to deceive.  
Now, when people, considering this possibility, are confused in their minds as to  
which view they should take,  
that this Sastra has been promulgated to deceive them,  
or that it has been stated according to the truth with complete attentiveness of mind, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> nanu ca bhagavatassarvajñatvēnāsaṁbhāvyamānāyāmapi bhrāntau sarvaśaktitvēna vipralabdhamapi bhavatīti  
kimidamapi śāstraṁ vyāmōhayitumabhihitam uta vastutō'vahitabuddhyā nibaddham iti? 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> anyatara-pakṣāvalambana-viklava-manasāṁ  
ka iva nirṇayōpāyaḥ?  
pratyuta vēda-virōdhād ēva viplavana-phalam ity adhyavasyāma 

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> what way is there to resolve their dilemma? We should prefer to decide that since it militates against Scripture it results in disaster.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anyatarapakṣāvalambanaviklabamanasāṁ ka iva nirṇayōpāyaḥ, pratyuta vēdavirōdhādēva viplavanaphalamityadhyavasyāma iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatrōcyatē "vipratiṣēdhāt" iti -  
samasta-śrutītihāsa-purāṇa-lōka-vipratiṣēdhāt।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. To this objection the Author replies vipratisedhat, i.e., on account of the contradiction of all śruti, epic, purana and worldly experience. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Brahmasūtra II. ii. 42
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatrōcyatē vipratiṣēdhāt iti, samastaśrutītihāsapurāṇalōkavipratiṣēdhāt।  
</details>

### nākāraṇam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi vinā kāraṇēna bhagavataḥ sarva-śaktitva-mātrād viplāvana-śaṅkā -  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If, without any reason, merely because the Bhagavan is omnipotent, the question is raised  
if He might bave intended to ruin His devotees, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi vinā kāraṇēna bhagavataḥ sarvaśaktitvamātrād viplāvanaśaṅkā - 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

hantaivaṁ sarvaśaktitvān  
narakē dhārmikān api ।  
pātayēn nēti sandēhān  
niścēṣṭaṁ jagad āpatēt ॥ +++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

why, then one could also raise the question whether He would not hurl even the virtuous into hell by a whim of His omnipotence and consequently the whole world would fall into inactivity! 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

hantaivaṁ sarvaśaktitvānnarakē dhārmikānapi ।  
pātayēnnēti sandēhānniścēṣṭaṁ jagadāpatēt ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api cāyaṁ sarvaśaktitvēna vipralipsamānaḥ  
kim atīndriyāsatyārthān vēdān ādau nirmāya   
sva-sva-nirmāṇa-smaraṇa-śaktim api hiraṇya-garbhādēr apahr̥tya  
tat-prabhr̥ti svādhyāya-paramparām imāṁ pravartitavān na vēti saṁśayānāḥ  
kathaṁ viśvasimaḥ ।+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[95]] 

Besides, we could also raise the question whether He did not wish to deceive people, because He is omnipotent, and thus created in the beginning the Vedas themselves with false meanings, which are also suprasensible, took away from Brahma etc. also the power of recollecting that He was the creator of the Vedas,  
and from then onward set in motion the transmission of Vedic instruction until the present day:  
how can we be sure about it? 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Note</summary>

[236]: Since Brahma is the creator of the world, he can know whether there were Vedas or not before creation; by taking away Brahma's memory, God in His omnipotence could start the myth of the preterpersonal origin of the Veda..
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api cāyaṁ sarvaśaktitvēna vipralipsamānaḥ kimatīndriyāsatyārthān vēdānādau nirmāya  sva-svanirmāṇasmaraṇaśaktimapi hiraṇyagarbhādērapahr̥tya tatprabhr̥ti svādhyāyaparamparāmimāṁ pravartitavānna vēti saṁśayānāḥ kathaṁ viśvasimaḥ ।  
</details>

### svarūpa-viruddham
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

athāsya saty api sarva-śaktitvē  
yāvac-chakti-karaṇē pramāṇābhāvād anavasthānād 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or the position can be taken that  
since there is no evidence that,  
while He is indeed omnipotent,  
He acted up to the full measure of His omnipotence, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

athāsya satyapi sarvaśaktitvē yāvacchaktikaraṇē pramāṇābhāvād anavasthānād 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

bhagavataś ca sva-bhāvāpta-kāmatayā vipralambha-prayōjana-virahād 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

since there is no purpose for Him to deceive people  
because He is satisfied in all His desires,  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

bhagavataśca svabhāvāptakāmatayā vipralambhaprayōjanavirahād 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vaiṣamya-nairghr̥ṇyādi-dōṣair mātrayā 'pi cāsaṁspr̥ṣṭatvāt 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and since He is not in the least affected by defects of partiality and cruelty etc.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. ibid. II. i. 34:

> vaiṣamya-nairghr̥ṇyē na, sāpēkṣatvāt, tathā hi darśayati।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vaiṣamyanairghr̥ṇyādidōṣairmātrayāpi cāsaṁspr̥ṣṭatvāt 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sarvaprāṇijātasya svabhāvasauhr̥dēna vyavasthānāt। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

because He abides with natural affection for all living beings; 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Śvetāśvatara III. 17:

> sarvasya prabhum īśānaṁ sarvasya śaraṇaṁ suhr̥t॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sarvaprāṇijātasya svabhāvasauhr̥dēna vyavasthānāt 
</details>

### dōṣāsmaraṇam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> vipralabdhuṁ praṇītatvē ca  
viduṣām adya yāvat svādhyāyādhyayana--tad-arthānuṣṭhānavatāṁ  
tat-kartr̥-dōṣa-vismaraṇānupapattēs  
tādr̥śāśaṅkā nāsti

iti cēt  
tad ētat sarvam anyatrāpi samānam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> and since, if He had composed ~~the Pañcaratra~~ in order to deceive, 
it would be impossible to demonstrate that  
the wise men who, up to now, learn its instructions  
and perform the contents of these instructions  
have forgotten the defects of its author,  
it must follow that such a suspicion does not arise; 

and if this view is taken, all this will equally apply to the other ~~Vedas~~ as well.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vipralabdhuṁ praṇītatvē ca  
viduṣāmadya yāvat svādhyāyādhyayana-tadarthānuṣṭhānavatāṁ tatkartr̥dōṣavismaraṇānupapattēstādr̥śāśaṅkā nāstīti cēttadētatsarvamanyatrāpi samānam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā hi -  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kim asyāvāpta-kāmasya  
sarvajñasya dayā-nidhēḥ ।  
alpa-sattvair a-labdhārthair  
vipralabdhaiḥ prayōjanam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

what possible purpose could He who is satisfied in all His desires,  
who is omniscient and a treasury of compassion  
have in deceiving the poor people  
who have failed to understand the meaning (of the Veda)? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

dayānidhēḥ ... See G.A. Grierson, Indian Antiquary, vol. 37, p. 260:

> India again owes the preservation of the idea of a God of Grace, of the Fatherhood of God, to the Bhāgavatas.

vipralabdhaiḥ ... ‘prāṇibhiḥ’ *iti viśēṣyam adhyāhāryam।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kimasyāvāptakāmasya sarvajñasya dayānidhēḥ ।  
alpasattvairalabdhārthairvipralabdhaiḥ prayōjanam ॥  
</details>

### mahājana-gr̥hītatā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vipralabdhuṁ kr̥taṁ tantraṁ  
kathaṁ vā parama-rṣayaḥ ।  
itas tataḥ praśaṁsanti  
tulya-vac chruti-mūrdhabhiḥ ॥  +++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or how could the supreme sages everywhere praise the Tantra as being equal to the Upanisads,  
if it had been composed in order to deceive? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vipralabdhuṁ kr̥taṁ tantraṁ kathaṁ vā paramarṣayaḥ ।  
itastataḥ praśaṁsanti tulyavacchrutimūrddhabhiḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā hi vēdais saha nirviśēṣaṁ  
vārāha-rāmāyaṇa-bhāratādau ।  
amuṣya tantrasya rahasyabhāvaṁ  
vadanti santas tam imaṁ vadāmaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For thus the saints declare in Vārāha Purana, the Ramayana and the Bharata etc. that this Tantra is an equally esoteric doctrine as the Vedas; and we declare the same. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘nirviśēṣaṁ’ samānam ity arthaḥ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi vēdaissaha nirviśēṣaṁ vārāha-rāmāyaṇa-bhāratādau ।  
amuṣya tantrasya rahasyabhāvaṁ va (paṭhantīti draviḍapāṭhaḥ ।)danti santastamimaṁ vadāmaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> vēdēna pañcarātrēṇa  
bhaktyā yajñēna ca dvija ।  
prāpyō'haṁ nānyathā prāpyō  
varṣalakṣaśatairapi ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[96]]

> "Through Veda, Pañcaratra, through devotion and sacrifice, O Brahmin, I can be attained,  
and not in any other way, even in hundreds of lacs of years. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Varāhapurāṇa Ch. 66. śls. 19, 14, 15a, 18a.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> vēdēna pañcarātrēṇa bhaktyā yajñēna ca dvija? ।  
prāpyō'haṁ nānyathā prāpyō varṣalakṣaśatairapi ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> pañcarātraṁ sahasrāṇāṁ  
yadi kaścid grahīṣyati ।  
karma-kṣayē ca mad-bhaktō  
yadi kaścid bhaviṣyati ॥  
tasya vēdāḥ pañcarātraṁ nityaṁ hr̥di vasiṣyati +++(=vatsyati)+++ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> If one among thousands will grasp the Pañcarātra and,  
at the expiry of his karman, will die my devotee, the Vedas and the Pañcarātra will dwell in his heart forever.237

[237]: not identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> pañcarātraṁ sahasrāṇāṁ yadi kaścid grahīṣyati ।  
karmakṣayē ca madbhaktō yadi kaścid bhaviṣyati ॥  
tasya vēdāḥ pañcarātraṁ nityaṁ hr̥di va(vatsya prāptē vasiṣyatītyārṣam ।)siṣyati ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yad idaṁ pañca-rātram mē  
śāstraṁ parama-durlabham ॥  
tad bhavān vētsyatē sarvaṁ  
mat-prasādād a-saṁśayam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> This supreme Pañcarātra doctrine of mine, which is not difficult to grasp, that you shall reach to all the world by my grace, doubtless.25 

[238]: not identified.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Varāhapurāṇa Ch. 66. śl. 18b.

Also Cf. ibid. śl. 11b:

> alābhē vēda-mantrāṇāṁ pañca-rātrōditēna vā॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadidaṁ pañcarātrammē śāstraṁ paramadurlabham ॥  
tad bhavān vētsyatē sarvaṁ matprasādādasaṁśayam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> purāṇaiścaiva vēdaiśca  
pañcarātrais tathaiva ca ॥  
**dhyāyanti** yōginō nityaṁ  
kratubhiś ca **yajanti** tam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> The Yogins mediate upon the Eternal One with Puranas, Vedas and Pañcaratras, and worship Him with the proper rites. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Rāmāyaṇa [ uttara ] Ch. X (Prakṣipta) [M.L.J. Press],p.1012. The reading found is:

> yajanti pañcabhir yajñaiḥ satataṁ madhusūdanam॥ [61b]

> yaḥ purāṇē ca vēdē ca pañca-rātrē ca paṭhyatē॥ [62b]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

purāṇaiścaiva vēdaiśca pañcarātraistathaiva ca ॥  
dhyāyanti yōginō nityaṁ kratubhiśca yajanti tam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> ēvam ēkaṁ sāṅkhya-yōgaṁ  
vēdāraṇyakam ēva ca ।  
paras-parāṅgāny ētāni  
pañca-rātrañ ca sattama ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Thus Samkhya and Yoga on the one hand, and Veda and Aranyaka on the other hand are one and the same; all together they are the members that constitute Pañcaratra
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

vēdāraṇyaka ... See Amarnath Ray, “Śrīkṛṣṇa and the source of the Bhagavadgītā,” Indian Historical Quarterly, Vol. IX, pp. 193-194:

> Kṛṣṇa was the great religious teacher who brought about a Sāṁkhya-Yoga-Vedānta synthesis....The first book which is fragmentary might have been a remnant of the Āraṇyaka of the Sāttvatas, spoken of in the Nārāyaṇīya account of the Mahābhārata [XII. 348. 31]. When the doctrines of bhakti and avatāra and desireless action were adopted by Kṛṣṇa's followers, they were called Bhāgavatas.

For a detailed account of the alliance between Pañcarātra and Sāṅkhya-Yoga and their influences and counter-influences, see G.A. Grierson, ‘The Nārāyaṇīya and the Bhāgavatas’, The Indian Antiquary, Vol. 37, pp. 255-258.

sattama ... Mahābhārata XII. 336. 76.

Cf. ibid., Ch. 337. śl. 1:

> sāṅkhyaṁ yogaṁ pāñcarātraṁ vedāraṇyakameva ca।  
jñānānyetāni brahmarṣe lokeṣu pracaranti ha॥

Also cf. ibid. śl. 59:

> sāṅkhyaṁ yogaḥ pāñcarātraṁ vedāḥ pāśupataṁ tathā।  
jñānānyetāni rājarṣe viddhi nānāmatāni vai॥

Commenting upon the verse “evamekam” in his Śrībhāṣya under II. ii. 39 (p. 834), Rāmānuja says:

> sāṅkhyaṁ ca yōgaś ca sāṅkhya-yōgam । vēdāś cāraṇyakāni ca vēdāraṇyakam । parasparāṅgāny ētāni, ēka-tattva-pratipādana-paratayaikī-bhūtāni; ēkaṁ pañca-rātram iti kathyatē । ētad uktaṁ bhavati — sāṅkhyōktāni pañca-viṁśati-tattvāni , yōgōktaṁ ca yama-niyamādy-ātmakaṁ yōgam, vēdōdita-karma--sva-rūpāṇy aṅgīkr̥tya tattvānāṁ brahmātmakatvaṁ, yōgasya ca brahmōpāsana-prakāratvaṁ karmaṇāṁ ca tad-ārādhana-rūpatām abhidadhati । karma--sva-rūpaṁ pratipādayanty āraṇyakāni । ētad ēva parēṇa brahmaṇā nārāyaṇēna svayam ēva pañca-rātra-tantrē viśadīkr̥tam iti । śārīrakē ca sāṅkhyōkta-tattvānām abrahmātmakatā-mātraṁ nirākr̥tam, na sva-rūpam । yōga-pāśupatayōś cēśvarasya kēvala-nimitta-kāraṇatā, parāvara-tattva-viparīta-kalpanā, vēda-bahiṣkr̥tācārō nirākr̥taḥ; na yōga--sva-rūpaṁ, paśupati--sva-rūpaṁ ca । ataḥ 
>
>> sāṅkhyaṁ yōgaḥ pañca-rātraṁ vēdāḥ pāśupataṁ tathā।  
ātma-pramāṇāny ētāni na hantavyāni hētubhiḥ 
>
> iti tat-tad-abhihita-tat-tat-sva-rūpa-mātram aṅgīkāryam । jina-sugatābhihita-tattvavat sarvaṁ na bahiṣkāryam ity ucyatē । ‘yathāgamaṁ yathā-nyāyaṁ niṣṭhā nārāyaṇaḥ prabhur’ ity anēnaikārthyāt ।

Also see Collected Works of Sir R. G. Bhandarkar (Bhandarkar Oriental Research Institute, 1933), Vol. I, pp. 248-294 for an article ‘The Rāmānujīya and the Bhāgavata or Pāñcarātra systems’.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> ēvamēkaṁ sāṅkhyayōgaṁ vēdāraṇyakamēva ca ।  
parasparāṅgānyētāni pañcarātrañca sattama? ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> vēdēna pañcarātrēṇa  
yaḥ paśyati sa paśyati ।  
idam mahōpaniṣadaṁ  
catur-vēda-samanvitam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> O excellent one! He who sees through Veda and Pañcaratra sees truly; this great Upanisada, consistent with the four Vedas...." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

vēdēna ... To be identified.

idaṁ ... Mahābhārata XII. 326. 100a.
</details>

vēdēna pañcarātrēṇa yaḥ paśyati sa paśyati ।  
idammahōpaniṣadaṁ caturvēdasamanvitam ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vacasām ēvam-ādīnām  
ānantyād uparamyatē ।  
itthaṁ-bhūtasya tantrasya  
viplavaṁ yadi śaṅkasē ॥  
sarvatra syādanāśvāsa  
ity ētad upadiśyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Since the number of these and similar statements is infinite, we stop here. If you still raise the question if there cannot be ruin in such a Tantra,  
then there can be no faith in anything. It is with this view in mind that the Author sets forth: 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

pañca-rātrasya parama-pramāṇa-bhūtasyāpi viplāvana-śaṅkāyāṁ sarvatrāpi aprāmāṇya-buddhyā anāśvāsa ēva bhavēt । vipratiṣēdhaś ca syād vaidika-laukika-vyavahārāṇām iti sūtrārthaṁ samuccinōti ‘sarvatra syād anāśvāsa’ ity anēna । ‘vipratiṣēdhāt iti’ ity ētat paryantam ēkaṁ vākyam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vacasāmēvamādīnāmānantyāduparamyatē ।  
itthaṁbhūtasya tantrasya viplavaṁ yadi śaṅkasē ॥  
sarvatra syādanāśvāsa ityētadupadiśyatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"vipratiṣēdhāt"   
iti।  
</details>

vipratisedAt.
</details>

Brahmasūtra II. ii. 42.
</details>
