## 15 virōdhābhāsē tāratamyam

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ēvañca -  

virōdhē'pi vikalpaḥ syād  
bhagavac-chāstra-vēdayōḥ ।  
**virōdha** ēva **nāstīti**  
prāg ēva **pratyapādayam** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore, even if there were a conflict between the Bhagavan's doctrine and the Veda, there still would be option between them; but we have already expounded that there is no conflict between them at all.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ēvañca -  

virōdhē'pi vikalpaḥ syād bhagavacchāstravēdayōḥ ।  
virōdha ēva nāstīti prāgēva pratyapādayam ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanv atra-bhavatāṁ +++(śābara-)+++bhāṣyakārāṇāṁ viruddhāṁśāprāmāṇyābhidhānaṁ katham iva?  
</details>

<details><summary>viśvāsa-ṭippanī</summary>

nātra śaṅkarō bhāṣyakāra uktaḥ - tasyānyatrēha khaṇḍitatvāt।  
na ca dramiḍabhāṣyakāraḥ - utpattyasambhavādhikaraṇē sūtrēṣu tad-vipratipattau pramāṇasyābhāvāt।  
na ca śrutaprakāśikōkta-pāñcarātrapāśupatādi-tulyatva-kathakaḥ kaścana - yāmunasya tatrānaṅgīkārāt।  
śrutipāramyavādinaṁ śabaranibhaṁ gauravāspadaṁ gr̥hītum alam। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

116\. OBJECTION. However, how can the venerable Author of the Bhasya 239 state that those parts which are in conflict are invalid: 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

Sabarabhasya and KMS.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This reference by Yāmuna to ‘bhāṣyakāra’ has been taken by some Vaiṣṇava scholars as speaking of Dramiḍabhāṣyakāra, who is traditionally said to have commented upon the Brahmasūtra. But this may be taken as a reference to Śaṅkara himself. 

Rāmānuja's Śrībhāṣya also seems to support this position. Cf. Śrībhāṣya under II. ii. 42, p. 832:

> yat tu paraiḥ sūtra-catuṣṭayaṁ kasyacid viruddhāṁśasya prāmāṇya-niṣēdha-paraṁ vyākhyātam, 

with the above passage : “nanv atra bhavatāṁ” etc. Also cf. Śaṅkara on the above sūtra, p. 259:

> yadyapy ēvaṁ-jātīyakō 'ṁśaḥ  
> samānatvān na visaṁvāda-gōcarō bhavati ।  
> asti tu aṁśāntaraṁ visaṁvāda-sthānam  
> ity ataḥ tat-pratyākhyānāyārambhaḥ 

etc.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanvatra bhavatāṁ bhāṣyakārāṇāṁ viruddhāṁśāprāmāṇyābhidhānaṁ kathamiva,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yady api virōdhaḥ - kr̥tvā cintayā parihr̥tas,  
tad api gambhīra-nyāya-sāgaram avagāḍhum a-parivr̥ḍhānāṁ kōmala-manasāṁ  
vēdānādarō mā bhūd ity-ēvam-param, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. "If there be conflict, it is carefully eliminated."  
This statement means that those of frail minds,  
who are not strong enough to plunge into the deep ocean of rules of interpretation, 
must not be [[97]] disrespectful to the Veda. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadyapi virōdhaḥ kr̥tvā cintayā parihr̥tastadapi gambhīranyāyasāgaramavagāḍhumaparivr̥ḍhānāṁ kōmalamanasāṁ vēdānādarō mābhūdityēvamparam, 
</details>

<details><summary>viśvāsa-ṭippanī</summary>

atraiva vēdasya subōdhataratvam uktam।  
tac ca vēdāṅgais tad-upabr̥ṁhaṇēna sidhyatīti suvacam। 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathaiva hi bhagavatō jaiminēḥ "karma-phalōpanyāsaḥ karma-śraddhā-saṁvardhanāyē"ti ।+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This is comparable to the venerable Jaimini's exposition  
that the fruits of acts serve to increase people's faith in the acts.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Vedārthasaṅgraha, p. 157:

> aśruta-vēdāntānāṁ karmaṇi aśraddhā mā bhūd iti dēvatādhikaraṇē ativādāḥ kr̥tāḥ; karma-mātrē yathā śraddhā syād iti ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathaiva hi bhagavatō jaiminēḥ karmaphalōpanyāsaḥ karmaśraddhāsaṁvarddhanāyēti ।  
</details>

## 16 śiṣṭa-bāhya-grahaṇē

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vēda-bāhya-gr̥hītatvād  
a-prāmāṇyam **avādi** yat ।  
ētad+++(→pāñcarātra)+++-bāhya-gr̥hītatvād  
vēdānāṁ vā kutō na tat ॥+++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

117\. The contention has been voiced that Pañcarātra is invalid because it is accepted by those who are outside the Veda." 240 
But why could one not equally well contend that the Vedas are invalid  
because they are accepted by those who are outside Pancarātra? 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[240]: supra § 17: vedabāhyagrhītatvāt. I have rendered grhīta by "accepted' to cover approximately the variety of meanings that Yāmuna detects in the word.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See the verse ‘vivādādhyāsitaṁ’ etc., p. 17 above.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vēdabāhyagr̥hītattvādaprāmāṇyamavādi yat ।  
ētadbāhyagr̥hītatvād vēdānāṁ vā kutō na tat ॥
</details>

### bāhyatvē gr̥hītatvē ca vikalpāḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca ।  

kiṁ cēdaṁ vēda-**bāhyatvaṁ**,  
kā vā syāt tad-gr̥hītatā ।  
kim aṅga vēdād anyatvaṁ,  
vēda-bāhyatvam ucyatē ॥  
+++(uta)+++ tan-niṣiddhārtha-kāritvam,  
āhō+++(svit)+++ tad-dvēṣa-śīlatā । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Furthermore, what exactly does this mean, being "outside the Veda,"  
and what means "accepted by those who are outside the Veda?"  
Does "being outside the Veda" mean  
"being different from the Veda"  
or "doing what is forbidden by the Veda"  
or "being hostile to the Vedas?"  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca ।  
kiṁ cēdaṁ vēdabāhyatvaṁ kā vā syāttadgr̥hītatā ।  
kimaṅga vēdādanyatvaṁ vēdabāhyatvamucyatē ॥  
tanniṣiddhārthakāritvamāhō taddvēṣaśīlatā । 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā -  

**gr̥hītatvam** +++(nāma)+++ adhītatvaṁ  
jñātatvaṁ vā vicāryatām ।  
kriyamāṇārthatā vā syād  
+dhētuḥ sarvatra **duṣyati** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise we must inquire whether "accepted" means learnt" or "known" or "observed."  
In all  cases the ground proves to be defective, 35 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā -  
gr̥hītatvamadhītatvaṁ jñātatvaṁ vā vicāryatām ।  
kriyamāṇārthatā vā syāddhētuḥ sarvatra duṣyati ॥
</details>
 
### vēda-bhinnair adhītatā jñātatā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatra tāvad -  

yadi vēdād **vibhinnatvaṁ**  
bāhyatvaṁ, sā'py **adhītatā** ।  
"vēdād anyais tribhir varṇair  
**adhītaṁ** vaidikaṁ vacaḥ ।  
pramāṇam +++(pāñcarātraṁ tv apramāṇam uktam)+++" ity anaikāntyaṁ  
hētōs tatra **prasajyatē** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

First of all, if "outside the Veda" means "different from the Veda,"  
and "accepted" means "learnt",  
then the ground proves to be occasional,  
since it equally applies to the Vedas themselves :  
the Vedic statements, which are valid,  
are "learnt" by members of the three estates,  
which themselves are "different from the Veda." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatra tāvad -  
yadi vēdādvibhinnatvaṁ bāhyatvaṁ sā'pyadhītatā ।  
vēdādanyaistribhirvarṇairadhītaṁ vaidikaṁ vacaḥ ।  
pramāṇamityanaikāntyaṁ hētōstatra prasajyatē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

jñātatvē 'pi gr̥hītatvē  
dōṣād asmān na mucyasē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If you take "accepted" to mean "known," you do not get rid of the same defect. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

jñātatvē'pi gr̥hītatvē dōṣādasmānna mucyasē ।  
</details>

### vēda-bhinnaiḥ kriyamāṇārthatā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pūrvōktaṁ vēda-bāhyatvaṁ,  
kriyamāṇārthatā yadi ॥  
gr̥hītatā'pi, vēdaiḥ +++(tad-gr̥hītaiḥ)+++ syāt  
tathaiva vyabhicāritā ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If the term "outside the Veda" means "different from the Veda,"  
and "accepted" means "observed,"  
then there would likewise be an occasional application of the ground to the Vedas themselves.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pūrvōktaṁ vēdabāhyatvaṁ kriyamāṇārthatā yadi ॥  
gr̥hītatā'pi vēdaiḥ syāttathaiva vyabhicāritā ।  
</details>

### pratiṣiddhārtha-kartr̥tvē
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pratiṣiddhārtha-kartr̥tvē  
vēda-bāhyatva-lakṣaṇē ॥  
vyabhicāras trayī-vākyaiḥ  
prāyaścitta-vidhāyakaiḥ । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If "outside the Veda" is taken to mean "performing forbidden acts," 
the ground has an occasional application to those statements of the Veda  
which enjoin expiatory ceremonies. ([241]: Manusmrti, 8.107.)
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pratiṣiddhārthakartr̥tvē vēdabāhyatvalakṣaṇē ॥  
vyabhicārastrayīvākyaiḥ prāyaścittavidhāyakaiḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

prāyaścitta-vidhāyakāni vākyāni  
"kūṣmāṇḍair juhuyāt" ityādīni  
pratiṣiddha-kāribhir adhīta-gr̥hītānuṣṭhīyamānārthāny ēva pramāṇānīti  
tādr̥śa-vēda-bāhya-gr̥hītatvam anaikāntikam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For since statements enjoining expiations, e.g. "One must sacrifice with the kusmanda verses,"  
whose content is to be "learnt", "known" and "observed," by those who perform forbidden acts, are authoritative,  
it would follow that the ground "because they are accepted by people outside the Veda" is occasional,242
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

People who do prohibited acts follow Vedic expiations; but if acceptance by people who commit forbidden acts is sufficient to deny the validity of what they accept, this means that the validity of the Veda would be denied.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Bodhāyanadharmasūtra, III. vii. 1:

> kūṣmāṇḍair juhuyāt yō 'pūta iva manyēta ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

prāyaścittavidhāyakāni vākyāni kūṣmāṇḍairjuhuyāt ityādīni pratiṣiddhakāribhiradhītagr̥hītānuṣṭhīyamānārthānyēva pramāṇānīti tādr̥śavēdabāhyagr̥hītatvamanaikāntikam ।  
</details>

#### vēda-dvēṣi-grahaṇam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi vēda-dvēṣi-jana-parigr̥hītatvād a-prāmāṇyaṁ pañca-rātra-tantrāṇām,  
hētōr asiddhatvāt,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor are the Pañcaratra Tantras invalid  
because they are "accepted" by people hostile to the Veda,  
for the ground is unproved. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The argument here is that the handling of Vedic texts by the unorthodox people like the Buddhists and the Jains, cannot bring down the authoritative character of those texts. Otherwise, the Vedas would long ago, have become invalid since the unorthodox schools of thought tried to explain the Vedic passages as they pleased contradicting their original significance. The authority of the Vedas is for all time to come and the wrong handling of those texts by others cannot undermine it.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi vēdadvēṣijanaparigr̥hītatvādaprāmāṇyaṁ pañcarātratantrāṇām,  hētōrasiddhatvāt,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca na vēda-dvēṣi-jana-parigrahaḥ prāmāṇyaṁ pratihanti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Besides, acceptance by people hostile to the Veda does not by itself refute the validity of what is accepted. +++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca na vēdadvēṣijanaparigrahaḥ prāmāṇyaṁ pratihanti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi hi pratihanyāt - 
nirargalas tarhi nāstikānāṁ panthāḥ +++(tat-parigrahēṇa)+++,  
tē hi vēda-prāmāṇya-prōtsādanāya prayasyantaḥ+++(←yas)+++ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If it did, the Path of the Heretics would be unbarred;  
for they endeavour to uproot the validity of the Veda. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi hi pratihanyānnirargalastarhi nāstikānāṁ panthāḥ, tē hi vēdaprāmāṇyaprōtsādanāya prayasyantaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kathañcid vēda-vākyāni  
**gr̥hītvā vipralambhanāt**+++(=vañcanāt)+++ ।  
anāyāsēna mithyārthān  
vēdān kuryur digambarāḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Thus the naked Jainas could effortlessly render the Vedas untruthful  
simply by accepting" the Vedas in some manner by way of deception.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Tantravārtika I. iii. 3, p. 85:

> lōkāyatika-mūrkhāṇāṁ naivānyat karma vidyatē ।  
yāvat kiñcid adr̥ṣṭārthaṁ tat dr̥śyārthaṁ hi kurvatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kathañcidvēdavākyāni gr̥hītvā vipralambhanāt ।  
anāyāsēna mithyārthān vēdān kuryurdigambarāḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha 

> tatrānadhikāriṇām adhyētr̥̄ṇām ēva  
> 
> > na cābhivyāharēd brahma  
> svadhā-ninayād r̥tē ।  
> 
> ity-ādivacana-paryālōcanayā  
> dōṣō na nirdōṣa-vēda-vākyānām 

iti cēt 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

118\. OBJECTION, A consideration of such statements as "He should never use the Veda, except at a funerary offering," (Manusmrti) shows that the defect affects only the unqualified students, not the defectless Vedic statements themselves.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Manusmṛti II. 172a. The reading found is: ‘nābhivyāhārayēt’ etc. A similar statement is found in the Gautama Dharmasūtra II. 9: ‘na brahmābhivyāhārayēt’ & c.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha tatrānadhikāriṇāmadhyētr̥̄ṇāmēva na cābhivyāharēd brahmasvadhāninayādr̥tē ।  
ityādivacanaparyālōcanayā dōṣō na nirdōṣavēdavākyānāmiti cēt 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tat-prastuta-tantrēṣv apy anadhikāri-śrōtr̥-janānām ēṣa dōṣaḥ,  
na nirdōṣa-tantrāṇām  
iti sarvaṁ samānam anyatrābhinivēśāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REPLY. Then the defect affects only the unqualified students in the case of the Tantras under discussion as well,  
and not the defectless Tantras themselves;  
so everything is the same, depending on what partisan view one takes.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatprastutatantrēṣvapyanadhikāriśrōtr̥janānāmēṣa dōṣaḥ, na nirdōṣatantrāṇāmiti sarvaṁ samānamanyatrābhinivēśāt ।  
</details>

### anadhikāri-grahaṇam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha mataṁ 

> vēdabāhyatvaṁ nāma vaidika-karmānadhikāritvaṁ  
tad-anadhikāribhir vēda-bāhyair gr̥hītatvāt  
caitya-vandana-vākyavad a-pramāṇam 

iti 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

244 Or if it be held that "outside the Veda" means "unqualified to perform Vedic acts,"  
and that Pañcaratra is invalid, like the caityavandana statements,"  
because it is accepted by those who, being unqualified, are outside the Veda, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

supra § 17: this Buddhist injunction is outside the Veda
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Bhaṭṭa Medhātithi, commenting upon Manusmṛti XII. 95, quotes from some unidentified source:

> nōdanāḥ caitya-vandanataḥ svargō bhavati ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha mataṁ vēdabāhyatvaṁ nāma vaidikakarmānadhikāritvaṁ tadanadhikāribhirvēdabāhyairgr̥hītatvāt caityavandanavākyavat apramāṇamiti 
</details>

#### anadhikāraḥ kva?
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tatrāpi kim akhila-vaidika-karmānadhikāri-jana-parigr̥hītatvaṁ hētuḥ,  
uta katipaya-vaidika-karmānadhikāri-gr̥hītatvam  
iti vivicya vyācaṣṭām ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

the following distinction must be 99 considered  
is the ground here that the Tantras are accepted by people unqualified for all Vedic rites,  
or by people who are unqualified for some Vedic rites?  
This point should be clarified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tatrāpi kimakhilavaidikakarmānadhikārijanaparigr̥hītatvaṁ hētuḥ, uta katipayavaidikakarmānadhikārigr̥hītatvamiti vivicya vyācaṣṭām ।  
</details>

#### anadhikārō 'khilē
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**na** tāvad agrimaḥ kalpaḥ  
**kalpatē** hētv-asiddhitaḥ ।  
**na** hi sō **'sti** manuṣyēṣu  
**yaḥ** śrautē kvāpi karmaṇi ॥  
**nādhikuryād** ahiṁsādau  
nr̥mātrasyādhikāraḥ । +++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na tāvadagrimaḥ kalpaḥ kalpatē hētvasiddhitaḥ ।  
na hi sō'sti manuṣyēṣu yaḥ śrautē kvāpi karmaṇi ॥  
nādhikuryādahiṁsādau nr̥mātrasyādhikāraḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

anyathā hi brāhmaṇa-hanana--tad-dhanāpaharaṇa--varṇāṅganā-saṁgama--vēdādhyayanādi kurvāṇāś caṇḍālādayō na duṣyēyuḥ - tad-anadhikāritvāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Now, the first alternative cannot be adopted,  
because the ground is not proved.  
For there is no human being who is not qualified for any shrauta rite whatsoever, e.g. non-violence etc.,  
because his humanity as such provides his qualification.  
Otherwise candālas etc. would do no wrong  
if they committed such crimes a brahmin-murder, theft of brahmin wealth, miscegenation with caste-women, study of the Veda etc.,  
simply because they were not qualified to observe these prohibitions. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anyathā hi brāhmaṇahanana-taddhanāpaharaṇavarṇāṅganāsaṁgama-vēdādhyayanādi kurvāṇāścaṇḍālādayō na duṣyēyuḥ tadanadhikāritvāt।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yasya hi yan na kartavyaṁ  
tasya hi tat-karaṇaṁ pratyavāyāya, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If a man does something he should not do,  
he commits an offence. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide Karmamīmāṁsā*, p. 93:

> While an injunction directs a positive act, a prohibition (niṣedha or pratiṣedha) serves to turn a man away from performing the action expressed in the verb and its object. The prohibition does not lead to any desirable result such as heaven; it serves none the less a useful purpose; the man, who obeys the direction not to eat the mysterious kalañja, by observing this taboo escapes the hell which else had been his fate. In disgusted technical phraseology of Mīmāṁsā, the negative applies not to the sense of the verb, but to the optative affix; as an optative urges us to action, so a negatived optative turns away from it.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yasya hi yanna kartavyaṁ tasya hi tatkaraṇaṁ pratyavāyāya, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ataḥ sarvēṣām īdr̥śa-vaidika-karmaṇi adhikārō vidyata ēvēty  
asiddhō hētuḥ,  
sādhana-vikalaś ca +++(caitya-vandana-)+++dr̥ṣṭāntaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It follows that everybody is qualified to these Vedic rites,243  
which shows that the ground is not proved  
and that the illustration falls short of the means of proof.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

in one sense.

For the observance of a prohibition is as much a ritual action as the observance of an injunction.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ataḥ sarvēṣāmīdr̥śavaidikakarmaṇi adhikārō vidyata ēvētyasiddhō hētuḥ, sādhanavikalaśca dr̥ṣṭāntaḥ ।  
</details>

#### anadhikāra ēkadēśē
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāpi katipaya-vaidika-karmānadhikāribhir gr̥hītatvād a-prāmāṇyaṁ samasta-vēda-vākyānām aprāmāṇya-prasaṅgāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor can the second alternative be adopted  
that the Tantras are invalid because they are accepted by people  
who are unqualified for certain Vedic rites,  
because that would entail the conclusion that all Vedic statements are invalid.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi katipayavaidikakarmānadhikāribhirgr̥hītatvādaprāmāṇyaṁ samastavēdavākyānāmaprāmāṇyaprasaṅgāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

asti hi sarvēṣāṁ katipaya-vaidika-karmānadhikāraḥ,  
brāhmaṇasyēva rāja-sūyē,  
rājanyasyēva sōma-pānē,+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For every man has some Vedic rites for which he is not qualified:  
the brahmin is not qualified for the Royal Consecration,  
the ksatriya not for the ritual drinking of soma. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

asti hi sarvēṣāṁ katipayavaidikakarmānadhikāraḥ, brāhmaṇasyēva rājasūyē, rājanyasyēva sōmapānē,   
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atō vyavasthita-varṇādhikāri-gr̥hīta-vēda-vacanair anaikāntikō hētuḥ, a-prayōjakaś ca ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Consequently, this ground has an occasional application to the Vedic statements,  
which are accepted by qualified persons belonging to the three estates,  
and is therefore inconclusive. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

aprayōjakatvam ēva pratipādayati ‘caitya-vandanataḥ ity-ādinā ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atō vyavasthitavarṇādhikārigr̥hītavēdavacanairanaikāntikōhētuḥ, aprayōjakaśca ।  
</details>

#### kāraṇadōṣaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

caityavandanataḥ svargō  
bhavatītīdr̥śī matiḥ ।  
na tat-parigrahān mithyā  
kintu kāraṇa-dōṣataḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As to the illustration,  
the view that heaven is attained by worshipping a caitya  
is not invalidated by its being accepted by heretics,  
but by the deficiency of its cause, [[100]]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

caityavandanataḥ svargō bhavatītīdr̥śī matiḥ ।  
na tatparigrahānmithyā kintu kāraṇadōṣataḥ ॥
</details>

### śiṣṭa-parigrahaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

uktaśca vaidika-samastāstika-pravara-bhr̥gu-bharadvāja-dvaipāyana-prabhr̥ti-maha-rṣi-jana-parigrahaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

119\. We have already said that Pancarâtra has been accepted by the Vedic, and among all orthodox pre-eminent, sages Bhṛgu, Bharadvāja, Dvaipāyaṇa etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See G.A. Grierson, “The Nārāyaṇīya and the Bhāgavatas”, Indian Antiquary Vol. 37, p. 254:

> The usual tradition is that it (the Bhāgavata doctrine) was transmitted: Deity—Nārada—saints including the Sun—Ṛṣis in his train—gods—Asita—to the world in different channels. Modern Bhāgavatas recognise two great teachers of their religion. One is Nārada, to whom is attributed Nāradīya Bhaktisūtra. Equally esteemed is the collection of Śāṇḍilyabhakti-sūtras. The author to whom it is attributed, composed the Śāṇḍilyavidyā quoted in the Chāndogya Upaniṣad III. xiv. 3.

See also p. 9 above, fn
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

uktaśca vaidikasamastāstikapravarabhr̥gu -bharadvāja -dvaipāyanaprabhr̥ti -maharṣijanaparigrahaḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

adyatvē'pi hi pañca-rātra-tantra-vihita-mārgēṇa  
prāsāda-karaṇa--pratimā-pratiṣṭhāpana--praṇāma-pradakṣiṇōtsavādīni pratyakṣa-śruti-vihitāgnihōtrādivat śrēyas-karatara-buddhyā 'nutiṣṭhataḥ śiṣṭān paśyāmaḥ। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And in the present day we can also observe how exemplary persons of great learning,  
believing that these rites are most effective in attaining bliss,  
perform the rites of temple-building, erection of idols, prostration, circumambulation and particular festival ceremonies,  
just as they perform the agnihotra and other rituals enjoined directly by Scripture. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

For a detailed account of temple-construction according to Pañcarātra-texts, see Agastyasaṁhitā 1-106; Ahirbudhnya Saṁhitā XXXVI. 31-49; Īśvarasaṁhitā XVI. 1, 219-247; 266-287; Kapiñjalasaṁhitā X. 61-66; 69-72; Jayākhyasaṁhitā XX. 73ff; Pādma ‘kriyā’ IV. 24-28, 35-45; V. 84-90; VIII; Pārameśvara X. 2-106; Pauṣkara XL. 92-109a, XLII. 71-118; Viṣṇutilaka VI. 1-342a, 449-498; Sanatkumāra ‘Brahma’ VIII; Sāttvata XXIV. 280-432a, XXV. 1-375; Hayaśīrṣa ‘Ādi’. XIII. 1-41; XXXVIII. 61; XLIV. 12-19.

For the installation of images, see Aniruddha XV, XXXIII, XXXIV; Īśvara XVI. 228-352, XVIII. 1-560; Jayākhya XX. 131b ff; Parama XVIII. 28-75; Pauṣkara XXXVIII. 1ff, 15-46; Sanatkumāra “Brahma” VI. 110 passim, IX. passim; Sāttvata XXV. 307ff; 320ff, XXVI. 375.

For a description of Utsavas, which are as many as fifty in number, see Agastya V. 1-2; Aniruddha XVII. 9-16a, XX. 1-16, XXIV, XXV. 1-4, XXVII; Īśvara X. 4a-10, XII. 1-233a, XIII. 1-265a, XIX. 469-473; Kapiñjala XXII. 3-5, 8-9; XXIII. 1-84a, XXIV. 1-69a; Pādma “caryā” X. 6-23, XI. 1-292, XIV. 1-85; Pārameśvara XVI. 1-55, XVII. 1-550, Śāṇḍilya I, XV. 1-126; Śrīpraśna XXX. 79-87; Sanatkumāra “Śiva” IX.

For the annual festival called Mahotsava, see Aniruddha XXI. 1-112; Īśvara X; Pādma “car” Xl; Śrīpraśna XXXI. 8, XXXVIII.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

adyatvē'pi hi pañcarātratantravihitamārgēṇa prāsādakaraṇa -pratimāpratiṣṭhāpana -praṇāma -pradakṣiṇōtsavādīni pratyakṣaśrutivihitāgnihōtrādivat śrēyaskaratarabuddhyā'nutiṣṭhataḥ śiṣṭān paśyāmaḥ, 
</details>

#### śrēyas-sādhanatā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na caitadācaraṇaṁ nirmūlam iti yuktaṁ  
sandhyā-vandanāṣṭakā-caraṇādēr api nirmūlatva-prasaṅgāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And it is improper to maintain that their conduct has no foundation,  
for that would entail that such smārta rites as crepuscular worship, astaka etc., are similarly without foundation. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na caitadācaraṇaṁ nirmmūlamiti yuktaṁ sandhyāvandanāṣṭakācaraṇādērapi nirmūlatvaprasaṅgāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

uktaṁ ca śiṣṭācārasya prāmāṇyam -  
api vā kāraṇāgrahaṇē -  
prayuktāni pratīyērann iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It has been said that the conduct of exemplary people is authoritative,246  
and also that even when they do not know the cause of their custom,  
they do know what is proper custom.

[246]: supra §14.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Pūrvamīmāṁsā I. iii. 7.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

uktaṁ ca śiṣṭācārasya prāmāṇyam api vā kāraṇāgrahaṇē prayuktāni pratīyēranniti ।  
</details>

### bhāgavata-parigrahē 'dōṣaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha bhāgavata-jana-parigr̥hītatvād iti +++(aprāmāṇyē)+++ hētuḥ,  
hanta tarhi tat-parigr̥hītatvād vājasanēyakaikāyana-śākhā-vacasāṁ pratyakṣādīnāṁ cāprāmāṇyaprasaṅgaḥ ।+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

120\. If the ground for the invalidity of Pañcaratra is that it is accepted by Bhagavatas,247 well, then the scriptural statements of the Ekayana Sakha and the Vājasaneyaka sakhas and the means of knowledge Perception, Inference etc., would also be invalid since the Bhagavatas accept those too! 

[247]: supra § 16.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

atha ... See p. 17 above, “ēvaṁ jātyā” & c.

vāsananēya ... The Ekāyanaśākhā belongs to the Śukla Yajurveda.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha bhāgavatajanaparigr̥hītatvāditi hētuḥ, hanta tarhi tatparigr̥hītatvād vājasanēyakaikāyanaśākhāvacasāṁ pratyakṣādīnāṁ cāprāmāṇyaprasaṅgaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha "tair ēva parigr̥hītatvād" iti +++(aprāmāṇyē)+++ hētuḥ  
tad-asādhāraṇānaikāntikam, asiddhañca ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This same ground, moreover, namely that Pancarãtra is invalid because it is accepted by the Bhagavatas, suffers from two defects; it is both specially-occasional and unproved.248

[248]: supra § 59.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha tairēva parigr̥hītatvāditi hētuḥ tadasādhāraṇānaikāntikam, asiddhañca ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kimiti vā tatparigrahādaprāmāṇyam? 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Why is Pañcarātra rendered invalid by their acceptance? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kimiti vā tatparigrahādaprāmāṇyam? 
</details>

#### nātraivarṇikatvāt
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

"atraivarṇikatvād" iti cēt  
kiṁ bhōḥ traivarṇikētara-savarṇa-rathakāra-niṣādādi-parigr̥hītānuṣṭhīyamānārthānām ātharvaṇavacasāṁ  
"rathakāra ādadhīta" "ētayā niṣāda-sthapatiṁ yājayēt" ity-ādi-vacasāṁ prāmāṇyaṁ nāsti ?  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If it is because they do not belong to the three estates,  
then the Atharvanic statements whose content is accepted and observed by rathakaras, nisadas and other groups  
which do not belong to the three estates  
(Statements like "The rathakara must add fuel,"  
"With [[101]] that he must sacrifice for the chief of the Nişādas,"249 etc.)  
would also be invalid.
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[249]: Quotations not identified; the groups enumerated are śūdras, and yet by Vedic injunction have to observe, i.e., to accept, the few Vedic injunctions addressed to them. Do they by their acceptance invalidate these injunctions?
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

rathakāra ... Cf. Āpastambaśrautasūtra V. 3.19.

ētayā ... Maitrāyaṇi Saṁhitā [ed. Dr. Leopold V. Schroeder] II. 2.4. The reading found is : “tayā niṣāda-stha-patiṁ yājayēt sā hi tasyēṣṭiḥ ।” For the Niṣādasthapati-nyāya see Śabara on Pūrvamīmāṁsā VI. i. 51, 52.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atraivarṇikatvāditi cēt kiṁ bhōḥ traivarṇikētarasavarṇarathakāraniṣādādiparigr̥hītānuṣṭhīyamānārthānāmātharvaṇavacasāṁ rathakāra ādadhīta ētayā niṣādasthapatiṁ yājayēt ityādivacasāṁ prāmāṇyaṁ nāsti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

astuvā'traivarṇika-parigrahō 'prāmāṇya-hētuḥ,  
ētēṣāṁ tu bhagavac-chāstrānugāmināṁ bhāgavatānām  
utkr̥ṣṭa-brāhmaṇyaṁ sarva-pramāṇa-samavagatam iti  
tat-parigrahaḥ prāmāṇyam ēva draḍhayati ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or, be it granted that the acceptance of certain rites by outcastes renders them invalid;  
yet, in view of the fact that the eminent brahminhood of these Bhagavatas  
who follow the doctrine of the Bhagavān  
is evident by all criteria of knowledge,  
their acceptance of Pañcaratra rather confirms its validity.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

For a detailed notice of the origination, transformation and philosophy of the Bhāgavata religion and its contribution to the Indian thought, see G. A. Grierson, “The Nārāyaṇīya and the Bhāgavatas”, Indian Antiquary, Vol. 37, pp. 251-262.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

astuvā'traivarṇikaparigrahō'prāmāṇyahētuḥ, ētēṣāṁ tu bhagavacchāstrānugāmināṁ bhāgavatānāmutkr̥ṣṭabrāhmaṇyaṁ sarvapramāṇasamavagatamiti tatparigrahaḥ prāmāṇyamēva draḍhayati ।  
</details>

## 17 bhāgavata-brāhmaṇya-pramāṇam

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

āha kēna punaḥ pramāṇēnaiṣāṁ brāhmaṇyamavagatam,  kēna vā'nyēṣām ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

He says: By the same means of knowledge by which the brahminhood of one set of people is evident  
the brahminhood of another set of people is evident.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

āha kēna punaḥ pramāṇēnaiṣāṁ brāhmaṇyamavagatam,  kēna vā'nyēṣām ।  
</details>

### śikhādibhiḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu cakṣur-visphāraṇa-samanantaraṁ śikhā-yajñōpavīta--pālāśa-daṇḍa--mauñjī-yujō dvija-kumārakān **paśyantō**  
"brāhmaṇā" ity **avagacchanti**।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

121\. OBJECTION. But when one sees the small sons of the twice-born who wear the customary hairtuft, sacred thread, palasa wood stick and munjagrass girdle, one knows, the moment the eyes fall on them, that they are brahmins.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nanu cakṣurvisphāraṇasamanantaraṁ śikhā -yajñōpavīta -pālāśadaṇḍa -mauñjīyujō dvijakumārakān paśyantō brāhmaṇā ityavagacchanti 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

iha vā kim ahar ahar adhīyamāna-vājasanēyakaikāyana-śākhān vilasad-upavītōttarīya-śikhā-śālinō 'dhyāpayatō yājayata pratigr̥hṇatō viduṣaḥ **paśyantō** brāhmaṇā iti nāvayanti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. And in our case, when one sees learned people who day after day study the Vajasaneyaka and Ekāyana śākhās, wear prominently their sacred threads, upper garments and hairtufts, impart teaching, sacrifice, receive priestly stipends---does one not instantly know that they are brahmins? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

iha vā kimaharaharadhīyamānavājasanēyakaikāyanaśākhān vilasadupavītōttarīyaśikhāśālinō'dhyāpayatō yājayata pratigr̥hṇatō viduṣaḥ paśyantō brāhmaṇā iti nāvayanti ।  
</details>

### yajanādibhiḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha 

> yājana-pravacana-pālāśa-daṇḍādīnāṁ duṣṭa-śūdrādiṣu vyabhicāra-saṁbhavād  
brāhmaṇya-siddhavat-kārēṇa pravr̥ttēś ca  
na tēbhyō brāhmaṇya nirṇayaḥ, 

tad-bhāgavatētara-viprāṇam api samānam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If it be held that outcastes, low-caste people etc., may also illegitimately sacrifice, teach, carry palata sticks etc. and that they behave as though they were legitimate brahmins, and that therefore neither costume nor conduct provides positive certainty that a man is a brahmin, then the same applies to other priests than Bhagavatas.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha yājana -pravacana -pālāśadaṇḍādīnāṁ duṣṭaśūdrādiṣu vyabhicārasaṁbhavād brāhmaṇyasiddhavatkārēṇa pravr̥ttēśca na tēbhyō brāhmaṇya nirṇayaḥ, tadbhāgavatētaraviprāṇamapi samānam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha saty api tēṣāṁ kvacid vyabhicārē,  
tat-sāmānyād anyatra +++(sad-bhāgavatēṣu)+++ vyabhicāra-śaṅkāyāṁ  

śuktau rajata-dhiyō vyabhicārāt,  
rajatē rajata-dhiyāṁ vyabhicāra-śaṅkāvat 
pratyakṣa-virōdhāt, anavasthānāc ca  
anupalabhyamāna-vyabhicārōdāharaṇēṣu tathātva-niścayas,  

tad+++(←rajata)+++-anyatrāpi samānam ।+++(5)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or be it granted that there are cases where people illegitimately display the marks of brahminhood;  
still, [[102]] though there may be doubt about the legitimacy of these marks in others because of their resemblance to pretenders  
(just as when there is a doubt that one may be mistaken about real silver too because one has mistaken nacre for silver),  
then there can be certainty of their being genuine brahmins  
in all cases when no misapprehension occurs,  
because otherwise doubt would conflict with Perception  
and lead to infinite regress.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha satyapi tēṣāṁ kvacidvyabhicārē  
tatsāmānyādanyatra vyabhicāraśaṅkāyāṁ śuktau rajatadhiyō vyabhicārāt rajatē rajatadhiyāṁ vyabhicāraśaṅkāvat pratyakṣavirōdhāt anavasthānācca anupalabhyamānavyabhicārōdāharaṇēṣu tathātvaniścayastadanyatrāpi samānam ।  
</details>

### gōtrataḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha matam 

> anyēṣāṁ brāhmaṇyaṁ tad-asādhāraṇa-gōtra-smaraṇād 

iti,  
tad bhāgavatānām api samānam,   
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

122\. Or if it be held that the others are genuine brahmins because they recollect those gotras which are peculiar to brahmins, the same applies to the Bhagavatas; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha matam anyēṣāṁ brāhmaṇyaṁ tadasādhāraṇagōtrasmaraṇāditi, tad bhāgavatānāmapi samānam,   
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

smaranti hi bhāgavatāḥ -  
vayaṁ bhāradvājāḥ vayaṁ kāśyapāḥ vayaṁ gautamāḥ vayamaupagavā iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for the Bhagavatas have the tradition: "We are descendants of Bharadvaja, of Kasyapa, of Gotama, of Upagava." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

smaranti hi bhāgavatāḥ -  
vayaṁ bhāradvājāḥ vayaṁ kāśyapāḥ vayaṁ gautamāḥ vayamaupagavā iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na cēdaṁ gōtrasmaraṇaṁ nirmūlaṁ sāmayikaṁ (ādhunikam) vā  
sarvagōtrasmaraṇānāṁ tathābhāvaprasaṅgāt । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor is this recollection or tradition of gotras unfounded or merely contemporary, for the same can be argued for all tradition of gotras. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cēdaṁ gōtrasmaraṇaṁ nirmūlaṁ sāmayikaṁ (ādhunikam) vā sarvagōtrasmaraṇānāṁ tathābhāvaprasaṅgāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

saṁbhāvyamāna-dōṣatvād  
vaṁśānāṁ yadi saṁśayaḥ ।  
tad-brāhmaṇyē tatō lōkaṁ  
sarvaṁ **vyākulayēd** ayam ॥ +++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If there were doubt about descent since error could conceivably occur,  
this would confuse the whole world about the authenticity of their brahminhood. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

saṁbhāvyamānadōṣatvād vaṁśānāṁ yadi saṁśayaḥ ।  
tadbrāhmaṇyē tatō lōkaṁ sarvaṁ vyākulayēdayam ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā hi ।  

jananī-jāra-sandēha-  
**jātaś** caṇḍāla-saṁśayaḥ ।  
**nirviśaṅkaḥ** kathaṁ vēdam  
**adhīṣē** sādhu sattama +++(prativādin)+++? ॥+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

After all, anyone may fear that he really is a candala  
if he suspects his mother of having had a lover;   
and how, my excellent opponent, can you be quite sure yourself that your birth entitled you to Veda-study? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ayaṁ bahu-vrīhiḥ ‘tvaṁ’ ity asya adhyāhr̥tasya viśēṣaṇam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā hi ।  

jananījārasandēhajātaścaṇḍālasaṁśayaḥ ।  
nirviśaṅkaḥ kathaṁ vēdamadhīṣē sādhu sattama? ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tēna bhāgavatānām a-vicchinna-param-parā-prāpta--vicitra-gōtra-**smaraṇa--paryavasthāpitaṁ**  
brāhmaṇyam **anapōditam āstē**  
iti na bhāgavatānām anyēṣāñca brāhmaṇyē kaścid viśēṣaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore if the brahminhood of Bhagavatas,  
which is completely established by the recollection of the various gotras  
which has been passed on in uninterrupted transmission, stands unchallenged,  
then there is no difference whatever in this  
between the brahminhood of Bhagavatas and of others.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tēna bhāgavatānāmavicchinnaparamparāprāptavicitragōtrasmaraṇaparyavasthāpitaṁ brāhmaṇyamanapōditamāstē iti na bhāgavatānāmanyēṣāñca brāhmaṇyē kaścidviśēṣaḥ ।  
</details>

### dēvatā-vivēkataḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi paraṁ 

> tē parama-puruṣam ēvāśritā ēkāntinaḥ,  
anyē kṣudra-daivatikās sādhāraṇā 

iti,  

kiṁ punar ētēṣāṁ brāhmaṇyē pramāṇam abhihitaṁ  
yad ēvānyēṣām?
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

123\. Further, if some who believe in the Supreme Person are monotheists and others who believe in [[103]] petty godlings are polytheists,  

is then the same authority stated for the brahminhood of the ones as well as of the others,
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

anyēṣāṁ brāhmaṇatvēna prasiddhānāṁ brāhmaṇya-grahaṇē yat pramāṇaṁ, tad ēva ētēṣāṁ bhāgavatānāṁ brāhmaṇya-grahaṇē pramāṇaṁ bhavatīti grantha-kr̥d-vacaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi paraṁ tē paramapuruṣamēvāśritā ēkāntinaḥ, anyē kṣudradaivatikāssādhāraṇā iti,
kiṁ punarētēṣāṁ brāhmaṇyē pramāṇamabhihitaṁ yadēvānyēṣām,
</details>

<details><summary>rāmamiśraśāstrī</summary>

tāṁstu bhagavānēva - 

> tē'pi māmēva kauntēya  
> yajanty avidhipūrvakam 

iti vinininda ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kēna vā tēṣāṁ brāhmaṇyam avagatam  
kin na ētēna,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

or how else is their brahminhood known  
if not by that same authority? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

asmākam ētēna vivādēna kō lābhaḥ? tathāpi śrūyatām ity āha ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kēna vā tēṣāṁ brāhmaṇyamavagatam kinna ētēna,
</details>

<details><summary>rāmamiśraśāstrī</summary>

na kēvalaṁ mamaiva brāhmaṇya-nirupaṇa-bhāra  
āvayōr ubhayōr ēva  
tasya nirūpaṇīyatvēna samatvād iti bhāvaḥ ।  
</details>

### nirṇaya-prakāraḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi ca kautūhalam -  

śrūyatām ubhayatrāpi  
brāhmaṇyasyāvadhārakam ।  
pratyakṣaṁ vā'numānaṁ vā  
yad vā'rthāpattir ēva vā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If this is the question, then listen:  
there remains a criterion to determine brahminhood in either case,  
either Perception, or Inference, or Circumstantial-Implication.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi ca kautūhalam -  

śrūyatāmubhayatrāpi brāhmaṇyasyāvadhārakam ।  
pratyakṣaṁ vā'numānaṁ vā yadvā'rthāpattirēva vā ॥
</details>

#### pratyakṣē śaṅkā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu kathaṁ pratyakṣaṁ brāhmaṇyamavagamayati,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> 124\. OBJECTION. But how can Perception convey that they are brahmins? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> nanu kathaṁ pratyakṣaṁ brāhmaṇyamavagamayati,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na hi prathamākṣa-sannipāta-samanantaram  
a-dr̥ṣṭa-pūrva-vipra-kṣatra-samāna-vayō-vēṣa- piṇḍa-dvaya-sannidhāv  
aja-gaja-mahiṣādi-viśēṣavad  
"ayaṁ brāhmaṇaḥ", "ayaṁ kṣatriya"  
iti vibhāgēna pratipadyāmahē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> For when we are close to two individuals whom we have not seen before, one a brahmin, the other a ksatriya, of the same age and the same appearance, we do not immediately observe the distinction that one is a brahmin and the other a ksatriya in the same way as we instantly observe the differentness of a goat, an elephant, a buffalo etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> na hi prathamākṣasannipātasamanantaramadr̥ṣṭapūrvavipra -kṣatrasamānavayōvēṣapiṇḍadvayasannidhāvajagajamahiṣādiviśēṣavad ayaṁ brāhmaṇaḥ ayaṁ kṣatriya iti vibhāgēna pratipadyāmahē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na ca  
> 
> > tat-pitrādi-brāhmaṇya-smaraṇa-sāpēkṣam akṣam ēva  
sannihita-vyakti-varti brāhmaṇyam avagamayati
> 
> iti sāmpratam,  
tat-smaraṇasyaiva  
+++(tat-pitr̥-)+++pūrvānubhava-virahēṇa vandhyā-suta-smaraṇavad anupapattēḥ ।  
+++(pūrvānubhava-sāhityē 'py anavasthā-dōṣēṇānupapattēḥ। )+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Nor is it proper to maintain that  
>
> > the visual sense conveys the brahminhood of a nearby individual  
in dependence on our recollection of his father's brahminhood etc.;  
for that recollection itself is impossible without a previous immediate cognition,  
just as the recollection of the son of a sterile mother is impossible. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca tatpitrādibrāhmaṇyasmaraṇasāpēkṣamakṣamēva sannihitavyaktivarti brāhmaṇyamavagamayatīti sāmpratam,  tatsmaraṇasyaiva pūrvānubhavavirahēṇa bandhyāsutasmaraṇavadanupapattēḥ ।  
</details>

#### anumānē śaṅkā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na cānumānāt -  
tat-pratibaddha-liṅgādarśanāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Nor can we know from Inference that a man is a brahmin,  
for we do not find a concomitant mark. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cānumānāttatpratibaddhaliṅgādarśanāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na ca śama-dama-tapaś-śaucādayō brāhmaṇyē liṅgam,   
tēṣāṁ brāhmaṇēna satā saṁpādyatvād, vyabhicārāc ca ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And such qualities as tranquillity, self-restraint, austerity, purity etc., cannot be taken as marks of brahminhood, because they are available only in the case of a good brahmin and because they are not exclusively confined to brahmins. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca śama dama tapaśśaucādayō brāhmaṇyē liṅgam,  tēṣāṁ brāhmaṇēna satā saṁpādyatvād vyabhicārācca ।  
</details>

#### arthāpattau śaṅkā

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na cārthāpratyā brāhmaṇya-nirṇayaḥ, anupapatty-abhāvāt, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Nor can Circumstantial-Implication furnish proof of brahminhood,  
because it is not lacking in reason 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cārthāpratyā brāhmaṇyanirṇayaḥ, anupapattyabhāvāt, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> > na ca vasantē brāhmaṇō'gnīn ādadhīta 
>
> ity-ādi-vākyārthānupapattyā brāhmaṇyanirṇayaḥ, brāhmaṇyādipadārthāvagamapūrvakatvāt tadvākyārthāvagamasya, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> [[104]]  
and the fact that the sentence-meaning of the statement, 
> 
> > "In spring the brahmin must add fuel to the fire," 250
>
> is otherwise unestablished  
does not therefore by Circumstantial-Implication  
furnish proof that a man is a brahmin;  
for knowledge of that sentencemeaning presupposes knowledge of the word-meaning of brahminhood etc.

[250]: not identified.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Taittirīya Brāhmaṇa I.1.2.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca vasantē brāhmaṇō'gnīnādadhīta ityādivākyārthānupapattyā brāhmaṇyanirṇayaḥ, brāhmaṇyādipadārthāvagamapūrvakatvāt tadvākyārthāvagamasya, 
</details>

#### pratyakṣam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nāyaṁ dōṣaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

125\. REFUTATION. All this does not make for a defect in my argument. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāyaṁ dōṣaḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hi 

> prathamākṣa-saṁprayōgasamaya ēva bhāsamānaṁ pratyakṣaṁ  
nānyad 

ity asti niyamaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

There is no invariable rule that  
Perception becomes manifest only at the first contact between sense and object and not otherwise. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi prathamākṣasaṁprayōgasamaya ēva bhāsamānaṁ pratyakṣaṁ nānyadityasti niyamaḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad ēvēndriya-vyāpārānuvr̥ttau satyām  
a-parōkṣam avabhāsatē  
tat pratyakṣaṁ  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Perception is that which illumines the unmanifest  
while there is continuity of the operation of the senses.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadēvēndriyavyāpārānuvr̥ttau satyāmaparōkṣamavabhāsatē tatpratyakṣaṁ 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ca brāhmaṇyam iti - tad api pratyakṣam,  +++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Thus there can be Perception of brahminhood; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ca brāhmaṇyamiti tadapi pratyakṣam,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

pratīmō hi vayam unmīlita-lōcanāḥ  
tat-santati-viśēṣānusaṁdhāna-samanantaraṁ  
vasiṣṭha-kāśyapīya--śaṭha-marṣaṇa--prabhr̥ti- vicitra-gōtra-kula-śāliṣu samācāra-śuciṣu  
vilasad-upavītōttarīya-śikhā-mauñjī-bandhēṣu  
sphuṭatara-sandadhad-brāhmaṇyam । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for when we keep our eyes open we note,  
immediately upon observing the particular differentiae of the genus brahminhood,  
that the brahminhood is quite clearly noticeable in those who belong to the families of the different gotras-Vasistha, Kasyapiya Sathamarṣaṇa etc.--,  
who are pure in their conduct,  
and who display the sacred thread, upper cloth, hairtuft and munja grass girdle. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pratīmō hi vayamunmīlitalōcanāḥ tatsantativiśēṣānusaṁdhānasamanantaraṁ vasiṣṭha-kāśyapīya -śaṭhamarṣaṇaprabhr̥tivicitragōtrakulaśāliṣu samācāraśuciṣu vilasadupavītōttarīyaśikhāmauñjībandhēṣu sphuṭatarasaṁdadhad brāhmaṇyam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na caitad a-laukikaṁ  
yat "santati-viśēṣānusaṁdhāna-sāpēkṣam akṣaṁ  
brāhmaṇyaṁ grāhayatī"ti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Nor does it run counter to ordinary experience that the eyes can convey brahminhood in dependence on the observation of the peculiarities of genus. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na caitadalaukikaṁ yatsantativiśēṣānusaṁdhānasāpēkṣamakṣaṁ brāhmaṇyaṁ grāhayatīti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sarvatra dēśa-kāla-saṁsthānādītikartavyatā'nugr̥hītam ēvēndriyaṁ  
sva-gōcara-paricchēdōtpādē kāraṇam bhavati। +++(5)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In every case the sense becomes the cause of the rise of determination of sense-object when favoured by the accompanying circumstances of place, time, configuration etc.251

[251]: read deśakālasaṃsthānāditi.[[??]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

sarvatra ... Cf. Ślokavārtika under I.1.5, śl. 26 (vanavāda) :

> tasyōpalakṣaṇaṁ cāpi kvacit kēnacid iṣyatē ।  
rūpādīnāṁ viśēṣēṇa dēśa-kālādy-apēkṣayā ॥

paricchēdaḥ = jñānaṁ, nirṇayō vā ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sarvatra dēśakālasaṁsthānādītikarttavyatānugr̥hītamēvēndriyaṁ svagōcaraparicchēdōtpādē kāraṇambhavati ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

karaṇa-mātrasyāyaṁ svabhāvō yad itikarttavyatāpēkṣaṇam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It is the natural function of the sense-organ as such to relate itself to these accompanying circumstances. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

karaṇa-mātram = karaṇa-sāmānyam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

karaṇamātrasyāyaṁ svabhāvō yaditikarttavyatāpēkṣaṇam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā ''ha -  

> na hi tat +++(jñāna-)+++kāraṇaṁ lōkē  
vēdē vā kiñcid īdr̥śam ।  
iti-kartavyatā-sādhyē  
yasya nānugrahē'rthitā ॥ 

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

As the author says: 

> "No organ of knowledge, whether in Veda or in ordinary process,  
becomes efficacious in determining the object  
that is to be realized through the accompanying circumstances  
unless it is favoured by these circumstances.252

[252]: not identified.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Ślokavārtika (Sambandhākṣepavāda) under I.i.5.śl. 37.

‘iti-kartavyatā-sādhyē’ aṅgādhīnē; ‘anugrahē’ upakārē; ‘arthitā’ sāpēkṣatā iti bhāvaḥ ।

Cf. Nyāyaratnākara (Chowkhamba edn.) on the above verse p.507:

> sarvatra cakṣurādau pradīpādy-arthitva-darśanād aikāntikaṁ sahāyāpēkṣaṇaṁ nāśaktim āpādayati । prastuta iti-kartavya-tayaiva karaṇatvaṁ, tad-abhāva ēva tasya sidhyati ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā ''ha -  
na hi tatkāraṇaṁ lōkē vēdē vā kiñcidīdr̥śam ।  
itikartavyatāsādhyē yasya nānugrahē'rthitā ॥ iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tataś ca santati-smr̥tyā  
**'nugr̥hītēna** cakṣuṣā ।  
**vijñāyamānaṁ** brāhmaṇyaṁ  
pratyakṣatvaṁ **na muñcati** ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[105]]  
Consequently the visual sense, when favoured by the recollection of genus,  
gives knowledge of brahminhood  
without the object giving up its perceptuality. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Veṅkaṭanātha quotes this and the following verse in his Nyāyasiddhāñjana V. p. 267.

Cf. Prakaraṇapañcikā III. p. 17:

> jātir āśrayatō bhinnā pratyakṣa-jñāna-gōcarā ।  
pūrvākārāvamarśēna prabhākara-gurōr matā ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tataśca santatismr̥tyānugr̥hītēna cakṣuṣā ।  
vijñāyamānaṁ brāhmaṇyaṁ pratyakṣatvaṁ na muñcati ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ca dr̥śyatē nānā  
sahakāri-vyapēkṣayā ।  
cakṣuṣō jāti-vijñāna-  
karaṇatvaṁ yathōditam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

So it is evident that the visual sense can be the instrument of knowledge of genus in dependence on a variety of accompanying factors. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ślōka-vārtika iti bhāvaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ca dr̥śyatē nānā sahakārivyapēkṣayā ।  
cakṣuṣōjātivijñānakaraṇatvaṁ yathōditam ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

suvarṇaṁ vyajyatē rūpāt  
tāmratvādēr asaṁśayam ।  
tailād ghr̥taṁ vilīnañ ca  
gandhēna tu rasēna vā ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Gold becomes manifest through its colour fromcopper etc., gheeis differentiated from oil, through its smell and taste; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

suvarṇaṁ vyajyatē rūpāt tāmratvādērasaṁśayam ।  
tailād ghr̥taṁ vilīnañca gandhēna tu rasēna vā ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

bhasma-pracchāditō vahniḥ  
sparśanēnōpalabhyatē ।  
aśvatvādau ca dūrasthē  
niścayō jāyatē dhvanēḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

fire, which is hidden by ashes, perceived through touching the ashes.

Sound may provide us with proof that there is a horse in the distance; 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Ślokavārtika (Vākyādhikaraṇa) śl. 358, p. 947:

> paśyataḥ śvētimārūpaṁ hēṣā-śabdaṁ ca śr̥ṇvataḥ ।  
khura-nikṣēpa-śabdaṁ ca śvētō 'śvō dhāvatīti dhīḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

bhasmapracchāditō vahniḥ sparśanēnōpalabhyatē ।  
aśvatvādau ca dūrasthē niścayō jāyatē dhvanēḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

saṁsthānēna ghaṭatvādi  
brāhmaṇatvādi yōnitaḥ ।  
kvacid ācārataś cāpi  
samyag rājyānupālitāt ॥ +++(4)+++

iti ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

a pitcher etc. are known through their configuration; brahminhood through descent, and also through conduct in certain particulars, which is completely protected by the king.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide ibid (Vanavāda) I. i.5, śls. 27 & 29.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

saṁsthānēna ghaṭatvādi brāhmaṇatvādiyōnitaḥ ।  
kvacidācārataścāpi samyagrājyānupālitāt ॥

iti ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yat samāna-vayō-vēṣa-  
piṇḍa-dvaya--**vilōkanē** ।  
tat-kṣaṇād akṣatō bhēdō  
**nāvabhātīti** bhāṣitam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It has been contended that when we see two individuals of the same age and appearance, the difference between the two does not immediately appear to eye;  
but the perceptuality of their differentness is not refuted by just this.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yatsamānavayōvēṣapiṇḍadvayavilōkanē ।  
tatkṣaṇādakṣatō bhēdō nāvabhātīti bhāṣitam ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**naitāvatā** vibhāgasya  
pratyakṣatvaṁ **nivartatē** ।  
sādr̥śya-dōṣāt tatra syād  
vibhāgasyānavagrahaḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In this case the non-perception of their differentness is caused by the defect of similarity. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

vibhāgō bhēdaḥ, viśēṣō vā ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

naitāvatā vibhāgasya pratyakṣatvaṁ nivartatē ।  
sādr̥śyadōṣāttatra syād vibhāgasyānavagrahaḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

samāna-rūpa-saṁsthāna-  
śuktikā--kala-dhautayōḥ ।  
vivēkaḥ sahasā nābhād  
iti kālāntarē'pi kim ॥  
pratyakṣō na bhavēd ēvaṁ  
vipra-kṣatra-viśāṁ bhidā ।  +++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The difference between nacre and silver, which are similar in appearance and configuration, may not be immediately visible, yet that does not mean that their difference is not visible at another time; and the same holds for the difference between brahmin, kṣatriya and vaisya. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

samānarūpasaṁsthānaśuktikā-kaladhautayōḥ ।  
vivēkaḥ sahasā nābhāditi kālāntarē'pi kim ॥
pratyakṣō na bhavēdēvaṁ viprakṣatraviśāṁ bhidā ।  
</details>

### santati-kāryatvam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadvā saṁtati-viśēṣa-prabhavatvam ēva brāhmaṇyam,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or else, brahminhood is that which arises from the differentiae of genus, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Prakaraṇapañcikā, III, p. 31:

> tēna santati-viśēṣa-prabhavatvam ēva brāhmaṇa-śabda-pravr̥ttāv upādhiḥ । tat-prabhavānām ēva karmasv adhikāra iti na kiñcid avahīnam । kē punas tē santati-viśēṣāḥ? na tē parigaṇayya nirdēṣṭuṁ śakyantē; kintu lōkata ēva prasiddhāḥ pratyētavyāḥ । tathā ca taj-janyatvē 'vagatē brāhmaṇa-śabdaṁ prayuñjatē lōkāḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadvā saṁtativiśēṣaprabhavatvamēva brāhmaṇyam,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tac cānvaya-vyatirēkābhyāṁ  
yathā''lōkaṁ kāryāntaravad avagantavyam ēva, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and such a product can empirically be known just like any other product  
by a process of positive and negative consideration, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

kapāla-dvaya-yōga ēva ghaṭōtpattiḥ; nō cēt । ēvaṁ, ētādr̥śa-pitr̥-mātr̥-kāraṇatva ēva brāhmaṇatvaṁ, na tv anyathā iti bhāvaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

taccānvayavyatirēkābhyāṁ yathālōkaṁ kāryāntaravadavagantavyamēva, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

+++(yathā)+++  

> kē punaḥ santi viśēṣā,  
yēṣu brāhmaṇa-śabdaṁ prayuñjatē vr̥ddhāḥ?  
kēṣu vā prayuñjatē?  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

e.g. "what are the specific characteristics to which the elders apply the term brahminhood, or to which ~~characteristics~~ is the term applied?" 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kē punaḥ santi viśēṣā yēṣu brāhmaṇaśabdaṁ prayuñjatē vr̥ddhāḥ kēṣu vā prayuñjatē, ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**uktaṁ** gōtrārṣēyādi-  
smr̥timatsv ity anēkaśaḥ ।  
āstām a-prastutā cintā  
prācī **prastūyatē** kathā ॥  
siddhaṁ gōtrādi-yuktatvād  
viprā bhāgavatā iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[106]]  
It has been said often that it applies to those who possess recollection of gotra, Vedic ancestry etc.; let us not start discussing this question again, or we must repeat our old argument:  

it is established that the Bhagavatas are brahmins, because they possess gotra etc.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

uktaṁ gōtrārṣēyādismr̥timatsvityanēkaśaḥ ।  
āstāmaprastutā cintā prācī prastūyatē kathā ॥  
siddhaṁ gōtrādiyuktatvād viprā bhāgavatā iti ।  
</details>

### vaiśya-vrātya-mūlaṁ na
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vaiśyavrātyānvayē janma  
yad ēṣām upavarṇitam ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

126\. The objection that was made that the Bhāgavatas are born from a vaiśya vratya: 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See p. 13 above, for the pūrvapakṣa view.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vaiśyavrātyānvayē janma yadēṣāmupavarṇitam ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> pañcamas sāttvatō nāma  
viṣṇōr āyatanāni saḥ ।  
pūjayēd ājñayā rājñaḥ  
sa tu bhāgavataḥ smr̥taḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

([253]: supra § 15. [[143]]  )

> "The fifth one, the Sarvata, must worship the sanctuaries of Visnu by royal decree;" 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

pañcamassāttvatō nāma viṣṇōrāyatanāni saḥ ।  
pūjayēdājñayā rājñaḥ sa tu bhāgavataḥ smr̥taḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> vaiśyāt tu jāyatē vrātyād  

iti vākyadvayēkṣaṇāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and 

> "he is also called a Bhagavata; he is born from a vaisya vratya." 

\- On the authority of the two statements.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Manusmṛti X. 23:

> vaiśyāt tu jāyatē vrātyāt sudhanvā ''cārya ēva ca ।  
bhāruṣaś ca nijaṅghaś ca maitras sātvata ēva ca ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vaiśyāttu jāyatē vrātyāditi vākyadvayēkṣaṇāt ।  
</details>

#### prayōgāntarāṇi
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atra brūmaḥ kim ētābhyāṁ  
vacanābhyāṁ pratīyatē ॥  
abhidhānānvayō vā syān  
niyamō vā'bhidhīyatām ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

To this we reply:  
precisely what do we learn from these two statements?  
Is there a simple connection of names,  
or must an invariable rule be stated ?

[254]: ie., is the same name used for several groups or only one? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atra brūmaḥ kimētābhyāṁ vacanābhyāṁ pratīyatē ॥  
abhidhānānvayō vā syānniyamō vā'bhidhīyatām ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na tāvat 

> "sāttvata-bhāgavata-śabdau vaiśya-vrātyābhidhāyakāv ēva"

iti niyantuṁ śakyau - apratītēḥ, atiprasaṅgācca, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In It is impossible to make it a rule that the words Bhagavata and Satvata denote a vaiśya vratya, for that is not known from the text, and it involves overextension. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na tāvat sāttvata-bhāgavata-śabdau vaiśyavrātyābhidhāyakāvēvēti niyantuṁ śakyau apratītēḥ, atiprasaṅgācca, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hi "pañcamaḥ sāttvata" ityatra  
sāttvata-bhāgavata-śabdayōr arthāntarābhidhāna-pratiṣēdhaḥ pratīyatē -  
śruta-hāny--aśruta-kalpanā-prasaṅgāt। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the statement, "the fifth one, Satvata," we do not find a denial that the words Bhagavata and Satvata denote other meanings, for that would mean ignoring the explicit and inventing the unstated. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi "pañcamaḥ sāttvata" ityatra  
sāttvatabhāgavataśabdayōrarthāntarābhidhānapratiṣēdhaḥ pratīyatē   
śrutahānyaśrutakalpanāprasaṅgāt। 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

iha hi vrātya-vaiśyānvaya-janmā yaḥ pañcamaḥ  
sāttvata iti tasya sāttvata-saṁjñānvayō 'vagamyatē  
pañcama-śabdasya prathama-nirdiṣṭatvēnōddēśakatvāt।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In our statement the fifth one,  
who is born from an vaisya vratya,  
is understood to bear the name of Satvata:  
"The fifth one, Sarvata...", since the word 'fifth' is the operative term as it is mentioned first. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

iha hi vrātyavaiśyānvayajanmā yaḥ pañcamaḥ sāttvata iti tasya sāttvatasaṁjñānvayō'vagamyatē pañcama śabdasya prathama nirdiṣṭatvēnōddēśakatvāt (uddēśyasamarthakr̥tvādityarthaḥ)।  
</details>

<details><summary>rāmamiśraśāstrī</summary>

uddēśyasamarthakr̥tvādityarthaḥ
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na ca pañcamasya sāttvatatvē  
sāttvatēnāpi vaiśya-vrātya-pañcamēna bhavitavyam,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And if the fifth is the Satvata,  
the Satvata is not necessarily also be the fifth, namely the vaiśya vratya. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca pañcamasya sāttvatatvē sāttvatēnāpi vaiśyavrātyapañcamēna bhavitavyam,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hi uddiśyamānasyāgnimattvē  
upādīyamānasyāgnēr dhūmavattvēna bhavitavyam  
+++(ayōgalō'pi syāt tatra)+++  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For when the stated subject (e.g. a mountain) is possessed of fire,  
the predicated fire does not necessarily possess smoke.255 

255. The argument is: if S is P, then P is not therefore S.

The example is 'parvato 'gnimin dhumavattvāt if we interchange S and P, we get parvato dhumavin agnimattvåt, but this is not true, for though there is no fireless smoke, there is smokeless fire. Similarly here: the fifth may be a sitvata or a vaidya vratya, but being the fifth does not make the sitvata a vaidya vratya, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

‘uddiśyamānasya’ dhūmavata ity arthaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi uddiśyamānasyāgnimattvē upādīyamānasyāgnēr dhūmavattvēna bhavitavyam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atō nēdr̥śa-smr̥ti-paryālōcanayā sāttvata-bhāgavata-śābditānāṁ vrātyatva-niścayaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Consequently the consideration if a smrti statement of this kind cannot give certainty that the words Satvata, Bhagavata etc mean vratya.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atō nēdr̥śa-smr̥ti-paryālōcanayā sāttvata-bhāgavata-śābditānāṁ vrātyatva-niścayaḥ ।  
</details>

#### ācārya-śabdādau vyabhicāraḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi punar 

> anayōr jāty-antarē 'pi prayōgō dr̥ṣṭa 

iti +ētāvatā tac-chabdābhidhēyatayā bhagavac-chāstrānugāminām api viprāṇāṁ taj-jātīyatva-niścayaḥ,  
tatas tatraiva saha-paṭhitācārya-śabdasyāpi nikr̥ṣṭa-vrātyāpatyē prayōga-darśanāt  
sāṅga-sa-rahasya-vēda--dātur dvija-parasyāpi vrātyatvaṁ syāt । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

127\. If it be argued that since these two words also may denote another caste (namely of the vaisya vratyas),  
then the mere fact that certain brahmins are denoted by these words proves that these brahmins belong to that caste,  
even though they follow the doctrine of the Bbagavan,  
it would also follow that, since we find the collocated word acaryas256 also used to denote the issue of a lowly vaisya,  
therefore an eminent brahmin who is an acarya imparting teaching of the Veda with its ancillae and its esoteric teachings is thereby denoted as being a vaisya vratya! 

[256]: In the Manu quotation supra § 15.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yadi ... This paragraph is in elucidation of the word “atiprasaṅgācca” used in the para “na tāvat” etc. above.

sahapaṭhitācārya ... The term ‘ācārya’ is from the Manusmṛti X. 23a:

> vaiśyāt tu jāyatē vrātyāt sudhanvā ''cārya ēva ca ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi punaranayōrjātyantarē'pi prayōgō dr̥ṣṭa iti ētāvatā tacchabdābhidhēyatayā bhagavacchāstrānugāmināmapi viprāṇāṁ tajjātīyatvaniścayaḥ, 
tatastatraiva sahapaṭhitācāryaśabdasyāpi nikr̥ṣṭavrātyāpatyē prayōgadarśanāt sāṅgasarahasyavēdadāturdvijaparasyāpi vrātyatvaṁ syāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha 

> > tasya vrātya-vācakācārya-śabdābhidhēyatvē'pi  
pramāṇāntarēṇāpluta-brāhmaṇya-niścayāt  
ācārya-śabdasya 
> 
> > ācinōty asya buddhim 
> 
> ity-ādi-guṇa-yōgēnāpi vr̥tti-saṁbhavān  
na vrātyatva-śaṅkā।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If, on the other hand, even though a true brahmin is denoted by the word ācārya which dea vratya, there still can be no suspicion that he actually is a vratya, because there is positive certainty of his brabminhood which is clearly proved by other means of knowledge, and because it is possible that the word acarya is used figuratively (ācārya as one who "accumulates"— acinoti the pupil's knowledge) for a Brahmin teacher, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Nirukta (Ānandāśrama Series 88) I. ii. 4, p. 36:

> ācāraṁ grāhayaty ācinōty arthān, ācinōti buddhim iti vā ।

Also Cf. Vihagendrasaṁhitā (ms.):

> ācinōti parān sarvān ācārayati sarvataḥ ।  
ācarēty api tān lōkān sa tu ācārya ucyatē ॥ [XXII. 14]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha tasya vrātyavācakācārya-śabdābhidhēyatvē'pi pramāṇāntarēṇāplutabrāhmaṇyaniścayāt  
ācārya-śabdasya ācinōtyasya buddhim ityādiguṇayōgēnāpi vr̥ttisaṁbhavānna vrātyatvaśaṅkā।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad atrāpi  
jāty-antara-vācaka--sāttvata-bhāgavata --śabdābhidhēyatvē'pi  
bhagavac-chāstrānugāminām amīṣām atispaṣṭa-viśiṣṭa-gōtrārṣēyādi-smaraṇa- dr̥ḍhāvagatatvād  
brāhmaṇyasya sāttvata-bhāgavata-śabdayōś ca  
sattvavati bhagavati bhakti-yōgēnaiva vr̥tti-sambhavān  
na vrātyatva-śaṅkā'vatāraḥ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

then in our case, too, the same argument can be made, namely thus: even though they are denoted by the terms Satvata and Bhagavata, which denote another caste, yet there can rise no suspicion that they actually are vratyas, because the brahminhood of these followers of the Bhagavan's doctrine is firmly known from the recollection of completely obvious clans, Vedic ancestry etc., and because it is possible that the terms Sātvata and Bhāgavata have a figurative denotation of sattva-vat and bhaga-vat.

(257, explained below, § 130.)
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad atrāpi jātyantaravācakasāttvata-bhāgavata -śabdābhidhēyatvē'pi bhagavacchāstrānugāmināmamīṣāmatispaṣṭaviśiṣṭagōtrārṣēyādismaraṇadr̥ḍhāvagatatvād brāhmaṇyasya sāttvata-bhāgavata-śabdayōśca sattvavati bhagavati bhaktiyōgēnaiva vr̥ttisambhavānna vrātyatvaśaṅkāvatāraḥ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ētad uktaṁ bhavati ।  

na caika-śabda-vācyatvād  
ēka-jātīyatā bhavēt ।  
mā bhūd ācārya-śabdatvād  
brāhmaṇasya nikr̥ṣṭatā । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In other words, 

the fact that the same word denotes both classes of people  
does not mean that therefore both belong to one and the same caste,  
lest the true brahmin be not made into a low-caste man because he is also denoted by the word AchArya.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

“śabdyatvāt” would have been a better reading. But no text preserves this reading. As it stands now, the term “ācāryaśabdatvāt” has to be explained as a Bahuvrīhi compound, qualifying the term “Brāhmaṇa”.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ētaduktaṁ bhavati ।  
na caikaśabdavācyatvādēkajātīyatā bhavēt ।  
mā bhūdācāryaśabdatvād brāhmaṇasya nikr̥ṣṭatā ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ca 'hari'-śabdasya  
dr̥ṣṭā maṇḍūkavācitā ।  
iti tac-chabda-vācyatvāt  
siṁhō maṇḍūka ēva kim ॥  
tathā gō-śabda-vācyatvāc  
chabdaś cāpi viṣāṇavān । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

We find that the word hari also means 'frog.' Does it follow that a lion is a frog because both are denoted by the same word? Then word itself would be horned, since 'word' is denoted by gau !" 

([259]: gauḥ can mean 'cow' and 'word." )
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This and the two succeeding lines are quoted by Sudarśanasūri in his commentary on Śrībhāṣya, I.i.1, Vol. I, p. 153.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ca 'hari'-śabdasya dr̥ṣṭā maṇḍūkavācitā ।  
iti tacchabdavācyatvāt siṁhō maṇḍūka ēva kim ॥  
tathā gō-śabdavācyatvācchabdaścāpi viṣāṇavān ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tataśca -  

sudhanvācārya ityādyā  
yathā'rthāntaravācakāḥ ।  
vrātyānvayē prayujyantē  
tathaivaitau +++(sāttvata-bhāgavatau)+++ bhaviṣyataḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Consequently, just as the words sudhanvan, ācārya etc., which denote more than one meaning, are also used for someone born from a vaiśya vratya, so also the words Bhagavata and Satvata.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

sudhanvā''cārya ... Manusmṛti X. 23a: “vaiśyāt tu jāyatē vrātyāt” etc.

yathā ... sudhanvādi-śabdā yathā arthāntara-vācakā, ēvaṁ sāttvata-bhāgavata-śabdāv apīti yōjanā । ‘yathārthāntara-vācakā’ iti na samastaṁ padam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tataśca -  

sudhanvācārya ityādyā yathā'rthāntaravācakāḥ ।  
vrātyānvayē prayujyantē tathaivaitau bhaviṣyataḥ ॥
</details>

#### avayava-rūḍhiḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad uktaṁ 

> yōga-rūḍhi-śakti-dvayōpanipātē  
sāttvata-bhāgavata-śabdayō rūḍhi-śaktir ēvāśrayitum ucitā

iti ,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

128. The contention that when the conventional meaning and the etymological meaning of a word collide, it is right to assume the conventional meaning of the term, in this case of the terms Bhagavata and Satvata, 

[260]: supra §15.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See “rūḍhyā” etc., p. 12 above.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yaduktaṁ yōgarūḍhiśaktidvayōpanipātē sāttvata-bhāgavata-śabdayō rūḍhiśaktirēvāśrayitumucitēti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad a-yuktaṁ -  
kl̥ptāvayava-śaktyaivābhidhānōpapattau satyām  
a-kl̥ptākhaṇḍa-śakti-kalpanā'nupapattēḥ +++(vakṣyamāṇa-rītyā)+++।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

is not correct;  
for when a denotation is appropriate  
which is the composite of the denotations of the component elements of the words,  
then it is not right to assume a non-composite denotation.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

avayava-śaktiḥ = yōga-śaktiḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadayuktaṁ kl̥ptāvayavaśaktyaivābhidhānōpapattau satyāmakl̥ptākhaṇḍaśaktikalpanā'nupapattēḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yō'pi hi  
sāttvata-bhāgavata-śabdayōr vaiśya-vrātyānvaya-janmani rūḍhi-śaktim abhyupagacchati  

abhyupagacchaty ēva +asāv anyatra  
sattvavad-bhagavac-chabdayōḥ prakr̥ti-bhūtayōs  
tad-utpannasya ca taddhita-pratyayasyārthāntarābhidhāna-sāmarthyam 

> sāttvataṁ vidhim āsthāya,  
janmāntara-kr̥taiḥ puṇyair  
narō bhāgavatō bhavēd 

ity-ādau। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For he who theorizes that the words satvata and bhagavata have their conventional meaning  
in denoting someone born from a vaisya vratya,  
must also theorize that the words sattvavat and bhagarut, which are the stem and the taddhita suffix built on the stem,261 have a different meaning in a sentence like, "having observed the satvata rules, a man becomes a Bhagavata because of the merits he has won in a previous existence." 262

[261]: taddhita suffix, cf. Panini.

[262]: "conventionally the two words are synonymous, 'etymologically' they have different meanings.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

sattvavad ... Parāśarabhaṭṭa in his ‘Viṣṇusahasranāmabhāṣya’ gives the following explanations for the term ‘sāttvata’ identifying the latter with ‘mahābhāgavata’ [ See Introduction to Jayākhya Saṁhitā ]

(i) sat brahma, sattvaṁ vā, tadvantaḥ sāttvantaḥ; brahma-vidhāḥ sāttvikā vā; tēṣām idaṁ karma śāstraṁ vā sāttvatam, tat-kurvāṇāḥ, tad-ācakṣaṇāś ca vā ।

(ii) sātayati sukhayaty āśritān iti sāt paramātmā; sa ētēṣām astīti vā sāttvatāḥ । sāttvatō vā mahā-bhāgavataḥ ।

The Mahābhārata, Āśvamedhikaparvan [Vavilla edn., Vol. XVIII] ch. 124, śls. 33-37 speaks in favour of the brahmanical status of the Bhāgavatas:

> apārthakaṁ prabhāṣantē śūdrā bhāgavatā iti ।  
na śūdrā bhagavad-bhaktā viprā bhāgavatāḥ smr̥tāḥ ॥  
sarva-varṇēṣu tē śūdrā yē hy abhaktāḥ janārdanē ।  
dvādaśākṣara-tattva-jñaḥ catur-vēda-vibhāgavit ॥  
acchidra-pañca-kāla-jñaḥ sa vai bhāgavataḥ smr̥taḥ ।  
r̥g-vēdēnaiva hōtā ca yajuṣā 'dhvaryur ēva ca ॥  
sāma-vēdēna cōdgātā puṇyēnābhiṣṭuvanti mām ।  
atharva-śirasā caiva nityam ātharvaṇā dvi-jāḥ ॥  
stuvanti satataṁ yē māṁ tē vai bhāgavatāḥ smr̥tāḥ ॥

taddhita ... amum ēva pratyayaṁ ‘aṇ’ iti svayam ēva nirdiśati ।

sāttvataṁ ... Mahābhārata, Bhīṣma, ch. 62. śl. 39b.

janmāntara ... Paramasaṁhitā, III. 38b.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yō'pi hi sāttvata-bhāgavataśabdayōrvaiśyavrātyānvayajanmani rūḍhiśaktimabhyupagacchati abhyupagacchatyēva asāvanyatra sattvavadbhagavacchabdayōḥ prakr̥tibhūtayōstadutpannasya ca taddhitapratyayasyārthāntarābhidhānasāmarthyaṁ sāttvataṁ vidhimāsthāya, janmāntarakr̥taiḥ puṇyairnarō bhāgavatō bhavēdityādau 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad ihāpi +++(pūrvēkta-taddhitānta←)+++tad-yōgēnaiva  
vrātyānvaya-janmani +++(prayōga=)+++vr̥tti-sambhavēna  
śakty-antara-kalpanāyāṁ pramāṇaṁ kramatē। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This goes to prove the assumption that  
in this case the word may have a double meaning by etymology alone,  
because it is possible for it to be used in the sense of "issue of a vaisya vratya." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadihāpi tadyōgēnaiva vrātyānvayajanmani vr̥ttisambhavēna śaktyantarakalpanāyāṁ pramāṇaṁ kramatē, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

saṁbhavati caitēṣām api sākṣād-bhagavad-ārādhanābhāvē 'pi  
vāsudēvasyāyatanaśōdhana-balinirharaṇa-- pratimā-saṁrakṣaṇādi-kriyā-yōgēnaiva  
sāttvata-bhāgavata-śabdābhidhēyatvam,  
tasyēdam iti saṁbandha-mātrē'pi cāṇ-pratyaya-smaraṇāt। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And it is possible that those vratyas too, despite the fact that they fail to [[109]] worship the Bhagavan directly,  
yet may be denoted by the words satvata and bhagavata,  
because of their work discipline of cleaning up Vasudeva's temple,  
clearing away the bali offerings,  
guarding the idol etc., for it is taught that the can suffix may occur in the sense of a simple relation, "this is of that." (263, Panini.)
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See Siddhāntakaumudī, IV. iii. 120.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

saṁbhavati caitēṣāmapi sākṣādbhagavadārādhanābhāvē'pi vāsudēvasyāyatanaśōdhana -balinirharaṇa -pratimāsaṁrakṣaṇādikriyāyōgēnaiva sāttvata -bhāgavata -śabdābhidhēyatvam, tasyēdam iti saṁbandhamātrē'pi cāṇpratyayasmaraṇāt,

#### vr̥ttisāmyān na vrātyatvam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>
