#### avayava-śakti-prādhānyam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca ।  

kl̥ptāvayava-śaktyaiva  
**labdhē** svārthāvabōdhanē ।  
naṣṭāvayava-mānatvaṁ  
**pratyācaṣṭa** ca sūtrakr̥t ॥  
prōkṣaṇīṣv artha-saṁyōgād 

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Moreover, when knowledge of the thing meant by a word is obtained from the denotation of the separate members that compose the word, then the Author of the Sūtras rules out the validity of a denotation in which the meanings of the component members are lost, namely in prokṣaṇīṣv arthasaṃyogāt. 274

[274]: KMS. 

[[111]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

naṣṭāvayavatvaṁ yōga-śakti-rāhityam । ‘nāma’ padēna pratipādikam ucyatē । naṣṭāvayava-nāmatvaṁ = rūḍhim ity ataḥ ।

prōkṣaṇīṣvartha ... Pūrvamīmāṁsā : I.iv.11. This aphorism means that in words like “prokṣaṇī”, the etymological significance itself is applicable; i.e., the word is to be taken in its etymological sense alone and not the conventional one, for the former is quite compatible with the latter. The advantage of this sūtra over the preceding sūtras is that all liquids are meant by the term “prokṣaṇī”, and not water alone.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca ।  
kl̥ptāvayava-śaktyaiva labdhē svārthāvabōdhanē ।  
naṣṭāvayavamānatvaṁ pratyācaṣṭa ca sūtrakr̥t ॥  
prōkṣaṇīṣv artha-saṁyōgād iti ।  
</details>

#### nigamanam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tataś ca sattvād bhagavān  
bhajyatē yaiḥ paraḥ pumān ।  
tē sāttvatā bhāgavatā  
ity ucyantē dvijōttamāḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Therefore, those emine~nt brahmins are called sāttvatas and bhāgavatas who because of their pure character (sattva) devote themselves to the Bhagavān who is the Supreme Person. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

For a definition of the term Bhāgavata, see Pādmasaṁhitā, Caryāpāda, II.91b-95a and XXI. 14-15. For an interesting account of the origin and significance of the term Sāttvata see J. Przyluski, ‘Sātvant, Sātvata and Nāsatya’, IIIQ, Vol. IX pp 83-91.

For a glorification of Pāñcarātrins along with Vaikhānasas, see Mahābhārata, Anuśāsana [Vavilla edn. Vol. XVI], ch. 78:

> yatayō mōkṣa-dharma-jñā yōginaś carita-vratāḥ ।  
pāñca-rātra-vidō mukhyās tathā bhāgavatāḥ parē ॥ [ 24 ]  
vaikhānasāḥ kula-śrēṣṭhāḥ vaidikācāra-vāriṇaḥ । [ 25a ]
 
> yāvad ētē prapaśyanti paṅktīs tāvat punanti ca ॥ [ 28b ]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tataś ca sattvād bhagavān bhajyatē yaiḥ paraḥ pumān ।  
tē sāttvatā bhāgavatā ityucyantē dvijōttamāḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

smr̥ty-antarāṇi ca bhāgavatānām utkr̥ṣṭa-brāhmaṇya-pratipādakānīti  
parastāt pradarśayiṣyantē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Later on we shall show that other smṛtis set forth the eminent brahminhood of the bhāgavatas.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

No such smṛtis are however, quoted by the author in the remaining portion of the text.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

smr̥tyantarāṇi ca bhāgavatānām utkr̥ṣṭa-brāhmaṇya-pratipādakānīti parastāt pradarśayiṣyantē ।  
</details>

### pr̥thaṅ-nirdēśaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yat punar uktaṁ - 

> samānē brāhmaṇyē  
kim iti sāttvata-bhāgavataikāntika-śabdair ēvaitēṣāṁ niyamēna vyapadēśa 

iti,  
tat parivrājaka-nigadādivad ity adōṣaḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

131\. The further objection,275 namely why these people should invariably be denoted by the exclusive names of Sāttvata and Bhāgavata, if their brahminhood were the same as that of others, can be answered thus: there is no defect in that, for it is as it is in the case of the names parivrājaka and nigada. 

[275]: supra § 15.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See p. 12 above, for the pūrvapakṣa-view.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yat punar uktaṁ samānē brāhmaṇyē kim iti sāttvata-bhāgavataikāntika-śabdair ēvaitēṣāṁ niyamēna vyapadēśa iti, tat parivrājaka-nigadādivad ity adōṣaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathaiva hi samānē brāhmaṇyē yajuṣṭvē ca  
kēcid ēva brāhmaṇāḥ  
kānicid ēva yajūṁṣi  
parivrājaka-nigada-śabdābhyām adhīyantē,  

> tiṣṭhantu brāhmaṇāḥ  

> parivrājakā ānīyantām,  

> yajūṁṣi vartantē na nigadāḥ, 

> nigadā vartantē na yajūṁṣi 

iti ca, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yathaiva hi ... See Pūrvamīmāṁsā, II. i. 35-37: "tēṣāṁ r̥k yatrārtha-vaśēna pāda-vyavasthā", "gītiṣu samākhyā", "śēṣē yajuś śabdaḥ", for the definitions of ṛk, sāman and yajus respectively. By the last of the above sūtras, the group of mantras called “nigada” also comes to be known as “yajus”.

tiṣṭhantu ... Cf. Śābara under II. i. 43, p. 89.

yajūṁṣi ... Cf. ibid. under II. i. 39, p. 89.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathaiva hi samānē brāhmaṇyē yajuṣṭvē ca kēcid ēva brāhmaṇāḥ kānicid ēva yajūṁṣi parivrājaka-nigada-śabdābhyām adhīyantē,  
tiṣṭhantu brāhmaṇāḥ parivrājakā ānīyantām, yajūṁṣi vartantē na nigadāḥ, nigadā vartantē na yajūṁṣi iti ca, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Certain brahmins are called bhāgavatas, just as certain brahmins are called parivrājakas, and certain yajuḥ formulae nigadas, though both are equally brahmins and equally yajuḥ formulae; namely in the statements:  

> The brahmins should remain,  
the parivrājakas must be fetched; 276  
"the yajuḥ formulae take place, not the nigadas;  
the nigadas take place, not the yajuḥ formulae;"277 

[276]: not identified.
[277]: not identified.  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathēhāpi bhaviṣyati,  

> nigadāś caturthaṁ mantra-jātaṁ  
yajūṁṣi vā tad-rūpatvād 

iti nyāyābhidhānāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and this is so because of the interpretation: 

> "the nigadas are the fourth mantra collection, or the yajuḥ formulae, because they are identical."
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide Pūrvamīmāṁsā II. i. 40.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathēhāpi bhaviṣyati, nigadāś caturthaṁ mantra-jātaṁ yajūṁṣi vā tadrūpatvād iti nyāyābhidhānāt ।  
</details>

### vr̥ttyā

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vr̥tty-arthaṁ dēvatā-pūjā-  
naivēdya-prāśanādibhiḥ ।  
daurbrāhmaṇyaṁ yad apy uktaṁ  
tatra pratividhīyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

132\. The contention278 that the bhāgavatas are bad brahmins because they perform pūjā to the God, partake of the offering substance etc. for a livelihood, is countered in the following manner: 

[278]: supra § 16.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See p. 15 above.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vr̥ttyarthaṁ dēvatā-pūjā-naivēdya-prāśanādibhiḥ ।  
daurbrāhmaṇyaṁ yad apy uktaṁ tatra pratividhīyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**na** hi bhāgavatais sarvair  
vr̥ttayē **'bhyārcitō** hariḥ ।  
dr̥ṣṭā hi bahavas svārthaṁ  
**pūjayantō** 'pi sāttvatāḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Surely not all bhāgavatas worship Hari for their profession, for many Sātvatas are found who perform pūjā for themselves. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi bhāgavatais sarvair vr̥ttayē 'bhyārcitō hariḥ ।  
dr̥ṣṭā hi bahavas svārthaṁ pūjayantō 'pi sāttvatāḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kēcid yadi paraṁ santaḥ  
sāttvatā vr̥tti-kārśitāḥ ।  
**yājayanti** mahā-bhāgair  
vaiṣṇavair vr̥tti-kāraṇāt ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If there are certain people who, while being Sātvatas, follow a reprehensible profession and perform sacrifices for respectable bhāgavatas professionally, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kēcid yadi paraṁ santaḥ sāttvatā vr̥tti-kārśitāḥ ।  
yājayanti mahā-bhāgair vaiṣṇavair vr̥tti-kāraṇāt ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na tāvataiṣāṁ brāhmaṇyaṁ  
śakyaṁ nāstīti bhāṣitum ।  
na khalv ādhvaryavaṁ kurvan  
jyōtiṣṭōmē patiṣyati ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

this fact alone does not mean that one may say that they are not brahmins. A vedic priest who officiates as an adhvaryu at a jyotiṣṭoma does not thereby lose caste. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na tāvataiṣāṁ brāhmaṇyaṁ śakyaṁ nāstīti bhāṣitum ।  
na khalv ādhvaryavaṁ kurvan jyōtiṣṭōmē patiṣyati ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yadi **na pratigr̥hṇīyuḥ**  
pūjaivāviphalā bhavēt ।  
pūjā-sādguṇya-siddhy-artham  
atas tē **pratigr̥hṇatē** ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

If the priest were not to receive fees, the pūjā itself would remain fruitless; they take fees in order to realize completely the excellence of the pūjā. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadi na pratigr̥hṇīyuḥ pūjaivāviphalā bhavēt ।  
pūjā-sādguṇya-siddhyartham atas tē pratigr̥hṇatē ॥

</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

arcanāntē hiraṇyaṁ ca  
tasmai dēyaṁ sva-śaktitaḥ ।  
anyathā pūjakasyaiva  
tatra pūjā-phalaṁ bhavēt ॥+++(5)+++  
hanty alpa-dakṣiṇō yajña  
ity-ādi-smr̥ti-darśanāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

At the conclusion of the worship one must give gold to the priest according to capacity; otherwise the fruit will go to the pūjā priest himself,  
as is shown by the smṛti: "A sacrifice for which a small fee is given kills (the sacrificer)."279 

[279]: cf. Manu, 11.40.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

arcanāntē ... Paramasaṁhitā, XVII. 46b-47a.

hantyalpadakṣiṇō ... Manusmṛti, XI. 40b.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

arcanāntē hiraṇyaṁ ca tasmai dēyaṁ sva-śaktitaḥ ।  
anyathā pūjakasyaiva tatra pūjā-phalaṁ bhavēt ॥  
hantyalpa-dakṣiṇō yajña ityādi-smr̥ti-darśanāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

r̥tvijā dravya-lubdhēna  
svayaṁ yāñcā-purassaram ॥  
yad ārtvijyaṁ kr̥taṁ karma  
tad ēva hi niṣidhyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It is however prohibited that a covetous Vedic priest officiate as a priest after he himself has put up his demands for a fee, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

r̥tvijā dravya-lubdhēna svayaṁ yāñcā-purassaram ॥  
yad ārtvijyaṁ kr̥taṁ karma tad ēva hi niṣidhyatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad yathā 

> yad āśaṁsamānam ārtvijyaṁ kārayanty  
> 
> > uta vā mē dadyād  
uta vā mā vr̥ṇīta  
> 
> iti  
tad dha tat parāg ēva yathā jagdhaṁ,  
na haivaṁ tad yajyamānaṁ bhunakti ।  

iti,+++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

e.g. in the statement: 

> ("There is an error called 'garbage"").  
> When the sacrificer appoints as an officiant priest  
who covets the office, thinking either  
"He should give me (a fee)"  
or "He should choose me."  
"This is as far from the sacrificer as garbage; this does not benefit the sacrificer."280 

[280]: AitBr., 3.46.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Aitareya Brāhmaṇa XV. ii. p. 418 [ Ānandāśrama Skt. Ser. 32, with Sāyaṇa’s commentary ]. The passage reads thus :

> taddhaitadeva jagdhāṁ yadāśaṁsamānamārtvijyaṁ kārayata uta vā me dadyāt uta vā mā vṛṇīteti taddha tatparāṇeva yathā jagdhāṁ na haiva tad yajamānaṁ bhunakti.

This passage points out that a careful yajamāna should avoid greedy priests who perform three types of objectionable offerings in sacrifices. Cf. ibid. p. 417: “trīṇi ha vai yajñe kriyante, jagdhaṁ, gīrṇaṁ, vāntaṁ”.

Vide Sāyaṇa’s commentary on it:

> tānyetāni trīṇi durbuddhibhir yajñe kriyante jagdhādisthānīyāni trīṇi, varjanīyānītyarthaḥ.

For more information on this, see Sāyaṇa’s commentary, p. 411.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad yathā 

> yad āśaṁsamānam ārtvijyaṁ kārayanty  
> 
> > uta vā mē dadyād  
uta vā mā vr̥ṇīta  
> 
> iti  
tad dha tat parāg ēva।  
yathā jagdhaṁ (vāntaṁ) na haivaṁ tadyajyamānaṁ bhunakti ।  

iti,
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

śraddhā-pūta-dakṣiṇā-dānaṁ  
tūbhayōr api śrēyaskaram ēva ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The donation of the sacerdotal fee which is purified by faith is felicitous for both, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

śraddhāpūtadakṣiṇādānaṁ tūbhayōrapi śrēyaskaramēva ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yō'rcitaṁ **pratigr̥hṇāti**  
**dadyād** arcitam ēva ca ॥
tāv ubhau **gacchataḥ** svargam  
ityādi-smr̥ti-darśanāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

as according to the smṛti, "He who receives the offering and he who deit|gives it both go to heaven."281

[281]: not identified.

[[112]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vide Manusmṛti. IV-238. The remainder of the verse is “narakaṁ tu viparyaye”. The term “arcitaṁ” should be understood in the sense of “arcanāpurassaraṁ”. It is an adverb and not a noun.

This verse is also found in the Mahābhārata, Āśvamedhika [ Vavilla edn. Vol. XVIII. ] ch. 112, śl. 30.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yō'rcitaṁ pratigr̥hṇāti dadyād arcitam ēva ca ॥
tāv ubhau gacchataḥ svargam ityādi-smr̥ti-darśanāt ।  
</details>

### dēvālakatā

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad api 

> vr̥ttyarthaṁ dēva-pūjanād dēvakōśōpajīvitvāc ca dēvalakatva-prāptir 

iti,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

133\. The statements282 that professional worship of the deity and living off the god's treasure makes a man a devalaka275 

[282]: supra § 16.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See pp. 15-16 above.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yad api vr̥ttyarthaṁ dēva-pūjanād dēvakōśōpajīvitvāc ca dēvalakatva-prāptir iti,  
</details>

#### dēvatāntara-vr̥ttau
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad api dēvatāntara-vr̥tty-arthārādhana- tat-kōśōpajīvana-viṣayam iti draṣṭavyam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

must be taken to refer to the professional worship of, and the living off the treasure of, other deities than Vāsudeva. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad api dēvatāntara-vr̥ttyarthārādhana-tatkōśōpajīvana-viṣayam iti draṣṭavyam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ca bhagavān vyāsaḥ -  

> bhavēd dēvalakō yō vai  
rudrakādy-upajīvakaḥ  

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Thus the blessed Vyāsa: "A devalaka is he who lives on Rudra etc." 283

[283]: This and the following quotations could not be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ca bhagavān vyāsaḥ -  
bhavēd dēvalakō yō vai rudrakādyupajīvakaḥ  
iti, 
</details>

#### dīkṣā-hīnāḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api bhavati śāṇḍilya-vacanam -  

> vr̥ttyarthaṁ yājinas sarvē  
dīkṣā-hīnāś ca kēvalam ।  
karma-dēvalakā ētē  
smr̥tā hyatra purā munē ॥  
tāṁś ca saṁvatsarād ūrdhvaṁ  
na spr̥śēn na ca saṁviśēt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And there is also Śāṇḍilya's word: 

> "All those who perform sacrifices professionally  
and are also not consecrated  
are the only ones who are traditionally known as karmadevalakas in this world, O sage.  
One should not touch them or consort with them for a year." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api bhavati śāṇḍilya-vacanam -  
vr̥ttyarthaṁ yājinas sarvē dīkṣā-hīnāś ca kēvalam ।  
karma-dēvalakā ētē smr̥tā hyatra purā munē ॥
tāṁś ca saṁvatsarād ūrdhvaṁ na spr̥śēn na ca saṁviśēt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā  

> kalpa-dēvalakāḥ kēcit  
karma-dēvalakā api ।  
atha trivarṣād ūrdhvam  
ayōgyā dēva-karmaṇi ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise: 

> "Certain people who are karmadevalakas and kalpadevalakas are unqualified for ritual before the deity for a period of three years. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ।  
kalpa-dēvalakāḥ kēcit karma-dēvalakā api ।  
atha trivarṣād ūrdhvam ayōgyā dēva-karmaṇi ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> yē kalpōktaṁ prakurvanti  
dīkṣā-hīnā dvi-jātayaḥ ।  
vr̥ttya-rthaṁ vā yaśō'rthaṁ vā  
**kalpa-dēvalakās** tu tē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Those brahmins who, without being consecrated, perform rites set forth in the Kalpa, either professionally or for the fame of it, are kalpadevalakas. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yē kalpōktaṁ prakurvanti dīkṣā-hīnā dvi-jātayaḥ ।  
vr̥ttyarthaṁ vā yaśō'rthaṁ vā kalpa-dēvalakās tu tē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> +++(kasyacid viprasya)+++ vr̥ttiṁ **kr̥tvā**, tu viprēṇa  
dīkṣitēna vidhānataḥ ।  
anyēna **yājayēd** dēvam  
aśaktaḥ svayam arcanē ॥  
yajanaṁ mukhyam ēvaitad  
gauṇam ēvānyathā bhavēt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

One must have pūjā offered by another professional priest who has been properly consecrated; (if) one is unable to worship the god oneself.   
This is the principal offering; in another manner it is secondary." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Paramasaṁhitā, XVII. 46a. 

Cf also ibid., 8b:

> anyēna vaiṣṇavēnaiva dēvaṁ śūraḥ prapūjayēt ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vr̥ttiṁ kr̥tvā tu viprēṇa dīkṣitēna vidhānataḥ ।  
anyēna yājayēd dēvam aśaktaḥ svayam arcanē ॥  
yajanaṁ mukhyam ēvaitad gauṇam ēvānyathā bhavēt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

anyathā +++(←gauṇārādhanam)+++ +ity adīkṣitēna +ity arthaḥ,  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

"In another manner,' that is to say, when it is done by a non-consecrated priest. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anyathā +ity adīkṣitēna +ity arthaḥ,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad ēva spaṣṭayati -  

> adīkṣitēna viprēṇa  
yēna kēna vidhānataḥ ।  
vr̥tty-arthaṁ yat kr̥taṁ karma  
taj jaghanyam udāhr̥tam ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

This the author elucidates: 

> "The rite performed professionally by 'some priest who has not been properly consecrated is called of the lowest degree." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad ēva spaṣṭayati -  
adīkṣitēna viprēṇa yēna kēna vidhānataḥ ।  
vr̥ttyarthaṁ yat kr̥taṁ karma taj jaghanyam udāhr̥tam ॥
</details>

#### nigamanam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ityādi-smr̥ti-śata-paryālōcanāt  

> pañcarātra-siddha-dīkṣā-saṁskāra-virahitānāṁ brāhmaṇānāṁ  
dēvakōśōpajīvana-vr̥ttyartha-pūjanādikam upabrāhmaṇatva-dēvalakatvāvaham 

iti niścīyatē। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

By considering these and a hundred similar smṛti statements we can be sure that living off the deity's treasure and professional pūjā offering of brahmins who go without the sacrament of consecration as established by Pañcaratra renders them sub-Brahmins and devalakas.276

276: This and the following quotations could not be identified.  

[[113]]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ityādi-smr̥ti-śata-paryālōcanāt pañcarātra-siddha-dīkṣā-saṁskāra-virahitānāṁ brāhmaṇānāṁ dēvakōśōpajīvana-vr̥ttyartha-pūjanādikam upabrāhmaṇatva-dēvalakatvāvaham iti niścīyatē। 
</details>

### nirmālyōpayōgād aśiṣṭatā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yat punaś 

> śiṣṭa-vigarhita-nirmālya-nivēdyōpayōgād bhāgavatānām aśiṣṭatvam 

iti -  
tatra brūmaḥ  
kim idaṁ nirmālyaṁ, nivēdyaṁ cābhiprētaṁ śrōtriyasya ?
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

134\. As to the statement284 that the bhāgavatas cannot pass for exemplary persons because they make use of flower and food offerings, which practice is abhorred by exemplary persons, to this we say: what does the śrotriya 285 mean by left-over flowers and leftover food? 

[284]: supra § 16.

[285]: a Brahman erudite in the Veda and following its observances.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

See p. 15 above for the opponent's view.

For a detailed discussion on this subject, see Vedānta Deśika’s Saccaritrarakṣā, Adhikāra III.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yat punaś śiṣṭa-vigarhita-nirmālya-nivēdyōpayōgād bhāgavatānām aśiṣṭatvam iti -  
tatra brūmaḥ kim idaṁ nirmālyaṁ nivēdyaṁ cābhiprētaṁ śrōtriyasya ?
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

+++(vigrahāyārpaṇasyānaṅgīkārāt)+++  
+++(nivēdanādy-aviśiṣṭaṁ)+++ puṣpaudanādi-mātraṁ cēt  
sarva-lōka-viruddhatā ।  
puṣpaudana-parityāgaṁ  
na hi lōkō'numanyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

When he takes it only as the flowers and the cakes,286 he is contradicted by all the world, for nobody approves of wasting flowers and cakes. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[286]: If he does not believe that God is present in the effigie, the offerings are obviously not used and cannot be characterized as left-overs. The priest's avoidance of them would simply amount to sinful waste.+++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

puṣpaudanādi-mātraṁ cēt sarvalōkaviruddhatā ।  
puṣpaudana-parityāgaṁ na hi lōkō'numanyatē ॥
</details>
  

##### kaumārīlādi-pakṣē
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

+++(dēva-nivēdana-)+++viśiṣṭa-pratiṣēdhō'pi  
na yuktas tad-asiddhitaḥ +++(ākṣēpaka-matē)+++ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Also, a particularized prohibition 287 is not in order, because it is not established. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[287]: He must make his prohibition specific, in order not to prohibit the priest from using food that is otherwise wasted. But he cannot determine the specification on his own terms.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

viśiṣṭa-pratiṣēdhō'pi na yuktas tadasiddhitaḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na hy anirūpita-viśēṣaṇā viśiṣṭa-buddhir āvir asti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

No notion of a particularized thing occurs when the particularization is not determined; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hyanirūpita-viśēṣaṇā viśiṣṭa-buddhir āvir asti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

na cēha viśēṣaṇaṁ nirūpayituṁ śakyatē। 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

and here it is impossible to determine the particularization. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na cēha viśēṣaṇaṁ nirūpayituṁ śakyatē, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> kim iti na śakyatē -  
yāvatā dēvōddēśēna parityāgō viśēṣaṇam।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> OBJECTION. Why should it be impossible, since the particularization is that it is forbidden to use food what has been offered up to the deity? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> kim iti na śakyatē -  
yāvatā dēvōddēśēna parityāgō viśēṣaṇam।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kim idānīṁ pañcarātra-śāstram api pramāṇam aṅgīkr̥taṁ bhavatā  
yēna pañcarātra-tantra-vihita-mantra-pratiṣṭhāpita-pratimāsu dēvatām abhyupētya  
tad-uddēśēna tyāgō viśēṣaṇam abhilaṣyatē? 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REPLY. Are you now accepting the validity of Pañcaratra? For only when one admits that there is a deity present in the idols that are erected with the sacred formulae enjoined by Pañcaratra Tantra can one postulate that the particularization of the prohibition lies in the offering-up to the deity. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The discussion here is, whether or not the usage of nirmālya, nivedya, etc., contradicts the genuine character of the Bhāgavatas. The Mīmāṁsaka cannot attribute non-brahmanical character to the Bhāgavatas, says the author, on the ground that they use nirmālya and nivedya prohibited is some smṛti-texts. First of all, the prohibition pertains to the nirmālya and nivedya offered to deities other than Viṣṇu. Secondly, the Mīmāṁsaka has to qualify the terms “nirmālya” and “nivedya”, even to refute their usage, because flowers and food in general cannot be termed so. He might say that “nirmālya” and “nivedya” are things offered by the Pāñcarātrins to some deity; but this statement lands him in trouble, since he does not admit of any deity with a personality and also because such a statement would imply his acceptance of the validity of the Pāñcarātra-texts. Without admitting their validity as the starting point, he cannot speak of a deity, and flowers etc., being offered to that deity.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kimidānīṁ pañcarātraśāstramapi pramāṇamaṅgīkr̥taṁ bhavatā  
yēna pañcarātratantravihitamantrapratiṣṭhāpitapratimāsu dēvatāmabhyupētya  
taduddēśēna tyāgō viśēṣaṇamabhilaṣyatē? 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

kathaṁ hi tat-prāmāṇyānabhyupagamē  
tat-pratipādyamānāyā dēvatātvam,  
kathantarāṁ ca tad-uddēśēna tyaktasya nirmālya-nivēdya-bhāvaḥ? 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For unless the validity of the Tantra is admitted, how can an idol which is set forth in the Tantra be a deity, and, a fortiori, how can the substance that is offered up for this deity's sake be nirmālya and nivedya,288

[288]: used flowers and used food offerings.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kathaṁ hi tatprāmāṇyānabhyupagamē tatpratipādyamānāyā dēvatātvam, 
kathantarāṁ ca taduddēśēna tyaktasya nirmālya-nivēdya-bhāvaḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na hi kācij jātyā dēvatā nāmāsti,  
yaiva hi haviḥ-pratiyōgitayā +++(na tad-antarā)+++ pramāṇa-bhūtāc śabdād avagamyatē  
sā tatra dēvatā 

iti hi vaḥ siddhāntaḥ ।  +++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> For a deity does not exist by just being a deity;  
only that deity which is known to be correlated with an oblation on the authority of scriptural testimony is the deity to that oblation; 

that is your own doctrine.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Tantravārtika under I. iii. 10, p. 172:

> vidhinaiva hi dēvatvaṁ pratikarmavadhāryatē । na jātyā dēvatātvaṁ hi kvacid asti vyavasthitam ॥

Cf. also Prakaraṇapañcikā, V. p. 105:

> dēvatōddēśēna dravya-tyāgō yāgaḥ ।......stōtraṁ śr̥ṇōmi yad guṇa-vacanē । yad uddēśēna ca haviṣāṁ tyāgaś cōdyatē, sā dēvatā । tatraiva yājñika-vr̥ddhānāṁ dēvatā-śabda-prayōgāt । yatra hi āgnēyādi-dēśanārthānuṣṭhānē pravr̥ttō 'gnim uddiśya havis tyajati, tatraivam āhur agnir atra dēvatēti । 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na hi kācij jātyā dēvatā nāmāsti, yaiva hi haviḥ-pratiyōgitayā pramāṇa-bhūtāc śabdād avagamyatē sā tatra dēvatā iti hi vaḥ siddhāntaḥ ।  
</details>

##### pāñcarātrika-pakṣē
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atha 

> pañcarātrikair dēvatōddēśēna parityaktatvābhyupagamān  
nirmālya-nivēdya-bhāvaḥ, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or if it be held that 

> something is nirmālya and nivedya because it is admitted by the Pāñcarātrikas that it is offered up to the deity, 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atha pañcarātrikair dēvatōddēśēna parityaktatvābhyupagamān nirmālya-nivēdya-bhāvaḥ, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

hanta tarhi,  
tair ēva parama-pāvanatayā'pi nirmālya-nivēdyōpayōgasyāṅgīkr̥tatvāt  
tadvad ēva pāvanatvam aṅgī kriyatām ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

well, in that case you must also admit its purity because the Pāñcarātrikas accept also that the utilization of nirmālya and nivedya is perfectly pure.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

hanta tarhi, tair ēva parama-pāvanatayā'pi nirmālya-nivēdyōpayōgasyāṅgīkr̥tatvāt tadvad ēva pāvanatvam aṅgīkriyatām ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

athāpāvanam ēva taiḥ +++(pāñcarātra-mōhitaiḥ)+++ pāvana-buddhyā parigr̥hītam iti na tat prāśastyam aṅgīkriyatē, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Or if you do not accept this peculiar excellence, since in your opinion the Pāñcarātrikas have accepted as pure something that is really impure,

</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

athāpāvanam ēva taiḥ pāvana-buddhyā parigr̥hītam iti na tat prāśastyam aṅgīkriyatē, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

hanta tarhy a-dēvataiva dēvatā-buddhyārōpēṇa taiḥ parigr̥hītēti  
na tad-uddēśēna tyaktasya nirmālya-nivēdya-bhāvō 'ṅgīkriyatām । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

—well, in that case you must accept it that the substance which is offered up is not really nirmālya and nivedya, since then you opine that the Pañcarātrikas have adopted someone who is not really a deity by mistaking him for a deity!
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

hanta tarhyadēvataiva dēvatābuddhyārōpēṇa taiḥ parigr̥hītēti na taduddēśēna tyaktasya nirmālya-nivēdya-bhāvō'ṅgīkriyatām ।  
</details>

#### nigamanam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ētad uktaṁ bhavati 

- puṣpaudanādi-svarūpa-mātra-tyāgasyāniṣṭatvāt,  
- sva-darśanānusārēṇa ca viśēṣaṇāsaṁbhavāt  
- para-darśanānusārēṇa viśēṣaṇa-nirūpaṇē  
  tasyaiva parama-pāvanatvāpātāt  

tatra prāmāṇyam abhyupagacchadbhir anyaiś ca  
nirmālya-nivēdyōpayōgō 'vaśyāṅgīkaraṇīya  
iti । +++(4)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In other words, inasmuch as the ~~offering up~~ abandonment of mere flowers, cakes etc. 289 is not approved,  
and because it is impossible to particularize the prohibition of utilizing these substances according to the terms of one's own doctrine,  
therefore the particularization must be determined in the terms of the others', i.e. the Pañcarātrikas', doctrine;  
and thus the offering up becomes greatly purifying.  
And inasmuch as therefore the utilization of nirmālya and nivedya becomes most purifying,  
it must needs be accepted by those who admit the validity of the Pañcarātra Tantra as well by others who do not.

[289]: without divine utilisation.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ētad uktaṁ bhavati puṣpaudanādi-svarūpa-mātra-tyāgasyāniṣṭatvāt sva-darśanānusārēṇa ca viśēṣaṇāsaṁbhavāt para-darśanānusārēṇa viśēṣaṇa-nirūpaṇē tasyaiva parama-pāvanatvāpātāt tatra prāmāṇyam abhyupagacchadbhir anyaiś ca nirmālya-nivēdyōpayōgō'vaśyāṅgīkaraṇīya iti ।  
</details>

#### pāñcarātrē 'niṣēdhaḥ
##### niṣēdhābhāsāḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

āha 

> kathaṁ punas tatra prāmāṇyam aṅgīkurvatā nirmālyaṁ nivēdyaṁ ca na pariharaṇīyam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[114]]

> 135\. OBJECTION. But how is it possible then that even one who admits the validity of Pāñcarātra  
should reject nevertheless the nirmālya and nivedya? 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

āha kathaṁ punas tatra prāmāṇyam aṅgīkurvatā nirmālyaṁ nivēdyaṁ ca na pariharaṇīyam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> niṣidhyatē hi tantrēṣu  
nirmālya-prāśanādikam ।  
yathā sanat-kumārīya-  
saṁhitāyām udīritam ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> For in the Tantras the tasting etc. of the nirmālya is prohibited. For instance, it is said in the Sanatkumārīya Saṃhitā: 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Published by the Adyar Library and Research Centre, Madras, 1969.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

niṣidhyatē hi tantrēṣu nirmālya-prāśanādikam ।  
yathā sanat-kumārīya-saṁhitāyām udīritam ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nivēditaṁ tu yad dhavyaṁ  
puṣpaṁ phalam athāpi vā ।  
tan nirmālyam iti prōktaṁ  
tat prayatnēna varjayēt ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> "The offering that is proffered (to the deity), flower or fruit, is called nirmālya; that must be avoided meticulously." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Śivarātra, V. 48b-49a. Also Cf. Paramasaṁhitā XII. 36b-37a:

> pūjāyāṁ viniyuktaṁ tu yad dravyam iha pūjakaiḥ ।  
nirmālyam iti vijñēyaṁ na kāryēṣu varjitam ॥

Cf also Vasiṣṭhasaṁhitā ( ms ) VII. 52b-5 a:

> nivēditaṁ ca yad dravyaṁ puṣpaṁ phalam athāpi vā ।  
nirmālyam iti taṁ [ tat ? ] caiva prayatnēna vivarjayēt ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nivēditaṁ tu yad dhavyaṁ  
puṣpaṁ phalam athāpi vā ।  
tan nirmālyam iti prōktaṁ  
tat prayatnēna varjayēt ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tathā pradēśāntarē -  
> 
> > nirmālyaṁ bhakṣayitvaivam  
ucchiṣṭam agurōr api ।  
māsaṁ payō-vratō bhūtvā  
japann aṣṭākṣaraṁ sadā ॥  
brahma-kūrcaṁ tataḥ pītvā  
pūtō bhavati mānavaḥ ।  
> 
> iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Similarly in another passage: "When one has eaten nirmālya, or the foodrests of someone who is not one's guru, one must observe a milk-vow for a month, continuously recite the eight-syllable formula, 
and drink the pañcagavya,279 in order to be purified."290 

[290]: The pañcagavya is a substance in which the 5 products of the cow are mingled.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

nirmālyaṁ ... Ṛṣirātra, VIII. 77b-78. Variants: “bhakṣayitvā cāpi” in the first line, “japtvā cāṣṭākṣara” in the second line and “pūtō bhavati sādhakaḥ” in the third line.

brahmakūrcaṁ ... A mixture of five products of the cow (pañcagavya) with darbha-water.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā pradēśāntarē -  

> nirmālyaṁ bhakṣayitvaivam ucchiṣṭam agurōr api ।  
māsaṁ payō-vratō bhūtvā japann aṣṭākṣaraṁ sadā ॥  
brahma-kūrcaṁ tataḥ pītvā pūtō bhavati mānavaḥ ।  
iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tathā indra-rātrē ।  
> 
> > na cōpajīvēd dēvēśaṁ  
na nirmālyāni bhakṣayēt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Likewise in the Indrarātra: "One should not live off the Supreme God, nor eat the nirmālya offerings." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

IX. 2a.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā indra-rātrē ।  
na cōpajīvēd dēvēśaṁ na nirmālyāni bhakṣayēt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tathā -  
> 
>>  na cōpabhōgayōgyāni  
nirmālyāni kadācana ।  
> 
> iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Also: 
> 
>>  "And the nirmālya offerings are never fit for consumption." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This is not found in the extant text of the Indrarātra-section, perhaps lost in the rest of ch. IX, which ends in a blank.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā -  

> na cōpabhōgayōgyāni  
nirmālyāni kadācana ।  
(na cōpabhōgayōgyānīti pā. ।)
iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tathā saṁhitāntarē -  
> 
> > nirmālyāni na cāśnīyān  
na jighrēn na ca laṅghayēt ।  
> 
> iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Similarly in another Saṃhitā: 
> 
> > "One should not eat the nirmālya offerings, nor smell them, nor step over them."
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.

Cf Paramasaṁhitā III. 44:

> nirmālyaṁ laṅghayēn naiva na bhuñjīta na saṁspr̥śēt ।  
na dadyāc ca na jighrēc ca rakṣēt.........ca ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā saṁhitāntarē ।  
nirmālyāni na cāśnīyān na jighrēn na ca laṅghayēt ।  
iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

>>  tad ēvam anēka-saṁhitā-samadhigata-niṣēdhasya nirmālyōpabhōgasya  
katham iva pāvanatvāṅgīkāraḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> How then can one accept the purity of the utilization of the nirmālya when we thus know from several Saṃhitā that it is prohibited?
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tadēvam anēka-saṁhitā-samadhigata-niṣēdhasya nirmālyōpabhōgasya katham iva pāvanatvāṅgīkāraḥ ।  
</details>

##### vilambya prayōgaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

atrāha dēvam uddiśya  
tyaktasyāpi ca vastunaḥ ।  
nāḍikā-daśakād arvāg  
upayōgō na nindyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. To this he says: The utilization of a proffered substance which has been offered up to the deity is not condemned if it is done ~~within~~ after a period of ten nāḍikās.291

[291]: one nāḍikā is a half muhūrta.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

atrāha dēvam uddiśya tyaktasyāpi ca vastunaḥ ।  
nāḍikā-daśakād arvāg upayōgō na nindyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā indra-rātrē ēva -  

> daśa-nāḍy-adhikaṁ pūraṁ  
sthāpayēt tu vicakṣaṇaḥ ।  
kāla-yōgas samuddiṣṭō  
rātrāv ahani caiva hi ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Thus in the same Indrarātra: 

> "The wise one must let the offering-cake stand for ten nāḍikās. This period of time has been prescribed both for night and for day. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

I. 10b-11a. Variants: sthāpayitvā for sthāpayēt tu and sa uddiṣṭaḥ for samuddiṣṭaḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā indra-rātrē ēva -  
daśanāḍyadhikaṁ pūraṁ sthāpayēt tu vicakṣaṇaḥ ।  
kālayōgas samuddiṣṭō rātrāv ahani caiva hi ॥

</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> a-kāla-yōgātiriktaṁ tu  
nirmālyaṁ paricakṣatē ।  
tatas tad apsu caivāgnau  
kṣipēd bhūmau khanēt tu vā ॥

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> They condemn the nirmālya that has stood for ~~more~~ other than this period of time;  
thereupon he must throw it in water, or in fire, or bury it in the ground." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

I. 11b, 10a. Variant: vā cāgnau for caivāgnau ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

kālayōgātiriktaṁ tu nirmālyaṁ paricakṣatē ।  
tatas tad apsu caivāgnau kṣipēd bhūmau khanēt tu vā ॥

iti ।  
</details>

##### anadhikāribhyō niṣēdhaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> ucyatē - nātra nirmālya-  
prāśanādi praśasyatē ।  
kiṁ tu pūraṇa-pūjāyāṁ  
viniyuktasya vastunaḥ ॥
nāḍikā-daśakē pūrṇē  
paścāt tyāgō vidhīyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> OBJECTION. But what is said here is not to praise the tasting etc. of the nirmālya, but to prescribe that the substance of the cake pūjā is thrown away after a period of ten nāḍikās. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

For an account of pūraṇapūjā, see Indrarātra, ch. I. See also Kapiñjalasaṁhitā, ch. 29.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ucyatē - nātra nirmālya-prāśanādi praśasyatē ।  
kiṁ tu pūraṇa-pūjāyāṁ viniyuktasya vastunaḥ ॥
nāḍikā-daśakē pūrṇē paścāt tyāgō vidhīyatē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> sāmānyēna nivēditasya puṣpaudanādēḥ  
kr̥ta-kāryatāyā nirmālyatvēna +apanayē prāptē  
nāḍikā-daśa-pūraṇaṁ pūjāṅgatayā sthāpanaṁ vidhīyatē 
> 
> > daśa-nāḍy-adhikaṁ pūraṁ sthāpayēt 
> 
> iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In the statement: 

> "He must let the offering cake stand for over ten nāḍikās,” 

the injunction is laid down that when the proffered flowers, cake etc. in general have been taken off as nirmālya,  
because they have now fulfilled their ritual function,  
they must be kept by way of accessory pūjā rite for a period of ten nāḍikās. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Indrarātra, I. 10b.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sāmānyēna nivēditasya puṣpaudanādēḥ  
kr̥ta-kāryatāyā nirmālyatvēna +apanayē prāptē  
nāḍikā-daśa-pūraṇaṁ pūjāṅgatayā sthāpanaṁ vidhīyatē daśanāḍyadhikaṁ pūraṁ sthāpayēt iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> tataś ca tantra-siddhānta-  
paryālōcanayāpi vaḥ ।  
haridrā-cūrṇa-naivēdya-  
pādāmbu-sparśanādikam ॥
na siddhyēt tantra-siddhāntaḥ  
kva, nu yūyaṁ kva cālpakāḥ ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> And consequently even a study of the conclusions of your own Tantras shows that the touching etc. of the turmeric powder, the food offerings and the water used to clean the idol's feet is not established by Tantric doctrine. Now, where are you!
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This is Yāmuna’s reply to the above arguments regarding nirmālya and naivedya.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tataś ca tantra-siddhānta-paryālōcanayāpi vaḥ ।  
haridrā-cūrṇa-naivēdya-pādāmbu-sparśanādikam ॥  
na siddhyēt tantra-siddhāntaḥ kva nu yūyaṁ kva cālpakāḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ahō vidyā-lavōllāsi-  
jihvā-grasta-vicētasaḥ ॥
sitāsitaṁ vacō bhāti  
sa-kalaṅkēndu-bimbavat । +++(5)+++   
yē hi yuṣmad-vidhā mūrkhās  
tēṣām ēva niṣēdha-gīḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. Where are you, loquacious debaters, witless fools who have been swallowed by your own tongue which plays around with a grain of knowledge! Your objection looks black and white at once, like the moon with its spots.  
This prohibition applies only to fools like you, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Sāttvata Saṁhitā, XXI. 45b-46:

> yo na vettyacyutaṁ tattvaṁ pañcarātrārthameva ca ।  
tathā sadvaiṣṇavīṁ dīkṣāṁ nānāśāstroktalakṣaṇām ॥  
na tena saha saṁbandhaḥ kāryaḥ................... ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ahō vidyālavōllāsi-jihvā-grasta-vicētasaḥ ॥  
sitāsitaṁ vacō bhāti sakalaṅkēndubimbavat ।  
yē hi yuṣmad-vidhā mūrkhās tēṣām ēva niṣēdha-gīḥ ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sēvyamānaṁ hi tat sarvaṁ  
vaiṣṇavair adhikāribhiḥ ।  
aghaugha-dhvaṁsanāyālaṁ  
sōma-pānam ivādhvarē ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

since all this is indeed to be observed by Vaiṣṇavas who are qualified to do so, and thus it is capable of wiping off a multitude of sins in the same way as the drinking of soma at a Vedic sacrifice; 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sēvyamānaṁ hi tat sarvaṁ vaiṣṇavair adhikāribhiḥ ।  
aghaugha-dhvaṁsanāyālaṁ sōma-pānam ivādhvarē ॥  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

anyēṣāṁ hi tad aspr̥śyaṁ  
purō-ḍāśaḥ śunām iva । +++(5)+++ 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

for it is not to be touched by others, just as the puroḍaśa cake292 is not to be touched by dogs! 

[292]: cake used at Vedic offerings.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Pādmasaṁhitā, Caryāpāda, XII.83b:

> śunāmiva puroḍāśo na nīceṣu tadīyate ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

anyēṣāṁ hi tad aspr̥śyaṁ purō-ḍāśaḥ śunām iva ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tad yathēśvara-saṁhitāyām -  

durlabhō bhagavad-bhaktō  
lōkē'smin puruṣaḥ suta ।  
tatrāpi **durlabhatarō**  
bhāvō vai yasya tattvataḥ ॥  
pādōdakaṁ prati **śubhas**  
siddhānnaiś ca **nivēditē** ।  
srag-ādikē **cōpabhuktē**  
hy **upabhōgārtham** ēva ca ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Thus in the Īśvara Saṃhitā, 

> "It is difficult to find in this world a true votary of the lord, my son,  
and, among those who are, it is even more difficult to find a disposition which is truly pure enough for the footwater, or to use the garlands etc. which have been mentioned in the doctrine,  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

These and a few other verses following, quoted by Yāmuna as from Īśvarasaṁhitā, are not found in the available āgamas of that name. The Īśvarasaṁhitā from which Yāmuna quotes appears to have been a different work. See Introduction to Jayākhyasaṁhitā ( Gaekwad Oriental Series ), p. 49.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tad yathēśvara-saṁhitāyām -  

durlabhō bhagavad-bhaktō lōkē'smin puruṣaḥ suta ।  
tatrāpi durlabhatarō bhāvō vai yasya tattvataḥ ॥
pādōdakaṁ prati śubhassiddhānnaiś ca nivēditē ।  
sragādikē cōpabhuktē hy upabhōgārtham ēva ca ॥
</details>

<details><summary>rāmamiśraśāstrī</summary>

(śrīmadbhāgavatē yathā'ha bhagavantaṁ śrīkr̥ṣṇam uddhavaḥ - 

> tavōcchiṣṭa-bhujō dāsās  
tava māyāṁ jayēmahi 

iti ।) 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> ataś ca bhāva-hīnānām  
abhaktānāṁ ca ṣaṇ-mukha ।  
niṣiddhaṁ bhagavan-mantra-  
dr̥k-pūtam akhilaṁ hi yat ॥ 

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>viṣayaḥ</summary>

prasādaḥ, nirmālyam, bhaktiḥ
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Therefore, O six-faced One, all this which is purified by the formulae and the glance of the Bhagavān is forbidden to those who lack this disposition and are not votaries." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ataś ca bhāva-hīnānām abhaktānāṁ ca ṣaṇmukha ।  
niṣiddhaṁ bhagavanmantra-dr̥k-pūtam akhilaṁ hi yat ॥ 

iti,

</details>

##### pāvitryam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā pradēśāntarē -  

> kuṅkumaṁ candanaṁ caitat  
karpūram anulēpanam ।  
viṣṇu-dēha-parāmr̥ṣṭaṁ  
tad vai pāvana-pāvanam ॥

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And in another passage: "The saffron, sandal, camphor and oils that have been taken off Viṣṇu's body are supremely purifying." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā pradēśāntarē -  

kuṅkumaṁ candanaṁ caitat karpūram anulēpanam ।  
viṣṇu-dēha-parāmr̥ṣṭaṁ tad vai pāvana-pāvanam ॥

iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā padmōdbhavē -  

> viṣṇu-dēha-parāmr̥ṣṭaṁ  
yaś cūrṇaṁ śirasā vahēt ।  
sō'śvamēdha-phalaṁ prāpya  
viṣṇu-lōkē mahīyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise in the Padmodbhava: "He who wears the powder that is taken of Viṣṇu's body on his head obtains the fruit of a Horse Sacrifice and glories in Viṣṇu's heaven." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā padmōdbhavē -  
viṣṇudēhaparāmr̥ṣṭaṁ yaścūrṇaṁ śirasā vahēt।  
sō'śvamēdhaphalaṁ prāpya viṣṇulōkē mahīyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathēśvara-saṁhitāyām ।  

> **upabhuktasya** sarvasya  
gandha-puṣpādikasya ca ।  
snānādāv **upayuktasya**  
dadhi-kṣīrādikasya ca ॥  
**dūṣaṇaṁ na** prayōktavyaṁ  
śabdair a-pratipatti-jaiḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Similarly in the Īśvara Saṃhitā, 

> "No blame should be put by statements arising from ignorance on all that is used, the perfume, flowers etc., (the water) of the idol's bath etc., and the curds, milk etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

This is the second instance where Yāmuna quotes from Īśvarasaṁhitā, which is yet to be recovered.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathēśvara-saṁhitāyām ।  

upabhuktasya sarvasya gandha-puṣpādikasya ca ।  
snānādāv upayuktasya dadhi-kṣīrādikasya ca ॥
dūṣaṇaṁ na prayōktavyaṁ śabdair apratipattijaiḥ ।
</details>

<details><summary>rāmamiśraśāstrī</summary>

(apratipattijaiḥ = nindā'sūyādy-āviṣkāra-kārakair ityarthaḥ ।)
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nirmālya-buddhyā dēvīyaṁ  
pāvanaṁ **dūṣayanti** yē ॥
tē **yānti** narakaṁ mūḍhās  
tat-prabhāvāpalāpinaḥ ।  

iti,
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Those who condemn this divine purifying agent because they consider it nirmālya, those witless detractors of its power will go to hell." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> nirmālya-buddhyā dēvīyaṁ pāvanaṁ dūṣayanti yē ॥
tē yānti narakaṁ mūḍhās tatprabhāvāpalāpinaḥ ।  

iti।
</details>

##### vaiṣvaksēnē niṣēdhaḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yāni punar dīkṣitam ēvādhikr̥tya  
samayānuśāsana-samayē nirmālyōpayōga-niṣēdha-parāṇi vacanāni  
tāni pāriṣadēśōpayōgōttara-kālābhiprāyēṇa draṣṭavyāni । 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

The above statements which to the consecrated prohibit the use of nirmālya at the time mentioned in the time instruction293 must be understood to mean a time subsequent to that when the (offerings to) the chief of the Bhagavān's retinue294 is being used. 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen - Notes</summary>

[293]: namely, in the above statement on the 10 nāḍikās.

[294]: Viśvaksena, to whom pūjā is performed after the main pūjā.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

itaḥ pūrvam abhaktānāṁ nirmālyādy-upayōga-niṣēdha-viṣayō vicāritaḥ । idānīṁ dīkṣitasyāpi tad-viṣayē vicāraḥ prastūyatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yāni punar dīkṣitam ēvādhikr̥tya samayānuśāsana-samayē nirmālyōpayōga-niṣēdha-parāṇi vacanāni tāni pāriṣadēśōpayōgōttara-kālābhiprāyēṇa draṣṭavyāni । 
</details>

<details><summary>rāmamiśraśāstrī</summary>

(bhagavat-pāriṣadānam īśō viṣvaksēnas  
tad-upayōgānantara-kālē niṣēdha-parāṇi draṣṭavyāni ।)
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yatō bhagavad-arthēna  
tyaktaṁ srak-candanādikam ।  
paścād abhōgyatāṁ yāti  
viṣvaksēna-nivēdanāt ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Since the garlands, sandal etc, which are offered up to the Bhagavān, later on, after the Viśvaksena offering, become unfit to eat, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Sāttvata Saṁhitā, X. 57-58.

> dijātēḥ datta-śiṣṭasya puṣpa-patrādikasya ca ।  
vihitaś cāmbhasi tyāgō viśvaksēnēnārcanē kr̥tē ॥  
dhartavyaṁ na ciraṁ cāgrē yat purā vinivēditam ।  
naivēdyaṁ mantra-mūrtīnāṁ kiñcit-puṣpa-phalādr̥tē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yatō bhagavadarthēna tyaktaṁ srak-candanādikam ।  
paścād abhōgyatāṁ yāti viṣvaksēna-nivēdanāt ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ata ēva nivēdy-ādi  
tatō'rvāg ēva sāttvataiḥ ।  
sēvyatē tēna tat tēṣām  
utkarṣasyaiva kāraṇam ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

therefore the Sātvatas use the nivedya etc. before that time. Consequently the use of the nirmālya is a cause of excellence for the Sātvatas.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ata ēva nivēdyādi tatō'rvāg ēva sāttvataiḥ ।  
sēvyatē tēna tat tēṣām utkarṣasyaiva kāraṇam ॥
</details>

#### dēvatāntara-nirmālyē

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca ।  

dēvatāntara-nirmālyaṁ  
śiṣṭair iṣṭaṁ vigarhitam +++(surā-pānavat)+++ ।  
idaṁ tu vaidikatvēna  
sōma-pānavad iṣyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

[[118]]

136\. Moreover, it is our postulation that the exemplary people hold the nirmālya of other gods in contempt; this is postulated like the drinking of soma (which is good) because it is Vedic (in contrast to the drinking of liquor which is evil). 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

dēvatāntara-nirmālyaṁ śiṣṭaiḥ vigarhita-svarūpēṇa iṣṭam ity arthaḥ ।

idaṁ tu ... Cf. Viṣṇusaṁhitā, XXXIX. 12-13a:

> nirmālyaṁ na spr̥śēdadyāt laṅghayēd vāśanaṁ kutaḥ ।  
sarvēṣām ēva dēvānāṁ nirmālyam aśuci smr̥tam ॥  
viṣṇu-bhuktaṁ tu puṣpādi śucīty ādadatē parē ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca ।  

dēvatāntara-nirmālyaṁ śiṣṭair iṣṭaṁ vigarhitam ।  
idaṁ tu vaidikatvēna sōma-pānavad iṣyatē ॥
</details>

#### nigamanam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yē nāma bhagavacchāstra-  
prāmāṇyaṁ nānujānatē ।  
na nirūpayituṁ śakyaṁ  
tair nirmālyam itīritam ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

So I have said that those who do not accept the validity of the Bhagavān's doctrine are unable to determine what is nirmālya. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yē nāma bhagavacchāstra-prāmāṇyaṁ nānujānatē ।  
na nirūpayituṁ śakyaṁ tair nirmālyam itīritam ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

nirūpaṇē'pi bhagavan-  
nirmālyam atipāvanam ।  
samasta-vaidikācārya-  
vacanair avasīyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

When it is properly determined (namely according to the Bhagavān's doctrine) the Bhagavān's nirmālya proves to be extremely purifying, as is demonstrated by the statements of all Vedic teachers. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nirūpaṇē'pi bhagavannirmālyam atipāvanam ।  
samasta-vaidikācārya-vacanair avasīyatē ॥
</details>

#### śabda-pramāṇam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

śabda-pramāṇakē hy arthē  
yathā-śabdaṁ vyavasthitiḥ ।  
na cātra śabdō nāstīti  
vaktavyaṁ badhirētaraiḥ ॥+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>viṣayaḥ</summary>

śabdaḥ, pāñcarātram
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

In a matter for which the only means of knowledge is verbal testimony, it must be so as verbal testimony says that it is. Unless one is deaf, one cannot say that there is no verbal testimony concerning it.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

śabda-pramāṇakē hy arthē yathā-śabdaṁ vyavasthitiḥ ।  
na cātra śabdō nāstīti vaktavyaṁ badhirētaraiḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā brahma-purāṇē ca paṭhyatē -  

> viṣṇōr naivēdyakaṁ śuddhaṁ  
munibhir bhōjyam ucyatē ।  
anyan nivēdya-nirmālyaṁ  
bhuktvā cāndrāyaṇaṁ carēt ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For instance it is said in the Brahma Purāṇa: 

> "The nivedya of Viṣṇu is declared by the sages to be pure and fit for consumption; one who eats other nirmālya and nivedya must perform the cāndrāyaṇa in expiation. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

viṣṇōr ... Passages to be identified.

munibhirbhōjyamucyatē ... Cf. Pādmasaṁhitā, caryā, XII. 81b:

> viṣṇōr nivēditēna śuddhaṁ pāvanānāṁ ca pāvanam ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā brahma-purāṇē ca paṭhyatē -  

viṣṇōr naivēdyakaṁ śuddhaṁ munibhir bhōjyam ucyatē ।  
anyan nivēdya-nirmālyaṁ bhuktvā cāndrāyaṇaṁ carēt ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> viṣṇu-dēha-parāmr̥ṣṭaṁ  
mālyaṁ pāpa-haraṁ śubham ।  
yō naraś śirasā dhattē  
sa yāti paramāṁ gatim ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> The mālya which is taken from the body of Viṣṇu takes away evil and is holy.  
He who wears it on his head goes to supreme bliss." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Pādmasaṁhitā, caryā, XII. 85:

> dharitaṁ viṣṇu-nirmālyaṁ candanādy anulēpanam ।  
ahar-niśaṁ dhārayatāṁ na punar-jananaṁ bhavēt ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

viṣṇu-dēha-parāmr̥ṣṭaṁ mālyaṁ pāpa-haraṁ śubham ।  
yō naraś śirasā dhattē sa yāti paramāṁ gatim ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ētēna -  

> nirmālyaṁ ca nivēdyaṁ ca bhuktvā cāndrāyaṇaṁ carēt ।  

iti smaraṇam api rudrakālyādiviṣayam ityāvēditavyam, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

It follows that the smṛti statement that a man who eats nirmālya and nivedya must perform the cāndrāyaṇa 295 should be taken to bear upon the nirmālya of Rudra, Kālī etc.

[295]: as quoted supra § 16.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be traced out. Cf. Pādmasaṁhitā, caryā, XII. 79a:

> brahmēśānādi-dēvānāṁ naiva bhōjyaṁ nivēditam ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ētēna -  

> nirmālyaṁ ca nivēdyaṁ ca bhuktvā cāndrāyaṇaṁ carēt ।  

iti smaraṇam api rudrakālyādiviṣayam ityāvēditavyam, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā mahā-bhāratē -  

> hr̥di dhyāyan hariṁ tasmai  
nivēdyānnaṁ samāhitaḥ ।  
madhyamānāmikāṅguṣṭhair  
gr̥hītvānna-mitaṁ punaḥ ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

(282: Mahābhārata quotations not verifiable.  )

Thus in the Mahābhārata: 

> "Meditating in one's heart upon Hari, one must offer food to Him with full attention, thereupon pick up this food again with the middlefinger and the thumb, 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be identified. 

Cf. Laghuvyāsasaṁhitā ( Aṣṭāviṁśatismṛtis ) ch. II. 74-76:

> svāhā-praṇava-saṁyuktaṁ prāṇāyānnāhutiṁ tataḥ ।  
apānāya tatō hutvā dhyānāya tad-anantaram ॥  
udānāya tatō hutvā samānāyēti pañcamam ।  
vijñāya cārtham ētēṣāṁ juhuyād ātmani dvi-jaḥ ॥  
śēṣam annaṁ yathā-kāmaṁ bhuñjīta vyañjanair yutam ।  
dhyātvā tan-manasā dēvam ātmānaṁ vai prajā-patim ॥

This type of taking food is called ‘anuyāga’. See Pāñcarātrarakṣā, p. 115: ‘īdr̥śaṁ ca bhōjanam ēvānuyāga-samākhyayā 'nyatra vyapadiśyatē ।’
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā mahā-bhāratē -  

> hr̥di dhyāyan hariṁ tasmai nivēdyānnaṁ samāhitaḥ ।  
madhyamānāmikāṅguṣṭhair gr̥hītvānnamitaṁ punaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> prāṇāya cēty apānāya  
vyānāya ca tataḥ param ।  
udānāya samānāya  
svāhēti juhuyāt kramāt ॥

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> and then sacrifice it bit by bit, saying: "Prāṇāya svāhā, Apānāya svāhā, Vyānāya svāhā, Udānāya svāhā, Samānāya svāhā." 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> prāṇāya cētyapānāya vyānāya ca tataḥ param ।  
udānāya samānāya svāhēti juhuyāt kramāt ॥

iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā pradēśāntarē  -  

> nivēditaṁ tu yad dēvē  
tad dadyād brahma-cāriṇē ।  

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Likewise in another passage, "what has been offered to the god must be given to a brahmacārin."296 

[296]: Mahābhārata quotations not verifiable.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

To be traced out.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā pradēśāntarē  -  

> nivēditaṁ tu yad dēvē  
tad dadyād brahma-cāriṇē ।  

iti ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā mahā-bhāratē -  

> pañcarātra-vidō mukhyās  
tasya gēhē mahātmanaḥ ।  
prāśanaṁ bhagavad-bhuktaṁ  
bhuñjatē cāgra-bhōjanam ॥

iti, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Thus in the Mahābhārata: 

> "The saintly knowers of the Pañcaratra ate in his house that which had been left over by the Bhagavān, as a means to attain to bliss, as supreme nourishment."297 

[297]: The ritual taking of food is considered a performance of the prāṇāgnihotra.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Śānti, ch. 322, śl. 23.  
Cf. Sāttvatasaṁhitā, ch. 17, śls. 423-424:

> dānānaṁ ca vratānāṁ ca tapasām yajña-karmaṇām ।  
nivēditavyaṁ yad dravyaṁ, dattaṁ vā yat purā ॥  
kartavyam anuyāgārthaṁ prāk tad ēva hi kēvalam ।  
tad bhāvitam atō 'śrīyāt pāvanaṁ prāṇānvitam ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā mahā-bhāratē -  

pañcarātra-vidō mukhyās tasya gēhē mahātmanaḥ ।  
prāśanaṁ bhagavad-bhuktaṁ bhuñjatē cāgra-bhōjanam ॥

iti, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tathā ca bhagavān śaunakaḥ 

> naivēdyaṁ svayam aśnīyād 

iti ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And likewise the blessed Śaunaka:  
"He himself eats the nivedya." 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Viṣṇudharma ( of Bhaviṣyapurāṇa ), Śaunakīya, ch. 92. śl. 32a:

> naivēdyaṁ svayam aśnīyāt maunīty ētad udaṅ-mukhaḥ ।

Cf. Pūjāsaṅgraha ( ms. ) folio 90b:

> svayaṁ vāpi tad aśnīyāt sarva-pāpa-viśuddhayē ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tathā ca bhagavān śaunakaḥ naivēdyaṁ svayam aśnīyād iti, ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ityādi-smr̥ti-śata-siddha-śuddhi viṣṇōr  
naivēdyaṁ bhava-bhaya-bhēdi yō vinindēt ।  
nāstikyāt smr̥ti-vacanāny upēkṣamāṇas tajjihvā-viśasanam ēva yuktam atra ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

He who condemns Viṣṇu's nivedya, whose purity is proved by hundreds of similar smṛtis and which dispels the fear of rebirth, really ignores the statements of the smṛti because of his heterodoxy and ought to have his tongue cut off.

[[119]]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ityādi-smr̥ti-śata-siddha-śuddhi viṣṇōr  
naivēdyaṁ bhava-bhaya-bhēdi yō vinindēt ।  
nāstikyāt smr̥ti-vacanāny upēkṣamāṇas tajjihvā-viśasanam ēva yuktam atra ।  
</details>

#### prāṇāgnihōtrē naivēdyam
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nanu prāṇāgnihōtrasya  
naivēdya-sādhanaṁ katham ।  
nir-iṣṭakaṁ na śiṣṭānām  
iṣṭaṁ hōmādi-sādhanam ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

137\. OBJECTION. But how can the nivedya be a means for the prāṇāgnihotra?283  
The exemplary people do not approve of a means for homa etc. for which ~~no building bricks are used.??~~ (no sacrifice has been made.) 

283: The ritual taking of food is considered a performance of the prāṇāgnihotra.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Vedānta Deśika quotes from "nanu" upto "yathānuṣṭhāna-tantratvaṁ" etc., below, in his Saccaritrārakṣā, p. 93.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

> nanu prāṇāgnihōtrasya naivēdyasādhanaṁ katham ।  
nir-iṣṭakaṁ na śiṣṭānām iṣṭaṁ hōmādi-sādhanam ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> na ca +++(śarīrārthaṁ)+++ dravyāntarākṣēpō  
hōmāyēty a-kalpatē ।  
rāgataḥ prāptam ēvānnaṁ  
yatas tēnōpajīvyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Nor can a substitution of another substance do duty as a homa,  
> because he lives off food that has been obtained according to taste. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ākṣēpaḥ kalpanam iti yāvat ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

na ca dravyāntarākṣēpō hōmāyētyakalpatē ।  
rāgataḥ prāptam ēvānnaṁ yatas tēnōpajīvyatē ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

> nāpi +++(sāyam-prātar-apēkṣayā)+++ bhukty-antarākṣēpō  
naivēdyāyōpapādyatē ।  
sāyaṁ-prātar dvi-jātīnām  
aśanaṁ śruti-cōditam ॥  
nāntarā bhōjanaṁ kuryād  
iti tat-pratiṣēdhanāt ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

> Nor can a substitution of another consumption be made to replace the nivedya,  
for scripture enjoins upon the twiceborn a meal in the evening and a meal in the morning,  
as follows from the prohibition: "One should not take food in between."
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

The remainder of the verse is ‘agni-hōtra-samō vidhiḥ ।’ Many Smṛtis attribute this to Manu. But Aparārka on Yājñavalkyasmṛti (p. 61) attributes this to Saṁvarta. Cf. also Saṁvartasmṛti ( Collection of 27 smṛtis, Ānandāśrama Skt. Series ), I.12.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

nāpi bhuktyantarākṣēpō naivēdyāyōpapādyatē ।  
sāyaṁ-prātar dvi-jātīnām aśanaṁ śruti-cōditam ॥
nāntarā bhōjanaṁ kuryād iti tat-pratiṣēdhanāt ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

naiṣa dōṣō yataḥ prāṇa-  
prabhr̥tir dēvatā-gaṇaḥ ॥  
guṇa-**bhūtaḥ śrutō** viṣṇōr  
viṣṇu-pāriṣadēśavat ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

REFUTATION. That is no defect, since the multitude of deities, like prāṇa etc. are revealed to be parts of Viṣṇu, in the same way as Viśvaksena, the chief of Viṣṇu's retinue. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

naiṣa dōṣō yataḥ prāṇa-prabhr̥tir dēvatā-gaṇaḥ ॥  
guṇa-bhūtaḥ śrutō viṣṇōr viṣṇupāriṣadēśavat ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathaiva hi bhagavan-nivēditam api puṣpaudanādi  
viṣvaksēnāya dīyamānaṁ nānaucityam āvahati ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For just as the flowers, cake etc., though proffered to the Bhagavān  
but actually given to Viśvaksena shows that. 
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathaiva hi bhagavannivēditam api puṣpaudanādi  
viṣvaksēnāya dīyamānaṁ nānaucityam āvahati ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā vā hōtur ucchiṣṭa  
ēva sōma-rasō 'dhvarē ।  
adhvaryv-ādēr viśuddhyai syād  
ēvam atra bhaviṣyati ॥+++(4)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

He is familiar under various guises, or just as at a sacrifice the soma juice that is left over by the hotṛ is pure to the adhvaryu, so it is also with the nirmālya.298

[298]: The hotar is the principal reciting priest at the soma sacrifice, the adhvaryu the main executive
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā vā hōturucchiṣṭa ēva sōma-rasō'dhvarē ।  
adhvaryvādēr viśuddhyai syād ēvam atra bhaviṣyati ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

api ca - 

bhōjyābhōjya-vyavasthāyāḥ  
śāstram ēva nibandhanam ।  
tac cēd bhōjyam idaṁ brūtē  
kiṁ vayaṁ vidadhīmahi ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Moreover, only scripture can be our criterion for what is to be eaten and what is not to be eaten. When it says that something is fit to be eaten, what injunction are we to invent ourselves? 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Bhagavadgītā, XVI. 24a:

> tasmāc chāstraṁ pramāṇaṁ tē kāryākārya-vyavasthitau ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

api ca ।  
bhōjyābhōjya-vyavasthāyāḥ śāstram ēva nibandhanam ।  
tac cēd bhōjyam idaṁ brūtē kiṁ vayaṁ vidadhīmahi ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā 'nuṣṭhāna-tantratvaṁ  
nitya-kāmyāgnihōtrayōḥ ।  
ēvaṁ prāṇāgnihōtrē'pi  
naivēdyāśana-tantratā ॥+++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Just as the same rule governs both the periodical and the desiderative agnihotra, so the same rule governing the eating of the nivedya applies also to the prāṇāgnihotra.

[[120]]
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ubhayōddēśēna sakr̥d anuṣṭhānaṁ tantram ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā 'nuṣṭhāna-tantratvaṁ nitya-kāmyāgnihōtrayōḥ ।  
ēvaṁ prāṇāgnihōtrē'pi naivēdyāśanatantratā ॥

</details>

### vaidika-karmātiraskāraḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yad apy uktaṁ 

> garbhādhānādi-dāhānta-saṁskārāntara-sēvanād  
bhāgavatānām a-brahmaṇyam 

iti tatrāpy ajñānam ēvāparādhyati,  
na punar āyuṣmatō dōṣaḥ,  
yad ētē vaṁśa-paramparayā vājasanēya-śākhā-madhīyānāḥ  
kātyāyanādi-gr̥hyōkta-mārgēṇa garbhādhānādi-saṁskārān kurvatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

138\. As to the remark299 that from the observance of different sacraments,  
from conception ceremony to cremation,  
it follows that the Bhagavatas are not brahmins,  
here again ignorance is to blame.  
It is not your Honour's fault  
that the Bhagavatas, who have the Vājasanevasakha in the transmission of their family line,  
observe the sacraments of conception ceremony etc. according to the manner laid down by the grhyasutras of Katyayana etc. 

[299]: supra § 17.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

yadapyuktaṁ ... See p. 14 above for pūrvapakṣa. Vedānta Deśika quotes from here upto the end of the text, in his Nyāyapariśuddhi, p. 168

yadētē ... Deśika quotes from here upto the end, in his Pāñcarātrarakṣā, p. 95.

kātyāyanādi ... See Kātyāyanagṛhyasūtra ( ms. ), p. 25ff for saṁskāras.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadapyuktaṁ garbhādhānādidāhāntasaṁskārāntarasēvanād bhāgavatānāmabrahmaṇyamiti tatrāpyajñānamēvāparādhyati, na punarāyuṣmatō dōṣaḥ, yadētē vaṁśaparamparayā vājasanēyaśākhāmadhīyānāḥ kātyāyanādigr̥hyōktamārgēṇa garbhādhānādisaṁskārān kurvatē ।  
</details>

#### ēkāyana-śākhā
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yē punaḥ sāvitry-anuvacana-prabhr̥ti--trayī-dharma-**tyāgēna** 
ēkāyana-śruti-vihitān ēva cattvāriṁśat saṁskārān **kurvatē**  
tē'pi sva-śākhā-gr̥hyōktam arthaṁ yathāvad anutiṣṭhamānāḥ  
na śākhāntarīya--karmānanuṣṭhānād brāhmaṇyāt pracyavantē,  
anyēṣām api para-śākhā-vihita-karmānanuṣṭhāna-nimittābrāhmaṇya-prasaṅgāt
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Those who perform the forty sacraments  
which are enjoined by the Ekayana scripture  
while giving up the dharmas of the Veda,  
from the recitation of the gāyatri onward, 300  
they properly follow the rules laid down by the grhyasutras of their own sakha  
and do not abdicate their brahminhood  
because they fail to follow the rites of a different shakha;  
since otherwise it would follow that other brahmins too would forfeit their brahminhood because they fail to perform the rites enjoined by other [[121]] people's Sakha.

[300]: namely, at the upanayana ceremony.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

ananuṣṭhānāt hētōr iti bhāvaḥ ।

pracyavantē ... Cf. the following quoted in the Pāñcarātrarakṣā, p. 110, as from the Pārameśvarasaṁhitā:

> niṣēkādīṁś ca saṁskārān sva-sūtrōktān samācarēt ।  
pañca-rātrōditān vāpi yē sva-vaṁśyair anuṣṭhitāḥ ॥

Cf. also Auśanasa Dharmaśāstra ( Smṛtīnāṁ Samuccayaḥ, Ānandāśrama Sanskrit Series 48 ), I, 48:

> niṣēkādyāḥ śmaśānāntāḥ kriyāḥ pūjāṅga-sūtra-dhr̥k ।  
pañca-rātrēṇa vā kaścit tantrōktaṁ dharmam ācarēt ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yē punaḥ sāvitryanuvacanaprabhr̥titrayīdharmatyāgēna ēkāyanaśrutivihitānēva cattvāriṁśat saṁskārān kurvatē  
tē'pi svaśākhāgr̥hyōktamarthaṁ yathāvadanutiṣṭhamānāḥ na śākhāntarīyakarmānanuṣṭhānād brāhmaṇyāt pracyavantē, anyēṣāmapi paraśākhāvihitakarmānanuṣṭhānanimittābrāhmaṇyaprasaṅgāt
</details>

<details><summary>rāmamiśraśāstrī</summary>

yadyapi anūpasr̥ṣṭāttiṣṭhatērnātmanēpadaṁ prāpnōtīti anutiṣṭhanta ityēva syāt  
tathāpi anuṣṭhānaśīlā anuṣṭhānaparāyaṇā ityarthasya pratipipādayitatvēna  
tācchīlyavayōvacanaśaktiṣu cānaś iti pāṇinīyēna cānaśpratyayō  
na tu śānacpratyaya ityavadhārayantu nipuṇāḥ ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

sarvatra hi jāti-caraṇa-gōtrādhikārādi-vyavasthitā ēva samācārā upalabhyantē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

For everywhere among brahmins we find customs that differ according to birth, caraṇa, gotra, qualification etc. 
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

caraṇa-śabdēna śākhōcyatē ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

sarvatra hi jāti-caraṇa-gōtrādhikārādivyavasthitā ēva samācārā upalabhyantē ।  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yady api sarva-śākhā-pratyayam ēkaṁ karma  
tathā'pi na paras-para-vilakṣaṇādhikāri-saṁbaddhā dharmāḥ  
kvacit samuccīyantē, 
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

Even though one ritual is understood for all śākhās,  
still all the various dharmas relating to mutually different qualified performers  
do not all together accumulate in any one place.  
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

Cf. Śābara on II. iv. 32, p. 142: “..sarva-śākhā-pratyayaṁ sarva-brāhma-pratyayaṁ caikaṁ karma cōdyata iti siddhaṁ bhavati ।”

See also Pūrvamīmāṁsā, II. iv. 18: “na caikaṁ prati śiṣyatē ।” and Śābara on this (p. 139): 

> na ca yat kāṭhakē 'gni-hōtraṁ tat kāṭhakam ēvaikaṁ puruṣaṁ prati vidhīyatē । taittirīyasyāpi tat vihitam ēva । puruṣa-viśēṣa-vacanābhāvāt ।...tasmāt sarva-śākhābhir ēkaṁ samāptaṁ karmōcyata iti ।
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yadyapi sarvaśākhāpratyayamēkaṁ karma  
tathā'pi na parasparavilakṣaṇādhikārisaṁbaddhā dharmāḥ kvacitsamuccīyantē, 
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

vilakṣaṇāś ca trayī-vihita-svarga-putrādi-viṣayōpabhōga-sādhanaindrāgnēyādi-karmādhikāribhyō dvijēbhyas  
 
trayy-antaikāyana-śruti-vihita-vijñānābhigamanōpādānējyā-prabhr̥ti-  
bhagavat-prāpty-ēkōpāyaka-karmādhikāriṇō mumukṣavō brāhmaṇā  
iti nōbhayēṣām apy anyōnya-śākhā-vihita-karmānanuṣṭhānam a-brāhmaṇyam āpādayati।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

And the Aspirants who are distinct from those brahmins who are qualified for rites of the aindrāgneya etc.,301  
which are means leading to the enjoyment of rewards like heaven etc.,  
as enjoined by the three Vedas,  
and who themselves are qualified for the rites of the Ekayana,  
rites which alone are the means of attaining to the Bhagavan,  
viz. knowledge, cleansing the way to the Lord, preparation of worship and oblation, as enjoined by the Ekayana scripture, are brahmins too.  
It follows that the non-observance of certain rites enjoined by different sākhās  
does not mean that either one forfeits his brahminhood-  

[301]: aindrāgneya, name of a śrauta ritual.
</details>

<details><summary>narasiṁhaḥ</summary>

trayyantaikāyana ... See Pādmasaṁhitā, I. 5b-6a:

> ādyam ēkāyanaṁ vēdaṁ sad-brahma-pratipādakam ॥  
tēnaiva saṁskr̥tā viprā mukhya-kalpādhikāriṇaḥ ।

vijñānābhigamana ... Ibid. Jñāna, II. 5b:

> vijñānaṁ bhagavaj-jñānaṁ taj-jñānān muktir ucyatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

vilakṣaṇāśca trayīvihitasvargaputrādiviṣayōpabhōgasādhanaindrāgnēyādikarmādhikāribhyō dvijēbhyas  
trayyantaikāyanaśrutivihitavijñānābhigamanōpādānējyāprabhr̥tibhagavatprāptyēkōpāyakakarmādhikāriṇōmumukṣavō brāhmaṇā itinōbhayēṣāmapyanyōnyaśākhāvihitakarmānanuṣṭhānamabrāhmaṇyamāpādayati,  
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

yathā caikāyana-śākhāyā apauruṣēyatvaṁ  
tathā kāśmīrāgama-prāmāṇyē prapañcitam iti  
nēha prastūyatē ।  +++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

that the Ekāyana sākhā is preterpersonal scripture has been enlarged upon in the Treatise on the Validity of Kasmira Agama,302  
and is therefore here not further discussed. 

[302]: Name of a work of Yāmuna.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

yathā caikāyana-śākhāyā apauruṣēyatvaṁ tathā kāśmīrāgamaprāmāṇyē prapañcitamiti nēha prastūyatē ।  
</details>

<details><summary>viśvāsa-ṭippanī</summary>

anēna yāmunō 'pauruṣēyatvam aṅgīcakārēti jñāyatē। +++(5)+++
</details>

<details><summary>rāmamiśraśāstrī</summary>

kāśmīrāgamapadēna kiṁ vivakṣitamiti na viśiṣya jānīmaḥ kāśmīrāgamaprāmāṇyanirūpaṇaparōgranthō'pi cāsmadr̥ṣṭēragōcara iti na kiṁcidīśmahē vaktum ।  
yatnēna tu tat sarvam āsādhya samayē prakāśayiṣyatē ।  
</details>

#### itarē bhāgavatāḥ
<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

prakr̥tānāṁ tu bhāgavatānāṁ  
sāvitry-anuvacanādi-trayī-dharma-bandhasya sphuṭataram upalabdhēr  
na tat-tyāga-nimitta-vrātyatvādi-saṁdēhaṁ sahatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

But since it is quite obvious that the Bhagavatas, which we are discussing here,  
are connected with the dharmas of the three Vedas, like the savitri recitation,  
there is no possible support for the suspicion  
that they are really vratyas  
because they would have abandoned these Vedic dharmas.
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

prakr̥tānāṁ tu bhāgavatānāṁ sāvitryanuvacanāditrayīdharmabandhasya sphuṭataramupalabdhērna tattyāganimittavrātyatvādisaṁdēhaṁ sahatē ॥
</details>

<details><summary>rāmamiśraśāstrī</summary>

gāyatrīmantrāpēkṣā-viṣayiṇī ṭippany [atra](https://vishvAsa.github.io/rAmAnujIyam/kriyA/venkaTa-nAtha-shAkhA/rAma-mishra-shAstri-sAvitrI-japApexA/) । 
</details>

## 18 samāptiḥ

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

tat-tat-kalpita-yuktibhis **śakalaśaḥ kr̥tvā** tadīyaṁ mataṁ   
yac-chiṣyair **udamardi** sāttvata-mata-spardhāvatām **uddhatiḥ** ॥  
yac caitat satataṁ mukunda-caraṇa-dvandvāspadaṁ **vartatē**  
**jīyān** nātha-munis sva-yōga-mahima-pratyakṣa-tattva-trayaḥ ॥  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

139\. May Nāthamuni 303 be victorious, he to whom the Three Principles are immediately evident by virtue of his own miraculous power, he by whose pupils the arrogance of the rivals of the Sāttvata Doctrine is terminated after their own view was rent to pieces by variously apposite arguments, he whose spirit is for ever the abode of the feet of Mukunda. 

[303]: Predecessor of Yāmuna at Śrīraṅga.  
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

tattatkalpitayuktibhisśakalaśaḥ kr̥tvā tadīyaṁ mataṁ ।  
yacchiṣyairudamardi sāttvatamatasparddhāvatāmuddhatiḥ ॥  
yaccētatsataṁ mukundacaraṇadvandvāspadaṁ vartatē ।  
jīyānnāthamunissvayōgamahimapratyakṣatattvatrayaḥ ॥
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

ākalpaṁ **vilasantu** sāttvata-mata-praspardhi--duṣ-paddhati--  
vyāmugdhōddhata-durvidagdha-pariṣad-vaidagdhya-vidhvaṁsinaḥ ।  
śrīman-nātha-munīndra-varddhita-dhiyō nirdhūta-viśvāśivāḥ  
santas santata-gadya-padya-padavī-**hr̥dyānavadyōktayaḥ** ।  
</details>

<details><summary>Buitenen</summary>

May, for the length of this Aeon, play on the pious, enchanting and irreproachable sayings of the extensive collection of prose and verse compositions which eclipse the cleverness of the befuddled, conceited and witless assembly of the evil crowd of the rivals of the Sāttvata doctrine, whose spirit has been increased by the glorious Nāthamunīndra,304 and by which all the unholy powers are cleansed,

[304]: Nāthamuni compiled the sayings of the Vaiṣṇava saints, the Āḻvārs.  

[[122]]
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

ākalpaṁ vilasantu sāttvatamataprasparddhiduṣpaddhativyāmugdhōddhatadurvidagdhapariṣadvaidagdhyavidhvaṁsinaḥ ।  
śrīmannāthamunīndravarddhitadhiyōnirdhūtaviśvāśivāḥ santassantatagadyapadyapadavīhr̥dyānavadyōktayaḥ ।
</details>

<details open><summary>vi॰pra॰</summary>

**iti śrī-yāmuna-muni-viracitam āgama-prāmāṇyam ॥**
</details>

<details><summary>mūlam</summary>

**iti śrī-yāmunamuniviracitamāgamaprāmāṇyam ॥**
</details>

# Appendix - +Dyugangā dyugaṅgā

## Goals dhyēyāni
Dyugangā is a work group dedicated to the promotion of ever-victorious Hindu ideals and arts. It's current focus is in presenting important texts for easy study. Long term goal (https://rebrand.ly/dg-archive) is to save texts to last for millennia into the coming post-electronic/ industrial age.

The texts may be presented as 

- audio files (eg: [MahAbhArata audio book project](https://sanskrit.github.io/groups/dyuganga/projects/audio/mbh-audio/)), 
- as web pages (eg. [Apastamba-gRhya-sUtra](https://vishvasa.github.io/vedAH_yajuH/taittirIyam/sUtram/ApastambaH/gRhyam/sUtra-TIkAH/), [Apastamba-dharma-sUtra](https://vishvasa.github.io/vedAH_yajuH/taittirIyam/sUtram/ApastambaH/dharma-sUtram/sarva-prastutiH/), [EkAgnikANDa commentary](https://vishvasa.github.io/vedAH_yajuH/taittirIyam/sUtram/ApastambaH/gRhyam/ekAgnikANDam/sarva-prastutiH/), [manu-smRti](https://vishvasa.github.io/kalpAntaram/smRtiH/manuH/sarva-prastutiH/05/), [raghuvaMsha](https://vishvasa.github.io/kAvyam/laxyam/padyam/kAlidAsaH/raghuvaMsham/sarva-prastutiH/01/), more [kalpa-texts](https://sanskrit.github.io/groups/dyuganga//projects/text/proofreading/kalpa-texts/), [tattva-texts](https://sanskrit.github.io/groups/dyuganga//projects/text/proofreading/tattva-texts/), [universal subhAShita DB](https://subhashita.github.io/saMskRtam/padyam/random/)), 
- as dictionaries (eg: [stardict](https://sanskrit-coders.github.io/dictionaries/offline/stardict))
- ebooks distributed on various platforms - (eg: [vishvasa.github.io/book-pub](https://vishvasa.github.io/book-pub), amazon, google play - [SVK](https://play.google.com/store/books/series?id=EeyGHAAAABCW8M) [SVT](https://play.google.com/store/books/series?id=deyGHAAAABDy8M) [kā](https://play.google.com/store/books/series?id=EuyGHAAAABCV8M)). Formats include md, pdf (A4, A5), epub, azw3, html, etc. 

We distribute these for free, and under a CC BY 4.0 license. (Platforms may levy their fees.) You may subscribe to mail-streams for past and future announcements ([dg](https://groups.google.com/g/dyuganga), [hv](https://groups.google.com/g/hindu-vidya/), [san](https://groups.google.com/g/samskrita)). 

The choice of material heavily depends on the special interests of its current lead (vedas, kalpa, purANa-s).

### saṁskr̥tānuvādaḥ
dyugaṅgā nāma kāryasaṁsthā - ajēyānāṁ bhāratīyapuruṣārthaparikalpanānāñca, hindukakalānāñca prasāraṇāya vartatē।  
tadīyas sthūlōddēśō'dhunā pramukhagranthānām adhyayanasaukaryāya prastutiḥ। tatō grantha-saṅkalana-kēndram iti vaktum alam। dūrōddēśas tu (https://rebrand.ly/dg-archive) ādhunika-śilā-taila-yugāt param api sahasrādhika-varṣāṇi yāvad grantha-rakṣā।

granthānām prastutir dhvanisañcikābhis syāt (yathā [mahābhāratapārāyaṇaprasāraṇē](https://sanskrit.github.io/groups/dyuganga/projects/audio/mbh-audio/)), jāla-kṣētra-pr̥ṣṭhair vā (yathā [viśvāsasya mantraṭippanīṣu](https://vishvasa.github.io/vedAH_sAma/paravastu-saama/devaH/agniH/mahAvaishvAnara-vratam/), [ēkāgnikāṇḍaṭīkā](https://vishvasa.github.io/vedAH_yajuH/taittirIyam/sUtram/ApastambaH/gRhyam/ekAgnikANDam/sarva-prastutiH/1_01a/)), śabda-kōśair vā'pi ([stardict](https://sanskrit-coders.github.io/dictionaries/offline/stardict))। imē 'smat-pakṣatō mukta-rītyā prasāryantē। sadyaśca granthāḥ saṁsthāgraṇyā ruciviśēṣam anusr̥tya citāḥ - vēdāḥ, itihāsa-purāṇāni, kalpa-vēdāṅga-granthāś cēti।

### Contribution, contact
asmat-samparkaḥ - @gmail - vishvas.vasuki, 95912 68506 (<http://rebrand.ly/dyuganga>)। Serious volunteering, donations and sponsorship are welcome  - they help offset operating costs (eg. worker payments, book distribution) and plan further projects. Project-specific sponsorship opportunities are occasionally advertised on our social media accounts and on certain mailing lists.

## vandanīya-vandanā
(anēnōdyamēna naiṣāṁ mahatāṁ sākṣāt sambandha ūhyaḥ ।)

<div class="js_include" includetitle="false" newlevelforh1="5" unfilled="" url="/rAmAnujIyam/vyakti-shlokAdi/paLHaveri-laxmI-nRsiMhaH.md"> 

iñjimēḍu-yati-siṁha-**rakṣitō**  
rājagōpa--budha-gōpa-**cāritaḥ**।  
siṁha-lakṣma-nara-nāma-bhāg **babhau**  
divya-sūkti-vana-mārga-**nāyakaḥ**॥

yad-ācāra-svabhāvābhyāṁ  
"jñēyam asty atra vaiṣṇavē"।  
iti niṣkarṣa-jijñāsē,  
**naumi** taṁ śrī-nr̥siṁhakam॥
</div>
